Chapter 4: Music

Chapter Summary

The choral auditions are here. Agatha and Rio start to get closer and share more about themselves. There is a little heat.

There is a poll for the musical choice on my Tumblr. You get to vote on it so please do and help me!

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Four

“I’m not singing,” Rio said the second she got to class the next morning. Lilia was scribbling away at some notes on her desk, drinking from a mug that read, “Keep the Drama on the Stage.”

“Then you’ll get a B,” Lilia replied, then reconsidered. “Maybe a B+. That monologue was good. I really felt that energy, that nervousness .”

“Then I deserve an A,” Rio huffed. “An A- plus , like you said.”

“Not for an incomplete audition,” Lilia scoffed, taking a sip of her coffee. 

“I thought it was just the monologue!” Rio exclaimed, throwing her hands up in the air. “That’s all it was supposed to be: some extra credit so my GPA doesn’t drop.”

“Don’t you have a 5.0 or something?”

“That’s impossible,” Rio huffed. “I have a 4.2.”

“Then you’re in no danger, doll. Not from a single B in a drama class.”

“It’s the principle of the matter, then,” Rio said. “I haven’t gotten a B on anything since sixth grade French. And there’s a reason I don’t take that class, anymore.”

“Afraid of a challenge?” A flicker of challenge flashed in Lilia’s eyes as she took another sip of her coffee. “I didn’t expect that from you , of all people.”

“I’m not singing,” Rio practically growled.

“Then you’re not getting an A,” Lilia retorted.

“This is…unfair.”

“My dear sweet child,” Lilia tutted. “ Many things are unfair. This is not one of them, though. I am the teacher. I set the rules for my assignments, even the extra credit ones. If you do not attend the choral auditions today and sing to the very best of your ability, then you will receive only partial credit. That means a B+, max.” She shrugged her shoulders. “If you’re okay with that, then, by all means, skip the audition. You’ll only be hurting yourself.”

Rio let out a little growl as she stomped off to her seat, the bell ringing above her head to signify the beginning of class. Agatha entered the room just seconds later, her hair pulled back in a messy ponytail, curly and wild, trailing behind her. She wore a deep, royal blue chunky sweater that went down to her knees, a white collar poking out from the neckline. She had on dark leggings and her leather boots to complete the ensemble. She smiled at Rio as she occupied the seat next to her.

Despite her annoyance at the drama teacher, Rio returned Agatha’s smile and coughed into her fist, opening it to reveal a poppy. She offered it to Agatha, who took it gratefully and stuck it into her hairband. 

From the front of the room, Lilia watched with a sly grin as she took another sip of her coffee, savoring the caffeine running through her veins before she stood and cleared her throat.

“Good morning, miscreants,” she said. “Let’s begin, shall we?”

As she turned and began to write something on the board, Rio leaned over toward Agatha. “I need your help.”

“With what?” Agatha asked, not taking her eyes off the board as she copied what Lilia was writing down in her notebook.

“The choral audition,” Rio said, flushing when Agatha finally looked at her.

“You’re doing it?” Agatha whispered, a little too loudly.

“Girls, refrain from speaking during my lecture, please,” Lilia said without even pausing in her writing. Agatha pressed her lips together, but still gave Rio a wide-eyed look of surprise. 

Rio tore a sliver of paper from her notebook and placed it at the edge of her desk before writing on it: She didn’t really give me a choice. Said she’d give me a B+ if I didn’t complete the audition.

“The horror ,” Agatha whispered after she read Rio’s note, snorting when Rio sent her a glare.

You gonna help me or not?

“Of course,” Agatha mouthed back. “But you owe me.”

Rio snorted and made a rose bud appear in her hand, offering it to Agatha, who took it, rolling her eyes. 

“Cute,” she whispered, her voice barely audible. “But that’s not what I meant.”

Still, she placed the bud at the corner of her desk for the rest of class, holding it gently in her palm as they walked out, forty minutes later, Rio following her out the door.

“What, exactly,” Rio asked, “do I owe you?

“Something of my choosing,” Agatha replied. “When the time is right.”

“That is ominous,” Rio said. “For all I know, you want my firstborn.”

“Well, I’ll need a minion,” Agatha said, “for all my evil deeds.”

Rio snorted. “Whatever it is,” she said, “if it helps me get my A, then it’s yours. But only if I get an A. An A -plus. ”

“Okay, then,” Agatha said. “Well, how good is your singing voice?”

“I wouldn’t know,” Rio said, already walking in the direction of her next class. “I don’t sing.”

“Come on,” Agatha huffed, “you never sang a song to the radio? You never sang Happy Birthday to anybody?”

“That’s different,” Rio said. “I’m not going to be singing Happy Birthday on stage. And when I sing to the radio, I can’t really even hear my own voice over the singer’s.”

“Still, you sing,” Agatha said. “That’s something.” The bell rang above them and she cursed under her breath. “Okay, I have to get to class. Meet me at lunch and we’ll go to the chorus room together; it should be empty.”

“Can you even play piano?” Rio asked, incredulously, even as Agatha started sprinting away from her.

“I know enough!” Agatha called over her shoulder. “See you at lunch!”

Rio raised one hand in a little wave, before using that same hand to comb through her fingers as she slipped into her next class. She was still wearing Agatha’s hoodie. It still smelled like her. 

She smiled as she took out her notebook.

 

At lunch, Rio bought herself a bag of Doritos, a soda, and a cookie - a winning lunch combo. Meanwhile, Agatha had a wrap, an orange, and iced tea.

“That’s what you’re eating?” Agatha asked as they walked in the direction of the chorus room and Rio ripped into her bag of chips, popping one into her mouth.

“Yup,” Rio replied, offering her the bag. “Want one?”

Agatha shrugged and took a chip, chewing it thoughtfully. “Not bad,” she said.

“Have you never had Doritos before?” Rio asked.

“Do you really think Evanora Harkness would buy snack food?” Agatha scoffed. “We had rice cakes and cornflakes for snacks. I had to hide Halloween candy before it was all donated. Once, I asked for some money for the ice cream truck, and she handed me rice pudding. I was five.”

Rio handed her the entire bag of Doritos. “Keep it,” she said. “You need it more than I do.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but ate another chip as they pushed open the door to the chorus room, which was, thankfully, deserted. She ushered Rio in and locked the door, conjuring up some of her purple to put a hex on it. That would keep the door locked for a good…twenty minutes, at least.

They walked together to the piano, where they put down their food and Agatha sat down on the bench, opening up the keylid and tapping out a few notes, feeling each one vibrate through her fingers.

“You seriously know how to play,” Rio asked, sipping her soda. 

“My mother forced me into lessons when I was four years old,” Agatha said. “I learned how to play a myriad of classical songs to entertain her friends at parties. I also learned some songs that could really annoy her.” 

She started to tap out a familiar tune and Rio’s eyes widened when she realized what it was.

“ Highway to Hell ?” she guffawed. “I bet she loved that.”

“She had absolutely no idea what it was,” Agatha retorted, continuing to tickle the ivories a bit. “Until she looked it up.” She rolled her eyes. “I was immediately taken out of piano lessons and forced to attend church camp.”

“Where you found out you were a lesbian,” Rio said.

“Yup,” Agatha replied, grinning, her cheeks going a little pink. She stopped playing piano and reached for her wrap, taking one half for herself and offering the other half to a surprised Rio. “I took half your lunch,” Agatha said. “The least I can do is offer you half of mine. It’s chicken and avocado.”

“Ooh, avocado,” Rio said, immediately taking the offered food and taking a bite. Agatha snorted, taking a bite of her own half.

They ate in silence for a while, Agatha occasionally tapping a few notes on the piano in between bites of her wrap and chips and sips of her tea, before she straightened up and stretched her neck.

“Okay,” she said. “You ready for this?”

“Absolutely not,” Rio replied, downing the rest of her soda and letting out a belch. “But let’s start anyway.”

“Okay,” Agatha said, “so what you’re going to do first are some vocal warmups.”

“Ugh.”

“Don’t be a brat,” Agatha huffed, a smile tugging at the corners of her lips. “Just do the Sound of Music thing.”

“The what?”

Agatha let out a groan, pressing her forehead to the top of the piano. “I forgot you have zero culture.”

“Excuse me ,” Rio huffed. “My culture is not movie-based. I’m Puerto Rican. And a little Irish.”

“Can you do a jig?”

“Not that Irish,” Rio laughed. “What’s the Sound of Music thing?”

“Do,” Agatha sang, pressing a deep key. “A deer, a female deer.” She cleared her throat. “Re,” she sang, pressing the next note, a bit higher, “a drop of golden sun. Mi, a name I call myself. Fa, a long, long way to run.” She swallowed, clearing her throat again, feeling Rio’s eyes on her. “So, a needle pulling thread. La, a note to follow so. Ti, a drink with jam and bread. And that will bring us back to,” she returned to the first note, “do.” She turned to Rio, who had taken a seat on the bench, next to her. “Easy,” she said. “You don’t have to do the whole song, though. Just the notes.”

“I don’t think I’ve ever heard you sing solo like that,” Rio said, her voice very soft, very quiet.

Agatha snorted. “Of course you have,” she said. “I’ve been the lead in every musical since freshman year, remember?” 

“But I’ve only ever heard you sing with music,” Rio said. “Not…uh…what’s it called when you sing without music?”

“A capella,” Agatha informed her. “Uncultured…” she muttered under her breath, but her smile was teasing.

“Yeah,” Rio laughed. “That. I’ve never heard you sing a capella. You’re usually accompanied by Alice or somebody else. Your voice is…really good.”

“Thanks,” Agatha said, her face flushing pink. She cleared her throat again. “Now let’s see if I can’t bring you up to my level before your big choral audition.” Rio groaned and Agatha rolled her eyes. “Don’t be such a baby,” she said. “Come on.” She tapped the first note. “ Do… ”

Rio took a deep breath before repeating her. “ Do …” she sang, a little too high.

“Lower,” Agatha said. “Listen to the note and try to match it.” She hit it again. “ Do …”

“ Do…” Rio sang.

“Good!” Agatha praised, noticing the way it was Rio’s turn to blush now. She hit the next note. “ Re…”

“ Re… ” Rio sang, matching her tone. 

“Fantastic! Mi… ” Agatha hit the next note.

“ Mi… ”

“ Fa… ”

“ Fa…”

“Ooh, that’s a little too high now. Fa… ”

“ Fa…”

“Good! So… ”

“ So… ”

“ La… ”

“ La… ”

“ Ti… ”

“ Ti… ”

“ Do. ”

“ Do. ”

Agatha beamed at her. “Great!” she said. “You actually have a pretty nice singing voice, you know that?”

“Pfft! No I don’t,” Rio said, looking away from her.

“Hey,” Agatha said, bumping her shoulder, “yes you do. You’re an alto, so you can’t sing as high as, like, a soprano, but you have a nice voice.” Rio smiled at her, a bit shyly. Agatha smiled back, blue eyes meeting brown. Rio’s eyes were as nice as her voice, warm and shiny and…

Agatha cleared her voice, looking down at the keys, trying to shake her head of those thoughts. Those were not the kind of thoughts she should be having right now. 

“So,” she said, “is there any song in particular that you like to sing?”

Rio shrugged. “None that I can think of,” she replied. “And I don’t know how many you even know on the piano.”

“Well, the fun part about spending six years in piano lessons,” Agatha said, “is that I learned how to play all the basic notes in every key you can imagine because I am nothing if not an overachiever.” Rio laughed and Agatha joined her. “And I learned how to sight-read, too. So I can play pretty much anything with the right sheet music. And I can play some songs without sheet music.”

“What’s a good song for an alto?” Rio asked. “You’d know better than me.”

“Do you like Sara Bareilles?” Agatha asked, tapping out the first few notes of one of her songs. “Love Song?”

“Love Song?” Rio asked, her cheeks turning pink.

“It’s not an actual love song,” Agatha assured her. “It’s, like, an anti-love song song.” She started playing, counting the beats, then started to sing: “ Head under water, and they tell me to breathe easy for a while. The breathing gets harder - even I know that. Made room for me, it’s too soon to see if I’m happy in your hands. I’m unusually hard to hold onto. ” She stopped playing and turned to Rio, who was watching her with interest. “Sorry,” Agatha said. “I’m a soprano. This song isn’t the best match for my voice. Yours would fit much better.”

“It was good,” Rio said. “Like I said, you have a great singing voice. I’ve always known that, but…wow. It’s just odd hearing it now without music.” At Agatha’s look, Rio rolled her eyes. “Without a whole orchestra, I should say.”

“You wanna give it a try?” Agatha asked. “Do you know the chorus?” Rio nodded her head, swallowing thickly. “Close your eyes,” Agatha whispered as she started playing again. “Just feel the music.”

“That is such a cheesy thing to say,” Rio snorted even as she did what Agatha told her to do, listening to the familiar melody.

“ Blank stares at blank pages
No easy way to say this
You mean well,
But you make this hard on me…

“I’m not gonna write you a love song
‘Cause you ask for it, ‘cause you need one.
You see, I’m not gonna write you a love song
‘Cause you tell me it’s make or break in this
If you’re on your way.
I’m not gonna write you to stay.
If all you have is leavin’, I’ma need a better reason to write you a love song
Today.”

Agatha stopped playing and began clapping, but Rio kept her eyes closed until she felt Agatha’s arms wrap around her shoulders, pulling her in for a hug, pressing her face into Rio’s shoulder. She felt her entire body burst into flame and was sure that her face was as red as a beet.

Agatha Harkness is hugging me repeated like a mantra in her brain until Agatha finally pulled back to look Rio in the face, still smiling brightly. Rio tried desperately to school her features, but she was certain that her cheeks were still way too red to be natural. 

Agatha either didn’t notice or pretended not to, and Rio was forever grateful to her for that.

“You did a great job!” Agatha said. “You really do have a nice voice. You’re going to be just fine during that audition.”

Rio let out a breath she didn’t even realize she was holding. “You’re sure?” she asked. “I’ve never sung in front of anybody before, let alone a whole room of people.”

“You’ve never been to a choral audition before?” Agatha asked. Rio shook her head with a shrug. “The only people in the room are Alice and Lilia. For the solos, at least. Before that, we do a company audition where we all sing the song together to get a feel for the melody and then Lilia calls us in, one by one, for our solos.”

“Why couldn’t she have done that for the monologues?” Rio huffed.

“Because part of that part of the process is being able to perform in front of an audience,” she said, putting her hand up when Rio tried to talk. “The choral part is more about getting the notes and melodies right in the songs. If you can do that alone, chances are you can do that in front of a crowd. Hypothetically. Alice usually works with those of us that turn into squawking seagulls in front of a crowd.”

“And that includes me?” Rio asked. 

“Hypothetically,” Agatha said, “ if you were to do the play. Which you’re not. This is just extra credit.”

“Yeah,” Rio said with a sigh, placing her forehead down on the top of the piano. She felt Agatha’s hand on her back, rubbing a soothing pattern up and down her back that sent sparks of electricity all over Rio’s body.

“You’re going to do fine,” Agatha whispered. Rio turned to see her mirroring her pose, facing her with their heads both resting on the piano. Her smile was kind and gentle, her fingers still stroking up and down Rio’s spine, absently. Their noses were just inches apart. All Rio would have to do is lean forward, just a little…

The bell rang and Rio practically fell backwards off the bench, caught only by Agatha’s arm, still on her back, catching her.

“Whoa!” Agatha said, laughing slightly. “Are you okay?”

“Fine,” Rio sat, sitting straight back up and ignoring the burn of Agatha’s hand still on her. She pushed her hair back and stood, grabbing her trash from the top of the piano and tossing it. She still had the cookie left and immediately held it out for Agatha to take.

“Oh,” Agatha said. “You don’t have to…you already gave me your Doritos.”

Rio shrugged and grabbed Agatha’s orange. “Fair trade,” she said, biting into it like an apple, skin and all. “See you later.” Agatha gaped at her as she walked away.

“You are a heathen !” Rio heard as she walked into the hallway. Her lips turned up in a smile even as she spit out the peel into a nearby trash can. 

 

Agatha found her sitting in the back of the auditorium during ninth period, her back against the wall. Rio was engrossed in a book that was open in her lap, placing post-its and taking notes on The Crucible as she bobbed her head to whatever was playing in her ear buds.

Agatha smiled down at her and quietly approached, sitting down right next to her on the floor. Rio didn’t even look up, which was fine with Agatha as she opened up her own backpack, pulling out the book she was reading for her own class ( Mexican Gothic ) and opening it up to her saved page.

After a few moments, she realized that Rio was singing under her breath as she read and Agatha strained to hear the song she was singing.

“ ‘Cause magic takes time
And I’ve got my sights
And they’re set on you.
And one day, this rhyme
Might make you smile
And then I’ll sing ‘Hallelujah’”

Agatha’s eyes widened, her attention taken completely from her book as she continued to listen to the smooth, soft melody coming from Rio’s lips, leaning back against the wall as she watched and listened to her. 

“ In the dark, I see
Through the raging sea
I’ll be ready.
You are worth the road to maybe.
I don’t break so easily
I can take it, you unleash
All your worry, all your doubt
Please believe me. ”

She closed her eyes, her voice getting a tiny bit louder as she felt the music moving through her.

“ It’s magic, my love
The way you feel.
It’s magic, my love
But still so real. ”

“You really are a good singer,” Agatha said, nudging her. Rio jumped and let out a little yelp, nearly falling over as she stared back at Agatha, her eyes narrowing.

“You should wear a bell,” she said.

“I wasn’t trying to sneak up on you,” Agatha lied. “You should just be more observant.” She went back to her book, but she didn’t miss the roll of Rio’s eyes, which made her grin. “What song is that, anyway? I like the lyrics.”

“They sound better coming from Kelly Clarkson,” Rio said, offering her the left ear bud. Agatha took it hesitantly. “It’s clean,” Rio huffed. “I don’t have waxy ears.”

Agatha still rubbed the earpiece with her shirt before placing it in her left ear. Rio restarted the song and they just sat there, listening. It was a soft melody, had a good beat, and felt magical in the way it tickled her eardrum and sent shivers down her spine. She was familiar with Kelly Clarkson’s music, and she liked it. But this was something else…

“I like it,” she said to Rio as the song came to an end, “but it doesn’t seem like the usual love song.”

“It’s not a love song,” Rio said, putting her earbuds away. “It’s about her ex-husband. The entire album is, actually. It’s about how she was so in love with him and blinded by that love that she ended up missing all of these red flags about him. She was giving him everything, and she didn’t even notice that he wasn’t giving her anything in return.”

“Oh,” Agatha said, frowning, “that’s kind of sad.”

Rio shrugged. “Not if you look at it as a divorce song,” she said. “Kelly is free, she has their kids, and she’s rich and hot.”

“Oh, so you think she’s hot?” Agatha asked, teasingly.

“I have a thing for brunettes,” Rio said, picking her book back up. 

Agatha felt her throat go dry at those words, but she said nothing as she mirrored Rio’s actions. They spent the rest of the period reading in companionable silence, Agatha twisting her own brown curls with her finger as she waited for the final bell to ring.

When it did, she was on her feet in an instant, pulling Rio up with her. Rio barely had enough time to put her book back into her backpack before she was being tugged out of the auditorium and down the hall, toward the chorus room.

There was already a line of people waiting outside the door, but the piano was playing inside. Agatha peeked through the window in the door, where Lilia had set a mountain of sheet music on the piano while Alice presumably warmed up. Jen was right next to the door, sipping something hot in a cup, loosening her vocal chords.

Good idea , Agatha thought though she would never voice the fact that Jen Kale of all people was capable of intelligent thought. She took her water bottle out of her bag and walked to the water fountain, filling it up with cold water, then used her powers to warm it up in the bottle, smiling as she watched the steam rise in it. She took a sip and sighed.

“What are you doing?” Rio asked as Agatha walked back to stand with her.

“Loosening my vocal chords,” Agatha said, taking a sip of water. “Can you grow some mint or a lemon or something?”

“ Por qué no los dos? ” Rio said, smirking as both appeared in her hands. She offered the mint leaf to Agatha, who tossed it straight into the water bottle, then pulled out her knife (which she technically wasn’t supposed to have on school grounds) and sliced the lemon open, handing it to Agatha, who squeezed the juice into the water.

Her next sip made her moan. “So good,” she said. “Try some.” She offered it to Rio, who blushed but took the water bottle, placing her lips right where Agatha’s had been only seconds prior. Her eyebrows lifted in surprise.

“That is good,” Rio said as the hot water slid down her throat, minty and citrus-y. Her entire body felt warm.

“I usually grab tea before a choral audition,” Agatha said, “but I was too distracted by my book this time around.”

That was not true in the slightest. She had warred with herself between getting up and going to the cafeteria for some hot water from a kettle and a green tea bag and staying next to Rio, pretending to read her book for class while also spending half her time giving her sidelong glances over the pages of her book.

It was almost a no-brainer, but that didn't mean Agatha didn't have some regrets.

“It’s a good one,” Rio said, motioning to the book poking out the top of Agatha’s hastily half-zipped bookbag.

“You’ve read it?” Agatha asked.

“Twice now,” Rio confirmed. “I’m all about the gothic genre.”

“Not surprising, lurker,” Jen muttered, taking another sip from her own hot drink. 

Agatha glared at her, looking this way and that before pointing a finger at the cup and sending a tiny blast of purple magic at it, zapping it from Jen’s hand and sending the cup falling to the ground, brown liquid spilling out all over the place.

“What the hell, Agatha!” she exclaimed.

“ Moi ?” Agatha sniffed, placing her hand to her chest as if scandalized. “You should really try owning your own mistakes, Jen. Be more mature and all that.”

Just then, the door opened and Lilia welcomed them in for their auditions. 

“Whomever’s mess that is, please make quick work of cleaning it up,” she said. Jen glared at Agatha, who gave her a smug little grin as she pulled a smirking Rio into the chorus room, the two of them getting a prime spot around the piano, where Alice was setting up her sheet music. 

The pianist glanced around, confused. “Where’s Jen?” she asked.

“She had a little accident in the hallway,” Agatha said. “Butter fingers on that one, you know.”

“I’m sure,” Alice muttered, rolling her eyes.

Jen ran in a moment later, the knees of her jeans a little damp from having kneeled down to clean her (re: Agatha’s ) mess. She came and stood right next to Alice, leaning down to press a peck to her lips, sighing almost in relief. Agatha’s jaw clenched and she turned away. 

This did not go unnoticed by Rio.

“Everybody, grab some sheet music,” Lilia instructed. Agatha was the first one to snatch it, handing one of the packets to Rio, who gave her a thankful smile. Her heart was thundering in her chest as she looked down at the title page, the notes running together like soup. “The first page,” Lilia continued, “is our choral piece. We will sing this as one, with Alice’s instruction, to get you all familiar with the tune. Then, you will all go outside and I will call you in, one by one, to do your solos. There will be a soundproofing hex on the chorus room during that time, so nobody outside of Alice or myself will be able to hear you.” She was looking directly at Rio, who rolled her eyes. “Okay, so let’s begin. Alice, take it away, pet.”

Alice smiled awkwardly at the small crowd of people, giving them a little wave. There were about a dozen people in the room, including the new boy, Billy, and two other boys, who had been staples in the club almost as long as Agatha and Jen. 

“The song that we’re going to be singing today is You Can’t Stop the Beat from Hairspray . Jen, I see that look. Babe, don’t worry; that is not the musical Lilia chose.” She didn’t even have to glance up at Jen to see the twist of the other girl’s lips. Agatha cackled a bit under her breath. Their school, with its very pasty makeup, could not do that musical even if they did have enough students in their club to pull it off, and Lilia knew that. Everybody knew that.

Still, it was a fun song to sing. 

“So, for those of you familiar with this song, you’ll notice that the music I gave you is pretty far into the song. That’s because we’re just going to be singing the group parts of the song. The solo parts are on different sheet music. You’ll be doing that later. For right now, just listen to me sing the part, then we’ll work on doing it all together. Okay?” There were murmurs of agreement and Alice smiled, nodding. “Great!” she said, chipperly. “Okay, so…” she took a deep breath and began to play and sing:

“ Ever since this whole world began,
A woman found out if she shook it,
She could shake up a man
And so I’m gonna shake and shimmy it
The best that I can today.

“‘Cause you can’t stop the motion of the ocean
Or the sun in the sky.
You can wonder if you wanna, but I never ask why
And if you try to hold me down, I’m gonna spit in your eye and say
That you can’t stop the beat!”

The room applauded as Alice stopped playing, and she blushed, smiling up at them. “Thanks, guys,” she said. “So does everybody get it then? Ready to start?”

“Shouldn’t we do vocal warmups?” one student asked, speaking even though she hadn’t been called on. Agatha couldn’t for the life of her remember the student’s name. Nor did she care.

“We will do that,” Alice responded, “when we’re preparing for solos. This song is also something of a vocal warmup.” She leaned forward, lowering her voice. “Lilia really wants to just power through this, but there will be plenty of time to warm up your voice, trust me.” The girl nodded. “Okay, so let’s begin. I’m gonna play the intro for you and give you the sign to start singing.” 

She began to play the piano again and Rio took a deep breath as she waited for her cue. She stuttered a little as they started singing, glancing sideways at Agatha, who gave her an encouraging nod. She shut her eyes and let herself feel the music as she sang the words she’d seen on the page, her photographic memory lending a helping hand.

“Amazing!” Alice said, clapping her hands. “You guys sound great! Okay, so let’s quickly do some vocal warmups before Lilia starts calling you for solos.” She nodded at the student who had raised her hand earlier. “Okay, so we’re gonna make some ridiculous noises with our mouths, but that’s completely normal, okay? Don’t feel embarrassed about it because literally every person around you is making the exact same noises. Let’s begin.”

Agatha and Jen were well-versed in vocal warmups, obviously. They’d done this all before, so it was no wonder that most of the other, more junior, students followed their lead just as much as they followed Alice’s. Rio did feel a little ridiculous making these weird dolphin-y noises deep in her throat, but at least she wasn’t alone in it. Agatha even made faces at her as she made the same noises. Rio had to fight not to laugh.

When they were done, Alice praised them. “Let’s go through the song once more,” she said, “then I’m going to let Lilia take over for the solos and I will simply be the pianist.”

She ran the song again, and Rio started to feel more confident with the beat, nodding her head along and keeping in rhythm. Agatha nudged her as they sang and they shared a smile.

“Amazing!” Alice said. “Okay, so everybody out in the hall. Lilia will call you in one by one, so stay close!”

They filed out of the door with their sheet music, taking several seats along the hall immediately outside the chorus room. As promised, the second that door closed, everything was silent due to Lilia’s hex.

“Still nervous?” Agatha asked as she and Rio sat with their backs to a set of lockers immediately across from the chorus room.

“Yes,” Rio snorted. “Of course. But at least, after today, I will never have to sing another show tune for the rest of my life.”

“Come on,” Agatha laughed. “Some part of you has to like this, even just a little.”

It was nice spending more time with you .

She didn’t say that, though. Of course she didn’t. She couldn’t.

“The songs are catchy,” she said. “Maybe I’ll add some show tunes to my music.”

Agatha’s eyes widened in delight. “Can I make you a playlist?” she asked. “There are so many songs that you should really listen to! Give me your phone.” She held out her hand, expectantly, and Rio rolled her eyes, unlocking her phone and going to her music app, handing it over, watching over Agatha’s shoulder as she started constructing a show tunes playlist.

“So,” Rio asked after watching her for a few moments, the door to the chorus room still firmly closed, “what’s going on with you and Jen?” She kept her voice low, though Jen was down the hall, too far away to really hear her.

“Me and Jen ?” Agatha huffed, giving Rio an incredulous look. “What are you talking about?”

Rio shrugged. “I have no idea,” she said, “but I noticed that every time she and Alice are even a little bit affectionate with each other, you tend to…look away. Are you jealous of Alice?”

“That she’s dating Jen ?” Agatha scoffed. “ No way . She can have Jen, for all I care.”

“So then you’re jealous of Jen?” Rio asked.

“ Never ,” Agatha huffed. “Not in a billion years would I be jealous of Jen.” Her jaw tightened and she looked away. “Not for this, anyway. It’s more…” She shrugged, looking back at Rio’s phone, quietly scrolling through songs to add to her playlist.

“What is it, then?” Rio asked. Agatha swallowed thickly, then took a deep breath. “You can tell me anything, bestie ,” Rio said, nudging her. That got a smile.

“Jen and Alice started dating in middle school,” Agatha said. “Between seventh and eighth grade, while I was at church camp. Before that, we were kind of friends. Not best friends, but we did theater together and we were always cast pretty adjacent to each other’s roles. We interacted a lot, you know? I sat with her and Alice at lunch, watching them grow closer. I was the first one to see their friendship start to lean towards something… more . I was happy for them, at first.”

“What happened?”

“Billy Maximoff,” Lilia called, opening the door. The teen boy unfolded himself from his gangly legs, swallowed thickly, and marched into the chorus room as though he were meeting his doom.

“Poor kid,” Agatha murmured. “She’s going to eat him alive.”

“Agatha,” Rio said, “what happened between you and Jen?”

Agatha sighed, sitting back against the locker, looking up at the ceiling, carefully avoiding Rio’s gaze on her. “She and Alice came back to school at the beginning of eighth grade, and they were holding hands. I really was happy for them,” she said. “I congratulated them, said it was about time they admitted what we already knew, and said that I was truly very happy for them. Alice was openly queer since, like, second grade. Jen had only just recently realized that she was bisexual. I…couldn’t be out. I still can’t really be out, but I think Jen and Alice know. So does most of the drama club. Theater is full to the brim with queer kids. It’s one of the reasons I’ve always felt so much like I belong, I think.” She smiled softly at Rio, but it didn’t quite meet her eyes. “Still, in middle school, outside of drama, it was something else to see two girls holding hands as they walked down the halls together. A different kind of drama.” She clenched her jaw again, willing tears not to fall. “My mom found out about Jen from Jen’s mother inviting us to her Coming Out party. She sent out these sparkly rainbow invitations to all of Jen’s bestest friends .” She wrinkled her nose. “Jen warned me before they were sent out, but my mom got to the mailbox first. She was enraged . She almost pulled me out of theater altogether. She said she wouldn’t have me acquainting myself with sinners like Jen! ” She rolled her eyes, swiped a tear from the corner of her eye. “She had absolutely no idea that she had literally sent me to a camp filled with sinners for three years running.” She laughed, humorlessly. “I convinced her that Jen and I weren’t even friends. That I hated Jen for what she was. That I would never be like her. I put on such a good show that she actually made me call Jen just to RSVP no to her sinful party.” Agatha looked away, ashamed. “I said a lot of horrible things on that phone call that I’m not proud of. I apologized to her a week later, but that was a little too late, I guess. Our friendship - if you could even call it that - never fully recovered.” She glanced toward Jen. “Now, when I look at her and Alice, being so happy with each other out in the open, free to kiss each other as much as they both want, there’s this stab deep in my chest, because I will almost certainly never have that. Not so long as my mother is in my life. She’d sooner kill me than let me turn to that kind of sin .”

Rio reached out, taking Agatha’s hand, interlocking their fingers, squeezing. “It will happen,” she said, firmly. “One day. You’ll get away from her, go to New York or something. You’ll be a famous actress or a spellcraft engineer or whatever you want to be, okay? Her brand of hatred can’t control you forever.”

Agatha turned to Rio, her eyes brimming with tears, and smiled, genuinely, leaning forward to press her forehead against hers. “Thank you,” she whispered, exhaling so that it brushed Rio’s lips. Rio tried to ignore the shiver that went down her spine, avoided closing her eyes so that when Agatha’s gaze met hers, she saw that she had her full and undivided attention. “You are literally the best friend I’ve ever had.” Something ached in Rio’s chest at hearing that, but she still smiled. “Unfortunately, that’s kind of a low bar.”

Rio shrugged, pulling back even as she kept a grip on Agatha’s hand. “I’ll take it,” she said. “Especially if it comes with more hoodies.” She tugged on the string of the Wicked hoodie that she still had not returned to Agatha.

Agatha rolled her eyes, sitting back up against the locker as she went back to crafting the playlist on Rio’s phone. She did it with one hand now, her other still clutching Rio’s.

The door to the chorus room opened and Billy exited, looking as though he’d just had a panic attack. There were tears in his eyes, but he was smiling as he met up with a boy a little ways down the hall.

“How was it?” the boy asked.

“Intense,” Billy responded. “But it was worth it, I hope.”

“You probably did great,” the boy said, slipping his hand into Billy’s as they made their way toward the exit.

“Rio Vidal,” Lilia called. Rio’s eyes widened, and she stood up, leaving her backpack next to Agatha as she released her fingers from her grasp. She looked down at Agatha with a frown, and the other girl gave her a thumbs up and a grin.

Rio grimaced back at her in her best imitation of a smile before turning and walking into the chorus room ahead of Lilia, who patted her back.

The second the door shut, she couldn’t hear anything outside of the chorus room. It seemed the hex worked both ways. Good.

“Hey, Rio,” Alice said, motioning her toward the piano. “Okay, so the solos start on page two. You’re only singing a few bars so that Lilia and I can get a feel for your strengths and weaknesses when it comes to singing, okay? No reason to stress or anything. I know this is an extra credit assignment, too. I just wanted to get it out of the way so that you didn’t have to wait all afternoon out in that hall.”

“Thanks,” Rio said. “So, uh, let’s get it started.”

Alice nodded and Rio opened to page two.

“I’m going to play it once through,” Alice said, “and then I’ll count you in when it’s your turn. This is a different part of the same song.”

She started playing, singing along with the music, the metronome going at a steady rhythm just next to her. Rio listened intently, following the notes on the page, committing them to memory.

“Keep your chin up when you sing,” Lilia instructed. “I don’t want your nose stuck in that paper. Just follow Alice’s lead.”

Rio nodded, swallowing thickly as Alice started the second playthrough.

“ You can’t stop an avalanche
As it races down the hill.
You can try to stop the seasons, girl,
But you know you never will.

“And you can try to stop my dancin’ feet,
But I just cannot stand still
‘Cause the world keeps spinning
‘Round and ‘round
And my heart’s keeping time
To the speed of sound.
I was lost ‘til I heard the drums
Then I found my way
‘Cause you can’t stop the beat. ”

Rio was breathing heavily by the end of it, but when she looked up, Lilia and Alice looked stunned. She grimaced.

“Was it that bad?” she asked. “Sorry, I’m not really a singer and I was kinda nervous.”

“You were fantastic! ” Alice exclaimed. “What do you mean you’re not a singer? Your voice is great!”

“What?” Rio asked, shocked. “No, I just…you don’t have to be nice, Alice. I’m not–”

“I’m not being nice,” Alice said. “You really do have a good voice. It’s a little untrained, but that’s nothing we couldn’t work on.”

“Um, that’s nice,” Rio said, scratching the back of her neck, “but I’m not really interested in voice lessons. This is just extra credit, remember?”

“Right,” Alice said, deflating a little bit. “Well, you were great. I’m sure you’re going to get an amazing grade. Right, Lilia?”

“Of course,” Lilia said. “After a few more songs, just like everybody else.”

Rio let out a sigh and rolled her eyes. “Okay,” she said, “what’s the next part?”

 

Nearing on twenty minutes later, Rio walked out of the room, her throat sore from all the singing. People watched her, whispering amongst themselves, but Rio ignored them. Her audition was at least three times longer than Billy’s had been, but that was only because Lilia had made her sing each part twice, instructing her on how and when to breathe between notes. Finally, she had released her, promising Rio an A+ for her work.

“You did good, kid,” she said, patting Rio on the shoulder as she walked out of the room.

Rio slumped right next to Agatha, who immediately handed her back her phone, finished with the playlist.

“Broadway’s Greatest Hits,” Rio read, “by Agatha Harkness. There’s, like, twenty hours of show tunes on this list. Two hours is just from Hamilton .”

“There’s no way to separate Hamilton songs from each other. They’ve formed a bond. You must listen to them all.”

“Theater kids are something else,” Rio laughed.

“We’re better,” Agatha said, with a smug grin.

“If you say so.”

“Agatha Harkness,” Lilia called. Agatha got right to her feet. “Come on,” Lilia said. “Let’s get this over with.”

“Watch my stuff?” Agatha asked Rio, who gave her a thumbs up as she placed her earbuds in, starting the first song on the list, a number from Little Shop of Horrors . She liked the beat. “Thanks,” Agatha said, following Lilia into the chorus room.

“Break a leg,” Rio called out after her, even as she relaxed into the show tunes. This nightmare was finally over…

 

Hours later, after the last student had finally left, Lilia and Alice were going over the cast list, trying to figure out who was going to play whom. Lilia had to have it up by the end of the next school day, but she was having some difficulty figuring it out. There weren’t that many talented boys in the club and she still needed somebody to play the male love interest. Chemistry was really something to consider here, as well as talent.

An idea came to mind and she wrote a name down under the character on the board in front of them: Rio Vidal .

“Rio’s audition wasn’t serious,” Alice reminded her. “It was just for extra credit. You can’t actually cast her.”

“Her auditions were exemplary,” Lilia shot back. “And she has amazing chemistry with our female lead, don’t you think?”

“I don’t think she’ll do it, though,” Alice said. “She’s not really a stage person.”

“With the right kind of support, I think she could be,” Lilia retorted. “If not, well we’ll have our understudy.” She wrote down another name next to Rio’s, labeled understudy . Alice’s eyes widened.

“That’s diabolical,” she said, her voice little more than a whisper.

Lilia gave her an evil grin. “I do my best.”

Chapter End Notes

I'm about to go to bed, so it's going to be at the top for at least the next eight or so hours (right under my pinned Lorna's Ballad video) Please vote in the poll and also share it with somebody who might like this fic.
