Chapter 5: Cast List

Chapter Summary

Rio sees the cast list and Lilia puts her plan into action. Slightly shorter than usual chapter, but the next up will be longer and up soon-ish.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Five

Agatha was practically vibrating with excitement, her pen tapping on the desk in a frenetic rhythm as she waited for the last bell to ring. During first period, Rio watched her with a small smirk, shaking her head as Agatha practically shimmied in her seat, unable to stay completely still for longer than a few seconds. Lilia definitely noticed this, but she said nothing, focusing instead on assigning their next monologues (Greek tragedy but with a modern accent) and giving Rio a pointed look now that she knew just how much effort she could put into her performance.

Rio just rolled her eyes, looking sideways at Agatha, who was staring at the clock as if she could speed up time with pure will.

“Lilia has somehow made everything slower,” she huffed as she and Rio packed up their things when the first bell of the day rang. “Why did that class take three times as long as it does any other day?”

“A watched pot never boils,” Rio said. 

“It will if I turn up the heat,” Agatha huffed, stomping out of the room. Rio laughed at her back, shaking her head as she turned in the opposite direction of the other girl, heading to the rest of her classes.

Agatha checked her phone incessantly for the entirety of that day, barely registering the marigold that Rio sprouted from her hand, planting it on Agatha’s head as she stared down at her phone. Rio watched her with amusement as she then stole half of Agatha’s sandwich, which the girl just barely nibbled at, waiting for the clock to strike 2:30.

“Are you okay?” Rio finally asked. Agatha didn’t even blink; it was kinda creepy. Rio snapped her fingers two inches from Agatha’s face. Agatha finally looked back up at her, still not blinking. “I have never seen you this intense about a school play before,” Rio said.

Agatha let out a deep breath, her entire body seeming to sag with it. “This is my last high school play,” she said, finally. “This is the last time I’m going to be up on that stage. I just…I want it to be a good one. Memorable, you know? And I need to have a better role than Jen.” She glared at the other girl.

“Why do you have such a need to get one over on Jen?” Rio asked, looking between them, confused. “After what you told me, I figured you’d be a little more…I don’t know, indifferent to her, at worst.”

“After that phone call,” Agatha said, lowering her voice as she leaned in toward Rio, “Jen started spreading rumors about me.” Rio’s eyebrows lifted at that. “Or, well, it’s more like she blamed me for spreading rumors around other people. And she said that I tried to sabotage her during theater rehearsals whenever she got a bigger role than I did.”

“Did you?”

“I plead the fifth.”

“Agatha,” Rio snorted. “Seriously?”

“No!” Agatha huffed. “She got food poisoning on opening night once and I was her understudy. She took the three other shows that weekend. But she said that I slipped something into her water bottle, but I just know it was the sushi she’d had that day at lunch. It looked green .”

Rio rolled her eyes, not quite sure if she believed Agatha or not. Either possibility was hilarious to her as she imagined Agatha sneaking around the dressing room like a cartoon villain, putting something (non-lethal) into Jen’s water bottle. Or, conversely, being utterly confused when the rumors of her poisoning Jen for the role got around.

She Really didn’t think Agatha was capable of it, though. She liked to act rather aloof, especially when it came to Jen, but knowing that they’d once considered each other friends and why that ended so abruptly? Rio knew that there had to be hurt somewhere deep down.

Not that she’d ever tell Agatha that. She preferred all her limbs attached to her body, thank you very much. 

By the time they got to ninth period, Agatha was pacing a hole in the ground, walking back and forth across the back of the auditorium, muttering to herself under her breath as Rio sat on the floor, doing her homework, looking up every now and again to see if Agatha had stopped.

She did not stop. Not until Rio sighed, stood up, and got in her way, practically tripping Agatha, who startled when Rio caught her by the shoulders, their noses practically brushing as Rio looked deep into her eyes and said, “Stop.” 

“I can’t,” Agatha huffed, trying to back away. Rio kept a tight hold on her.

“Agatha,” she said, her voice exasperated after watching this girl - who was usually so cool, calm, and collected - fall apart at the seams all damn day. “No matter how much you worry and pace and mutter about whatever, the results won’t change. You’ll still get a lead in the musical, even if it’s not the one you would have preferred. You’ll still do a phenomenal job, as always , and you’ll probably even end up with one of those stupid student award things at the end of the year. But you need to stop worrying, okay? We have…” Rio looked at the clock on the wall, “fifteen minutes before that list is posted. Then you’ll know. And you can start preparing to knock the socks off of everybody who comes to see it, okay? And, if Jen gets a better role than you…you can poison her and take all the glory for yourself.”

Agatha snorted out a laugh at that, her head falling to rest on Rio’s arm, which still held her in place. “You’re right,” she groaned. “I know that you’re right. But I am just so filled with energy right now. I am…ugh! I need to do something. Pacing feels like the right thing to do.”

“It’s not,” Rio said. “Why don’t you…tell me what play you’re hoping Lilia picked. And why. You like giving speeches, don’t you?”

Agatha lifted her head, surprise in her eyes as she considered Rio, searching her eyes. “Seriously?” she asked. “You’d want to listen to that? I can get pretty intense about theater stuff.”

“I hadn’t noticed,” Rio said with a deadpan expression, delighting in the way Agatha’s cheeks pinkened. “Seriously, though,” Rio laughed. “Go ahead. I’d rather listen to you go on and on about musicals than watch you freak out about one. Which musical are you hoping to do for your last play?”

“Grease,” Agatha replied, “but I don’t think I’d even want to play Sandy.”

“Is that a lead?” Rio asked, finally releasing Agatha so that they could sit back down. Agatha pulled her knees up against her chest while Rio sprawled out, taking as much space as she could. 

“Yes!” Agatha huffed, shoving at her shoulder. “You’ve never seen the movie?”

“I don’t know how many times we need to have this conversation,” Rio retorted. “Just assume I’ve never seen any movies, ever, in my life, okay? Unless they star, like, Marilyn Monroe or Judy Garland.”

“Really?” Agatha laughed. “You like old movies?”

“They’re classics for a reason, aren’t they?” Rio huffed. “Just keep talking.”

“Okay, so Grease is basically this Romeo and Juliet-esque love story between this really preppy, innocent girl named Sandy, and this greaser-type guy named Danny. They meet over a summer break at a beach, where Danny saves Sandy from drowning and they have this kind of summer romance thing. But Sandy is Australian, so they think it’s only really going to last the summer, but then they get back to high school and Danny - who Sandy thought was this very sweet, sensitive guy - is there and it turns out that he’s this misogynistic jerk who basically told all of his friends that they slept together. Sandy, on the other hand, is the new girl in this school where there are two cliques called “The T-Birds” which is the one Danny belongs to, and “The Pink Ladies” which quickly integrate Sandy into the group.”

“So, Sandy is the lead? Why wouldn’t you want to play her?”

Agatha wrinkled her nose. “I don’t relish the idea of playing a girl who’s fawning over some jerk the entire musical. I’d rather play Rizzo.”

“Who’s Rizzo?”

“Mean girl type, but she’s really tough and almost certainly a closeted lesbian, despite having a pregnancy scare. She’s kind of the antithesis to Sandy. She’s witty and snarky and I had a huge crush on Stockard Channing when I was little.” Agatha got all dreamy-eyed, sighing with her hand to her chest. “You’ve gotta see this movie, Rio,” she said. “You’ll love her, too.” She eyed Rio up and down. “Actually, you’d make a killer Rizzo, too.”

Heat bloomed in Rio’s chest and she cleared her throat. “But I’m not an actor,” she reminded Agatha.

“Right, well, semantics.”

Rio snorted, shaking her head. “What other plays would you choose?” she asked.

“Beauty & the Beast,” Agatha said. “I have the perfect hair for Belle. Ooh, or I could play the Enchantress, but that role is pretty brief. Mrs. Potts might be nice, too.” Rio could see that, her cheeks warming as she pictured Agatha in the golden dress, being spun around a dancefloor, barrel curls in her hair. “Or Cinderella,” Agatha said. “The Rodgers and Hammerstein version. Whitney Houston and Brandy were amazing.”

“Never seen it,” Rio lied. She’d seen that one too many times to count when she was little. Her mother had bought it one year for Christmas and she’d watched it with her parents, all cuddled up on the couch. She loved that movie.

Agatha looked absolutely affronted by the idea that she hadn’t seen it, so Rio kept up the facade. 

“Okay, so that’s another movie added to our list,” she said.

“Our list ?” Rio asked, tilting her head in confusion.

“Of movies I’m going to force you to watch one day,” Agatha said, “as your best friend.”

“Then I’m making my own list,” Rio retorted. “You’re going to watch the original A Star is Born , with Judy Garland.”

“Bold of you to assume I haven’t already seen it,” Agatha retorted. “But I’m down to watch it again, so long as you watch West Side Story .”

“As if I haven’t already seen that one,” Rio said. “That was my mom’s favorite movie for years . I love Rita Moreno.”

“Be still my heart,” Agatha teased, pressing her hand to her chest then laughing. “Okay, I’ll make a list and you make a list and we’ll plan a night - or two or three - to watch all the movies on them. At your house.”

“ My house?” Rio asked, feeling herself start to get red again. “Why my house?”

“Because my mother hates musicals,” Agatha said. “And having any kind of company. She gave me an earful when you came over that one time.” She rolled her eyes, putting up a hand when Rio opened her mouth. “Don’t apologize,” she said. “It’s not your fault. She just can’t stand to see me happy.”

Rio frowned, pressing her lips together. She hated the way her heart clenched at that, but she said nothing; Agatha would almost certainly hate anybody who showed her any kind of sympathy, especially when she obviously didn’t want it. 

“What other plays?” she asked.

“Oh, um,” Agatha thought for a moment, “The Music Man. I’d prefer to play Harold, though, over Marian. He goes to this small town in Indiana and sells the people there music lessons for their children, claiming that they’re going to start a band. But he doesn’t know how to play any instruments. It’s a scam. But he ends up falling for the pretty blonde librarian who had originally wanted to take him down. It’s kind of cute.”

“Hmm, does that one have a movie?”

“Several,” Agatha confirmed. “I’ll add it to the list.” 

They were silent for a moment before Rio smiled. “Hey, Agatha?”

“Hmm?”

“It’s 2:34.”

Agatha was on her feet in seconds, racing out of the auditorium and into the hall, practically leaving a trail of smoke in her wake. Rio snorted and stood, gathering their things to follow her outside. She’d heard the last bell ring while Agatha was talking, but something about how passionately she spoke about musicals made her reticent to interrupt. She’d probably hear about it later, though.

As Rio stepped out of the auditorium, there was a group of students making a half-circle around the wall where Lilia was tacking a piece of paper to the bulletin board. She turned, spotting Rio, and smirked at her before walking through the crowd and waving her hand, dissolving whatever enchantment had kept the desperate theater kids from surging forward to search for their names on the paper.

Agatha, as always, was first. She let out a gasp, then an excited yell, raising her hands above her head.

“It’s Wicked !” she exclaimed. “And I’m Elphaba!”

There were a few whoops around the crowd, people reaching forward to pat her on the back, and one dark hand reaching forward in an attempt to tug Agatha away and give the rest of them some space to see what else was written, but Agatha shrugged it off, her arms falling slowly to the side as her eyes continued to scan the list.

Then she turned and looked straight at Rio, her mouth slightly agape.

“You might want to see this,” she said, her voice low but still audible even over the din of other students. A few of them looked at her as curiously as Rio did, then their eyes found whatever she had seen on the cast list and, one by one, two dozen pairs of eyes turned to Rio in shock, making her feel like a bug under a microscope.

Rio stepped forward, still carrying their backpacks and Agatha’s coat, frowning at the look of shock still etched on Agatha’s face. She looked past the other girl, her eyes scanning the page, looking for whatever it was that had caught everybody’s attention.

Then she saw it.

In bold, italicized lettering, right next to the name Fiyero (which Rio vaguely remembered from the book) was her own name : Rio Vidal . 

The backpacks and coat slipped from her grasp, her limbs going limp as she struggled to comprehend what she was seeing. What the fuck was she seeing?!

She looked at Agatha, who still looked absolutely shell-shocked and a little concerned as though she were waiting for the full force of Rio’s reaction to this news.

Rio, without saying a word or even bothering to lean down and pick up the items she’d just dropped, turned on her heel and ran off, making a beeline for the second floor and Lilia’s classroom, ready to tear the damn thing off of its hinges. 

Surprisingly, the door was open. Even more surprisingly, Lilia looked unconcerned as she sat at her desk and sipped a mug of tea. When Rio appeared in her doorway, she smiled serenely up at you.

“Good afternoon, Miss Vidal,” she said, a dreamy quality to her voice that unnerved Rio even further. “I was wondering when you’d show up. And so quietly , too. What a pleasant surprise.”

“What the hell ?” Rio growled, stomping into the room, her fists clenched at her sides. “Why is my name on the cast list?”

“Because,” Lilia replied, casually, “I decided to add you to the cast. You know, your audition made quite the lasting impression on me.”

“It wasn’t a real audition ,” Rio snarled. “We agreed that it was just extra credit! I’m not an actor.”

“You could’ve fooled me,” Lilia said. “I’ve never seen such a passionate monologue in my life. And your voice .” She took a deep breath, sipping her tea again. “I never knew such a lovely voice might come out of you. I might have offered you extra credit much sooner if I did.”

“And tricked me into doing one of your stupid plays earlier?” Rio huffed. “Not a chance. I’m not going to be in your play, Lilia. All I want is my A in the class for that audition. You and I both know I earned that much.”

“You’ll get your A,” Lilia agreed. “As promised. But I do want you to reconsider your role in the play. Fiyero plays a considerable role. He’s Elphaba’s love interest, you know.”

“I don’t give a…what?” Rio asked, her face flushing. Of course she knew that. Fiyero and Elphaba had an affair in the book. She was sure that the musical had changed that only slightly. “Yeah, I know,” she said, flushing. The thought of Agatha playing Elphaba stuck in her mind like glue now. Her name was just two above Rio’s on the list. 

Jennifer Kale was playing Galinda, which Rio would have laughed at had she not been immediately incensed by Lilia’s gall at casting her as the main love interest.

“That doesn’t change anything,” Rio insisted, though from that knowing glint in Lilia’s eyes, she knew she wasn’t quite believed. 

“Doesn’t it?” Lilia asked. “I mean, if you were to take the role, then you might be saving Agatha Harkness the headache of having to kiss a nearly prepubescent boy.”

“What?” Rio asked, wrinkling her nose. “What are you talking about?”

“Your understudy, dear,” Lilia said. “Of course we have to consider understudies before fully casting the play. Billy Kaplan is only a freshman, but his acting is decent and he has a lovely voice, though it cracks more often than I would like. He was perfect for Boq, but I did consider him for the role of Fiyero, as well. You were just the better candidate.” She took another sip as Rio frowned at her. “Of course, if you’re dropping out of the play, we’ll have to move some things around. We can bump Billy up to your role and his understudy can move up from the chorus. It should be just fine, so long as you’re sure that’s what you want to do.”

Rio pressed her lips together, firmly. Agatha was desperate to make this last high school play memorable for herself. She wanted to go out on a good note; one last big adventure before college, before she got to leave Westview. and everyone in it, in the rearview mirror. Billy looked like a nice kid, but he was also awkward and inexperienced and definitely wouldn’t have been able to meet Agatha’s level of talent on the stage. 

Agatha wouldn’t complain - not that much, anyway - but Rio just knew she’d be miserable. And Rio didn’t want Agatha to be miserable - anything but, in fact. So she gritted her teeth, clenching her fists, and nodded.

“Fine,” she said, “I’ll do the play. But I want an A+ in the whole class, not just my last assignment.”

“Making demands now, are we?” Lilia tutted. “Is that a smart idea?”

“Very much so,” Rio bluffed. “I can step away from this play right now. I can tell my mother that you’re trying to emotionally blackmail me, using my best friend’s happiness as a bargaining chip. My mom’s a lawyer, you know. This conversation would be very interesting to her, I think.”

Marisol Vidal was a paralegal, but Rio was certain that Lilia didn’t know that.

The woman showed no signs of backing down, but she did tilt her head. “If you want the A+ in the class,” she said, “you have to earn it. No half-assing your role in the play. You follow directions and you show up for rehearsals when called. You put in the effort I now know that you’re capable of. Is that understood?”

“Well,” Rio huffed, “I did sign a contract. It’s obviously not legally -binding considering I didn’t have a lawyer or legal guardian present, but I’m not the kind of person who goes back on my word.”

“Good,” Lilia said. “Then, assuming all goes to plan and you fulfill your end of the bargain - meaning you still hand in all necessary assignments for the rest of the year because goddess knows I cannot give missing work a good grade - you will receive an A-plus at the end of the school year. Better start working on your Valedictorian speech now, darling.”

Rio inhaled slowly through her nose then exhaled through her mouth, closing her eyes for a few seconds before she opened them. “Deal,” she said.

“Excellent,” Lilia said. “You can pick up your script and call sheet during homeroom on Monday, which won’t be too hard considering you’ll be here, anyway. Won’t you?”

“Whatever,” Rio grumbled, turning to walk back out into the hall. Her eyes widened when she saw Agatha sitting on a bench in the hall, Rio’s backpack next to her, her own coat and bag on her lap. “What are you doing?” Rio asked as she approached.

“This is how far I have to be,” Agatha said, “to not be accused of eavesdropping. Which I did not do, by the way.” She took a deep breath. “So you’re out of the play, huh? I kinda thought Lilia would pull some kind of shit like this, but I didn’t expect Billy , of all people, to be your understudy.” She wrinkled her nose. “He’s, like, a stretched-out toddler.”

Rio let out a laugh at that. “He’s only three years younger than us.”

“He’s a zygote ,” Agatha huffed. “But I’ve kissed Freshman before,” she said. “I’ve kissed, ugh, boys before. I can do it again. It’s fine.”

“You don’t have to do it again,” Rio said. “Because I’m…doing the play.”

Agatha’s eyes widened at that, her mouth gaping open a little as she looked up at Rio. “What?” she asked, her voice a little bit breathy. “Are you…are you serious ?”

“Yeah,” Rio said. “Um, Lilia said she’d give me an A-plus on every assignment for the rest of the year - so long as I turn them in, obviously - if I did the play. It’s kind of hard to say no to that kind of incentive, you know? So…I’m in.”

Agatha got to her feet and immediately wrapped her arms around Rio, hugging her so tightly that the wind was taken straight from her lungs - but that may have also been because of the scent of Agatha’s perfume, which immediately invaded Rio’s nostrils, replacing every ounce of oxygen in her lungs. After a beat or two, Rio wrapped her arms around Agatha in return, stroking her fingers down her hair, fully catching the sharp intake of air Agatha let out at the touch.

Then Agatha was pulling back, blushing bright pink but smiling up at her.

“You are the best , Rio Vidal,” she said. “You are going to have so much fun. Trust me. This is such a great play.” She turned, picking up Rio’s backpack and handing it to her. “Come on,” she said, “I’m going to buy you some tea to celebrate.”

“I don’t drink tea,” Rio said, lifting an eyebrow as she slipped on her backpack. She watched as Agatha slipped into her coat, rolling her eyes.

“Coffee then,” Agatha said.

“I like the smell,” Rio said. “Can’t stand the taste. Too bitter.”

“Hot chocolate?”

“ Now you’re speaking my language,” Rio said with a grin.

“Hot chocolate date it is, then,” Agatha said, hooking her arm through Rio’s and dragging her back down the hall, toward the stairs. 

“D-date?” Rio stammered, despite herself.

Agatha rolled her eyes. “We’re playing love interests now, Vidal,” she said. “Gotta get used to the flirty behavior now.”

“Right,” Rio said, clearing her throat. “Right. Of course. Um, how do you feel about Jen playing your bestie?” She was desperate to change the subject.

“Ugh,” Agatha groaned, rolling her eyes. “I don’t wanna talk about it, but it is not gonna be fun.”

“I disagree,” Rio said. “I think it’ll be plenty fun…for me.”

“You are very close to losing out on free hot chocolate,” Agatha warned.

“I’ll be good,” Rio said even as she gave her a mischievous smile. Agatha snorted.

“Somehow,” she said, holding Rio’s arm more tightly, “I doubt it.”

Chapter End Notes

The polls was SO CLOSE for both the play chosen (between Wicked and Grease) and between Galinda/Glinda and Morrible for Jen's character. I personally think her playing Glinda is the far funnier choice and I am so grateful that won out in the end.

Let us see what happens next! Please review

Chapter 6: Read Through

Chapter Summary

The first read-through for the musical. Agatha and Rio continue getting closer and Agatha has some...revelations.

Chapter Notes

I am so happy that y'all chose this play. It's going to be so much fun.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Six

Lilia’s classroom was filled with even more theater kids than usual that Monday morning, all there to pick up their scripts and call sheets. Lilia handed them out to each individual student, advising anybody playing a lead role to buy a three-ring binder to keep them in, lest their scripts and sheet music get lost or torn apart. 

For Rio, however, everything was already in a binder. Agatha’s and Jen’s were, as well. Rio frowned at her, almost suspiciously, and Lilia rolled her eyes. “I had a few extra in the back,” she said. “I expect them back on closing night, capisce? Don’t take advantage of my kindness.”

“You’re literally blackmailing me into this role,” Rio huffed. “I don’t think I’m the one who’s about to accuse you of being kind in any way, shape, or form.”

“You’re going to have fun,” Lilia said, “trust me.” She eyed Agatha, who was already pouring over the script and music, a bright grin on her face. “More than you probably even realize.”

Rio rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t hide the blush on her face as she grabbed the binder from Lilia and stomped off to her seat next to Agatha. Agatha was mouthing along to the words on the page, her pencil already making notes in the margins. Rio couldn’t help the soft smile that turned up the corners of her mouth. She was kind of adorable like this - like a kid on Christmas.

Agatha glanced up and Rio immediately looked away, opening up her own binder to see the Call Sheet clipped on top. All of her call days and times were highlighted in blue, but there was bold print on the top that said “SUBJECT TO CHANGE” and she groaned, turning the page. The music was next. It wasn’t stapled together and Alice had helpfully color-coded all Rio’s parts for her to learn. She was in a decent number of songs, which made her stomach clench, but it would be fine, she was sure. She glanced sideways at Agatha, who was still deeply invested in her binder. 

Yeah , Rio thought to herself, it’ll be fine.

 

Their first rehearsal was at three PM that day. Agatha and Rio placed their backpacks in the dressing room before Agatha dragged Rio down the street for hot chocolate and a pastry at the nearby cafe. They were lucky to get there before the line got too long.

“You excited?” Agatha asked as they waited in line.

“Define excited ,” Rio retorted, wrinkling her nose. “I’m not sure the nausea I’m feeling really fits.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “It’s just the read-through today, Rio,” she huffed. “No big deal. It’s just so we can start to get a feel for these characters.”

“I’m certain you’ve seen this play already,” Rio retorted, “ several times. You definitely already have a feel for your character.”

“Well, yes,” Agatha admitted, “I have seen this play. Three times in person. And, like, twenty times online. But every production is different. It depends on the actor playing the role. Besides, this isn’t just for me , but for the entire cast. You never really know how people are going to mesh during a play, you know? I mean, I honestly think Lilia made a huge mistake casting Jen as Glinda. She should have been Madame Morrible or The Wizard or something, but that’s not my call.”

“Okay, so I know the Wizard,” Rio said, “but Morrible is…?”

“I thought you read the book,” Agatha huffed, stepping up the barista with a friendly smile. “Hi,” she said. “One venti hot matcha and a croissant. And she’ll have a venti hot chocolate with cinnamon and almond milk and a pain au chocolat. Thanks.” 

“You memorized my order?” Rio asked, flushing.

“It’s not a hard order,” Agatha snorted, reaching into her pocket. Rio beat her to it, though, scanning her app to pay for their treats from her own account. At Agatha’s furrowed brow, she shrugged.

“You paid last time,” she said, “and I have plenty of credit in my account. My mom loves this place.”

“Names?” the barista asked.

Agatha placed her hand over Rio’s mouth before she could answer. “I’m Elphaba and she’s Fiyero,” she said, grinning ear to ear.

“Interesting names,” the barista said, writing them on the cups. “Your pastries will be at the end of the bar with your drinks.”

“Thanks,” Agatha said, hand still over Rio’s mouth with Rio glaring down at her. Rio opened her mouth, licking Agatha’s palm, and the other girl let out a squeal, snatching her hand away as Rio cackled, walking past her. “That was disgusting !” Agatha huffed, following after her. Rio stuck out her tongue. “Real mature.”

“It’s just a tongue,” Rio snorted. “You’ve never felt a girl’s tongue before.” The second the words were out of her mouth, she wanted to take them back, her face blooming visibly bright red. Agatha’s face matched the shade, though she looked away from Rio’s gaze, clearing her throat.

“I have,” Agatha said, her voice barely more than a whisper, her cheeks still flaming, “but never on my palm .” She rubbed said palm on her sweater again, flexing her fingers. “Gross.”

“We’re going to kiss, eventually,” Rio reminded her, again wishing she had not spoken the words aloud. “In the play,” she clarified. “Unless we do one of those fake stage kisses, where we just…I actually don’t know how to do a stage kiss.”

“It’s not hard,” Agatha retorted with a nonchalant shrug, “but every production I’ve seen has been…very real. One of our duets ends with a pretty passionate kiss and the implication is that our characters…uh…” She cleared her throat, looking away again. “You know,” she finished, weakly.

Agatha had seen Wicked over twenty times in her life. Her mother had begrudgingly agreed to let her see the play when her school planned a field trip for it in the fifth grade, as a part of their “graduation” festivities. Agatha had begged to go see it for weeks, picking up extra chores and doing whatever it was that Evanora asked of her until she had signed the permission slip and handed over the money for the discounted ticket. 

The play had taken her breath away. She had spent what little money Evanora had given her on the soundtrack after the show, blasting the music almost nonstop for months afterward. Evanora had had to put a silencing spell on Agatha’s bedroom to get any peace and quiet while she listened to that “sinful noise”. 

Agatha saw it two more times by her senior year of high school only because she’d saved up nearly every penny of money anybody had ever given her to do so. She’d gone alone to the city to see it, taken a train and two buses to Manhattan and sat as close to the stage as she could afford to, the show leaving her breathless every time.

Elphaba Thropp was truly her dream role, but the fact that she ended up with Fiyero instead of with Galinda had always bugged Agatha. When she was younger, she hadn’t understood why. Then camp happened and she started to get it. She was still disappointed every time it was Fiyero who showed up at the end of the play to run away with Elphaba, though.

But now…now she was kind of happy that Elphaba ended up with Fiyero instead of Glinda, if only because Fiyero was being played by another girl. And not just any girl. Rio Vidal .

Agatha Harkness wasn’t blind or stupid. She’d seen the way that Rio looked at her, and had noticed how Rio had watched her for the last three years. Rio could have said no anytime Agatha asked for her help running lines, but it was like the thought had never crossed the other girl’s mind. And the flowers . Nearly every time Agatha saw Rio, the other girl had a flower held out to her, a little smirk on her lips. Agatha had kept them for as long as they lived, sitting on her desk or in her locker until they began to wilt and wither. With Rio, however, the supply of flowers never dwindled.

It was obvious how Rio felt about her, even before Agatha knew that she was already out as a lesbian. And Agatha wouldn’t lie and say that she hadn’t thought about it. She had. Many times. She’d imagined reaching out to hold Rio’s hand at lunch or even in Lilia’s class. She imagined leaning forward that extra inch sometimes to press her lips to Rio’s, allowing herself the luxury of kissing the other girl. She hadn’t kissed another girl since her last year of church camp, just before sophomore year at Westview High. The drama club wasn’t lacking in sapphic representation, and everybody more or less knew her romantic inclinations, but she wasn’t ready to step into anything yet. Not when it had a way of possibly getting back to her mother.

Agatha couldn’t stand to live with her mother if she knew what Agatha was.

So she tamped down the feelings for Rio. She called Rio her “best friend” because it was easier than admitting to the other girl what she, herself, already knew: she was in love with Rio Vidal. She had been since freshman year of high school, when she’d first locked eyes with her just outside the auditorium, right before her first audition.

That’s why she sought Rio out to help her run through lines. That’s why she sat directly across from Rio at lunch, next to her in every class they’d had together. She still kept her distance for the first three and a half years of high school, but now…

As they walked back to the high school together, snow began to fall around them. Rio had given back Agatha’s hoodie that morning, apologizing for having spilled the contents of a breakfast burrito on it, and opted for a fur-lined denim jacket instead. It didn’t look nearly warm enough for the below-freezing, snowy weather they were having. Rio’s hands clutched the hot chocolate like a lifeline, her fingerless gloves doing absolutely nothing to keep the blue from creeping down her fingers. 

“For Goddess sake,” Agatha huffed, unwinding her scarf from around her neck and reaching out, tugging on Rio’s arm to keep her from walking any further. Rio frowned down at her in confusion. Without a word, Agatha winded her deep violet scarf around Rio’s neck, sticking the ends down the opened collar of her jacket, then immediately marched forward, taking a sip of her matcha. When she didn’t immediately hear the other girl’s footsteps behind her, she rolled her eyes, looking over her shoulders. “Are you coming?” she asked. “Or have you officially been frozen solid?”

Rio cleared her throat and picked up her step, jogging slightly to catch up with Agatha, nudging her arm as she took another sip of her hot chocolate. Agatha nudged her back, feeling her arm flutter with warmth where they touched, even as the snow continued to fall over them.

When they finally returned back to the school, it was still five to three, so they had plenty of time to finish their pastries and get into their seats on the stage before the reading was meant to begin. 

A few of the techies had organized long tables and chairs on the stage into a circle for the main cast to sit at while they read. Lilia’s seat was center stage, but she rarely stayed there, preferring instead to wander around the circle and the auditorium at large, directing them from the back and making notes.

All the chairs were labeled with the names of their characters. Agatha groaned when she saw that Glinda and Elphaba were meant to sit next to one another. Jen was already in her seat, reading her script. Agatha rolled her eyes as she sat down. Thankfully, Fiyero was on the other side of her, Rio taking her seat and propping her feet up on the table, resting her binder on her knees as she took another sip of her hot chocolate, which was quickly cooling now.

Agatha said as far away from Jen as she could manage, which ended up with her shoulder touching Rio’s, sending flames through her body from the point of contact. She ignored it, flipping through her own script. She had spent most of ninth period with a green highlighter, highlighting all of her lines with it. She’d also highlighted the lines that came directly before hers with different colors depending on who was speaking, determined to learn her cues.

She’d helped Rio do the same.

Rio was still wearing her scarf and Agatha wondered, amused, if she’d get it back anytime soon. Purple wasn’t exactly Rio’s color, but Agatha could probably make one in a deep, forest green for her, if she asked.

“Okay,” Lilia said, finally approaching the stage, her own oversized binder in her hands, “is everybody here?”

Agatha glanced around the table. Billy was sitting with the girl who was playing Nessarose, a sophomore girl that Agatha vaguely recognized as the girl who played Vi Moore from last year’s production of Footloose . She was a nice girl, and she smiled at Billy, who gave her a shaky grin back. He was a nervous wreck. He’d learn, though, and build his confidence onstage. 

Every other character with a speaking role was seated around the circle. Lilia counted them out on her fingers, smiling with delight. 

“Fantastic!” She clapped her hands. “Good, now let us begin .” She dropped her binder on the table with a resounding thud , flipped open the top, and started reading. “Scene one. Opens with the song No One Mourns the Wicked , which all of our Ozians will sing gleefully, celebrating the death of the Wicked Witch of the West, aka Elphaba Thropp.” She motioned to Agatha, who raised her hand, grinning. There were a few chuckles. “Then,” Lilia went on, “one of our Ozians will say this next line. Who wants it?” She looks out at the auditorium, where a few members of the chorus (aka the Ozians ) sat to listen in on the reading. A few raised their hands, clamoring for a speaking role. Lilia pointed to one girl sitting in an aisle seat. “Name?” she asked as the girl stood, clutching her own script. 

“Leslie Harris,” the girl said, her braces shining in the light of the auditorium. She had a slight lisp. “Freshman.”

“Nice,” Lilia replied, uninterested. “Okay, you shall be Ozian One from now on. We’ll give you a cute name later on. Say your line.”

The girl nodded, looking down at her script. “Look!” she said, pointing at Jen. “It’s Glinda!”

“The tech crew is still working on your bubble, Jennifer,” she said. “The hope is that we can find a way for you to float down to the stage, but, more likely, you’ll actually be rolled across on a wheeled apparatus of some kind.” 

Jen gave her a thumbs up, looking down at her script for a second before lifting her head up. “It’s good to see me, isn’t it?” she asked, her voice higher than usual as she smiled around at the others in the circle. There were several sounds of agreement as they read from the script. Agatha rolled her eyes. “No need to respond,” Jen continued, “that was rhetorical . Fellow Ozians…” She looked at Lilia. “Should I sing?”

Lilia shrugged. “You can if you want,” she said, “but you still need to work with Alice to lower the range of the song. It’s written for a soprano.”

“Ooh,” Jen said, “then I’ll skip it for now. Um…okay, I’ll just do the last part.” She cleared her throat, then sang, “For you and…”

“Somebody else for Ozian Two,” Lilia called out, picking a boy in the third row.

“Eddie James,” he said, running a hand through his hair.

“From now on, you are Ozian Two, until we can pick a new name for you,” Lilia said, writing it down in her notes. “Go ahead.”

“Glinda!” Eddie said. “Exactly how dead is she?”

“Well, there has been much rumor and speculation…” Jen said. “Innuendo. Out uendo. But let me set the record straight. According to the Time Dragon Clock, the melting occurred at the 13th hour; a direct result of a bucket of water thrown by a female child. Yes , the Wicked Witch of the West is dead !”

“More singing and singing,” Lilia said. “Then Ozian one, this will be your line. Go!”

Leslie stood up again, looking down at her script. “Glinda,” she said, looking up at Jen, “why does wickedness happen?”

“That’s a good question,” Jen replied, smiling kindly, tilting her head a little; “one that many people find…confusifying. Are people born wicked, or do they have wickedness thrust upon them? After all, she had a childhood. She had a father, who just happened to be the governor of Munchkinland…”

“And then we go into the flashback,” Lilia said. “Theo, you are playing the dual role of Frex Thropp and Dr. Dillamond, aren’t you?” 

Theo Parker, a dark-skinned boy with deep dimples, nodded. He’d been in the drama club since freshman year, just like Agatha and Jen. He was a senior now.

“Yeah,” he said, his voice cracking a little bit. He cleared his throat. “Sorry,” he said, deepening his voice. “I’ve only been on T for the last three months. It’s taking some time to really take effect.” He blushed, his shoulders hunched. 

“Don’t worry about it, kiddo,” Lilia said, affectionately. “Give it all you’ve got.” If she played favorites, Agatha thought, Theo would definitely be on the short list.

He cleared his throat again. “I’m off to the assembly dear,” he said, smiling at the girl who was playing Nessarose (and, also, incidentally, Nessa and Elphaba’s mother, Melena).

“She had a mother,” Jen said, “as so many do…”

“More singing,” Lilia muttered. 

“And, like all families,” Jen continued, “they had their secrets.”

“Illicit affair, yadda yadda,” Lilia said. “Ginette, my Wizard, you come in and sweep Mrs. Thropp off of her feet.” The girl playing Melena blew a kiss at Ginette, a curly-haired junior, who pretended to catch it and place it against her heart.

“And, of course,” Jen continued as Glinda, “from the moment she was born, she was…well… different !”

“Oh, you!” Agatha said, acting bashful. It was Jen’s turn to roll her eyes, but she was also smirking a little.

“Leslie,” Lilia said, “you take the Midwife.” She noted it down in her book as Leslie jumped to her feet, excitedly.

“Ahh!” she said, excitedly. “It’s coming!”

“Now?” Theo asked.

“The baby’s coming!”

“And how?”

“I see a nose!”

“I see a curl!”

“No singing,” Lilia said. “We’ll do that when Alice is here. Just let me hear you scream. You just saw a shockingly green baby come out of a very not -green woman’s body. Go!”

Theo and Leslie screamed.

“Good enough,” Lilia said. “Olivia?” She turned to the girl playing Melena. 

“What is it?” she asked, sounding genuinely concerned. “What’s wrong?”

“More singing,” Lilia murmured. “Theo.”

“Take it away…” He took a deep breath, clenching his jaw. “Take it away!” His voice squeaked on the last word, but he just shook his head as Lilia waved it off. 

“So you see,” Jen said, “it couldn’t have been easy!”

“A lot of singing,” Lilia said. “Jen.”

“Well, this has been fun !” Jen said, smiling toothily around the circle. “But, as you can imagine, I have much to attend to, what with the Wizard’s unexpected departure. So, if there are no further questions…”

“Eddie.” Lilia pointed at the boy in the audience, who jumped to his feet.

“Glinda,” he said, “is it true you were her friend?”

“Everyone, gasp,” Lilia directed. They did as they were told, all staring at Jen, who immediately looked unnerved.

“Well…I…you see…um…yes.”

“Louder gasp.” The gasps doubled in volume almost.

“Well, it depends,” Jen said, side-eying Agatha, “on what you mean by ‘friend’. I did know her. That is, our paths did cross…at school.” 

She took a deep breath, and Agatha wondered if she remembered all the times they’d sat together during sixth grade lunch, when they’d swap halves of their sandwiches or trade snacks. Or the times they’d run lines together, when they weren’t competing for the same roles. For the first time in years, she kind of wished that they could go back to that time, before Agatha’s mother had forced her to make that phone call, had pressured her into saying those things to Jen, to make her hate Agatha…to keep them both safe from her mother’s overzealous hatred.

But then she remembered the rumors that Jen had helped circulate about her out of pure pettiness and she turned away from the other girl, clenching her jaw.

“But you must understand,” Jen continued, reading from the book, “it was a long time ago, and we were both very young.”

“Scene change, singing, singing, singing. Enter Agatha, Frex, and Nessarose. Everybody stares at the shockingly green young woman.”

“What?!” Agatha huffed, jumping straight into her lines. She didn’t even have to look at the script now. “What are you looking at?” She furrowed her brow, then her eyes widened. “Oh, do I have something in my teeth?” She bared her teeth to the circle, receiving a few chuckles. She rolled her eyes with a sigh. “Okay,” she said, “let’s get this over with. No, I’m not seasick. Yes , I’ve always been green. No, I didn’t chew grass as a child.”

“Elphaba!” Theo huffed, his voice deep and authoritative.

“Oh, this is my younger sister, Nessarose,” Agatha said. “As you can see, she is a perfectly normal color.”

“Elphaba,” Theo huffed, “stop making a spectacle of yourself! I’m only sending you here for one reason…”

Agatha sighed. “Yes, I know,” she said. “To look after Nessarose.”

“My precious little girl,” Theo said, handing Olivia a pencil. “A parting gift.”

“Now, father…” She mimed opening a box, her eyes widening in delight. “Jeweled shoes!”

“As befits the future governor of Munchkinland,” he said, fondly. “Elphaba…take care of your sister. And try not to talk so much!”

“Dad of the Year exits,” Lilia said, causing a few snickers.

“Elphaba…” Olivia said, sympathetically.

“Well, what could he have gotten me ?” she huffed. “I clash with everything!”

“Enter Madame Morrible,” Lilia said. “A newcomer this year, Alison Davis. Are you related to Principal Davis?” she asked, looking at the young, blonde teen. She looked to be either a sophomore or a junior.

“Grandmother,” they replied. “Um, Sonny is preferred. As are they/them pronouns, if you don’t mind.”

“Of course not!” Lilia said, writing down more notes. “Go on.”

“Welcome, new students!” Sonny said, giving them all a cool smile. They had their hair up in a ponytail and three piercings in each ear. Their eyes were thickly outlined, but they wore no other makeup. Their smile was almost predatory as they got into character. “I am Madame Morrible, headmistress here at Shiz University.”

“Are you okay with the character’s feminine pronouns and titles?” Lilia asked. “We can modify as necessary.”

“Thanks,” Sonny said, “but I’m cool with it. It’s just a character I’m playing.”

“If that ever changes,” Lilia said, “you let me know. Continue.”

Sonny smiled gratefully at her, looking back down at their script. “And whether you’re here to study logic, literature, or linguification, I know I speak for my fellow faculty members when I say we have nothing but the highest hopes for some of you. Now, regarding room assignments…” Agatha, Olivia, and Jen all raise their hands via the script. “Yes, is this regarding room assignments?” They look at Jen.

“Oh, Madame, thank you for asking,” Jen said, acting touched, “but I’ve already been assigned a private suite.” Lilia motioned for everybody to groan. “But you can all come visit me whenever you want!” At Lilia’s cue, a few sighs of relief went up around the room. 

They continued reading their lines as Rio listened, sipping at her cold hot chocolate until she couldn’t stand it anymore and walked it over to the trash can at the edge of the stage. When she got back, they still hadn’t reached her entrance. She continued to listen, following along in her script until they reached the page she’d been waiting–and dreading–for.

“Here we are, sir!” one of the girls across the table said, putting on a gruff, gravelly voice. “Shiz University!”

“What?” Rio groaned. “Already?”

“Yes, sir.”

“What a shame,” Rio said. “Well, we’ll see you soon, Avaric. Don’t worry, I won’t last longer at this school than I did at any of the others.” She painted on a cocky grin.

Then it was Billy’s turn. The boy’s hands shook as he looked down at his script.

“Uh, m-miss G-G-Galinda,” he started.

“Nope,” Lilia said. “Start over. Wait, first stand up.” Billy did as he was told. “Okay, now shake out those limbs,” Lilia directed, demonstrating by shaking out one hand, then the other. “Get all of that nervousness energy out through your fingers and your toes. Come on!” Billy blushed bright red as he did as he was told. Shaking one hand, then the other, then each of his legs in turn. “Shake your whole body to remove any more nervous shakes,” Lilia said, twisting her body. “Come on, don’t be shy. We’ve all been there, haven’t we?”

Words of affirmation and a few claps in the main circle, accompanied by more clapping from the audience out in the auditorium.

“Okay,” Lilia said, clapping her hands. “Let’s get back to it. From the top of the line. Go.”

Billy took a deep breath, closing his eyes for a second before he began again.

“Uh, miss Galinda,” he said, looking at Jen, “I know I’m just a munchkin, but munchkins have feelings, too, and I’ve been trying to tell you mine, for you . But sometimes it seems like you don’t even know I’m there.”

“That’s not true, Biq,” Jen said, sincerely.

“It’s Boq,” Billy retorted, frowning.

“Biq, do you know who that is?” Jen asked, stage-whispering. “That’s Fiyero Tiggular , that Winkie Prince whose reputation is so scandalacious!”

Billy made a face. Rio gave him a toothy grin, trying to act confident.

Jen looked in Rio’s direction, batting her eyelashes. “Were you looking for something?” she asked. “Or some one ?”

Agatha felt a jab of jealousy in her gut. She tried to hide it, but something in Jen’s face flashed with recognition. 

“Uhhh…yeah,” Rio said, sounding bored and distracted. “History…class?” She shrugged, looking at her nails. “I dunno…somewhere?”

“History building is way over there, my friend,” Billy said, pointing offstage.

“That class just ended!” Jen said, with a laugh, rolling her eyes.

“Oh! Perfect timing!” Rio said, brightly. “So, uh, what does one do for fun around here?”

“Nothing really,” Jen said, once again leaning around Agatha to smile at Rio. “Until now…” She was practically purring. Agatha wrinkled her nose and pressed herself a little bit more firmly against Rio’s side. 

This did not go unnoticed by Rio, whose eyes widened slightly at the increased pressure of Agatha’s touch and she lost her spot on the page, her eyes scanning it for a moment longer than should have been necessary.

“We’ve been studying!” Billy huffed, lending Rio a helping hand.

“Well,” she said, finding her line right after his, “I see that, once again, the responsibility to corrupt my fellow students falls to me . Fortunately, I’m up for the task.”

“Very good,” Lilia said. “More singing, then…” she pointed at Rio.

“So!” Rio said. “What’s the most swank…ified…seriously?”

“Suspend your disbelief,” Lilia huffed. “Keep going.”

Agatha snorted next to her, her shoulders shaking, pressing her even further against Rio, and Rio had to take another deep breath before trying the line again.

“So, what’s the most swankified place in town?” she asked, gritting her teeth through the ridiculous word.

“That would be the Ozdust Ballroom!” Jen said, excitedly.

“Sounds perfect!” Rio replied, still feeling every inch of Agatha’s arm against hers.

God, if she couldn’t even concentrate when Agatha was just sitting next to her, what was she going to do during their solo, when she was expected to sing and then…then…

Her face felt very hot all of a sudden.

She tried to clear her head as she followed along with the exchange between Boq and Galinda, before picking up at her next cue.

“You’re good,” she said.

“I don’t know what you mean,” Jen replied, aloof. “But I do happen to be free tonight, so…”

“So, I’ll be picking you up around eight?” Rio said, trying not to sound completely disgusted by the idea.

“Singing, singing, blah, blah…” Lilia said.

“You’re perfect!”

“You’re perfect.”

“More singing…”

“It’s absurd !” Agatha said, as Elphaba. “This silly, rich boy appears and everyone’s off to worship him and some cultish social gathering!”

“Even me!” Olivia said, beaming. “Isn’t it wonderful!? Boq was too shy to ask me at first, but once Galinda encouraged him…”

“Galinda?!” Agatha gasped. 

“Don’t you dare say another word against her!” Olivia said, frowning at Agatha. “I’m about to have the first happy night of my life, all thanks to Galinda!”

“Singing,” Lilia said.

“Please, Elphaba, try to understand!”

“I do,” Agatha said, softly.

The read-through continued in the same vein for a long time. Jen and Agatha played well with the friendlier scenes between their characters, showing how truly talented they were as neither even looked at the other, keeping their distance the entire time. 

Then they came to a scene between Agatha and Fiyero, after Doctor Dillamond had been taken away.

“Can you imagine,” Agatha said, looking at Rio, “a world where Animals are kept in cages and they never speak?”

“Now, he may seem a bit agitated,” another student to their right said, with a sort of Einstein-esque accent, “but that is easily remedied.”

“What should I do?” Agatha asked Rio.

“I don’t know,” Rio answered.

“Well, somebody has to… do something!”

“Magic happens, people panic,” Lilia said.

“What’s happening?” Rio asked. 

“I don’t know. I got mad…and…” She shrugged, running a hand through her hair. Rio caught the scent of her shampoo and cleared her throat, focusing on her script.

“Alright!” she said. “Just don’t move! And don’t get mad at me…” She mimed picking something up. “Well,” she said, looking at Agatha, “are you coming?”

Agatha nodded, silently, her cheeks pink as they shared eye contact for a moment before breaking it.

“Careful!” she said. “Don’t shake him!”

“I’m not!”

“We can’t just let him loose anywhere, you know. We have to find someplace safe.”

“Don’t you think I realize that?” Rio huffed. “You must think I’m really stupid or something!”

“No…” Agatha said, shrugging one shoulder. “Not really stupid.”

“Why is it that every time I see you,” Rio said, “you’re causing some kind of commotion?”

“I don’t cause commotions,” Agatha retorted. “I am one.”

“That’s for sure.”

“Oh!” Agatha exclaimed, turning to face Rio fully. “So you think I should just keep my mouth shut! Is that what you’re saying?”

“No,” Rio said, holding her hands up in surrender. “I’m-”

“Do you think I want to be this way? Do you think I want to care this much? Don’t you know how much easier my life would be if I didn’t?”

Rio could see real tears brimming in Agatha’s eyes, but she couldn’t tell if she was still acting.

“Do you ever let anyone else talk?” Rio retorted, trying to keep her voice steady, but it came out louder than she’d intended.

Agatha’s eyes widened a bit. She swallowed thickly, looking down. “Oh,” she said, “sorry.” She was silent for a moment. “But can I just say one more thing? You could have just walked away back there.”

“So?”

“So, no matter how shallow and self-absorbed you pretend to be–”

“ Excuse me,” Rio huffed, “there’s no pretense here. I happen to be genuinely self-absorbed and deeply shallow.” That got a few laughs from the room, including Lilia. Rio felt a small thrill at that.

“No, you’re not,” Agatha said, softly. “Or you wouldn’t be so unhappy.” She looked straight into Rio’s eyes on that one, her blue ones seemingly searching Rio’s brown.

Rio swallowed thickly, her gaze leaving Agatha’s intense gaze for the safety of her next line.

“Fine,” she said, clearing her throat, “if you don’t want my help…”

“No, I do !” Agatha said, reaching out and placing her hand on Rio’s wrist. Rio’s eyes widened in response, as did Agatha’s, who quickly removed her hand as if she’d been burned. She turned to look at the invisible lion cub in its invisible cage. “Poor little thing,” she said. “It’s heart is trembling. I didn’t mean for…” she trailed off.

“Then what did you mean to do?” Rio asked. “Why was I the only one you didn’t do it to?”

They shared a long look that may have gone deeper than their characters. Agatha broke the gaze, looking down at her script.

“Oh, look,” she said, pointing at Rio’s face. “You’re bleeding. It must have scratched you.” She touched Rio’s face, her thumb swiping over her cheekbones, red blooming under the touch.

“Yeah,” Rio said, her heart pounding in her chest. She wondered if Agatha could feel the thundering in her pulse. “Or maybe it scratched me…” she said, just barely remembering the line. There was laughter around them, breaking Rio from her trance. She turned away from Agatha. “I better get to safety. I mean the cub. I better get the cub to safety.”

“He exits,” Lilia said. 

“Fiyero…” Agatha said, her voice gentle as she continues to look at Rio, her eyes now tracing the other girl’s profile.

Shit , a voice said in her head as she slowly turned her gaze away from Rio’s face. Shit, shit, shit .

She was in deep, deep shit.
