Chapter 7: Not That Girl

Chapter Summary

The first week of rehearsal continues. Jen and Agatha have a conversation. There is some pining here as well.

Chapter Notes

I listened to the OBC soundtrack while I wrote this. Tears were shed. Enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Seven

Tuesday

Music rehearsals started at three PM, but Agatha wasn’t called until three-thirty and Rio’s calltime was at four. The rest of the cast, however, had to be there to rehearse “No One Mourns the Wicked” with Jen at the center.

Agatha had been planning to spend her free period and the time before call writing an analysis on some short story she still hadn’t read in English, but then Rio had shown up in the library, set down her things at Agatha’s table, and reclined in her chair with a book in her hand, and Agatha’s gaze never stayed on her own laptop for longer than two minutes at a time. 

She didn’t know what was wrong with her. She had been just fine the last three years, accepting Rio’s flowers and crushing on her from a distance - not a far distance, but at least they’d never held hands. Well, actually, they had held hands, but not in that way. She was good about keeping her feelings locked up. She had mastered the art of compartmentalization; she’d had to, living with Evanora. She had to get used to the disappointment of her mother never bothering to show up for her shows, barely congratulating her when she made the Honor Roll or received commendation from the school for her perfect grades, or even thanking Agatha when she had dinner ready when Evanora got home from work. She had learned how to feign indifference even when her heart clenched at her mother’s dismissal. She had crafted a mask to hide her true feelings from the world. From her mother. 

From Rio.

And now the mask was starting to slip. 

She groaned in frustration as she read the same sentence for the third time in a row, her brain absorbing absolutely nothing. Rio’s gaze flitted toward her, one eyebrow raising in an unspoken question. Agatha waved her off, closing her eyes as she ran her hand through her hair, which she had taken down from the messy bun she had it in earlier. The updo had given her a headache that now throbbed at her temples. That was probably why she couldn’t focus. It definitely had nothing to do with the girl sitting across the small table from her.

She felt a tap on her shin and looked down to see the toe of Rio’s sneaker pressing into her leg. Agatha flushed as she looked up, only to see Rio holding something out to her. Three tiny white pills. She furrowed her brow at the other girl.

“Tylenol,” she said. “I know it’s mortal, but I haven’t quite mastered the art of healing yet. I don’t want to screw up your brain.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but stuck out her hand, smiling gratefully as Rio dropped the pills into her palm. She grabbed her water bottle and took a long sip, then tipped her head back and dropped the pills into her mouth, swallowing it all down with a tiny cough. 

When she looked back at Rio, the girl’s eyes were back on her book, but there was a tiny flush on Rio’s cheeks that gave her away. Agatha’s face warmed in response, a smile fighting against her restraint as she turned back to the laptop, trying desperately to focus on the words, but they were slightly…blurry.

Agatha groaned again.

“It’s going to take a while to really work,” Rio advised. “Maybe put your head down for a few minutes.”

“I can work through a headache,” Agatha groaned, “but now my eyes are betraying me.” Rio wrinkled her nose at Agatha as she reached into her bag and pulled out a pair of almost comically large glasses, with thick frames and slightly pink tinted lenses. She slipped them onto her face, sighing as the world turned a soft shade of rose around her, making the bright blue lights above them soften enough so that they were no longer contributing to her headache. She looked at Rio, whose eyes were wide. Though she couldn’t really tell with the tint, she was certain that Rio was blushing again. “I know,” Agatha sighed, “I look like a dorky owl. But, sometimes, it’s the only way I can see the letters on the screen clearly.”

“No, you,” Rio started to protest, but then she pressed her lips together, sighing through her nose. “Yeah, you definitely look like a dorky owl, actually,” she conceded, “but it’s…cute.”

Agatha was certain she was the one blushing now. She looked back at her computer screen. “Shut up,” she muttered.

Rio laughed. “Seriously, Agatha,” she said. “Glasses are a good look for you. How come I’ve never seen you wear them before?”

“I usually don’t, at school,” Agatha informed her. “I got them in eighth grade for reading - sans the rose tint, which is mainly for migraines - and some asshole boy called me Archimedes and started making owl noises at me.” Her face burned hotter, avoiding Rio’s sympathetic gaze. “So I refused to wear them at school. I get by pretty well, but reading tends to give me a headache without them. I always wear them at home. My mother would kill me if I didn’t.” She rolled her eyes.

“Boys are assholes,” Rio huffed. “You look adorable. Those glasses really suit you. Very classy.” She leaned in, lowering her voice. “Are you feeling better about them now?”

Agatha couldn’t stop the laugh that spilled from her lips. “Marginally,” she said. “And I seriously need them right now, anyway. I need to get this paper done before my call time. Lilia is probably going to have me doing all my solos and then we’re going to do our duets. Isn’t that fun ?” She gave a mock clap before her face fell into a bored expression.

“You know,” Rio said, “for a self-described theater kid, I thought you’d be more excited about the first music run-through.”

“I am,” Agatha said. “It’s the headache that’s making me grumpy, but I think the medication is actually starting to work. Thanks for that.” She patted Rio’s hand, ignoring the slight shock that was sent through her hand. She flexed her fingers, placing them back on her keyboard. “I’m just not looking forward to my duets with Jen.”

“She can’t be the only person you dislike in this club,” Rio huffed.

“She’s the only one with any real talent,” Agatha retorted. “I don’t have to deal with the other ones because they never get the big roles. Jen has been my only worthy rival since we were, like, eight. As much as it pains me to say it, she really has a good stage presence.”

Rio let out a mock gasp of shock and Agatha grinned, shrugging.

“A diva has to recognize another diva,” she said, flipping her hair. Rio let out a cackle at that, returning to her book. Agatha shot her another smile over the top of her laptop before focusing back on her computer screen, finally able to absorb the words in Raymond Carver’s “Cathedral”. 

 

“Agatha Harkness, lovely for you to join us,” Lilia said, as Agatha and Rio walked into the auditorium, two minutes shy of Agatha’s calltime. Rio rolled her eyes and took a seat in the back row, going back to her book as Agatha made her way to the front, glancing at the clock.

“I’m early,” she huffed. “My calltime is 3:30. It’s 3:27.”

“You know those times are just suggestions,” Lilia huffed. Agatha threw her arms up in frustration, dropping her bag in front of the stage and rummaging through it for her binder. She walked toward the piano, where Alice and Jen were sitting together, going over something as Alice gently played the notes for the reprise of “Not That Girl”. The notes were lower to better match Jen’s alto voice.

Why Lilia couldn’t have just chosen a soprano for the part, she’d never know.

“Okay, out of the way, Kale,” Agatha said. “Your turn is over now.”

“Give us a second,” Alice said, politely. “One more time, Jen.”

Jen nodded, glaring at Agatha over her shoulder before clearing her throat. “ I’m not that girl…” she sang, her voice smooth and melodic, her back straight, her hand on her abdomen, feeling her diaphragm. 

She sounded good, but Agatha would never admit it. Instead, she tapped her foot, looking at her wrist as though she wore a watch (she didn’t) and cleared her throat, obnoxiously. 

“Why do you always have to be such a child?” Jen grumbled, getting up from the piano bench.

Agatha mocked her in a high-pitched tone, making a face as Jen pushed past her to take her seat in the audience, pulling out her phone and headphones. Agatha rolled her eyes and saddled up to the piano, ignoring the disapproving look Alice sent her way. She didn’t need the other girl’s approval, anyway.

“We’re starting with The Wizard and I ,” Alice informed her. “But, first, warm-ups.”

Alice led her through her vocal warm-ups: funny noises to most, but important to loosen up the vocal cords. Agatha took these seriously, flexing her neck to the left and right as she vocalized, following the keys on Alice’s piano, relaxing her shoulders, and feeling her diaphragm in her abdomen.

When she was done, she turned to her first song.

“The Wizard and I” had been one of her favorites when she’d first seen the show. The actress performing it had given her chills, her voice strong and smooth and electrifying . Agatha had been on the edge of her seat as she watched the young woman command the stage, looking so small for only a moment, standing there alone at its edge, but then she opened her mouth and it was like she grew ten sizes right before Agatha’s very eyes.

It was so much better than magic.

“Sonny is out today,” Alice said, “so we’re just going to skip straight to your part.” Agatha nodded, skipping ahead to where her lines began. “Okay,” Alice said, positioning her fingers over the keys. She started playing and Agatha waited for her cue to start singing.

“ Did that really just happen?
Have I actually understood?
This weird quirk I’ve tried
To suppress or hide
Is a talent that could
Help me meet the Wizard
If I make good?

“So I’ll make good.”

Alice’s tempo picked up and she smiled at Agatha, nodding encouragingly. “Good job,” she whispered, continuing to play. Agatha grinned back, turning the page on her music.

“ When I meet the Wizard,
Once I prove my worth
And then I meet the Wizard,
What I’ve waited for since,
Since birth !

“And with all his wizard wisdom
By my looks, he won’t be blinded.
Do you think the Wizard is dumb?
Or, like Munchkins, so small-minded?
No!

“He’ll say to me, ‘I see who you truly are;
A girl on whom I can rely!’
And that’s how we’ll begin,
The Wizard and I…”

“Fantastic!” Alice said as Agatha started to walk toward the stage, hopping up the steps, unable to stay still. Her music was in her arms, but she didn’t even glance at her binder once.

“Once I’m with the Wizard,
My whole life will change.
Because once you’re with the wizard,
No one thinks you’re strange!
No father is not proud of you.
No sister acts ashamed.
And all of Oz has to love you
When by the Wizard, you’re acclaimed.”

Agatha saw Rio in the back, still half-reading though her eyes kept rising over the edge of her book, wide with interest. Agatha smiled confidently at her, really allowing herself to get into the song, her fingers twitching around the binder as she continued to move about the stage, commanding it, feeling in her element.

“ And this gift or this curse
I have inside
Maybe at least, I’ll know why
When we are hand in hand,
The Wizard and I…”

She took a breath, stepping forward to the edge of the stage, like she remembered all three of the actresses she’d seen do, staring out at the audience, focusing her eyes just above Rio’s head, at the clock beneath the balcony seats.

“And, one day, he’ll say to me,
‘Elphaba, a girl who is so superior,
Shouldn’t a girl who’s so good inside
Have a matching exterior?
And since folks here to an absurd degree,
Seem fixated on your verdigris,
Would it be all right by you
If I de-Greenify you?’”

She swallowed, letting out a small laugh on the next line.

“Of course, that’s not important to me,
‘All right, why not?’ I’ll reply.
Oh, what a pair we’ll be
The Wizard and I…
Yes, what a pair we’ll be,
The Wizard and…”

She squared her shoulders, her fists clenching at her sides.

“Unlimited…
My future is unlimited…
And I’ve just had a vision
Almost like a prophecy.
I know, it sounds truly crazy
And true, the vision’s hazy
But I swear, someday there’ll be
A celebration throughout Oz
That’s all to do
With meeeeeeeee.”

She threw down her music, stepping back. She wasn’t reading it anywhere. She locked eyes with Rio, who was now leaning forward, book forgotten, eyes locked on Agatha. Agatha smiled at her as she got ready for her very favorite part.

“And I’ll stand there with the Wizard,
Feeling things I’ve never felt.
And though I’d never show it,
I’d be so happy, I could melt!
And so it will be
For the rest of my life.
And I’ll want nothing else
‘Til I die.

“Held in such high esteem,
When people see me, they will scream
For half of Oz’s favorite teeeeeaaaaammmm.”

She placed her hand on her diaphragm to control her breathing.

“The Wizard…and I….” She held the note for as long as she could, egged on by Alice at the piano beaming at her, then nodding to let her know when she could cut the note. 

Agatha inhaled lungfuls of air as those sitting in the audience got to their feet and applauded. Rio actually let out a whoop, clapping the hardest. Agatha flushed at that, smiling shyly as she reached for her music, clearing her throat. It had been a long while since she last really sang for anything other than an audition, let alone a full song and not just the first few bars.

“That was incredible ,” Alice exclaimed, getting to her feet while still clapping. “I have no notes! Have you done this show before?”

“I have not,” Agatha admitted, sitting on the edge of the stage. “But this is quite literally my dream role; I may have already memorized every note.”

“It shows,” Alice said. “Okay, so next solo is… ‘I’m Not That Girl’. Can I assume that’s also memorized?”

“Of course,” Agatha said, turning to that page in the music. She cleared her throat.

Alice nodded, sitting back down, placing her hands on the keys. Agatha nodded to her and she began to play.

“Hands touch,
Eyes meet.
Sudden silence
Sudden heat.
Hearts leap in a giddy whirl…”

She looked out at Rio, whom she noticed had gotten closer to the stage, sitting in the third row, book tucked away somewhere, out of her hands, as her gaze fixed on Agatha, unrelenting this time, even when Agatha locked hers on it.

“He could be that boy…
But I’m not that girl.”

Her chest ached with those lyrics, but she persisted, glancing away as she got back to her feet on stage, walking a little off to the side, singing to a different part of the audience.

“Don’t dream too far
Don’t lose sight of
Who you are.
Don’t remember that rush of joy.
He could be that boy…
I’m not that girl.”

She took a short breath and walked to the other side of the stage, still avoiding Rio’s gaze, though she could feel it on her face, making her cheeks warm.

“Every so often, we long to steal
To the land of What-Might-Have-Been.
But that doesn’t soften the ache we feel
When reality sets back in.
Blithe smile, lithe limb.
She who’s winsome,
She wins him.”

Agatha glanced at Jen, who was smiling lovingly at Alice, whose face was flushed as she glanced back at her girlfriend, smiling softly as she continued to play. Agatha swallowed thickly, carrying on.

“Gold hair with a gentle curl…
That’s the girl he chose.
And heaven knows…
I’m not that girl.”

Tears pricked at the corners of her eyes and Agatha blinked them away, trying to ignore the maelstrom of feelings that swirled inside of her. 

“Don’t wish
Don’t start.
Wishing only
Wounds the heart.
I wasn’t born for the rose and the pearl.
There’s a girl I know…
He loves her so…
I’m not
That girl…”

Tears spilled from Agatha’s cheeks, and she was quick to wipe them away, sniffling a little as she let out a watery chuckle.

“Sorry,” she said. “Whew, that song always gets me.” She placed a hand against her chest, relieved when she caught Alice wipe away a tear as well.

“Yeah,” the other girl agreed. “That’s an emotional one. Do you need a minute?”

Agatha looked out at the audience to see Rio still staring at her, concern etched in her brows, asking a question that Agatha wasn’t quite ready to answer. She looked away, clearing her throat.

“Yeah,” she said. “Actually, can I just run to the bathroom for a second? I’ll be right back.” Alice nodded, making some notes in her book. “Thanks,” Agatha said, jogging offstage.

She made a beeline straight for the dressing room, which was pretty empty, except for the bookbags and books of some of the chorus members, who often used the room as storage during rehearsals. There was also a bathroom stall toward the back of the room. Outside the stall was a sink with a mirror above it. Agatha approached it, turning on the tap and cupping her hands as she leaned down, splashing water on her face.

She took a deep breath as she scrubbed at her eyes, willing the tears to stop. It was just a stupid showtune, written for straight people, about a girl pining for the boy that she didn’t think she could have. The fact that she did end up getting him in the end was unimportant. 

Because you can’t have that , a tiny asshole voice in her head said. Not right now, anyway . Your mother would never accept it . 

More tears filled her eyes and a sob wracked her body, though she fought tooth and nail against it, her knuckles turning white on the sides of the porcelain sink. 

“Are you okay?”

Agatha jumped, her eyes snapping open to find Jen Kale staring at her in the mirror. She frowned, her heart falling a little bit at the sight. She’d thought it was…well, it didn’t really matter who she thought it was because this was infinitely worse.

“What do you want, Jen?” Agatha huffed, she put soap in her hands and started to wash them as if that was the only reason she was in here.

“Are you okay?” Jen repeated. “Did you not hear me or something?”

“I’m fine,” Agatha said, shortly. “Why do you care? You gonna tell all your little friends that I had a meltdown in the dressing room just because I cried a little at an emotional song?”

“What?” Jen said, furrowing her brow. “No! Why the hell would I do that ? That would be stupid.”

“Hasn’t stopped you before,” Agatha said, turning off the tap and reaching for the paper towel dispenser. It was empty. She dried her hands on her sweater, turning around to face Jen, head-on.

“What are you even talking about?” Jen asked, folding her arms across her chest. “I’ve never…” her eyes widened. “You still think I told everybody that you poisoned me that one time? Agatha, I told you that wasn’t me!”

“Who else could it have been, Jen?” Agatha huffed. “Everybody was talking about it at school the next week. People were avoiding me like the plague, acting like I was going to slip something into their food!”

“I don’t know who it was,” Jen insisted, “but it was not me. I don’t deal with drama like that. I’m too good for gossip and lies.” Agatha scoffed. “I am ,” Jen insisted. “And at least I don’t have internalized homophobia!”

“What are you even talking about?” Agatha said, narrowing her eyes. “I’m not–”

“Don’t even ,” Jen said. “I’ve seen that little bracelet you wear. I may be bi but I know what those colors mean, okay? Even if you don’t want to come right out and admit it, already. Hell, you even gave a matching bracelet to your girlfriend.”

“She’s not my girlfriend,” Agatha said, a little too loud. She lowered her voice to a whisper. “She’s not . I…I can’t…”

“Can’t what?”  Jen asked. “Can’t admit to yourself that you’re actually gay ? What is the issue? Afraid to admit that all the horrible things you said about me were actually just you projecting your own self-hate?”

“My mother ,” Agatha hissed, “made me say all that.” The second the words were out of her mouth and she saw the impact they had on Jen (wide eyes, mouth agape) it felt as though a weight had been lifted off her shoulders, though anger continued to simmer in her stomach. “When your mom’s stupid ‘Coming Out Party’ invitation arrived, she wanted to storm over to your house herself and cuss your mom out. She was also going to recommend conversion therapy to your parents. The only way I could get her to stop was to tell her that you weren’t worth the trouble, that we weren’t even friends.” Agatha grit her teeth, feeling another wave of tears coming. “She told me to call you then. She told me to tell you that I didn’t want to be friends with your kind.”

“Did she make you say all the terrible things you said to me?” Jen asked, her voice quiet, her hands fisted at her sides. “All the slurs you called me.”

Agatha looked down at the floor. “No,” she admitted. “She didn’t tell me to say any of it. But she was encouraging it. She stood there the whole time I spoke, smiling proudly at me.” She took a deep breath. “That was the only time I think she’s ever actually been proud of me.” She looked up at Jen, whose expression was hard, unreadable. “It’s not an excuse,” Agatha continued. “I shouldn’t have said any of what I did. I shouldn’t have used those words against you. I’m sorry.”

“It took you long enough,” Jen said. “Four years is a long time, Agatha.”

“Yeah, well…” Agatha shrugged. “I meant to do it a long time ago, but if my mother got wind of it…”

“I understand,” Jen said, softly. “And, for what it’s worth, I’m sorry that I let people believe that you poisoned me that night.”

“I knew it!” Agatha said, pointing at her.

Jen rolled her eyes. “Calm down, dingbat,” she said. “I didn’t start the rumors. I just…didn’t dispel them. That was wrong of me.”

“Yeah, it was,” Agatha said, haughtily. Jen gave her a deadpan expression and Agatha cleared her throat. “I accept your apology.”

“And I accept yours,” Jen said, solemnly, “but we’re still not friends.”

Agatha scoffed. “Who wants to be friends with you, anyway?” she said, sticking out her tongue.

“Real mature, Harkness,” Jen said, but the corners of her lips were curling into a smile.

“Bite me,” Agatha retorted, but she returned the smile.

They weren’t friends, not like they used to be, but this was different than how they’d been just an hour ago. The air was clear between them, at least.

“Now, go tell Rio you have the hots for her,” Jen said, pointing a thumb over her shoulder.

Agatha’s entire face bloomed red. “What?” she said. “N-no I d-don’t!”

“Girl, please,” Jen said, placing her hands on her hips and setting a look of pure incredulity on Agatha. “You two are not subtle. She spent her entire audition looking directly at you ,” she said, “ while doing an incredibly romantic monologue about having a crush on somebody. And you just basically sang your entire solo to her !”

“She’s playing Fiyero !” Agatha huffed. “ Of course I sang it to her.”

“That song is supposed to be about her character,” Jen pointed out. “Not to her. You didn’t have to do all that.”

“Whatever,” Agatha huffed. “You know I can’t be…with her.”

“And why not?” Jen asked. “Just because of your mother? Do you know how many closeted kids we have in this club who are dating people their parents definitely wouldn’t approve of?” She shook her head. “That’s just an excuse. A lame one, if you ask me.”

“Yeah, well, nobody asked you,” Agatha said. But her protest was weak. She swallowed thickly, thinking of Rio and of her obvious crush on Agatha. Rio had never been good at hiding it. Agatha wondered if she was any good at hiding her own feelings for the girl, as good as she thought herself at compartmentalizing. Was there a way that Rio already knew how she felt about her?

“Tell her,” Jen said, her voice soft. “Before she gets tired of waiting on you. Tell her before you miss your chance.”

“Why does it even matter?” Agatha groaned. “I’m leaving Westview after graduation. My audition at Juilliard is next month. If I get it–”

“ When you get in,” Jen interrupted. At Agatha’s wide eyes, she shrugged. “I’m big enough to admit when somebody has talent,” she said. “I’m auditioning next month, too. And I hear Rio has her eyes on Columbia…”

Agatha’s face flushed at that, the thought of them getting into neighboring schools in the city, far enough away from her mother that she could…that they could…

She shook her head, freeing herself from those thoughts, those hopes . Now wasn’t the time for that. She needed to focus on other things. The play. Getting into Juilliard. Getting out of her mother’s house. Graduation…

She had no time for soft brown eyes and sly smiles and flowers grown from the palm of slender hands.

“I’ll think about it,” she told Jen, squaring her shoulders. “I just…I have a lot to think about right now.”

“Well, don’t over think it,” Jen said. “You spend too much time thinking and not enough time acting, life is going to pass you by.”

“Thank you, Aristotle,” Agatha huffed, walking past Jen to the door.

But the words stuck in her brain, playing on a loop even as she moved on to the next solo, avoiding Rio’s gaze for as long as possible before her blue eyes naturally deep, warm brown and stayed there.

This is going to be a lot harder than I thought.

Chapter End Notes

These damn lesbians and their teen angst and their pining and this stupid song about a girl pining for a boy being almost a perfect metaphor for a closeted girl pining for the girl she's been in love with for three years *grumble grumble*

Chapter 8: As Long As You're Mine

Chapter Summary

Duet time! Also a cute little mami and me moment for the Vidal ladies! There's some flirting and a little...surprise at the end. Enjoy!

Chapter Notes

I am getting hyped up for this movie, y'all. The Wicked Movie to be clear. If there were a AAA movie coming out, I would be unresponsive. But I am waiting until Discount Tuesday because I am a broke ass bitch. Still, I hope you like this chapter and it gets you hyped up for the movie as well.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Eight

Agatha left before Rio finished working on her solo. She stayed for a while, cheering her on from the audience like Rio had done for her, but then she started looking at her phone, furrowing her brow and rubbing her temples. Then, with a sigh and an apologetic wave, she grabbed her things and headed out the back doors of the auditorium, careful not to make too much noise as she left.

Rio felt her loss, acutely, but maybe it was better that Agatha not see the frustration she went through as she and Alice went over the lyrics to “Dancing Through Life” over and over and over again. She kept getting the notes wrong or her voice kept breaking or she waited too long or held a note too long or not long enough or…

You name it and Rio fucked it up. 

Finally, Alice took a deep breath and told her that they’d reconvene the next day, before the call for duets. 

Duets . Rio had forgotten that they were meant to also rehearse their duets. She had at least one of those with Agatha. A very important one, apparently.

Agatha had added all the Wicked songs to the playlist she made her, and Rio had even looked up the performances online, which is where she stumbled upon Slime Tutorials. She was halfway through Act One of the original broadway cast’s performance of Wicked when her mother popped her head into her bedroom with a furrowed brow.

“ Mija ?” she asked. “Are you listening to showtunes ?”

Rio had flushed, shutting her laptop. “No!” she said, unable to meet her mother’s eyes.

Marisol gave her That Look, her head slightly tilted, her eyebrow raised, one hand on her hip, the other on the doorknob. Rio knew better than to straight-up lie to The Look™. She rolled her eyes, opening the laptop back up and turning the screen so that her mother could see it.

“Ooh,” Marisol said. “Is that that musical about the brujas ? You know I’ve been wanting to see it forever . Scooch over.”

She didn’t even give Rio the chance to move on her own, shoving her aside as she climbed into her daughter’s full-sized bed, cuddling in against her shoulder. Rio laughed, rolling her eyes again, but she didn’t protest. Instead, she started the musical over again, resting her cheek against her mother’s head.

“Why are you watching this?” Marisol asked at one point, pausing the video. “I never took you for a musical fan. I know you’re in that club at school, but it’s all the background stuff, right?”

“Yeah, mami,” Rio said. “It is. Building the set, painting it…that’s usually what I do.”

“ Usualmente? ” Marisol asked, her brow raising again in a silent question.

Rio answered it. “I ended up auditioning this year,” she said, “for extra credit in Drama.” She took a deep breath. “The drama teacher thought it would be hilarious to actually cast me in a lead role.”

Marisol’s eyes grew to the size of saucers and she sat up, wrapping her arms around Rio’s shoulders. “Congratulations, mi amor !” she exclaimed, pressing kisses to Rio’s face until she was giggling and pushing her away. 

“Mami!” she laughed. “Mami, quit it!”

“I’m just so proud of you,” Marisol said, placing another kiss to Rio’s forehead, “for stepping outside of your comfort zone and for showing everybody just how much talent you have! You were always such a beautiful singer. My own little Selena !”

“Mom, Selena was Mexican,” Rio laughed. “We’re Puerto Rican.”

“And who played her in the movie?” Marisol retorted. “A Puerto Rican , mm?”

“Flawless logic,” Rio said, “but I’m nowhere near Selena or J. Lo. I just…I’m okay.”

“You are brilliant ,” Marisol said, lovingly, pressing another kiss to her head. “ Mi niña preciosa. ” She hugged Rio tight and Rio melted into the embrace, as always. Nobody gave better hugs than her mami. “So,” Marisol said, “which one are you playing? The green one or the blonde one?”

“They have names, you know,” Rio laughed. “And I’m not playing either, actually.”

“Okay, then the scary lady?” Marisol asked, pointing at Madame Morrible on the screen.

“Nope,” Rio said. “I’ll let you know when they’re on the screen, okay?” Marisol nodded and they cuddled back up against the pillows, Rio with her head on her mother’s shoulder now. 

They watched as Idina Menzel absolutely knocked the socks off of everybody in the audience, then laughed at the comedy that is “What is this Feeling?” while Rio imagined Agatha and Jen going toe-to-toe in the number. Then came Fiyero’s entrance, not long after…

Rio paused the video again. Marisol turned to her with a confused frown, her nose wrinkling in that way that people often said Rio did. She swallowed thickly, waiting for her mother to get it.

When she did, her eyes widened and she looked back at the screen, to the slightly grainy picture of the guy who had originated the role of Fiyero, then back to Rio, then back to Fiyero.

“No!” she gasped, a smile breaking across her face. “They cast you as him ?”

“There are apparently not enough guys in high school drama,” Rio said with a shrug. “They had to fill the gaps somewhere.”

“Still,” Marisol said, “this is such a big deal, baby. I am so,” she kissed Rio’s forehead, “freaking,” kiss, “ proud ,” kiss, “of you! You let me know the second tickets go on sale and I will be there in the first row.”

“Okay, okay,” Rio said. “I will. Just stop kissing me. You’re leaving lipstick all over my face!” Marisol laid a big, smacking kiss on her cheek out of spite, but Rio was laughing. “Ugh,” she said. “I’ll be right back.” 

She scrambled over Marisol’s body to get out of the bed, padding to the door.

“Grab some snacks from the kitchen, too, please,” Marisol called as Rio exited the room. Rio threw a thumbs up over her shoulder as she entered the hallway, making her way to the bathroom.

As soon as she entered the tiny bathroom, she laughed at her reflection in the mirror. Her mother had left several comically-perfect kiss marks on her cheeks, forehead, and even one on her chin. She turned on the tap and started to run a washcloth under it, but then thought better of it for a second, pulling out her phone.

She snapped a selfie, putting on an embarrassed smile, making sure all the kiss marks were very visible, before attaching the picture to a message to Agatha.

I think somebody may be more excited than me about my role in the play 😏

Agatha didn’t respond right away, so Rio placed her phone back into her pocket and scrubbed off the makeup, making sure that there was not a single spot of lipstick left on her face before tossing the cloth into the hamper in the corner of the small space and heading back down the hall, toward the kitchen.

Their house wasn’t tiny, but it also wasn’t huge, like Agatha’s. It was split-level, with a couple of steps to get from the main living area to the hallway that led to their bedrooms and bathroom. Their front yard was plenty big, as was their backyard. Rio still had a swingset from when she was a kid, which still held her weight from time to time, when she just needed a moment to think. She saw it out the window from her kitchen as she grabbed a bag of white cheddar popcorn from the pantry, then two sodas from the fridge. 

Marisol wasn’t a stickler for rules. She was fine with Rio having food in her bedroom so long as she cleaned up after herself and didn’t leave crumbs for ants and roaches to find. She liked to keep a tidy home. Honestly, so did Rio. Her bedroom was pretty neat. She had all the usual teen stuff: posters on her walls, a desk littered with papers, shelves lined with books and other knick knacks, plants littering all available surfaces, and a pride flag just above her bed. 

But everything was in its place. Her end table had enough clear space for their sodas as she climbed back onto the bed, opening the back of popcorn as they balanced the laptop on a pillow across their legs and pressed play.

“This is so good,” Marisol said, munching on the popcorn. “Who’s playing her?” She pointed to the Glinda onscreen.

“I don’t know the actress’s name, but she’s kinda famous,” Rio said, pulling out her phone to look it up. Her eyes widened and cheeks pinkened when she saw the text that appeared on her screen.

“I don’t mean the actress, querida ,” Marisol huffed. “I’m talking about the person who’s gonna play her at your school.”

“Oh,” Rio said, putting her phone back into her pocket without checking what Agatha had sent her. “A girl named Jennifer Kale. Jen.”

“Ooh,” Marisol said, in a teasing tone, “ Jen . Is she pretty?”

“She’s okay,” Rio said, shrugging one shoulder, showing clear disinterest.

“Hmm,” Marisol said. “Just ‘okay’ then?”

“She’s pretty,” Rio admitted because it was true. Jennifer Kale was tall and slender and her face wasn’t bad to look at. She just wasn’t Rio ’s type. “But she’s not really…for me.”

“Okay,” Marisol conceded. “Well, then, how about the other girl? Elphaba?”

Rio’s stupid blushing cheeks gave her away, immediately. Marisol’s grin widened into a knowing smile.

“Ooh,” she said. “Is she cute? I bet she’s so cute. Huh?” She poked Rio in the side and her daughter let out a surprised yelp, glaring at her.

“Her name is Agatha,” Rio said, trying to keep her tone even, to not give anything away. She was failing quite miserably at it. “She is, like, the star of the drama club,” she said. “She stars in all the plays, so it’s really not a surprise that she was cast as–”

“That,” Marisol said, “is not what I asked. I said, ‘is she cute?’” She paused the video, which was on Elphaba’s face in the middle of “Defying Gravity”, a broomstick in the green witch’s hand. 

“Yes,” Rio said, between gritted teeth. “She’s cute, okay?” Her blush deepened and Marisol let out a little squeal, wrapping her arm around Rio and squeezing until Rio couldn’t breathe.

“And you like her, don’t you?” Marisol said. Rio opened her mouth to protest, but Marisol held up one hand. “Don’t you even try to lie to me, mija . You and I both know better.”

Rio sighed, pressing her cheek to her mother’s shoulder. “Yes,” she muttered against the fabric of Marisol’s sweater.

“What was that?” Marisol asked, trying to push Rio’s face away from her shoulder to better hear her. “ No comprendé. ”

“Yes!” Rio said, more loudly. “I like her, okay? She’s…cute.”

“That’s not the only reason, though, is it?” Marisol asked, shaking her shoulder a bit with a knowing smile on her face. “Come on , Ri Ri! You never tell me about your crushes.”

“You have met three of my girlfriends,” Rio huffed.

“But that was years ago,” Marisol huffed. “You haven’t brought home a girl since…” She trailed off with a sigh, leaning her head on Rio’s as she burrowed more into her shoulder. “He would be so proud of you, you know.”

“I know,” Rio said. “He’d probably be shocked that I was in a play, though.”

“Not when he saw what role you were playing,” Marisol teased. “That would be just like you to get the role of the heartthrob.”

“Oh, yes,” Rio said. “Because girls at school just swoon when they see me coming in my plaid and ripped jeans.”

“Hey, I wouldn’t doubt it,” Marisol said. “You are so beautiful . I’m sure plenty of girls are fawning over you.”

Rio scoffed, but she was blushing. She cleared her throat. “Agatha is…talented,” she said, ignoring the happy noise her mother let out as she turned her attention to her. “She’s smart, too. She wants to study spellcrafting.”

“Ooh,” Marisol said. “Does she have the grades for it?”

“She has a 4.0,” Rio said. 

“Still,” Marisol said. “It’s very dangerous, isn’t it?”

“That’s what she likes about it,” Rio said, with a soft smile. “She said, ‘what’s like without a little risk?’”

“Oh,” Marisol said, softly, as she brushed Rio’s hair back with her fingers. “You don’t just like her, do you, amor ?” 

Rio frowned, flushing bright red again. “It doesn’t matter, either way,” she said. “Even if she liked me back, we can’t…” She shook her head, looking away.

“Why not?” Marisol asked. “She she not…” She lifted her eyebrows, trying to convey without speaking. 

Rio snorted. “Gay?” Marisol nodded. “She…is,” she said. “But…it’s complicated, mami.”

“How so?” Marisol pushed the laptop away, sitting up to face her daughter, face getting serious. Rio looked down. “ Mija, digame.”

“She doesn’t have a mami like mine,” Rio said, her voice cracking a bit as she looked back up at Marisol. Tears were already brimming in her eyes. She’d only met Evanora Harkness briefly, but the woman was cold as ice. And, if what Agatha said about the woman was true, she was just as horrible as she’d seemed, forcing Agatha to make that phone call to Jen, encouraging her to say nasty things in order to appease her. To a child , a fourteen-year-old girl.

“ Pobrecita ,” Marisol said, hugging Rio to her, but Rio knew that Marisol wasn’t speaking about her. Rather, she was speaking of Agatha, who was stuck living with an unsupportive mother.

Rio didn’t know what she would have done if her parents had been so unsupportive. She didn’t think she’d have made it this far if she wasn’t free to be exactly who she was. She didn’t know if she could stand not having her mother to embrace her and share snacks and a movie at the end of a long day.

Marisol pressed another kiss to Rio’s head then reached for the laptop, pulling it back onto its perch on the pillow. “I will pray for that girl,” she said. “I hope she is able to be herself, authentically, one day soon.”

“Me too,” Rio said, placing her head back against Marisol’s shoulder as she started the video again. “Me too, mami.”

 

Wednesday

Rio was already in Homeroom when Agatha walked in, unusually subdued. She was wearing a sweater in an unflattering shade of mustard yellow and a pair of olive-colored corduroy pants. Her hair was pulled back into a half-updo and braided. There were bags under her eyes.

“You okay?” Rio asked when Agatha sat down, heavily, in her seat.

“I’ve been better,” Agatha sighed. “I’m sorry I had to leave in the middle of your solo yesterday,” she said with a sheepish smile. “I forgot that it was my mother’s friend’s birthday.”

“Um….okay?” Rio wanted to say so what , but that was rude. Agatha must have heard it in her tone, anyway.

“My mom has a very old friend group,” she said. “Whenever there’s a birthday, we have to go to some fancy restaurant for dinner with all her friends and their kids. They’re her coven , she says.” Agatha scoffed. “We only see them on birthdays and holidays. Some coven .”

“Seems like you didn’t have a great night,” Rio said.

“How astute,” Agatha snorted. “One of my mom’s friends got this sweater for Christmas.” She motioned to the ugly mustard thing she was wearing. “It wasn’t ‘her style’, so she offered it to my mother, who insisted that it was my favorite color.” She made a face and Rio couldn’t hold back a laugh. “She made me take a picture before I left for school, so she could show her friend how much I love it.”

“Why are you still wearing it?” Rio asked.

“So I can get food on it at lunch,” Agatha retorted. “Something messy that’s gonna leave a stain so bad my mother won’t even be able to get it out with magic.”

“Diabolical,” Rio laughed.

“I try my best.” Agatha’s smile was soft, easy, and relaxed. “You never texted me back last night.”

Rio’s eyes widened. Between watching the musical and talking with her mother, she had completely forgotten about the text Agatha had sent her in response to the selfie Rio had taken. She hadn’t even really looked at her phone since then. Now, she pulled it out, clicking on the text notification.

Ags: Jessica Rabbit, I’m guessing?

“You know I have no idea who that is,” Rio snorted. 

“You…seriously?” Agatha huffed. “Okay, I’m adding Who Framed Roger Rabbit? to my list of movies then.”

“Roger?” Rio asked. “Who’s Jessica Rabbit then?”

Agatha opened her phone, typed something in real quick, then lifted her phone to show Rio the screen. Rio’s eyes widened at the sight of the cartoon redhead in the sparkly red dress.

“Is this a kids’ movie?” she asked.

“Absolutely not,” Agatha snorted. “But I did watch it when I was, like, ten. I watched a lot of things I shouldn’t have been watching at ten, though.”

“Same,” Rio said. “Sorry I didn’t text back. I was hanging out with my mom, watching…” She pressed her lips together as Agatha narrowed her eyes.

“Watching what?” she asked.

“ Wicked ,” Rio murmured. Agatha’s eyes widened in delight. “I found a slime tutorial, okay?” she said. “I wanted to see the show for myself. My mom caught me.”

“ Caught you?” Agatha cackled. “Rio, you weren’t watching porn .”

“I probably would have been less embarrassed, honestly,” Rio huffed.

“Wow,” Agatha said. “Ouch.”

Rio rolled her eyes. “You know what I mean,” she said. “My mom was so shocked that I was listening to showtunes that she didn’t even knock before entering my room.”

“Don’t all moms do that?”

“Not mine,” Rio said. “She’s all about consent…for the most part. She didn’t ask permission to climb into bed to watch the musical with me, but that’s actually pretty normal for her.”

“Is she the one that got the lipstick all over your face?” Agatha asked, with a soft smile. “I thought you just didn’t know how to apply it or something.”

“I still don’t,” Rio said. “You could teach me.”

As soon as the words passed her lips, she wanted the ground to open up beneath her and sink into the earth, never to return. She hadn’t meant it to be flirty - not really - but it had come out kind of…suggestive. Pink bloomed over Agatha’s cheeks, and Rio suspected her own cheeks mirrored them. 

“Alright, let’s begin,” Lilia said at the front of the room, forcing their attention away from each other as they turned forward in their seats, avoiding each other’s gaze. Rio didn’t miss the tiny glint of amusement in Lilia’s eyes, though, as she looked out at the classroom.

At them .

 

Rio was already in the auditorium when Agatha arrived. She was working on her solo with Alice, again, growing even more frustrated with each mistake she made. Alice was sweet about it, encouraging her, teaching her how to control her breathing and her voice. She had Rio do breathing exercises and voice warmups. Rio flexed her hands at her sides, walking around the piano, unable to stand still. Agatha walked up to the front of the auditorium, standing in her way and catching Rio’s gaze with her own, not saying anything. She just looked into Rio’s eyes as the other girl continued to sing, following Alice’s notes.

“ Dancing through life,
Skimming the surface,
Gliding where turf is smooth.
Life’s more painless
For the brainless.
Why think too hard
When it’s so soothing
Dancing through life?
No need to tough it
When you can slough it
Off as I do.
Nothing matters,
But knowing nothing matters.
It’s just life,
So keep dancing through…”

“That was fantastic, Rio!” Alice said as she stopped playing. “Perfect, even!” She looked at Agatha. “You are the Rio whisperer,” she said.

Agatha laughed awkwardly, rubbing the back of her neck. “I didn’t do anything, really,” she said. “She just needs to relax. I can’t always be on stage. I don’t even think I’m really in this song. Not until later, at least.”

“Still,” Alice said. “You’re a big help.” She wrote down some notes on her sheet music. “We’ll keep working on it, especially when George gets here for choreography. He’ll teach you how to dance and sing at the same time.”

“Oh Goddess,” Rio groaned, closing her eyes as she placed her forehead on the piano. “I forgot about that.”

“You’ll do fine,” Agatha said, patting her shoulder. She felt a small shiver run through Rio’s body at the touch. She bit back her own smile as she cleared her throat and looked at Alice. “Is Jen here yet?”

“She’s getting us some tea,” Alice said. “Should be back any moment. Wanna do vocal warmups or wait for her?”

“I’ll wait,” Agatha said. “You done with Fiyero?”

“I think she’s done with me, more like,” Alice said. “You can take her. Her call time isn’t until four, anyway. We’re gonna start with ‘As Long As You’re Mine,’ okay?” 

Agatha’s face immediately bloomed red, but she nodded, tugging Rio away to sit down. The other girl went willingly, plopping down in a seat near where their stuff sat. Her head lolled back, her eyes staring, unseeing, up at the ceiling. 

“What did I get myself into?” she groaned. “I can’t dance.”

“You’ll be fine,” Agatha chuckled, sitting down next to her. “George is a miracle worker. He’s been teaching dance for centuries . Literally. He’s one of Lilia’s oldest friends. Literally .”

Rio snorted. “I know,” she said. “I’ve been in this club for as long as you have, remember? I met George in freshman year. He’s kinda…”

“Genius, active, talented ?”

“Insane,” Rio said, turning her head to look at Agatha. “He yells a lot. And I’m pretty sure that cane is for show.”

“Probably,” Agatha agreed, “but I think we kind of need him, too, to whip us into shape. Trust me, you’ll be dancing like Fred Astaire in no time.” There was a moment of silence. “Fred Astaire was a famous dance–”

“I know who Fred Astaire was!” Rio huffed, shoving her shoulder. Agatha cackled, her head falling to Rio’s shoulder. She felt Rio stiffen under her cheek at the touch, but she didn’t move away. Instead, she felt Rio’s own cheek fall to her head, her shoulder relaxing a little.

Agatha let out a breath she didn’t know she was holding, allowing herself a moment to bask in Rio’s warmth, closing her eyes as she let herself imagine, just for a moment…

“We ready to do this?” Agatha shot up in her seat at the sound of Jen’s voice. She looked up just in time to see the taller girl walking down the aisle, holding a tray of coffee cups in her hand as she approached Alice. She smirked over her shoulder but said nothing as she leaned down to press a kiss to her girlfriend’s lips, handing over one of the steaming cups at the same time. 

“Yeah,” Agatha said, after too long of a pause, “yeah. Let’s do this.” She offered Rio an awkward smile before making her way down the aisle, too, only glancing once over her shoulder at Rio, whose face was incredibly flushed as she sat there, staring after her. Agatha offered her an awkward smile, then turned back to the piano, where Jen had placed a steaming cup in front of her.

Agatha furrowed her brow, looking from the cup to Jen, then back to the cup.

“It’s just green tea,” Jen said, nonchalantly. “Don’t think too hard about it. You need something to loosen the vocal cords. I am not about to sing with a pitchy witch.”

“ Me? ” Agatha huffed. “ Pitchy ? In your dreams, Kale.” She snatched up the cup and took a sip, sighing as the hot liquid slid down her throat. “Thanks,” she said. 

“Don’t mention it,” Jen said. “I got one for Rio, too. It’s hot chocolate. Wanna run it up to her?”

“Why are you being so nice?” Agatha asked.

“I had a coupon,” Jen said, taking a sip of her drink. “Just bring the girl the drink and get your greenie ass back here for warmups.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t suppress her grin as she snatched the hot chocolate from the tray, as well as her own drink, and jogged back up the aisle, holding out the hot chocolate to Rio, whose eyes widened in surprise.

“What’s that?” she asked.

“Peace offering from Jen, I think,” Agatha retorted. 

“You’re sure it’s not poisoned?” Rio asked. Agatha paused with the drink halfway to her lips. “She’s a potions witch, isn’t she?”

Agatha shrugged after a moment, taking another sip. “YOLO,” she said. 

Rio let out a shocked laugh and shrugged, taking a sip herself. “Thanks,” she said.

“Thank Kale,” Agatha said, walking away.

“Thanks, Kale!” Rio shouted, startling the other girl a little bit. Jen turned to her with a furrowed brow, giving her a shaky thumbs up. Rio smirked, taking another sip of the hot chocolate. It certainly didn’t taste poisoned.

Alice led Agatha and Jen through some basic vocal warmups before they all turned to the music for “What is this Feeling?” 

“Whenever you’re ready,” Alice said, placing her fingers on the keys. “Jen, you start us off.”

Jen cleared her throat, straightening her back.

“My Dearest, Darlingest Momsie and Popsical,” she said, with a bright smile.

“My Dear Father,” Agatha said, with a more droning, bored voice.

“ There’s been some confusion
Over rooming here at Shiz,” they sang together, their voices harmonizing well together. Rio watched, sipping her hot chocolate as it seemed to take even them by surprise.

“ But of course, I’ll care for Nessa ,” Agatha sang.

“ But of course, I’ll riiiise above it ,” Jen sang, coughing a bit. Alice stopped playing.

“Try to take the octave a little lower,” she said, playing a lower note. Jen nodded. “Once more?”

“ But of course, I’ll riiiiise above it ,” Jen sang, a bit more easily. Alice nodded and continued to play as they harmonized once more.

“ For I know that’s how you’d want me to respond.
Yes, there’s been some confusion

For you see, my roommate is…”

“Unusually and exceedingly peculiar
And altogether quite impossible to describe…”

Jen looked Agatha up and down. Agatha frowned and rolled her eyes, looking to the audience (mainly Rio).

“ Blonde, ” she said in a deadpan voice.

Jen pretended to twirl a lock of hair from her bald head, which actually made Agatha snort out a laugh and shake her head. She schooled her features again as Alice continued to play. Jen’s part came first.

“ What is this feeling
So sudden and new?”

“I felt the moment
I laid eyes on you.”

“My pulse is rushing.”

“My head is reeling.”

“My face is flushing.”

“What is this feeling?” they sang in unison, looking at each other now.

“ Fervid as a flame
Does it have a name?
YeeeeeeeeeEEEEESSSSSSS

“Loathing.
Unadulterated loathing.”

“For your face,” Jen sang, motioning to Agatha’s face.

“ Your voice, ” Agatha retorted, wrinkling her nose.

“ Your clothing.”

“Let’s just say
I loathe it all.
Every little trait,
However small,
Makes my very flesh
Begin to crawl
With simple utter loathing.”

The two girls began to circle each other, stepping right into character as they looked each other up and down as Elphaba and Glinda.

“ There’s a strange exhilaration
In such total detestation.
It’s so pure, so strong.
Though I do admit it came on fast
Still I do believe that it can last.
And I will be loathing
Loathing you
My whole life long.”

“Okay,” Alice called out. “Everybody in the audience, please grab your music. No matter what part you play, I need you to be my chorus right now. I know choral rehearsal isn’t until tomorrow, but please do me this favor.”

Jen glared out at the audience, raising an eyebrow in challenge to anybody who might try to argue. Nobody did.

“Okay,” Alice said, beaming as the audience members all turned to the correct page. “On my mark…go!”

“ Dear Galinda, you are just too good,” they sang, their harmonies slightly mismatched, but that wasn’t important at the moment. “ How do you stand it? I don’t think I could. She’s a terror, she’s a tartar. We don’t mean to show a bias, but Galinda you’re a martyr.”

Alice and Jen shared a look. Alice played a lower note than the song typically called for, and Jen nodded.

“ Well, these things are sent to try us.” Alice gave her a quick thumbs up, smiling brightly at her as she continued to play.

“ Poor Galinda, forced to reside
With someone so disgusticified.
We just want to tell you
We’re all on your side.
We share your
Loathing…”

“Layer it,” Alice directed.

“What is this feeling
So sudden and new?
I felt the moment
I laid eyes on you.
My pulse is rushing.
My head is reeling.
Oh, what is this feeling?

“Does it have a naaaame?
Yes….Loathing!
There’s a strange exhilaration
In such total detestation.
It’s so pure, so stroooong.

“Though I do admit it came on fast
Still I do believe that it can last.
And I will be loathing
For, forever loathing
Truly, deeply loathing youuuuuuuu
My whole life looooonnnnnnggggggg.”

Agatha and Jen turned to each other fully. Even standing at her full height, Agatha was several inches shorter than Jen, but she kept her shoulders squared staring up at her as Alice finished the last notes of the song, then she surged forward, curling her fingers into claws.

“Boo!”

“Eep!”

Agatha let out a truly impressive witch cackle, which was echoed by a few people in the audience.

“Amazing!” Alice said. “The chorus isn’t too shabby, either! Give yourselves a round of applause.” There was a smattering of applause in the audience. “We’ll work more on the chorus part tomorrow, but that was a solid start!” She looked at Jen and Agatha. “Ready for ‘Popular’?” she asked.

“I was born ready,” Jen said, taking a soothing sip of her tea. She cleared her throat, stretching out her neck. “Okay,” she said, looking at her girlfriend. “Let’s do this.”

 

By the time four o’clock rolled around, Agatha and Jen had almost perfected all of their duets (and there were a lot of them) and Alice was practically vibrating with excitement as she dismissed the latter. 

“You did so well today, baby,” she said, pressing a kiss to Jen’s lips. Jen practically melted, her arms wrapping around Alice as she pressed her forehead to the shorter girl’s.

“You’re going to give yourself a hump,” Agatha murmured, receiving a glare from Jen that she steadfastly ignored. “Okay, now get out of here so I can work with my…with Fiyero.” 

Jen had a knowing glint in her eye but said nothing as she pressed one last kiss to Alice’s lips before setting herself up in a nearby seat in the audience, reaching into her bookbag for something to do. 

When Agatha turned to summon Rio closer, she found the other girl only inches away, and Agatha let out a surprised gasp. Rio laughed and Agatha glared at her.

“Very funny,” she huffed, flicking Rio’s shoulder. “Need to get you a bell.”

“A blue bell?” Rio asked, holding up her fist in front of her. When she opened it, an indigo-colored flower popped up, growing out of her hand. She offered it to Agatha. “My lady,” she said.

Agatha rolled her eyes, fondly, and took the flower, placing it atop the piano.

“Do your warmups, casanova,” she said. 

“As you wish,” Rio said, stepping up to the piano. Alice led her through some of the same vocal warmups that she’d done with Jen and Agatha. Rio flushed as she was forced to make the same ridiculous sounds, but Alice only encouraged her, making the sounds with her. 

When Rio was finally warmed up, Alice instructed her and Agatha to turn to the correct song. Before they started, she gave them both a look, her cheeks tingeing pink.

“What is it?” Agatha asked.

“Um, well, it’s just that…as you probably know,” Alice said, “Elphaba and Fiyero, um, kiss during this number. It’s okay if you don’t want to do that, but we do want to leave some space for the kisses to happen in the song. Obviously, the original writers of the musical already considered the kisses, but I just want to let you know, in case you weren’t aware, you know?”

“I’ve seen the play, like, a million times,” Agatha said. “I know when they kiss.”

“How many times, exactly, do they kiss?” Rio asked. She knew. She had seen the play just the night before, but her brain was starting to short-circuit right at that moment. Agatha held up three fingers, her cheeks going pink. “Oh,” Rio said. “Right. Cool. Cool, cool, cool, cool, cool.” She nodded, swallowing thickly.

“Like I said, though,” Alice said, “you guys don’t have to kiss right now. I just want you to consider how long or short the kiss needs to be to fit within the constraints of the song, you know? It can’t really be a peck on the lips with you just staring at each other until your next lyrics. So, um, just count the Mississippis, I guess.” She shrugged. “I don’t know.”

“Okay,” Agatha said. She looked at Rio. “You okay with that?”

Rio nodded, unable to speak for a second. She just gave Agatha a thumbs up. Agatha couldn’t help the tiny laugh she let out. She slapped her hand over her mouth when Rio glared at her.

“Sorry,” she said, reaching out to pat Rio’s shoulder. She cleared her throat. “Sorry.” She turned back to Alice. “Okay,” she said, “um, let’s start. Just give us a sign when we should count?” Alice gave her a thumbs up as she turned to the correct music. “Okay,” Agatha said, looking down at her own music even though she had already memorized every word before this play was even cast at the school-level.

The intro was long, the two girls looking at their music, following the bars until Alice gave Agatha the sign to start singing. Agatha nodded, inhaled deeply, and began.

“ Kiss me too fiercely,
Hold me too tight.
I need help believing
You’re with me tonight.”

“ My wildest dreamings
Could not foresee
Lying beside you
With you wanting me…
But just for this moment,
As long as you’re mine

And if it turns out,

“ Maybe I’m brainless,
Maybe I’m wise,

Under your spell.
And somehow I’m feeling

“ Every moment,
As long as you’re mine,
I’ll wake up my body
And make up for lost time. ”

“ Say there’s no future,” Rio sang, looking right into Agatha’s eyes, her hand skating across the piano to brush against hers, “ for us as a pair… ”

“ Just for this moment,
As long as you’re mine,
Come be how you want to
And see how bright we shine.

“Borrow the moonlight

Holding you….”

“As long as you’re miiiiiiiinnnnnnnnnneeeeeee.”

Agatha pulled back a little, chuckling.

“What is it?” Rio asked, her breath a little short as she searched Agatha’s eyes, not really even acting. They were truly mesmerizing.

“Nothing,” Agatha breathed. “It’s just, for the first time, I feel… wicked. ”

Rio’s smile vanished as Agatha surged forward, pressing their lips together in a heated kiss, her hands cradling Rio’s cheeks. And then it was over. Agatha pulled away with a gasp, her cheeks flushed and her lips swollen. 

“Shit,” she said, placing her hand over her mouth. “Shit, I’m so sorry. I shouldn’t have–”

“Agatha,” Rio said, reaching for the other girl even as she pulled away. She could see panic and tears brimming in the other girl’s eyes. “Agatha,” she said again, her voice low like she was speaking to a timid animal, “it’s okay. I–”

Before she could say anything else, though, Agatha turned and bolted from the room.

Chapter 9: Floating

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Rio have a discussion that leads to...something, maybe.

Agatha also has a discussion with Lilia, which leads to a lot of things she didn't think she wanted to know.

Chapter Notes

I saw Wicked (twice) and it was AMAZING. I'm seeing it a third time on Friday (technically tomorrow, I guess, as it's three AM here.)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Nine

“Go after her.”

Rio blinked, turning to Jen Kale, who was standing beside the piano now, just a foot away from her. 

“What?” Rio asked, looking between her, Alice, and the curtain behind which Agatha had just disappeared. She was probably in the dressing room again. Like the last time she had run away. That time, Jen had gone after her though Rio had wanted to. She honestly didn’t know what she hadn’t. “I don’t…I’m probably the last person she wants to see right now.”

“Didn’t stop me,” Jen said. Damn, that was good logic.

“I…” Rio looked toward the curtain again, as if expecting Agatha to pop back in, all better.

That obviously didn’t happen.

From this angle, Rio could see the tears wetting Agatha’s cheeks, sliding down her face to cling to her chin. Her shoulders were shaking with sobs, her breaths coming out in gasps, little choking sounds leaving her lips.

Leave.” She stood up, looking in the mirror, trying desperately to smooth out the frizzy mess that had become of her hair. Rio jumped to her feet, but she didn’t walk away. Instead, she stepped forward, cautiously placing her hands on Agatha’s waist.

When Agatha didn’t push her away, Rio lifted one hand to place with the strands of Agatha’s hair. Agatha let out a soft moan, her cheeks flushing again. Rio smirked behind her and Agatha’s eyes narrowed at her.

“I like you,” Rio said, softly.

“I noticed,” Agatha hummed, turning on the tap to wash her hands.

“You like me,” Rio added. Agatha’s face flushed, visibly, in the mirror. She pressed cold, wet hands to her cheeks and eyes, trying to bring down the swelling from earlier tears.

“Maybe,” Agatha said, sniffing. She couldn’t hold back her grin.

“Would you, maybe, like to go out sometime?” Rio asked, a little bit nervously, her heart pounding against Agatha’s back. “With me.”

“You see, I almost said yes,” Agatha said, “but then you said it would be with you , and that’s a deal-breaker.” Her voice was teasing, a mischievous glint in her eyes.
