“Oh, are you?” Agatha chuckled, feeling her heart getting lighter with each word Rio spoke. “You’d make that sacrifice for me?”

“I would do quite literally pretty much anything for you, Agatha Harkness,” Rio whispered in the space between their lips. “I’m doing this play so you won’t have to kiss a freshman.”

Agatha pulled back, furrowing her brow. “What?” she said. “I thought it was to get an A in Lilia’s class.”

“That too,” Rio admitted. “But I would have been fine with the A- she was offering instead. But then she went on about you having to kiss a freshman - a boy at, that - and I didn’t want your last production to be ruined, so I said that I’d do it so–mph!”

Agatha’s lips were on hers in another earth-shattering kiss. Rio’s eyes widened momentarily, her hands falling to Agatha’s wrists as Agatha cupped her face, pressing their lips together so forcefully, Rio was certain they would bruise.

When they pulled back again, Agatha physically shoved Rio away from herself. “Get. Out,” she said. “I need to fix myself up. Again.”

“You say that like it’s my fault,” Rio said, but she was grinning as she backed toward the toward, tripping slightly as she stared at Agatha. Agatha turned back to check her reflection in the mirror, running her fingers through her hair as she tried to make herself look more presentable. “So, um, do you wanna see a movie this weekend?”

“Depends on what’s playing,” Agatha shot back, casually.

“Does it really matter?” Rio asked, tilting her head as she reached for the doorknob.

Agatha met her eyes in the mirror. “Friday,” she said, decisively. “After school.”

“Cool,” Rio said, her heart skipping a beat like a stupid love song. “Cool. Yeah. Um, I’ll pick the movie?” Agatha nodded. “Right. Cool.”

“You said that already,” Agatha teased.

“Well, it is,” Rio retorted. “It’s very cool. Um, I’ll see you out there. Bye.”

“Fix your face!” Agatha called out, even as Rio rushed through the door, slamming it behind her.

By the time Rio got back out into the auditorium, she had already wiped Agatha’s lip gloss off of her lips and wiped the smile from her face. She stepped back through the curtain to find Alice and Jen, and half of the drama club, looking straight at her. She swallowed thickly, attempting to ignore the prying eyes as she returned to the piano.

“Is she okay?” Alice asked. “You guys were in there for a while.”

“She’s fine,” Rio said. “Don’t mention it. Seriously, Alice. Don’t.” Her gaze was serious. Alice nodded. “Jen, you too.”

“Mention what?” Jen said, sipping the last dregs of her tea. “I didn’t see shit.”

“Damn straight,” Rio said.

“Bi, actually,” Jen retorted with a cheeky grin.

Rio snorted, shaking her head.

A second later, Agatha reappeared through the curtain, lip gloss reapplied, eyes dry and fresh, her hair a little frizzy, but looking more normal than it had seconds after Rio’s fingers had run through it. 

“Sorry,” she said, sitting on the edge of the stage, pointedly away from Rio, who was standing on the other side of the piano from her. “I just…I got a little carried away back there.” She grimaced. “Didn’t mean to attack you like that.” She barely glanced at Rio. “Any notes?” she asked Alice.

“Oh, uh,” Alice looked at her music. “Yeah. Um, mainly for me. I said there were three kisses during the song. The first one, though, is actually before it. The second one is in the middle. Third one is directly after it. But, um, again, we don’t have to do that today. Again.”

“You had one job,” Rio whispered in her ear. Jen swatted her away from Alice while the other girl mouthed an apology. 

“We should go over the song once more if that’s alright with you. It sounded good, but we need to work on the pacing a little more.”

“Fine with me,” Agatha said, nonchalantly.

“Same,” Rio said, clearing her throat. She started to walk over to Agatha, but the other girl gave her an imperceptible shake of the head. Rio nodded, staying where she was with her music as Alice started the song up again.

 

The next two days dragged on like molasses in the city of Boston in January of 1919. It was torture having to sit so close to Agatha without being able to kiss her. More than it had been in the last three years. At least then she hadn’t known what Agatha’s lips had tasted like, hadn’t known how hot her hands burned as they ran up and down Rio’s back while they kissed. 

Thursday

Agatha wore her Wicked hoodie to school the day after they first kissed. It was the same one that Rio had worn for nearly a week straight. The same one that Lilia had commented on.

“Nice hoodie,” the drama teacher said, with a knowing smirk, as she collected their essays on…Rio couldn’t even remember what she’d written about, her eyes glued to Agatha, whose hair was in a braid over her shoulder, revealing a part of her neck that wasn’t covered by the hoodie. She glanced sideways at Rio during class, offering her shy smiles as they locked eyes every now and then. 

Lilia caught their longing gazes several times during the class, narrowing her eyes at them. She knew that something had changed, shifted…but not exactly what. She hadn’t been at the last few rehearsals, preferring to let Alice take over the vocal practices while she graded essays in her office, which was close enough to the auditorium for it to count as oversight.

She obviously didn’t miss the fact that Agatha was now wearing Rio’s hoodie. Or was it Agatha’s ? Why had Rio been wearing it earlier? What was going on? For a Divination witch, she felt as though she didn’t know shit.

They continued on in the same vein, sharing glances and shy smiles in the hall. Once, Rio even took a chance as she was about to brush past Agatha, reaching out to stroke her fingers, fleetingly. She smirked when she heard Agatha’s sharp intake of air, glancing over her shoulder to see Agatha doing the same.

At lunch, they sat across from each other, as always, but Agatha’s foot found Rio’s under the table, her cheeks turning pink as Rio’s converse hooked under her boot, locking the two feet together as they ate their lunch. Agatha didn’t even blink when Rio exchanged her bag of Fritos for half of Agatha’s sandwich as it had become so common that nobody else at the table even noticed.

Jen was sitting a little more closely than usual, watching them. She rolled her eyes. “Disgusting,” she muttered to Alice, nodding to the pair, who weren’t really being subtle at all - not to Jen, at least.

“Are they…?” Alice didn’t finish the sentence, but Jen nodded nonetheless. “Aww.”

“Not ‘aww’,” Jen huffed. “Gross.”

“Love wins,” Alice retorted, taking a bite of her sandwich.

“Not with Agatha’s mother, it doesn’t,” Jen muttered back, frowning at them. She felt a pang of sympathy for Agatha then. It was a feeling very unfamiliar and uncomfortable to her, but she couldn’t help it.

She had known, back when Agatha first made that call to Jen after she came out in eighth grade, that Agatha didn’t actually mean any of the horrible stuff she’d said. But that didn’t really make it hurt any less. No matter how horrible Jen knew Agatha’s mother was, the fact that Agatha had let that vileness cross her lips just to save her own skin…it had hurt.

The rift still wasn’t fully healed, even after Agatha had apologized, but Jen was more willing to let it go when she realized what Agatha was actually dealing with now. It was going to be a long road for the two of them, though.

“Do you mind if I sit here?”

Agatha and Rio and Alice and Jen and the rest of the drama kids sitting at their table looked up to see Billy Kaplan, the freshman who played Boq, standing at the end of the table with his food tray, practically shaking with nerves. His shoulders were slightly slumped as he waited for a response. 

Rio watched in real time as Agatha softened at the sight of him, before moving over, making just enough space for him to sit down at the table. She said nothing, however, just looking pointedly from the spot to Billy before turning to look back at Rio, offering her a shy smile. 

Billy sat down, slowly, as if afraid that Agatha would change her mind in the next second and shove him from the table, but she obviously didn’t. He gave her a grateful smile and she smirked at him.

“So, Fresh Meat,” she said, “is this your first time doing theater?”

“No,” Billy said. “It’s, uh, my second, actually. I took part in a production of Fiddler on the Roof at my synagogue last year. I met a couple of other actors there that were already attending this school. They said I had talent and that I should try out.”

“Who’d you play?” Jen asked from down the table.

“I was in the chorus,” Billy admitted. “But I was the understudy for Motel,” he said, proudly.

“Not bad, mascota ,” Rio said, biting into her sandwich.

“Thanks,” Billy said. “Um, what does mascota mean?”

“Pet,” Agatha said. “She called you a pet.”

“Pet,” Jen said, “that’s a good nickname for him. He looks kinda like a puppy.”

“Don’t be mean, Jen,” Agatha said, shooting her a glare.

“Who’s being mean?” Jen huffed in return. “Puppies are adorable. You are adorable, Bobby.”

“Billy.”

“Whatever, Pet.”

“Okay,” Billy said, looking down at his sandwich, but he was smiling.

After school, all the principals had to show up for the group choral rehearsals and sing their parts where appropriate while the rest of the chorus worked with Alice to get their parts down. Lilia was there that time, watching from the balcony though she did not interrupt. Her gaze kept finding Agatha and Rio, who were seated on the stage with the other leads, their arms brushing as they looked down at their music, singing along with the rest of the chorus. They shared shy glances now and then, just like they had in class, but nothing more.

“Hmm,” Lilia hummed as she continued to watch them for the rest of practice, up until they left together at the end, their fingers brushing as they walked toward the exit.

Friday

If possible, this day went by even more slowly. Agatha once again wore her Wicked hoodie, her hair up in a messy bun on her head. She gave Rio a shy smile as she entered Lilia’s class and took her seat. Rio offered her a violet this time, laying it on her desk. Lilia rolled her eyes at them, but she also bit her tongue.

They were cute. She was going to let them continue to be cute.

Agatha could barely focus in most of her classes for the rest of the day, though. She had never had trouble taking notes before, but now she found herself daydreaming about Rio’s hands and lips and that thing she did where she pressed her tongue into her cheek and that cute little gap between her front teeth and–

“Miss Harkness?” Agatha jumped when Mr. Herb called her name, frowning at her with genuine concern. “Do you need to go to the nurse? You look a little flushed and your eyes are glassy.”

“I’m fine,” Agatha said, flushing even more deeply and clearing her throat. “Just…warm. I had something spicy for lunch.”

Rio had tangled their legs under the table again, though she had mostly spoken to one of her tech friends about what tech crew was planning on for the set, now that Rio wasn’t there to lead them. Agatha had barely been able to finish her salad as Billy Kaplan talked her ear off about…she hadn’t even really been listening, but he was super passionate about whatever it was. He could not stop talking or even take a breath.

Agatha would never admit this, but she found him…endearing. He reminded her of herself when she was a child, still enamored with theater, excited by the spectacle of it all. Her mother had never cared for it, but at least she hadn’t kept Agatha from taking part in it, especially when Jen’s mom had been the one to drive her home from rehearsals until Agatha was old enough to walk home on her own. 

She would never in a million years admit that she had a soft spot for Billy Kaplan, though. She’d rather die a painful death at her mother’s hands.

“You sure?” Mr. Herb asked, bringing her back from her thoughts. “You look unwell.”

“I’m very well, actually,” Agatha insisted. “Thanks.”

She straightened her back and tried to focus as the Latin teacher went back to teaching his lesson on…shit, what was he saying? Agatha still couldn’t quite focus. She had only two more periods of classes before she had to meet Rio during their free together. They were going to leave campus then to make their way downtown to the movie theater. Rio hadn’t told Agatha what movie they were going to see, but she hoped it was boring.

The minutes on the clock seemed to tick backwards.

Finally , when she arrived at the auditorium during ninth period, she was shocked to find that Rio wasn’t there at all. She checked her phone, which had an apology and a single name: Goode.

Agatha groaned. Mrs. Goode was the Economics teacher that was always the hardest on Rio. She gave Rio the grades she deserved, but she made Rio work harder for them than for any other class. Now she was keeping Rio from their first official date.

Agatha groaned as she slumped down in a seat at the back of the auditorium.

“Miss Harkness!” a voice said, not two seconds later, from behind her. “Fancy seeing you here.”

Agatha turned to see Lilia walk in, carrying a stack of heavy-looking books.

“Mind giving me a hand?” she asked. “My old bones aren’t what they used to be, you know?”

Lilia Calderu never missed a chance to remind everybody in the room that she was very, very old. Agatha rolled her eyes at it, but she still stood and took half the books from Lilia’s arms, following her to the stage.

“What are these for?” Agatha asked, grunting under the weight of the books. “And can’t you make things float? Or shrink them?”

“This seemed easier at the time,” Lilia said. “I cannot remember why. They’re props that the library loaned us for the show. They said nobody has so much as looked at them in over a year, anyhow. They were in the stacks.”

“The stacks?” Agatha asked. “What’s that?”

“The part of the library where nobody ever goes?” Lilia retorted. “Except horny teenagers, maybe.” She cackled when Agatha’s cheeks turned pink. “We all know about the escapades, but I’m not about to go snooping around to see some inexperienced dolt feel up a teenage girl and wet his own pants.”

“Jeez,” Agatha huffed, dropping the books on the stage.

“Don’t be a prude,” Lilia scoffed. “You think your generation is the first to find a private place to make out? Or do… other things.”

“Blah, blah, blah,” Agatha said, covering her own ears. “I can’t hear you!”

“Whatever,” Lilia said, waving her off as she placed the books onto a prop table backstage. “Kids these days.”

“Okay, boomer,” Agatha snorted.

“I’m not a boomer, baby,” Lilia retorted. “I was born in the–”

“The sixteen-hundreds, yeah yeah,” Agatha said. “I know . We all know.”

“It was the fifteen-hundreds , actually,” Lilia corrected. “Sicily, 1592. My father was a wealthy merchant. We were distantly related to some kind of royalty. I can’t really recall the details. He didn’t deal with me much. I was raised more by my mother and her coven, away from him.”

“Why?” Agatha asked. “I mean, didn’t he, like, love you? You were his daughter.”

“I believe he did love me,” Lilia said, “but we also had kind of a complicated relationship.” She shrugged. “He wasn’t a witch. He didn’t interfere with my mother and her coven - bankrolled them, actually - but he also didn’t have much to say to me when I started showing signs of also being a witch. His sons didn’t show any such signs, so he paid a little more attention to them.” 

“That must have been…hard,” Agatha said, her voice soft. 

Lilia shrugged again, walking to sit at the edge of the stage. “I had my coven,” she said. “My mother, too. She was a sweet lady, my mother. But tough as nails.” She shook her head, smiling fondly. “If the fever hadn’t taken them all…”

“Fever?” Agatha asked.

“Remnants of the Black Death,” Lilia said. “It cropped up a few times all over Italy, killing some and leaving others weak. My coven all got sick, myself included. I survived, but others did not. My entire coven was wiped out. My mother and brothers, too.”

“That must have been difficult,” Agatha said.

“You can’t even imagine ,” Lilia sighed. “It left my father and I alone. He was weak. He had a cough for the rest of his life that he just couldn’t shake. It died when I was in my twenties, still searching for somebody to continue my lessons. Other witches wouldn’t touch me with a ten-foot pole, though.”

“Why?”

“I could see Death,” Lilia revealed. “One of my special divination powers. I knew when and how somebody was going to die, ever since I was a child. People conflated it with me actually condemning others to death, like I had any kind of choice.” She scoffed. “I was alone for a long time.”

Agatha was quiet. She had never heard any of this from the older witch. Sure, she had mentioned growing up in Sicily, being a divination witch, and coming across hundreds, if not thousands, of important figures over the course of history, only to end up as a theater teacher in a public high school in New Jersey, but she never really considered where that journey must have started.

“How did you survive all that?” Agatha asked, her voice quiet in the large theater. 

“My wife,” Lilia said, with a soft smile.

Agatha’s eyes grew to the size of saucers as she stared at Lilia. “Your wife ?” she asked. “You’re married .”

“I was,” Lilia said. “A long time ago.” She held up her left hand, which held many rings (as did the other hand) but one stood out on her fourth finger. It was a simple silver band, a traditional wedding ring.

“What happened to her?” Agatha asked, heart clenching in fear at the answer.

“She was mortal,” Lilia said. “I used my magic to keep her alive for two hundred years past her prime, keeping her young for as long as I possibly could…but not everything lasts forever.”

“If she was mortal, and you were a witch,” Agatha said, “how did you two even meet?”

“Romeo and Juliet kind of story,” Lilia said. “Except we weren’t from enemy families, nobody died because of our relationship, and we were both women. For obvious reasons, though, our romance was forbidden at the time. Two women were unable to wed in 1600’s Sicily, but we did it anyway.” She smiled, fondly. “I married her under a Peruvian pepper tree, with only the birds as our witnesses, but I wouldn’t have had it any other way.”

“That sounds…romantic,” Agatha said, her voice quiet, her eyes staring down at her feet. 

Lilia glanced at her and reached out, taking her hand, squeezing it. “In a lot of ways, kid,” she said, “time has been good to the queer community. If Rosalie was still alive today, we could turn on the TV and see dozens of openly queer women gracing our screens, and nobody would even blink twice at it these days. Well, nobody except the people that everybody agrees are bigots, who are liked only by other bigots. I could walk down the street, holding my wife’s hand, and not be worried about being burned at the stake for it. Or stoned to death. Or drowned. Or–”

“I get it,” Agatha said, holding up her hand. “There weren’t many options back then, huh?”

“Oh, there were plenty of options for torture,” Lilia said, “all of which scared the shit out of us. So we left Sicily for greener pastures.”

“And you somehow landed here ?”

Lilia cackled. “Westview is a nice place,” she said. “Rosie would have liked living here with me. We could have made a home together, maybe had a few kids, you know? It just wasn’t in the cards. But we were happy with the time we got, as little as it seems right now, as a four-hundred year old witch, widowed nearly two hundred years now.”

“Sorry for your loss,” Agatha said.

“She’s waiting for me, somewhere,” Lilia said. “I’ll see her again. And I appreciated all the time we did get to spend together, here on the mortal coil.” She looked over at Agatha. “You never know how much time you’re going to get, kid. Not even me, not even with my special divination powers. Live every moment to the fullest.”

“I’m seventeen ,” Agatha huffed. “I have plenty of time left, if you’re anything to go by.” Her eyes widened. “Unless…do you see death on me?” She looked all around, as if she could see it too. Lilia cackled.

“I can’t see it anymore, kid,” Lilia said. “But, no, I don’t think you’re dying anytime soon. Better fucking not; we got a show to put on in three months’ time.”

It was Agatha’s turn to cackle. “I feel so loved,” she said.

“You are,” Lilia assured her, smiling softly. Agatha paused at that. “You’re a pain in my ass, sometimes, but you are loved.” She frowned at the expression on Agatha’s face. “Don’t get all misty-eyed on me now, Harkness. I hate sentimentality.” Agatha nodded, swiping at her eyes. “I just…you should know that you always have a place here, alright? A place where you can be yourself and not fear bigotry or the black plague.” Agatha chuckled at that, sniffling slightly. “You are loved here. You’ve been the star of pretty much every show since your first semester. I know you’re not very close to many of the other members of the club, but theater has a way of bringing people together. There’s not a lot of judgement here. It’s been this way for thousands of years. It’s why I’ve decided to settle here until it’s time for me to go and meet my wife again. Just…don’t forget that, okay? That’s all I’m saying. You’ll always have a place to go when shit gets rough.”

Agatha nodded, still swiping at her eyes. “Thanks,” she said, her voice breaking. Her chin quivered slightly.

“Don’t mention it,” Lilia said. “Ever.”

Agatha laughed. Lilia smiled, reaching out to place her hand on Agatha’s shoulder. 

“Your girlfriend is here,” she whispered just before Rio burst through the doors to the auditorium.

“Sorry I’m late!” she said, running down the aisle, struggling to wrestle some books into her backpack. “Mrs. Goode was talking to me about my stock market report and I…oh. Hey, Lilia.”

“Rio,” Lilia replied, nodding to the other girl. Agatha was staring at her, wide-eyed. Lilia offered her a knowing smirk. “I’ll leave you two be,” she said, hopping down from the stage and grunting as her joints creaked. “Oh, Goddess,” she groaned. “Don’t ever get old, girls. It’s the worst .”

“Noted,” Rio said, smirking. Then she looked at Agatha, seeing her eyes still shiny with tears, the surprised expression on her face. “You okay?” she asked.

Agatha nodded, snapping out of it. She offered Rio a smile. “Yeah,” she said. “I’m fine. Let’s go.” Surprising Rio, she took her hand, linking their fingers and dragging her toward the back door. Rio stared at their hands, then over her shoulder to where Lilia was pretending not to notice Agatha’s bold display, limping her way toward the other doors out of the auditorium.

Rio wanted to ask what was going on, but she decided against it. She didn’t want to risk Agatha letting go of her hand, after all.

Chapter End Notes

So we have begun the little romance, but that doesn't mean we're done with the angst.

Also, I DID succeed in making myself cry with this chapter, but can you guess which part made the tears fall?

Happy Thanksgiving to all my fellow Americans. I hope you have a nice meal wherever and whomever you are spending the holiday with.

Chapter 10: Something Bad

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Rio's movie date goes very well...so why is Agatha acting so weird the following Monday? What happened over the weekend that has her avoiding her girlfriend?

ANGST

Chapter Notes

The following chapter may contain mentions of child abuse. Be warned.

Also my hate campaign against Evanora Harkness will never end. If she has no haters, assume I am dead and buried.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Ten

If you had asked Agatha a single thing about the movie they’d “watched” she wouldn’t have been able to tell you with any kind of certainty what it was called, who was in it, or what the plot was. She could tell you how Rio’s hands felt on her waist, how her thumb stroked the skin just below where her hoodie had ridden up. She could tell you how Rio’s skin tasted under her tongue, how she had scraped her teeth over her thundering pulse, how she’d sunk her fingers into Rio’s hair to keep her still.

She could tell you about how they were the only two people in the theater at two PM on a Friday, when most others were either in school or at work. She could tell you the sound of Rio’s stifled moans under Agatha’s hand as she covered it, trying desperately not to get kicked out of the theater - though she doubted anybody truly cared being that they were the only two there. She could tell you how Rio’s neck looked as they walked out of that theater, how Agatha had handed over her hoodie to hide the bite marks that littered her throat, how Rio’s goofy smile stayed plastered on her face as they walked, shoulders brushing, back toward the school.

They didn’t have rehearsal that day, but they both lived in that direction, anyway, and neither was ready to say goodbye until Monday.

For as much as Evanora didn’t care where and what Agatha did after school before she got home, weekends found her practically locked inside the house. Saturdays, she was expected to study or clean the house (without using magic as that would have been the easy way out) and cook dinner that her mother would criticize no matter how it turned out. Sundays, they had church in the mornings, and then Evanora forced Agatha to attend Bible study, sure that Agatha will be made righteous by reading a book she’d already been forced to read several dozens of times in the past. Then, they ate an early dinner with the church ladies. It was always bland.

Agatha and Rio said goodbye at the corner where Agatha had to go right and Rio had to turn left. Agatha wanted to kiss her more than anything. Hell, she wanted to follow Rio home and never look back. 

Neither of those things were possible just yet, so instead she reached out and squeezed Rio’s hand.

“I’ll see you on Monday,” she said, smiling affectionately at the other girl.

Rio tilted her head, her eyes sparkling with emotion as she made a flower appear in her free hand. “ Hasta que nos volvamos a encontrar. ” She handed Agatha a simple daffodil, and Agatha swallowed thickly, holding it against her chest. She quickly looked around, relieved to find that they were completely alone and out of sight of anybody else, before she lifted Rio’s hand to her lips, brushing a quick kiss against her knuckles. Then she let go and practically sprinted in the direction of her house, keeping the flower pressed to her chest.

Rio watched her go, eyes wide and face flushing, her skin tingling where Agatha’s lips had touched it just seconds ago. Her entire body felt as though it were on fire, actually, despite the snow swirling around her. 

As she started home, she found herself counting the seconds until Monday morning arrived.

 

On Monday, Agatha was quiet.

She didn’t sit next to Rio, opting instead for a seat at the front of the classroom, her shoulders slightly slumped as she avoided Lilia’s gaze, her eyes focused on her notebook. Rio watched her from her usual seat, frowning at her back, at the severe bun that Agatha wore, with clothes that weren’t in her usual shades of purple. 

She had tried texting Agatha all weekend, but she’d never responded. Rio had worried that maybe her mother would see the messages, so they’d been subtle at first.

What was the homework for chemistry again? I forgot to write it down.

Did you do the reading?

What’s the difference between por and para? I can’t remember the acronyms.

Nothing overtly flirty or familiar, not until Agatha gave her the all-clear that their messages were safe from prying eyes. It had been one of the rules they’d set just before the weekend started, Agatha still worried that her mother would find out somehow, though the woman had never taken an interest in her daughter’s life before. Not really.

Agatha hadn’t written back at all. There wasn’t even any indication that she’d read Rio’s texts, let alone tried to text back. Rio had hoped to ask Agatha at school, but Agatha practically ran out of the room the second the bell rang, leaving Rio in her dust.

At lunch, it was more of the same. 

Agatha sat away from Rio, several people separating them as she spoke with Billy, pointedly looking away from Rio, who consistently tried to catch her attention. Rio caught Jen’s eye as the other woman looked between them, looking just as confused as Rio felt. Alice, too. 

Rio stood from the table halfway through lunch, motioned for the others to follow her out into the hall, where they crowded into the stairwell leading to the second floor.

“What’s going on with Agatha?” Rio asked them.

“How are we supposed to know?” Jen huffed. “ You’re the one she’s been making out with.”

“Shh!” Rio hissed. “Don’t speak so loud!”

“She’s suckered you into being her dirty little secret, huh?” Jen said, raising one eyebrow.

“It’s more complicated than that,” Rio snapped.

“I know,” Jen muttered. “Sorry. I have no idea what’s going on with her, either. She won’t even glare in my direction today. You think maybe something happened with her mother?”

“That’s what I was thinking,” Alice said. “I tried to ask her for her notes in AP chem and she bolted.” She shrugged. “I don’t know what problem she would have with me except the openly gay thing.”

“Whatever it is, it’s terrifying her,” Jen said. “I’ve honestly never seen her like this, and I’ve known her since we were practically zygotes. I don’t think it could really be anything but her mother.”

“How do I get her to talk to me?” Rio asked. “Or any of us? If she’s avoiding us like the plague, how do I get her to tell me what’s wrong?”

“Bobby!” Jen said, snapping her fingers.

“Billy,” Alice corrected.

“Whatever,” Jen said, waving her off. “The pet. She’s talking to him . So we just gotta use him to get to her.”

“I don’t know…” Alice said. “I don’t think we should get him involved in this.”

“Do you have any better ideas?” Rio huffed. “Friday, we were just fine , and now my own girlfriend won’t even look at me.”

“Ha!” Jen said. “I knew it!”

“Shut up and just…I dunno, do you have his number?”

“Why would I?” Jen snorted.

“I do,” Alice said, pulling out her phone. Jen just blinked at her.

“Text him and tell him to meet us out here but not to let Agatha know. Tell him it’s an emergency.”

“I hate lying to him,” Alice said.

“When did you two become friends ?” Jen asked.

Alice shrugged. “We have a common free period. Technically, it’s his study hall, but he has it in the music room and I spend my free there. He’s learning how to play the guitar and asked me for some pointers.” She tapped out a quick message: Jen and I need to ask you something. Meet us in the stairwell real quick? Be subtle.

Two minutes later, the lanky teen boy was stumbling out into the hallway, looking for them. He glanced all around before he found Alice waving him over.

“Hey,” he said, running his hand through his hair, “what’s up?”

“Nothing much–”

“What’s up with Agatha?” Rio demanded, cutting Alice off as she stepped toward the boy. He was tall and gangly, easily a full three inches taller than her, but he cowered under her gaze, taking a nervous step back.

“Wh-what do you mean?” he asked, his voice breaking. “N-nothing’s wrong with her.”

“You didn’t notice that she wasn’t acting kind of weird today?” Jen asked, hands on her hips, eyebrows raised disbelievingly. 

“No?” Billy said, with a shrug. “I don’t know her that well, though. She didn’t seem weird to me. Is she acting weird?”

“Well, she’s not sitting with her, um, best friend ,” Alice pointed out, motioning to Rio. “She’s not even looking at her. At any of us, for that matter. You don’t find that weird?”

“I thought she and Jen didn’t like each other,” Billy said. “Aren’t you two, like, rivals.”

“It’s complicated,” Jen said. “She really didn’t give you any hint that something might be wrong?”

“Not really,” Billy said. “She’s mostly talking about acting choices I could make as Boq. She hasn’t really even mentioned any of you today. Sorry.”

“You have to get her to talk to me,” Rio said. “Today. At rehearsal. You need to convince her to…I don’t know. Meet me in the dressing room or something! Somewhere nobody can spy on us.”

“Who would want to spy on you?” Billy asked.

“Enough questions, Benny!” Jen huffed.

“Billy,” Alice and Billy corrected.

“What ever ,” Jen grunted. “Just tell her that Lilia needs to speak to her or something and get her alone.”

“I don’t know…” Billy said. “If she really doesn’t want to talk to Rio, do you think it’s fair if I–where did that knife come from?” His face went pale and eyes went wide as he stared at the dagger in Rio’s hand, pointed straight at him. She didn’t speak, one eyebrow raised in question. Billy swallowed thickly. “Okay,” he said. “Got it. Hear you loud and clear. I’ll, uh, tell Agatha that Lilia wants to meet her before rehearsal.” He started backing away. “If you’ll excuse me, I have to go now.” He turned and sprinted back into the cafeteria.

Rio watched him go with a sigh, before tucking the knife back into her pocket, the weapon shrinking in her hand. They weren’t technically allowed to have weapons in school, but this was technically just an enlarged figurine.

Billy didn’t have to know that though.

“You think it will work?” Alice asked. 

Rio just shrugged her shoulders before leaving the stairwell, forgoing the cafeteria in favor of walking in the direction of her next class, unable to stand being ignored for another second.

 

Agatha, as predicted, didn’t show up anywhere Rio could have found her during ninth period, including the choir room, the music room, the library, or even the auditorium. 

Rio spent the whole period looking for her, growing hopeless the longer she searched, praying that Billy would follow through with his promise. She hoped the thought of Rio brandishing a knife at him was enough of a threat. 

When the final bell rang, Rio headed for the dressing room, intent on waiting there for Agatha to meet her, praying that she wouldn’t see past Billy’s charade. The kid might be good on stage, but he was still a nervous wreck when it came to lying for real.

To her surprise, the second she opened the door, a hand wrapped around her wrist and she was tugged right inside, stumbling further into the room as the door to the dressing room was shut and locked. 

Rio turned to ask what the hell was going on when her eyes widened at the sight of Agatha, whose eyes were red-rimmed as though she had been crying for hours . Rio surged forward, wrapping her arms around the other girl and Agatha didn’t even attempt to resist, sinking into the circle of her arms, her body already shaking with sobs.

For a long moment, Rio just held her, feeling a lump starting to form in her own throat as Agatha broke down in her arms. Agatha’s hands clenched in the material of the hoodie Rio was wearing - the one that Agatha had given her to wear the last time they spoke - tugging on it as she pressed her face into Rio’s shoulder.

“What’s wrong?” Rio asked after holding her for far too long. “Agatha, what’s wrong? Are you okay?” She pulled back, cupping Agatha’s cheeks, her thumbs wiping away as many tears as possible as she tried to look into her eyes. “Agatha?”

Agatha shook her head, her bottom lip trembling. “She knows,” she sobbed, hiccuping a little. “She knows.”

Rio’s entire body froze. “Who knows?” she asked. “Your mother? What does she know?” Agatha just shook her head, more tears falling. “Agatha, tell me,” Rio pleaded. “Let me help you.”

“You can’t,” Agatha sobbed. “You…she knows about you . She knows that you’re…that…” She shook her head again.

“Does she know that we’re dating?” Rio asked, fearing the answer.

Agatha shook her head, leaving Rio even more confused.

“Then what?” Rio asked. “What does she know?”

“She knows,” Agatha sniffled, “that you’re gay . Which means…God, if I’m seen anywhere near you, she’s going to take me out of school. She already spent most of yesterday after church screaming at me for having you in our house that one time. I had to swear I had no idea that you were gay. I had to promise that I wouldn’t even talk to you at school.” She dissolved into more tears, her body slumping against Rio’s. 

Rio had never seen Agatha like this. She had never known her to cry this hard, to be this upset over anything before. And her mother had done this. She had turned one of the strongest people Rio had ever known into this broken person. Rio wrapped her arms around Agatha as tight as she dared, pressing a kiss to her hairline as she walked her to a wall, sliding down it with Agatha held against her, until the other girl was in her lap, her body curled toward Rio.

Rio could tell that she had been holding this in, but for how long she couldn’t tell. It might have been since just this morning as she left for school, or it might have been since yesterday when her mother screamed at her. It had to hurt, holding in all that emotion, but Rio wondered if it was something that Agatha had gotten used to with her mother.

She didn’t doubt it.

It took Agatha nearly ten straight minutes before her cries started to die down, her face still pressed to Rio’s shoulder as Rio massaged the tension out of her shoulders and back, rocking her a little bit in an attempt to soothe her.

“How did she find out?” Rio asked, her voice gentle so as not to spur Agatha into more tears.

“One of her friend’s stupid kids goes to this school,” Agatha grumbled. “Harper.” She rolled her eyes as she slid off of Rio’s lap, rubbing her eyes as she folded her knees up against her body, resting her chin on them, still looking vulnerable as she shook her head. “She saw the pride flag you hung in your locker. Mom overheard her telling one of her bible study friends about it and how she wondered if my mother knew the kind of company her daughter keeps.” She sniffled again, swiping at her eyes. “Self-righteous bitch. I can’t stand any of them. I can’t wait to leave here and…” She pressed her lips together, more tears leaking from her eyes. Rio reached out for her again, but Agatha held up a hand. “I’m fine,” she said, sniffling. “I just…I don’t want to even think about it right now. This ,” she motioned to the dressing room, “is the safest place for me to be. It’s the only place I can be free right now. At least until my eighteenth birthday.”

“April second,” Rio said. Agatha blinked up at her and Rio tilted her head. “What? You thought I didn’t remember when your birthday was? I give you a whole bouquet of flowers every year.”

“No,” Agatha said, with a soft smile, “I just…God, I have to remind my mother when my birthday is every single year. You just already know it by heart and I don’t think I ever even told you when it was.”

“I figured it out pretty easily,” Rio said, “when Lilia had everybody in Theater sing you Happy Birthday in freshman year, just like she does for everyone’s birthday. My memory is pretty good, so I kept that filed every year thereafter.”

“I don’t know if I can wait that long,” Agatha said. “My mother took my phone on Saturday, but she wouldn’t tell me why. When she saw that you were the one who was texting about homework and connected the dots yesterday…she went insane. I’ve never seen her so angry.”

“Are you safe at home?” Rio asked.

Agatha shrugged. “I have no idea, honestly,” Agatha said. “She’s never struck me. She never laid a finger on me. She cuts me down with her words constantly, but she has never been physically abusive. She can keep me from leaving the house with magic, though. She put a spell on all the doors that locks me in at night, so I can’t even sneak out. I don’t know how to break it.”

“We’ll figure it out,” Rio promised, reaching for her hand to squeeze it. She leaned forward, pressing her forehead to Agatha’s. “I’m not going to let anything happen to you, okay?” Agatha nodded. “Now, who the fuck is Harper?”

Agatha sighed. “She’s a junior,” she said. “We don’t have any classes together, but she has friends who gossip. I see her in the hall sometimes, staring at me. She and her mom are the biggest busybodies. They involve themselves in everybody’s business at church, spreading rumors and whatnot. I think my mother likes Harper way more than she likes me. She’s always comparing us, as if Harper isn’t a straight-C student with the fashion sense of an oversized toddler.” Rio snorted at that. “I’m never going to be good enough for her,” she said. “Am I?”

“I don’t know,” Rio replied, honestly. “From what you’ve told me…I don’t know. I think you should stop trying so hard, though. It feels like it might be putting too much pressure on you. I don’t want to see you break again.”

“Again?” Agatha huffed. “You thought that was me breaking ?” She shook her head. “No. That was…that was just another day for me, honestly. I just usually do that kind of shit completely alone. It was actually nice having somebody here to comfort me this time.” Her eyes widened slightly as she turned cautiously toward Rio. “Did it scare you?”

“A little bit,” Rio said, once again reaching out for her, tugging Agatha against her side as she wrapped her arms around her shoulders, pressing a kiss to her temple. “But not away from you. I’m more scared for you. I hate that your own mother makes you feel that way. My mom would never.”

“Wow, okay,” Agatha snorted. “Humblebrag much?”

Rio laughed, shaking her head as she hugged Agatha more tightly. “I mean ,” she said, “that my mother would never treat you that way. She is the world’s topmost ally. When I came out, she made it known that I was to bring over anybody who needed support who didn’t receive it in their own homes. She made herself knowledgeable about everything there is to know about the LGBTQ community. She took me to my first Pride when I was thirteen, when I still had braces.”

Agatha sat bolt upright. “You had braces?” she asked. “Do you have pictures?”

“I do,” Rio said, “but you’d have to come over to my house to see them. Do you think you’d be able to?”

“My mom doesn’t follow my every move,” Agatha huffed. “I know some masking spells to disrupt the tracker she put on me for at least an hour or so at a time. But it might take a while for her to actually loosen her hold on me now. I had to beg her to be allowed to continue with the play. She doesn’t know that you’re playing Fiyero or that Jen is playing Glinda.”

“Won’t she eventually find out?” Rio asked.

“I hope not,” Agatha said. “At least not until I can leave her house for good.”

“Where would you even go?” Rio asked, her voice quiet, unable to suppress her worry.

“Anywhere but my mother’s,” Agatha said. “But, um, Billy’s parents…they’re foster parents. He thinks they might be willing to help me. Maybe. He obviously hasn’t asked me, but they took in his brother, Tobey.”

“I didn’t even know he had a brother,” Rio said. 

“We barely know anything about the kid,” Agatha snorted, “but his parents are pretty supportive of him.” Rio blinked at her. “Did…did you not know that he’s gay?”

“I mean…I don’t think I actually even thought about it,” Rio said. “I don’t think about the sexual or romantic preferences of… boys .” She practically gagged on the word, making Agatha bark out a laugh. “Is he cool with you telling me that?”

“He’s not in the closet,” Agatha said. “He’s never really tried to hide it. He’s dating one of the boys in the ensemble. Teddy, I think. Eddie? I don’t remember. They’re cute together. I saw them holding hands in the hallways a few times. I wish we could do that, but I’m not even allowed to look at you.”

“No offense, but I hate your mother,” Rio said.

“None taken. I think I hate my mother, too.” She leaned toward Rio, pressing a kiss to her lips. “You are the only good thing in my life right now,” she said, “so of course she wants to take you away from me. It’s just what she does.”

“She won’t be able to this time,” Rio promised. “I’ll make sure of it. Okay?” Agatha nodded. Rio placed another kiss on her lips.

There was a knock at the door, forcing the girls apart. 

“Who is it?” Rio called out, her voice vaguely threatening.

“It’s Jen,” the voice said on the other side. “Is Agatha there?”

Rio looked at Agatha, who nodded. “Yeah,” she called back.

“I’m here,” Agatha added. “What do you want?”

“Girl, rehearsal is starting. George is here.”

“George?” Agatha gasped, jumping to her feet. “George is here?”

“Yes!” Jen huffed. “Come on! He wants to see his Elphaba. And his Fiyero, probably, I guess. But mostly his Elphaba.”

“Come on,” Agatha said, practically vibrating with excitement. “George is here!”

“Should I be jealous?” Rio teased as Agatha practically dragged her to the door, unlocking it.

“Of a centuries-old gay man who can dance better than pretty much anybody else in the world, who calls me Bambina and showers me with compliments anytime he sees me? Probably.” She winked at Rio as she opened the door and followed Jen back out to the stage, letting go of Rio’s hand.

Rio watched her go with a soft, affectionate smile, but she couldn’t let go of the turmoil that was churning in her gut at the same time.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 11: Sneaking Around

Chapter Summary

George arrives to teach Rio how to dance (ie torture her) and Agatha has a lot to think about while she's in her girlfriend's arms.

Slight time jump.

Chapter Notes

This one is short bc my ADHD just will not cooperate. I will post another one soon, I promise.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Eleven

Rio couldn’t feel her legs. She was certain that at some point they’d been sawed off haphazardly, leaving her with even bloody stumps. But when she looked down the length of her body, she could still see the green converse she’d worn to school in lieu of footwear that would have been conducive to dancing. 

Still, she was sure that that was just an illusion, a trick of the mind. She pressed her face down flat on the stage, groaning as more pain rippled from her legs to the rest of her body.

“You are so dramatic ,” Jen snorted, sitting down next to her on the stage. “It wasn’t that bad.”

“Some of us didn’t start taking ballet before we could even walk, Kale ,” Rio huffed.

“Girl, this is nothing ,” Jen said, poking Rio’s left calf. The girl’s leg acted on reflex, her knee bending automatically, nearly kicking Jen in the face. “He really did do a number on you though, huh? Okay, I think I have something that can help.” Rio felt something cold and wet drip onto her calves and she jumped a little.

“What is that?” she asked, though she made no attempt to move. Not that she could move, anyway. 

“Little something from Potions class,” Jen said. “Turns out I’m pretty gifted at them. It’s meant for period cramps, but it can work on most muscles in the body. Just give it a minute.”

Rio felt the cold liquid turn warm on her legs, then hot, but not in a burning sort of way. It was more like she’d been covered by an electric blanket. The heat spread from her calves up to her thighs and down to her feet, relaxing the muscles that had previously been sore from learning – and failing to learn – dance moves at the hands of a sociopath with a cane. She let out a moan as all the pain from just moments ago melted away.

She fucking loved magic.

“What do we say?” Jen singsonged at her, poking her now-relaxed calf muscles. Rio grumbled at the ground, her words muffled. “What was that?” Jen asked, stretching her ear toward Rio’s upper half.

Rio turned her head. “Thank you, okay? That…damn, what’s in that? Will I be able to walk home?”

“Probably,” Jen said. “But it wears off in a few hours. If you ask nicely, I might fill up a tiny bottle for you to bring home.”

“Do I have to?” Rio whined. “Isn’t the image of me being in pain enough for you?”

“Absolutely not,” Jen said. “Now, say please.”

“ Please ,” Rio said, between gritted teeth. Jen beamed in her line of vision, placing a tiny glass bottle in front of her. 

“Was that so hard?” she said, chipperly.

“ Yes ,” Rio grunted, pushing herself to sit up. She snatched the bottle from the ground and tucked it into the pocket of her jeans. “How much should I use?”

“Two drops is what I used just now,” Jen said. “Any more might put you into a coma. It’s super potent.”

“And they taught this in Potions class?” Rio huffed.

“I may have also found a stronger version in one of my mom’s spell books,” Jen said, with a shrug, lounging back on her hands, crossing her ankles over one another as she stretched out her legs. “Speaking of moms,” she said, glancing toward where Agatha was talking with George, who pinched her cheek and spoke praising words to her like she was his granddaughter. She looked back to Rio. “Did you two talk?” Rio nodded. “And it’s what we thought?” Another nod. “Fuck. That woman is a cunt.”

Rio’s eyes widened in shock at that. “I don’t think I’ve ever heard you say that word before.”

“Well, we don’t talk much,” Jen said. “And I only save it for special occasions…like when somebody is actually a cunt. Though cunt might be too good a word for what Evanora is. She’s more of a dick, but that doesn’t pack the same punch, you know?” She shook her head, sucking her teeth. “I hate her. I’ve always hated her, even when Agatha and I were kids. She always gave me this look , like I was some kind of lesser being, like a bug she kept trying to squish but could never quite catch.” Jen pressed her lips in a thin line for a moment. “Everything she touches turns to shit.”

“Except Agatha,” Rio said, a bit defensively. “Agatha is the only good thing she’s ever done.”

Jen didn’t say anything, but Rio didn’t miss the tiny nod.

She let out a sigh. “Agatha and I are going to be fine,” she said. “But, uh, if you know a hyper-religious girl named Harper, maybe see if you can find a potion that will make all her hair fall out or something, I dunno. Be creative.”

“I’m taken,” Jen said with a yawn.

“So am I,” Rio retorted. “But, seriously, do it. Please. You’d make everybody’s day way more entertaining.”

“I’ll do my best,” Jen said. “Don’t kill yourself with that potion. Two drops, Rio. I’m serious.”

“Alright, alright,” Rio said, rolling her eyes. “Thanks.” She practically sprinted away the second the word was out of her mouth, not wanting to see Jen’s smarmy smirk.

She made it halfway up the aisle before George called out to her.

“Fiyero!” Rio paused, her eyes going wide (partly in fear; the majority in fear, honestly) as she turned to him. “Come here.” He knocked his cane on the ground. Rio eyed the exit longingly, then sighed as she slumped over to him, stopping a few feet away. Agatha attempted to avoid looking at her, but she could see those shy glances every now and then, the corners of Agatha’s lips turning up. “You did a good job,” George said, “for a novice. Tomorrow, you do even better, yes?”

“Okay,” Rio said, nodding. “See you tomorrow, George. Agatha.” She nodded to her girlfriend, and Agatha spared her another, slightly longing, glance before turning away again. 

Rio would take it. She gathered her bag from one of the seats in the back and made her way out into the cold January air.

 

“Who was that?” George asked, catching Agatha off-guard as she watched Rio leave the building, her heart aching. She missed her so much already.

“Fiyero,” Agatha retorted, looking up at the old man who’d become kind of a father to her in the last three years. “Remember?”

“But who is she to you , bambina?” George had that knowing glint in his eyes. He knew too much for his own good.

“Nobody,” Agatha scoffed, glancing around to make sure that nobody was listening. 

Most of the cast and crew had gone home, already. George just wanted to work with the main cast, especially ‘Fiyero’, who had the biggest solo dancing part in the whole musical. He had worked Rio through the basics of her Dancing Through Life sequence, but every time she made a misstep or went off tempo even just a smidge, he banged that cane and made her start over. By the end, her legs were like jelly.

Goddess, there may have been something wrong with her.

“Don’t lie to me, bambina,” George warned. “I know that there is something there. The way she looks at you? The way she said your name just then?” He clutched his chest. “The epitome of romancia ,” he said. “Reminds me of my Manuelo.” He sent a kiss up to the sky.

“You said Manuelo was in Barcelona,” Agatha said. “Why are you acting like he’s dead?”

“He may as well be, he’s so far away from me,” George huffed. “He teaches Salsa only three times a year and of course it has to be when I’m back in the States.”

“Will he be here for opening night, at least?” Agatha asked.

“He would not miss it for the world, bambina,” George said, tapping her cheek. “Now, no more stalling; tell me about your Fiyero.”

“She’s not my Fiyero,” Agatha huffed, her face going pink. “She’s just…” She struggled to find any words, to lie to this man. “It’s complicated.”

“Agreed,” Agatha said, looking down at her feet. “I like Rio–”

“Who?” George asked, furrowing his bushy brows. 

“Fiyero,” Agatha laughed. “Rio is her real name.”

“Is she Italian? Rio means river.”

“She’s Puerto Rican,” Agatha said. “Her last name is Vidal.”

“Rio Vidal,” George said. “River of life. Beautiful name. Odd girl. Weak legs.”

“Hey!” Agatha laughed. “That’s my…” Her eyes widened, her teeth sinking into her bottom lip as George grinned at her. “My mom doesn’t like her,” she said, softly, looking down again. “She won’t even let me speak to her.”

“How would she know?” George asked, cupping her chin to get Agatha to look back up at him. “Is she all-knowing like the divine mother?”

“Worse,” Agatha huffed. “She has spies. Real-life flying monkeys.”

“Ach,” George said. “Even the flying monkeys have their limits. And soon enough they were rid of the Wizard’s control over them, remember? And you will be rid of your mother’s control some day. Don’t let it ruin your life in the meantime.”

“Everybody says that,” Agatha huffed. “But it’s not that simple. I still have to live with her now . I can’t get away.”

“ Soon , bambina,” George said. “I know you are almost eighteen now, yes? You will be away from her soon.”

“My birthday is in April,” Agatha said. “Four months.”

“Almost three now,” George said. “Tomorrow is the last day of January. And then you are one step closer to freedom. Hang in there. And hang onto your dolcezza, si? It will be worth it in the end.”

Agatha nodded, slowly, praying that he was right.

 

Weeks passed by quickly after that. George’s visits to the theater became more common. He showed up every Monday and Thursday to go over choreography with the leads, especially Rio, walking her through her dances until she could get through at least half of it before he knocked his cane on the ground.

Before every rehearsal, Agatha and Rio would meet in the dressing room, locking the door to the outside world as they just held each other - and sometimes did more than hold each other. Agatha felt safest in Rio’s arms, away from her mother’s spies’ glowering gazes. Harper’s friends had started staring at Agatha throughout the school day, looking her up and down in obvious judgement, sneering at her in the halls. Agatha tried her best to ignore them, doing whatever she could to act normal –or as normal as she could while hiding a pretty significant part of herself.

But in the dressing room, she was free to be herself. With Rio.

She could kiss Rio, hug Rio, hold her hands, kiss her hands, and just…exist as a gay teenage girl. There was no pretense with Rio – not anymore. Since she’d allowed Rio to see her true feelings, her desire for her, Agatha felt as though a weight had been lifted off of her shoulders. Rio just held her, just kissed her, just showered her with affection that Agatha had rarely known in her life.

It was addicting.

She found herself craving it the second rehearsal began and they had to leave the comfort of the dressing room, her fingers lingering around Rio’s hand at the door before they parted. Rio always pressed a soft, lingering kiss to Agatha’s cheeks before letting her go. Agatha gave her one last, longing look before exiting the dressing room.

It wouldn’t become a problem until Lilia got the costumes in. Then the dressing room would be stuffed not only with too many clothes, but also too many people. They’d have to start spilling over into the choir room to get changed, eventually, like they did for every school play. But that was then and this was now. Now, they had space to be together.

It had been two weeks since Agatha’s breakdown. It was mid-February now, inching toward Valentine’s Day. They couldn’t do anything for the holiday, obviously – at least not outside the dressing room. Rio had promised her chocolates and flowers and kisses behind closed doors, but that’s not what Agatha really wanted.

She wanted freedom . She wanted to not feel as though she had to hide her love for Rio Vidal – though she had yet to say the words aloud, even to herself. She wanted to walk through Downtown Westview, holding Rio’s hand, fingers interlaced, sneaking kisses every now and then as they shared hot chocolate, hugging her tight, sharing dinner in a nice restaurant (one affordable for teenage girls, obviously) and just… being together in the open.

But her mother made that impossible.

Agatha had looked up the laws regarding emancipation in New Jersey. It was a pretty long process: one that wouldn’t make much sense to continue once she turned eighteen in a few months and could legally move out of her mother’s home. Then Evanora’s tracking spell would expire as her daughter reached the age of majority. It was one thing that magic customs and the legal system had in common: once a witchling reached eighteen, they were no longer considered the ward of their parents. 

Agatha could be free.

But what would that mean? Where would she even go ?

Billy had brought up the possibility of his parents taking her in. He had asked Agatha if he could tell them about her. His mother had always wanted a daughter, Billy said, and they weren’t against taking in more kids. Agatha would technically be an adult, but she would still be a teenager, attending high school and then college. She’d only live with them for a few months, if anything. Then she’d be in a dorm room, attending school in New York on a scholarship, free from her mother’s control over her.

Would it even be worth it to move out before then? Would she survive living with her mother until she officially had to leave for college?

Did she want to do more than just survive ?

She told him okay, anyway, but said that she couldn’t make any decisions just yet. Billy seemed to understand that, at least. He was a good kid, though Agatha would never admit it to his face – or to anybody’s, for that matter. She still had her pride, stubborn as it was.

Two days before Valentine’s Day, she was perched in Rio’s lap as these thoughts ran through her mind. Rio was just holding her, back pressed to the wall. They had made out for a while, but Agatha had suddenly just had the urge to hug Rio, to press her face into Rio’s neck. The last round of hickeys she’d left had healed by then, so she pressed her nose to soft, unblemished skin, grinning when she felt Rio shiver underneath her. Rio’s arms were wound around her waist, pulling her closer every few moments, her lips brushing Agatha’s temple, inhaling the scent of her hair, sighing in contentment.

“I heard you were applying to Columbia,” Agatha said, out of the blue.

“Hmm?” Rio blinked down at her, as if coming out of a daze. “Oh, um, yeah. Kinda. I applied Early Decision, actually.”

“And?” Agatha asked, pulling away to look her in the eyes. “Did you get a response?”

“Yeah,” Rio said, her cheeks going pink as she avoided Agatha’s eye. “In December, actually.” She pressed her lips together.

“Oh no,” Agatha said. “You…you didn’t get in, did you?”

“I did,” Rio assured her. “I did get in. Got a full academic scholarship, too.”

“Rio, that’s awesome!” Agatha exclaimed, cupping her cheeks to force Rio to look into her eyes. “Congrats!” She pressed a kiss to Rio’s lips, feeling the other girl’s hot cheeks on her palms.

“Thanks,” Rio said, smiling softly. She cleared her throat. “I don’t really like to brag about that kind of thing, though.”

“Why not?” Agatha huffed. “You brag plenty about being the smartest person in our school, Miss Valedictorian .”

“The hardest- working ,” Rio corrected. “Not the smartest. There are plenty of students just as smart as me who just prefer not to work as hard for their grades. Also, the photographic memory helps.”

“And the supportive mom, I bet,” Agatha commented, not bitterly.

“You do good in school with an unsupportive mom, though,” Rio pointed out.

“I do well in school,” Agatha corrected.

“You see?”

Agatha snorted, pressing her face back into Rio’s neck. “We should celebrate,” she murmured, pressing a kiss to Rio’s collarbone.

“With what?” Rio asked. “A new hickey?”

“You sound way too excited at the prospect of being bitten,” Agatha snorted, scraping her teeth over Rio’s pulse, which jumped. Rio let out a soft sigh. “Freak.”

“Don’t act like you don’t love giving hickeys,” Rio huffed, poking her in the side. Agatha let out a tiny yelp, and Rio grinned. “I wish I could give you hickeys,” she said, sighing. 

“It’s not safe,” Agatha murmured. “My mother…”

“I know,” Rio said. “That’s why I’m all too happy to receive them. You can live vicariously through me.”

“Weirdo.”

“You love it.”

Agatha was silent for a moment, smiling against Rio’s throat. She did want to give her another hickey. Maybe later.

“How does your mom feel about the hickeys?” she asked.

“She…hasn’t said anything about them,” Rio answered. “Oddly enough.”

“Are you hiding them?” Agatha asked.

“How would I do that?” Rio snorted. “Alice asked me last week if I got attacked by a vampire or something because of that one you left on my jaw. There’s no way my mom didn’t notice it.”

“Then why wouldn’t she ask about it?” Agatha asked.

“I think she wants me to be the one to tell her. She doesn’t like being overly invasive…usually. She had to pry the information about my crush on you out of me.”

“Aww, babe, you had a crush on me,” Agatha cooed, poking her cheek.

“We’re dating ,” Rio snorted, looking down at her.

“Still,” Agatha said, cuddling more closely to her. “I hope I get to meet her soon,” she said. “Your mom. She sounds…nice.”

“She’s great,” Rio said, nodding. “She’ll love you. She’ll probably try to feed you, though. You’re definitely too skinny for Marisol Vidal’s liking.”

“As long as the food is good,” Agatha said, grinning. “Is it good? Because my mother can’t cook for shit and then she criticizes my cooking.” She rolled her eyes.

“That sounds like heaven,” Agatha said, “and I don’t even know what that is. I think I might be hungry.”

“You want some Doritos?” Rio asked, reaching for her backpack. She pulled out a half-eaten bag, handing it over to Agatha. “I saved you some from lunch.”

Agatha plucked the bag from her fingers, pressing a kiss to her lips. “You are too good to me,” she murmured against Rio’s lips.

“You deserve more than you think you do,” Rio murmured back, pushing Agatha’s hair away from her face. She placed another kiss on her girlfriend’s forehead as Agatha opened up the bag and plucked out a chip. 

They sat in silence for a bit, Agatha munching on the Doritos, placing one against Rio’s lips every so often, allowing her to share the snack, before she was finished, tossing the empty bag into the nearby trash can. 

It was almost time for rehearsal to begin, but Agatha was reluctant to leave Rio’s arms. It was Monday, so they had the whole rest of the week to meet up and make out, but Rio didn’t want it to end just yet, not for today, anyway. She was suddenly feeling extra clingy.

“Do you want to have a picnic for Valentine’s Day?” she asked, her voice quiet and shy.

“A picnic?” Rio asked. “Where?”

Agatha shrugged. “Here?” she suggested, looking around them. “I mean, where else?” She shrugged.

“I don’t know if I want to eat here,” Rio said. “It smells.”

“We just ate Doritos in here,” Agatha huffed. “And we’ve been making out in here for the better part of two weeks.”

“The better part, huh?” Rio asked with a wide grin, wiggling her brows.

“You are a child,” Agatha huffed, sliding out of her lap.

“No, wait,” Rio said, reaching out to tug at her sweater, trying to pull her back. “I’ll be good.”

Agatha froze at that, her body going stiff.

“Ags?” Rio asked, clambering to her feet when Agatha didn’t move. “Are you okay?”

“I’m fine,” Agatha mumbled, but she sounded…far away. Rio placed her hands on Agatha’s shoulders, squeezing slightly. “I’m okay,” Agatha repeated, turning in her arms. She tucked herself back against Rio’s body, wrapping her arms around her waist, nosing her pulse again, her hands rubbing up and down Rio’s back, pouring all her affection into the other girl. She ghosted her lips against Rio’s collarbone before pulling back. “Where else could we possibly have a picnic,” she asked, “where my mother’s cronies wouldn’t catch me and report back to her?”

“We could ask our favorite teacher,” Rio suggested. “I’m sure Lilia would love to help us.”

“Didn’t you say she was full-on avoiding me just a few weeks ago?”

“That was when you and Jen were stalking her,” Rio snorted. “I fear she may have been justified. But now that you’re no longer following her around, annoying the hell out of her, maybe she’d be willing to let us use her room for our date – or at least find us a place to go that nobody else would even think to look .”

“Maybe…” Agatha said. “Otherwise, like it or not, we’re having our Valentine’s Day picnic right here . In this smelly room.”

“Honestly,” Rio said, looking down into Agatha’s bright, happy blue eyes, “as long as you’re here, I might just be okay with that.”

Agatha smiled up at her, pressing her lips to Rio’s in another kiss. “That was so cheesy,” she huffed. 

“Yeah, but you loved it,” Rio teased as Agatha pulled away, their hands clasped between them as she dragged her to the door.

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t bite back her grin. 

Rio Vidal was goofy and cheesy and affectionate, and Agatha loved all of it.

She loved her . But she couldn’t say that. Not yet.

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Rio plan their Valentine's Day picnic. There's some good food involved.

Chapter Twelve

Lilia Calderu didn’t have many moments of peace and quiet as a high school drama teacher. She had tests to grade, assignments to markup, and projects to assign. But her lunch period was not used to do any of that. That was for eating , and when she didn’t get to eat during that period, she was noticeably grumpy for the rest of the day.

When there was a knock at her door, she was already feeling that bug up her ass, a headache spreading from her temples. She was about to bite some poor kid’s head off before she even opened the damn door.

“What do you–oh, hello, Agatha. What do you want?” Her voice softened just a bit when she saw this student in particular. Agatha had been somewhat of a thorn in her side for the last three and a half years, but lately she had been…subdued. At least during class time. 

She no longer sat next to Rio Vidal, opting instead to sit at the front of the classroom, as close to Lilia’s desk as possible, but she didn’t annoy her with any questions, comments, or concerns – like most of the teacher’s pets that Lilia had had over the last few decades. Instead, she had been quiet, rarely raising her hand, and doing all of her work without even making a single peep. Lilia had honestly been worried about her, sending looks to both Jennifer and Rio, both of whom just shook their heads at her.

Every time Lilia considered asking Agatha to stay after class or come by during lunch, Agatha had either already sped out of the room or she’d just ignored the note that Lilia left on her desk. Lilia had stopped trying.

Now, here she was, on her own, smiling shyly up at Lilia. Lilia had never known Agatha Harkness to be shy at all. It was a little unnerving.

“We need some help,” Agatha said, stepping into the room and shutting it. Purple burst from her hand, covering the door.

“Who’s we?” Lilia asked, furrowing her brow.

“Hello,” a voice said from behind her. Lilia jumped, spinning around, her eyes narrowing as Rio popped her head in through the window, clambering in to perch on the counter.

“Why must you scale the building when there’s a perfectly good, unlocked door right here?” Lilia huffed.

“Because it’s more fun this way,” Rio said, shutting the window and hopping off the counter. “Besides, we can’t exactly be seen together right now.” She motioned to Agatha, who frowned, looking down at her feet.

“Is this about your mother?” Lilia asked. 

Agatha’s eyes widened. “George told you?”

“George didn’t need to tell me anything,” Lilia said. “I have eyes. You told George and not me ? Rude.”

“This isn’t exactly the kind of thing you tell your teacher,” Agatha huffed. “It’s…embarrassing.”

“What’s embarrassing about it?” Lilia asked, placing a hand on Agatha’s shoulder. “It’s nothing that you’ve done.”

“Still,” Agatha said. “My mom is…she has recruited girls from my Bible study group to watch me during school. Because she found out that Rio is a lesbian.”

“What a goddamn bitch,” Lilia huffed. “No offense,” she said to Agatha.

“None taken,” Agatha retorted. “Please, offend away.”

Lilia snorted, shaking her head. She pulled Agatha into a hug. The girl was less than a tenth of her age but a full three inches taller than her, but she tucked her head right into Lilia’s shoulder, squeezing back tightly. Lilia felt tears prick at the corners of her eyes. 

She had been teaching at Westview High for decades , ever since her wife passed and she needed to give her life some other kind of meaning, and she could count on one hand how many students she had actually hugged like this. Of course, she loved all of her students, and so many of them loved her. They still visited her, invited them to their shows, on and off Broadway, sent her wedding invitations, Christmas cards, birth announcements, etc. 

But she’d felt true genuine affection for so few. 

Agatha Harkness was one of those few. Lilia had thought, after her first meeting with Evanora Harkness, that it may have been because she could relate to having a cold, distant parental figure in her life, but it became pretty clear that there was something different.

When she looked at Agatha, she saw somebody like herself. A young woman, terrified and alone, hiding her true self from the world. Agatha Harkness had exuded confidence from the moment Lilia first saw her in her class, sitting front and center, head held high when she was given her first monologue assignment. She had blown the class away, Lilia included, but even then Lilia could see that there was something beneath the surface.

It was in the way she glanced at the girl next to her, at Rio . It was in the way her face changed color whenever she found a flower on her desk. It was in the way she smiled when Rio said something to her. Agatha had tried to hide her feelings for the other girl, but Lilia recognized the signs.

She’d been there once, too, after all. 

So she hugged Agatha, probably too tightly. But the girl didn’t pull away from her. Agatha hugged her back even more tightly.

“So,” Lilia said, once she’d finally pulled away, wiping casually at her damp eyes, “what is it I can do for you two?”

“Tomorrow is Valentine’s Day,” Agatha said.

“I am aware,” Lilia said. “I am spending it with a gay man while he laments over his far-away husband and I think about my long-dead wife.”

“Sounds like a blast,” Rio commented.

“With enough wine, anything is a blast,” Lilia said. “Proceed.”

“We want to have a picnic,” Agatha continued.

“In February ?” Lilia asked. “There’s snow on the ground.”

“We wanna have it inside,” Agatha huffed. “In here, if possible.”

“Here?” Lilia sniffed, looking around her classroom. “Not very romantic.”

“I can grow flowers in my hands,” Rio said. “I can make it romantic.”

“Fair point,” Lilia said. “When, exactly, would you be having this picnic? Not during rehearsal, I hope.”

“I spoke to Alice,” Rio said. “She’s running through some chorus numbers tomorrow. She won’t even need us until four-thirty, which gives us plenty of time to have our picnic. And you don’t have a class in here during ninth, right?”

“That is correct,” Lilia said, “but I’m unsure if I should be loaning my classroom out to amorous students.” She lifted a brow at them. 

“Ugh! Lilia! No!” Agatha wrinkled her nose. “We’re not gonna do… that .”

“You don’t have to sound so disgusted,” Rio huffed, frowning at her. 

“You’re not helping,” Agatha huffed. “And I’m not disgusted at it, per say. I just…that’s not what we’re trying to do here, Lilia, okay? I just…I want to have a few hours where I don’t have to worry about hiding who I am and who I…am seeing.” She flushed when Rio’s eyes widened at that stutter. “We’re just gonna have some food, maybe watch a movie, and just… be . Away from my mother and her stupid spies.”

“Would one of those spies happen to be Harper Caulfield?” Lilia asked, smirking. “I heard a rumor that somebody slipped something into her drink during gym class one day. Now she’s having a bit of a nose issue.” She eyed Rio.

“Don’t look at me,” she said. “I don’t even have gym with Harper. And we can’t be the only ones that find that bitch annoying.”

Lilia eyed Agatha, who shook her head. “Wasn’t me,” she said. “I’m not great with Potions.” Her eyes widened then, a blush spreading across her cheeks as she looked at Rio. Lilia didn’t miss the nearly imperceptible nod Rio gave her or the small smile that spread across Agatha’s lips.

They had some idea who might have done it, but neither one was about to admit that to a teacher, she knew, no matter how much they liked Lilia. So she let it go. She also had a pretty good idea who it was, though.

“You can use the room,” Lilia sighed. “Just make sure you clean up after yourselves and no funny business . I mean it, Agatha.”

“Why are you looking at me ?” Agatha huffed.

“You think I’m blind ?” Lilia snorted. “You think I haven’t seen Rio’s neck the last few weeks? She looks like she got attacked by a damn vampire !”
