“The severing of a trace?” Lorna asked. “Probably. I don’t want to lie to you about that. But it will likely be quick, non-lasting pain. Honestly, it’s more likely that you’ll feel much better afterwards. Relieved.”

Agatha nodded. She didn't doubt that for a single second. Still, it was scary.

“You too, Mr…” Lorna looked up at George.

“George,” he said. “Just George, please. Like Cher.”

“Good Goddess,” Lilia scoffed, rolling her eyes. George nudged her shoulder as he sat down on the ground next to her. The girls sat down next to their respective mothers, forming a circle around the pentagram. Agatha felt a wave of disappointment that Rio didn’t sit closer to her. She was now wedged in between Alice and Jen, who sat next to their own respective mothers.

Naomi placed the jade bowl with the crushed ingredients in the center of the pentagram. Lorna added the fresh vervain stalk, muttering something under her breath as she waved her hand over the bowl, which immediately ignited in a bright orange flame.

“Okay,” she said, looking around at the other faces in the circle, “we are ready to begin.”

Chapter End Notes

So, what did you think of the moms.

In my head, Niecy Nash plays Naomi Kale, if only because I absolutely adore that woman AND her wife.

Chapter 16: Incantations

Chapter Summary

The spell is cast.

Very short chapter, but the next one will be up shortly.

Chapter Notes

The spell is cast, how long it lasts, I cannot divine.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Sixteen

“Before we begin,” Lorna said, looking at Agatha, “did you bring the item you needed to bring?” 

Agatha nodded, reaching into her pocket for the baggie that contained her mother’s locket – a personal item from the person from whom she is trying to sever her connection. 

It was one of her mother’s favorite pieces of jewelry. It wasn’t an heirloom or anything; it was just a locket that she wore sometimes. But she’d had it for years, so it was personal enough for the spell as far as she was concerned. Agatha handed it over to Lorna, who opened the baggie and pulled the locket out by its chain. She held it over the flame in the center, dangling the locket over it for a second until the fire stretched out, flames licking at the locket, reaching for it, climbing up until it nearly brushed Lorna’s fingers. Lorna let go, allowing the locket to be fully engulfed by the orange flames. They sparked blue for a moment – the color of Evanora Harkness’s magic. 

“And the other bit?” Lorna asked. Agatha nodded, again, and pulled a single hair from her head, handing it over. Lorna took it with a nod and dangled it over the bowl, much like she’d done with the locket. The flames latched immediately, engulfing Agatha’s hair in less than two seconds, licking at Lorna’s fingers. Agatha gasped, and Lorna offered her a gentle smile. “It’s fine,” she said. “It’s my magic. It can’t hurt me.” 

Agatha nodded, but she was still nervous. Her palms were sweaty.

Lorna let the hair go, and the fire flashed purple for a second before changing to a deep indigo, representative of the bond between Agatha and Evanora. Agatha’s heart clenched in her chest. She swallowed thickly, taking a deep breath through her nose.

“We must all join hands as we begin,” Lorna instructed as the bowl continued to flicker in the center of the star. “The bond cannot be broken until the spell is complete.” She looked straight at Agatha. “If you feel pain or discomfort, that means that it’s working. Do not let go of anybody’s hands until the flame goes out. It’s very important.”

Agatha nodded, her pulse thrumming in her neck. Her heart was pounding in her chest. She wiped her sweaty palms off on her sweater before reaching for Alice’s hand on her right and Jen’s hand on her left. Their grips were tight on hers. Agatha looked at Alice, first, who nodded back to her, offering a gentle smile. She looked at Jen, who just offered her a nod with a firm stare. 

This was the closest any of them had ever been to each other in years. It felt…strange. But also oddly comforting.

Jen and Alice each took their mother’s hand. Lorna took Rio’s hand while Rio took her mother’s. Marisol reached for Lilia’s hand, and Lilia grasped George’s, who closed the circle by reaching for Naomi’s hand. When the circle of hands finally closed, the flaming bowl in the center pulsed, the fire growing a bit more for a second or two before going back to a more mild burn.

“This is not a super complicated spell,” Lorna said, “at least not in matters of incantation. We only need to repeat two short phrases. Since all of you girls have been studying Latin, I’m sure none of you should have an issue with this, right?” The girls all nodded, glancing at each other and the adults around them. “Good.” Lorna cleared her throat. “You just have to make sure that you speak clearly and firmly, okay? No mumbling. Keep your backs straight and channel all your magic into the center of the pentagram. Align your intentions.”

“What are our intentions?” Alice asked, looking up at her mother.

“To free Agatha,” Lorna replied, patiently. Alice nodded, straightening her back as she looked at the center of the circle. The rest followed suit.

The indigo flame grew slightly larger as all eyes focused on it, watching as it engulfed the ingredients in the bowl, as Evanora’s locket and Agatha’s hair changed the fire. Agatha’s pulse began to thrum and she felt an ache at the base of her spine. It was mild, but it was there.

“Now,” Lorna continued, “we must all repeat the same two phrases in unison, again and again until the first changes color.” She looked at Agatha. “What color is your magic?” she asked.

“Purple,” Agatha responded. Of all the teens in the circle, she was the only one whose magic didn’t match her mother’s. 

Was that why her mother hated her so?

“When the color changes to purple, we can stop,” Lorna said. “It will be a clear shift from the current color, unmistakable. Do not stop chanting until it happens, understood?”

Everybody around her nodded. 

“Okay,” Lorna said, squaring her shoulders and tightening her hold on Rio’s and Alice’s hands. “The first phrase is ‘ hoc vinculum separabis’ . Repeat it.”

“Hoc vinculum separabis,” they echoed. 

Sever this bond , Agatha’s mind translated. A dull ache shot up her spine. 

“The second one is ‘Restituat libertatum,’ ” Lorna added.

“Restituat libertatum,” the group echoed automatically.

Restore her freedom.

“Good,” Lorna said. “Now, we must repeat these phrases until the bond breaks completely. Keep your eyes on the bowl. Jen, Alice, keep a tight hold on Agatha’s hands. Do not let go until the fire is purple.” The girls nodded. “Okay. Let’s begin.”

“Hoc vinculum separabis,” she began.

“Hoc vinculum separabis,” they echoed.

“Resitituat libertatum,” she said.

“Resitituat libertatum,” they echoed.

“Hoc vinculum separabis,” they all said in unison.

There was a burning sensation at the base of Agatha’s spine. 

“Resitituat libertatum,” they chanted.

The burning sensation snaked up her back, wrapping over her shoulders, scorching a trail down her fingers, making her muscles seize. Without her permission, Agatha’s hands started to release their hold on the others’, but Jen and Alice just held on more tightly, almost painfully.

But Agatha’s entire body was in pain, anyway, so what was a little more.

They continued to chant, their voices perfectly in unison now, as Agatha struggled. She tried to join in, but the pain was too much, sending burning pain all over her body like she was being burned alive. She cried out, stomping her feet on the ground in front of her, but kept a tight hold on Jen and Alice, trying her damnedest not to break the circle. 

Agatha’s eyes were shut automatically in response to the pain, but she wrenched one open, glancing around the circle through her tears.

Rio was looking at her with concern etched in her brows, her own hold tight on her mother’s and Lorna’s hands. Agatha gave her the best smile that she could muster – it probably looked more like a grimace as another wave of pain shot through her. She nodded to her girlfriend in encouragement. Rio nodded back, straightening her back and tightening her grip on the two hands holding hers as she repeated the incantations more loudly. 

“Hoc vinculum separabis. Restituat libertatum.”

Then Agatha began to glow. 

Her hands in Jen and Alice’s emitted an electric blue light. It spread up her arms and over her chest, wrapping around Agatha’s entire body, the glow growing in intensity the more they chanted. As the glow outside Agatha’s body intensified, the burn coursing through her body diminished, and she felt like she could breathe more easily. Sweat dotted her brow as the pain left her body, but she was beginning to feel better.

Lighter.

She looked at the flaming bowl. The flames were still indigo, but she could see them beginning to flicker out. The group was still chanting, their words strong and clear, their voices increasing in volume. Agatha watched as the glow around her began to dissipate, leaving blue sparks in its wake before they, too, evaporated. The pain in her body was almost completely gone now, leaving just a dull ache in her back. She relaxed, releasing a labored breath. She closed her eyes for a long moment, just inhaling and exhaling for a long moment before she realized something:

It was quiet.

Nobody was speaking. Nobody was chanting .

She opened her eyes and the fire was a deep violet. 

 

Chapter End Notes

Give me some comments and the next chapter will be up in less than 24 hours.

Chapter 17: First Taste of Freedom

Chapter Summary

Another short chapter. Agatha starts to figure things out after finally being freed. A tiny bit of angst.

tw: panic attack

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Seventeen

“How do you feel?”

Agatha and Rio were sitting on the floor still, their backs against the wall in Lilia’s classroom as they watched Lorna and Naomi wipe up the star from the floor. Marisol had picked up the jade bowl and poured the contents into a baggie that Lilia held out for her, the latter plucking the still-intact locket from the ashes. A soft glow emanated from the locket now, subtle but there. Agatha wondered how it had survived.

“Different,” Agatha answered, laying her head down on Rio’s shoulders. “Kind of achy.”

“My mom can probably help with that,” Rio murmured against her temple, wrapping her arm around Agatha’s waist. “Her healing powers are way better than mine.” 

“It’s not that bad of an ache,” Agatha sighed, closing her eyes as she sank into Rio’s embrace. “It honestly feels way better than the alternative.”

“Do you think your mom knows yet?” Rio asked.

Agatha nodded. “If it affected her even half as much as it affected me, then I’m sure she’s well aware of what just happened.”

“You won’t have to worry about her anymore,” a voice said above them. Agatha opened her eyes to see Lorna Wu standing there in front of them. She offered Agatha a gentle smile and a hand to help her to her feet. Agatha missed Rio’s warmth the second that she left her embrace, but Rio was standing, too, not too long after her. Lorna turned Agatha’s hand so that it was facing up and placed the locket into it. “As long as you wear this,” she said, “your mother can’t come anywhere near you.”

“But couldn’t she track it?” Agatha asked. “I mean, it’s a personal item of hers.”

“Because of the severance spell we just did,” Lorna explained, “she no longer has ties to this locket, either. It is now an amulet that will protect you from her. So long as this is on your person, she cannot harm you.”

“Are you sure?” Agatha asked, hesitantly taking the locket that Lorna offered. 

“I am certain,” Lorna promised. “She won’t even be able to touch you. There’s a chance that she won’t even be able to see you, but I make no promises.” She placed her hands on Agatha’s shoulders and looked deep into her eyes. “You will be safe.”

Agatha nodded. “Thank you, Ms. Wu,” she said. “This means…so much.” She felt a lump form in her throat as her eyes welled with tears. Lorna pulled her into a hug, cradling the back of her head with her hand, her body rocking slightly in a way that was somehow incredibly comforting to Agatha. Agatha pressed her face into Lorna’s shoulder, trying to stem the tears that were pressing insistently against the corners of her eyes, begging to be released.

“Anytime, sweetie,” Lorna said, pulling back. She cupped Agatha’s cheeks in her hands, swiping a tear away with her thumb that Agatha hadn’t even known escaped. “Now, let’s talk about where you’ll be living in the coming months.”

“I already offered her the spare room at our place,” Naomi piped up. “She can stay as long as she needs to.”

“Alice and I set up the guest room at the house,” Lorna informed her. “If she wants options.” She looked to Agatha, who suddenly felt very overwhelmed.

“Oh, uh,” she stuttered, looking between the two women. “I don’t want to intrude. Besides, my friend, Billy, said that his parents might be willing to take me in. They’re foster parents, so–”

“You really wanna live with a teenage boy?” Naomi huffed. “Live with a couple of ladies! It will be so much fun.” She clapped her hands. “Of course, you can go wherever you wanna go, sweetheart. No pressure.”

Agatha looked between Naomi and Lorna, then to their daughters, who were standing a few feet away. “What do you two think?” she asked, addressing Jen and Alice. “I don’t want to intrude on either of you.” 

She was looking specifically at Jen. Their relationship was better, and she knew that Jen didn’t truly blame her anymore for what happened all those years ago (and what had happened since), but she still didn’t want to intrude if it was going to be uncomfortable for her.

Goddess , what had happened to her? A year ago, she would have delighted at making Jennifer Kale uncomfortable. Rio had softened her.

“Doesn’t matter either way to me,” Jen said, nonchalantly. “We’d have separate bathrooms. The spare room is literally on the other end of the house, so it’s no like I’d be bothered by your presence that much.” She eyed Rio. “Or the lurker’s, which I’m certain will become a semi-permanent fixture at the house now?”

“Stop calling her that,” Agatha growled, immediately feeling defensive. Then she sighed. “Alice?”

Alice shrugged. “I wouldn’t mind it at all,” she said. “It could be kind of fun, actually, to have somebody else around. Especially when Mom’s doing her shows and Jen’s not available to hang out. I mean, not that I expect you to always hang out with me. I’m not going to bother you about it or anything.” She cleared her throat. “You’d have your own bathroom at our house, as well, if that means anything to you. And the guest room has a queen-sized bed.”

“Sold,” Agatha said. She grimaced as she looked up at Naomi. “Sorry, Mrs. Kale. Thank you for your offer, though.”

“The invite still stands if you ever change your mind,” Naomi said, pulling Agatha into a tight squeeze. “And you are required to accompany Lorna and Alice to Sunday dinner this week. No excuses.”

“Sounds fair,” Agatha said, cracking the first smile since being freed. She looked down at her palm, in which the amulet still sat. 

It was one of her mother’s favorites, she knew. Or at least she wore it enough to matter to her. She felt some kind of bitter satisfaction knowing that she had taken it from her, that this piece of jewelry she often wore now belonged to Agatha, keeping Evanora from ever hurting her again. She slipped the chain over her head. The cameo at the end of the chain was made from cowry shell, etched with three familiar figures: Maiden, Mother, Crone. The three goddesses. The three stages in a woman’s life, supposedly. She had admired this cameo whenever her mother wore it. It went well with pretty much everything. She wondered if she’d ever get to possess it, maybe when her mother passed.

She had doubted it. And then she’d stolen it.

Because screw Evanora Harkness.

Agatha tucked the amulet beneath her sweater and patted it, allowing it to ground her, before smiling up at the two women before her. Lorna and Naomi were two women she’d known since childhood, almost as long as she’d known her mother’s church friends, but they’d always been much nicer to her, even when Agatha felt that she didn’t exactly deserve their kindness. Naomi had never said a bad word about her as far as she could tell. Neither had Lorna.

They were always there, just waiting for her to ask for their help and more than willing to give it to her. They were exactly what good mothers were supposed to be, and Agatha felt regret that it took her so long to see that.

“Alright, girls!” Lilia said, clapping her hands. “It’s time to get to rehearsal. George wants to start blocking your scenes, and he tells me that Rio still has a lot of work to do on her dance.”

Rio groaned behind her, pressing her face to Agatha’s back, and Agatha bit her cheek to keep from laughing. Rio wrapped her arms around Agatha’s waist, and Agatha patted her hands. 

“Come on,” she said. “Let’s go.”

“Don’t wanna,” Rio moaned, her hold tightening.

“Well, I have to go,” Agatha laughed. “I’m literally the star of the show.”

“ Co- star,” Jen corrected from across the room, grabbing her things.

“Nobody sings ‘Popular’ at karaoke, Jenny,” Agatha shot back with a fake sweet smile. “Not nearly to the level of ‘Defying Gravity’ anyway.” 

Jen waited until neither her mother nor Lorna was looking before she flipped Agatha off before walking out the door. Agatha rolled her eyes, smirking.

“Come on,” she said, turning her head to look at Rio, “let’s go before George decides that he actually wants to torture you.” She smiled at Lorna. “Thank you so much for all your help,” she said, glancing at Naomi. “Both of you. It…it means so much to me.” Her voice broke in that moment, tears once again leaking from her eyes without her permission. She swiped them away with her fingers. “Sorry,” she said. “Sorry.” She sniffled.

“Don’t apologize,” Naomi said, placing a comforting hand on her shoulder. “Nothing wrong with a good cry. You’ve had a stressful day. Hell, you’ve had a stressful life . You gotta let yourself feel it, or it’s gonna all build up and make you explode one day. If you need a moment, I’m sure Lilia won’t mind waiting just a little bit longer.” She looked toward the drama teacher, who was all but tapping her foot. Naomi narrowed her eyes, warningly. “Isn’t that right, Miss Calderu ?”

“Of course not,” Lilia said. “Just…don’t take too long, okay? I’ll be downstairs.” She was out of the room before anybody could even blink.

“I don’t think I’ve ever seen her move that fast,” Agatha said. 

“Nobody fucks with the Kales,” Naomi huffed, grinning. She pressed a kiss to Agatha’s cheek. “Be safe,” she said. Agatha nodded, offering her a grateful smile. 

“I’ll pick you girls up when rehearsal is over,” Lorna said. “Wait for me inside, okay?”

Agatha nodded, and Lorna squeezed her arm before following Naomi to the door, the two women striking up a conversation like teenage girls, laughing with each other as they walked. 

Agatha wondered if she’d have something like that when she was older, if she’d have friends that she could laugh with. She didn’t have much in the way of friends before because her mother had commanded most of the time she didn’t spend at school and controlled whom she was able to talk to. And the girls from bible study were not exactly the kind of people Agatha wanted to associate with. But now…now she would be living in the same house as Alice. Now, maybe she could try for an actual friendship with her. And maybe even with Jen.

Maybe…

“You should come over for dinner,” a voice said, breaking Agatha from her thoughts. She blinked and suddenly Mrs. Vidal was standing in front of her. “Sometime this week, si? I’ll make something tasty!”

Agatha blinked at her, shaking away the fog that seemed to fill her head. She offered Marisol a smile and a nod. “That sounds great!” she said. “Those pasteles Rio brought were so good. I’m eager to try some more food.”

“Ooh, I like her,” Marisol said, reaching for Agatha’s hand and pulling her against her side, away from Rio. “I’ll make so much food you’ll be eating leftovers for a week, mi amor .” She laid a big, smacking kiss on Agatha’s cheek. Agatha flushed.

“Mami,” Rio practically moaned, “stop stealing my girlfriend from me.” She tugged on Agatha’s hand, pulling her back into her arms. “We gotta get to practice. I’ll see you later, okay?” She pressed a kiss to Marisol’s cheek. “You know how to get out of here?”

“Of course,” Marisol said. “I’ve been here many, many times for your parent-teacher conferences. I’ll be fine. You go and do your little dance.” She pulled Rio in for a kiss square to the center of her forehead, leaving a mark. “ Sé buena. ”

“ Siempre ,” Rio retorted, grinning at Marisol’s scoff as she tugged Agatha out of the room. Agatha waved to Marisol as Rio dragged her into the hallway.

Halfway down the hall, Agatha suddenly pulled her hand out of Rio’s, causing the other girl to turn and look at her. Agatha avoided Rio’s gaze, her eyes looking all around them, everywhere but at Rio.

“What’s wrong?” Rio asked.

“N-nothing,” Agatha said. “I just…somebody might see.”

“So?” Rio asked, raising one eyebrow as she turned fully to Agatha, stopping their momentum just as they reached the top of the steps. “You’re free now, Agatha; you don’t have to worry about your mother anymore.”

“I know,” Agatha said, still looking around the hall, which was empty. It was nearly three-thirty now. Anybody still in the school was in whatever after-school activity they took part in, far away from this hallway. There was literally an auditorium of people waiting right downstairs for them.

But what if Harper and her cronies were among them today, for whatever reason? What if they went down the stairs and she was there, waiting with a camera? What if she immediately told Agatha’s mother? What if Evanora showed up at the school?

Suddenly, the air was too thin and Agatha couldn’t breathe. Rio knew immediately that something was wrong. She reached for Agatha, hands on her face as she tried to ground her in reality, but the world was still spinning around her.

“Agatha,” Rio said. “Agatha, breathe.” She felt Rio’s hand leave her cheek and start rubbing up and down her spine. Like magic, air suddenly filled her lungs, but it wasn’t enough. Her head was still murky. She closed her eyes tightly and felt herself get lowered to the ground. She felt Rio’s warmth around her, felt fingers in her hair and a separate hand continuing to rub up and down her back. She felt lips on her temple. She heard Rio’s soothing words, but the world refused to stop spinning.

Rio wrapped her in a tight hug, holding Agatha against her shoulder as she continued to talk her down from a panic attack. Because that was what this was, wasn’t it? A panic attack. Why did she suddenly have them so often? What was wrong with her?

“Nothing is wrong with you,” Rio insisted against the shell of her ear. 

Shit. Had Agatha said that out loud?

“You are completely fine,” Rio continued. “You’re okay. You’re safe. You’re free. She can’t hurt you anymore. Nobody can hurt you. I won’t let them.”

Agatha whimpered, turning to press her face into the crook of Rio’s neck. She breathed in Rio’s earthy scent, keeping her arms wrapped tightly around the other girl as she came back to herself. Soon enough, the world came back into focus. Everything was sharper, clearer. She could breathe better. She could hear the words that Rio was whispering in her ear. It was the same phrase over and over and over again.

“ Estoy aquí para ti, mi amor ,” she whispered. “ Te quiero mucho. Estoy aquí. ”

Te quiero mucho.

The literal translation of that phrase, Agatha knew, was ‘I want you very much’, but that wasn’t how it was used in Spanish-speaking countries.

Te quiero mucho .

In their Spanish class, they had learned that it had a much deeper meaning. It was used to express love and affection to those one felt closest to. Love and affection.

Love . 

Rio had just told Agatha that she loved her for the first time. 

Maybe.

Maybe she didn’t mean it that way. Maybe she just meant it as a way to get Agatha to calm down, to relax, to come down from her panic. Maybe she was just mindlessly saying phrases that her own mother had used to help Rio through hard times. Maybe. Maybe. Maybe.

Agatha’s heart rate picked up again, but she was no longer panicking. Her face was flaming as she continued to press it into Rio’s neck, unable to look the other girl in the eyes as she attempted to figure out what to do about this. This was a declaration of love, after all. Should she just ignore it? Should she say it back? What should she do?

“You okay?” Rio whispered in her ear, still rubbing her back. “You’re not shaking anymore.”

Agatha hadn’t even realized she’d been shaking in the first place. 

She pulled back from Rio’s embrace, looking at her face, but not exactly meeting her eyes and praying Rio didn’t notice.

“Yeah,” she said. “I think I’m okay. Just…shaken.” She took a deep breath, relieved that she was finally able to get enough air into her lungs. “I just…I’m not used to this. PDA, I mean. It’s…it was different when we were just friends, when I was dragging you down the sidewalk back to the school. It was easier to ignore feelings then, to play it off as just being friends. I mean, I kinda always knew we weren’t ever really just friends, but still. You know?” She cleared her throat, pushing herself to her feet then reaching out to help Rio up. “I spent the majority of my life hiding who I am from my mother. As much as I want to feel completely free and happy that I’m out from under her control…some part of me is still terrified that she’s going to come after me, that she’s going to somehow have some kind of say in what I do or who I associate with. Like she’ll still be able to keep me from seeing you.” She swallowed thickly as she finally locked eyes with Rio, whose brows were furrowed. “It might take a while to feel fully comfortable holding your hand and kissing you in public, but I’m going to make every effort to do so. I promise.”

She squeezed Rio’s hand quickly before letting go.

Rio nodded, tilting her head as she offered her a soft smile. 

“Take your time,” she said. “I’ll be here.”

Agatha returned the smile and rolled her eyes affectionately. “See,” she said, “when you say things like that , it’s actually kind of hard to resist kissing you.” She glanced up and down the hallway, checking for anybody that might be spying on them. When she found nobody, she quickly leaned in, pressing her lips firmly against Rio’s before pulling back with a shy smile. Rio’s cheeks bloomed pink – more pink than the actual first time they had kissed in the auditorium.

It was adorable.

Agatha smiled at her and made her way to the stairs. “You coming?” she asked, looking over her shoulder as she descended. “George is waiting.”

Rio let out a long groan that echoed through the stairwell. “Why’d you have to ruin the cute moment we just had!” she whined. “Now I gotta think about that old man. Ugh!” 

She followed after Agatha as the latter laughed, shaking her head.

Chapter End Notes

I hope y'all liked this one. There will be some time jumps starting in the next chapter. We haven't seen the last of Evanora, unfortunately, either.

Chapter 18: Might As Well

Chapter Summary

A little rehearsal and a little bitch

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Eighteen

George Whatever-His-Last-Name-Was was a complete sociopath, Rio decided. He enjoyed torturing poor, defenseless children with the art of dance. He enjoyed turning their legs into jelly and making them perform for him. He was a sick, sick individual.

“Oh, don’t be so dramatic,” Jen Kale huffed, sitting on the stage next to Rio’s prone body as the girl stared, unblinkingly, up at the rafters. She swore she couldn’t feel her legs. Her toes could have fallen off and she wouldn’t even know it. Hell, did she even still have feet ? 

She twisted her ankle and grimaced. Yeah, she still had feet. They hurt like hell.

“Bite me, Kale,” Rio grunted, glaring sideways at her, unable to even turn her head to see her.

“No thanks,” Jen said. “You probably taste bitter and salty as hell.”

Rio didn’t even have the energy to flip her off, but it’s the thought that counts, isn’t it?

“Need more drops?” Jen asked, leaning over Rio’s face to look her in the eyes, one of her brows raised.

“I have some left of that vial you gave me,” Rio informed her. “It’s in my right pocket.”

“I’m not reaching into your pocket, Lurk–er, Rio,” Jen said. “You’re gonna have to do that on your own.”

“But my arms feel like gelatin,” Rio groaned, tossing her arms up as if to demonstrate. One of her hands slapped her in the face. “You see? You think I meant to do that? Come on, Jen!”

“Get Agatha to do it,” Jen huffed. She looked around. “Where is Miss “Star of the Show” anyway?” George was working with Ginette (the Wizard) on her movement for “I Am a Sentimental Man” but Agatha wasn’t anywhere in view. “Agatha?”

“She’s in the chorus room with Alice,” a voice called from the audience. Jen turned to see Billy and Sonny playing some kind of card game in the aisle. 

“Thanks, Bonny,” she said.

“You know that’s not my name!” Billy complained.

“It’s your ship name!” Jen retorted. “Billy and Sonny. Bonny . Adorable!”

“I have a boyfriend!”

“Gross!”

They spoke at the same time, their cheeks flaming. Jen just snickered, turning back to Rio, who was giving her a pitiful look. She rolled her eyes.

“Fine,” Jen huffed, reaching into Rio’s pocket and retrieving the elixir that she’d given Rio not too long ago. “Where does it hurt?” she asked, pulling out the dropper. 

Once Rio could fully control her body again, she and Jen made their way to the chorus room. George had finished with Rio for the day (thank goddess ), but she’d still felt the need to sneak out of the room, lest he decide he needed her for something else.

Agatha was standing on the risers like they were her stage as she sang “Defying Gravity”, belting the song out like her life depended on it.

“What the hell?” Jen said, as the door shut behind them, “you’re doing this song without me ? I’m in this number, too, you know!”

“Shut it, Kale,” Agatha huffed, wiping sweat off her brow. “This isn’t about you. This is about me trying to hit the right note.” She cleared her throat.

“You’re doing just fine,” Alice assured her. “Don’t think too hard about it.”

“I need to get the note,” Agatha repeated. “Or else what is this all for?” She squared her shoulders. “One more time.”

Jen and Rio sat on the counters by the windows as they watched and listened to Agatha perform. Rio had always been blown away by how captivating Agatha was when she sang. She commanded a room, filling it with her presence and drawing in the audience like a Venus flytrap. Her blue eyes captured souls and held them in her gaze as her voice serenaded them like a siren. She must have been part-siren, Rio had decided the first time she watched one of Agatha’s musical rehearsals in their freshman year.

She had been working on scenery that day. She wasn’t yet the stage manager, but she already had more expertise than most of the seniors or juniors in how to use the power tools. She was just painting that day, though, listening to the performers as they worked with the old music director – a teacher who had since left the school – on their solos. 

When Agatha stepped up to the piano, though, Rio had stopped painting and turned all her attention on the other girl, her body going warm at the sight of Agatha with her purple binder in her hands, barely glancing at the music as she sang her lines with the utmost confidence.

As a freshman, Agatha had been a bit pimply with early puberty. She had some baby fat softening her face and midsection, her movements a little awkward as she got used to a recent growth spurt, but her voice…Rio still felt chills go down her spine when she remembered the first time she’d heard Agatha’s singing voice all on its own. 

She hadn’t had a huge role as a freshman, but it was big enough that when she sang her solo on opening night, she’d brought nearly every theatre-goer to their feet in thunderous applause. Rio still remembered the way Agatha had flushed under her stage makeup, holding her position as she waited out the applause, breathing heavily as the last note hung in the air.

The local paper had written about the performance the following Monday, giving Agatha her well-deserved flowers, jokingly telling Broadway to come get their newest star. Lilia had cut that article out of her paper and taped it to her wall, next to dozens of other complimentary local theater reviews of their shows, and highlighted Agatha’s name in it. 

It was still on the wall in her classroom.

“So if you care to find me,” Agatha sang, placing her hand over her diaphragm, like Lilia had shown them all those years ago, “look to the Western sky. As someone told me lately, everyone deserves the chance to fly!” She took a breath after that, coughing a little. “Dammit!” she cursed, stomping her foot. “I keep taking the wrong breath. I should know when to breathe by now!”

“Don’t be too hard on yourself,” Alice said. “Just try again. We’ll keep trying until you get it…or until my mom picks us up. Whichever comes first.”

“She probably will,” Agatha grunted, shaking her head. “Why can’t I get this? I’m usually so good with this kind of thing.”

“It’s been a long day,” Rio suggested. “Maybe table this for later? When you’re less stressed. Why don’t you work on your monologue for Juilliard?”

“Ooh, I could also use some practice on mine,” Jen said, nodding. “Are you going for classical or more modern for yours?”

“I…have no idea,” Agatha admitted. “I haven’t even thought about it yet.”

“Girl, the auditions are on Saturday,” Jen said. “You better start thinking.”

“Yeah,” Agatha said. “But, um, all my monologues are packed up right now.” She motioned to her backpack, where Lilia’s magic bag was still packed away. “I really don’t want to unpack everything right here.”

“That’s cool,” Jen said. “Lilia has a bunch of monologues right here.” She went to a filing cabinet and opened a drawer, pulling out a few packets of paper. “We’ve got some Tennessee Williams, some Oscar Wilde, some Arthur Miller…what’s your poison?”

“Let me see…” Agatha said, walking over to look through the packets.

Rio and Alice watched them, smiling affectionately at their girlfriends.

“So,” Alice said, “do you wanna work a little on your solo?”

“Not a chance,” Rio huffed. “My entire body is aching from the dancing I just had to do. Let me rest for a little bit.”

“Fair,” Alice laughed. “Wanna come over tonight? I’m sure my mom won’t mind. I’m pretty sure she’s hiring a caterer for Agatha’s first night with us.”

“Seriously?” Rio asked, looking down at her. Alice looked dead serious. “Like, forreal?”

“You’ve met my mom before, haven’t you?” Alice snorted. “She is the most welcoming person ever. It’s almost annoying. But it’s sweet. She loves having company over – especially my friends. And I don’t have many friends.”

“Ugh, my mom is the same way ,” Rio groaned. “‘ Mija, when are your little friends coming over for dinner? ’” She rolled her eyes.

“It’s creepy how well you can imitate your mom’s voice,” Alice said. 

“I’ve had nearly eighteen years of practice,” Rio replied with a grin. 

“It’s unnerving.”

“Aww, thanks.” 

“This one looks good,” Agatha said, looking at a sheet of paper. “Short, simple, but it looks like it has a lot of range. You think Lilia will let me take it?”

“Make a copy,” Jen said. “I’m sure she won’t care.”

Agatha nodded, holding the sheet in front of her, focusing all of her attention on it, and then pulling her hands apart, which made a perfect copy of the monologue she’d picked out. Jen’s eyes widened.

“Where did you learn that?” she asked.

“Internet,” Agatha replied. “It’s a fairly simple spell; I’ll send you the link.”

“You better,” Jen said, placing all the papers back into the drawer and closing it. She opened her mouth to say something else, but before she could the door to the chorus room burst open and Sonny burst in, their eyes wide and wild. 

“What’s up?” Alice asked, immediately getting up from her seat.

“Um,” Sonny said, looking around the room, their eyes ultimately landing on Agatha, “something’s going down. We’re all supposed to go to the auditorium for lockdown.”

“Lockdown?” Jen asked. “Is there…is there a…?” She didn’t want to say it, the thought seizing her with fear.

“I don’t think so,” Sonny said, answering her unfinished question. “Lilia and George just want us in the auditorium. Especially Agatha.”

“Me?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow. “Why would they want…me?” The realization hit her before she even finished her sentence. “Oh.” Cold spread to every single inch of her body, icy and suffocating. “She’s here, isn’t she?”

“I think so,” Sonny said. “My grammy told me about her. I’m so sorry.”

“It’s whatever,” Agatha huffed, grabbing her bag and tucking her monologue into it. “Let’s just go.” 

She started to walk toward the door, but Rio reached out, taking her hand, squeezing her fingers. Agatha clenched her teeth, but not in anger, as she looked at her. 

“You’re not alone,” Rio whispered. “We’re here with you. We’re going with you. She can’t even touch you, okay?” 

Agatha nodded, forcing a tiny, brief smile. Inside, her insides felt tight and her lungs didn’t feel as though they were producing enough oxygen to keep her standing. On the outside, though, Rio Vidal was holding her hand and maybe that was enough for right now.

Then she felt another hand slip into hers on the other side and she turned, her eyes wide when she saw Jen Kale looking down at her, eyes hard as iron, jaw clenched. She said nothing, but she squeezed Agatha’s hand just as tightly as Rio was.

Agatha felt a tear slip down her cheeks, but she didn’t let go of either girl’s hand to wipe it away. Instead, she held on more tightly.

Alice came up next to Jen, holding her hand and offering a gentle smile to Agatha. Sonny took Rio’s hand, joining in on their little parade, and they all five stepped out into the hall.

There were lights flashing on the walls, the silent alarm going off, indicating a lockdown drill. This wasn’t a drill, though. Agatha’s fingers clenched around Rio’s and Jen’s hands. They squeezed back, their eyes facing forward as they made their way down the short hall to the auditorium’s back door. Lilia met them there, by the dressing room, ringing her hands.

“There you are!” she said, breathing a sigh of relief. “Thank Goddess ! I thought you had left ! Your mother is here.”

“Is she in the building?” Agatha asked, icy fear climbing up her spine.

“No, thankfully,” Lilia said, “but she’s projecting .”

Agatha groaned, rolling her eyes. She knew exactly what that meant. Her mother had done that particular trick a few times in Agatha’s youth. Agatha was certain that she only used it when she wanted to utterly embarrass Agatha in front of anybody who could possibly be her friend.

She was surprised it took finally dissolving the trace Evanora had on her for her to finally do it at the high school.

She honestly should have expected this.

Agatha let go of Jen and Rio’s hands and followed Lilia out into the auditorium, fighting the fear that seized her heart in her chest when she heard her mother’s voice demanding to know where her child was.

She almost refused to walk any further. 

But then she felt Rio at her back, felt Rio’s hands on her hips, heard her soothing whispers in her ear.

“Don’t be afraid. I’m right here. I’ve got you. You’re not alone.” 

Agatha nodded, forcing her feet to keep moving forward, past the curtains, until she was standing at the front of the stage, looking up at her own mother’s disembodied head glaring down at her. The second Agatha appeared, Evanora’s eyes zeroed in on her.

“There you are!” she barked. “What the hell is going on here, Agatha Harkness!? What have you done ?”

“I don’t know what you mean,” Agatha replied, coolly, hiding her shaking hands in the pockets of her jeans. 

“Don’t you play dumb, Agatha!” Evanora growled. “You’ve done something to your trace! You’ve blocked me from seeing you!”

“What trace?” Agatha asked. “There is no trace.”

“What are you talking about?” Evanora huffed. “You’re only seventeen! There’s meant to be a trace on you until you’re eighteen years old! It’s the law !”

“There’s actually no law that states that,” Lilia supplied, stepping up next to Agatha.

“Of course there is!”

“Actually, no,” another voice said. Agatha’s eyes widened at the sight of Principal Davis standing in the aisle of the audience. “The trace was meant as a protective measure. It was meant for parents to keep an eye on their child and possibly even locate them if they were lost or kidnapped. It was never meant to control a near-adult. Children and teens can have a trace on them until they’re eighteen, but it isn’t required, per se. And, in this case, I’m certain that a trace on Agatha would do more harm than good.”

“Who are you to make that decision?!” Evanora roared, her head doubling in size, turning red with her anger. 

Principal Davis didn’t even flinch. “It wasn’t my decision to make,” she said, simply. “I wasn’t even involved in the spell that broke the trace, but I do fully support it. And I support Agatha’s decision in breaking it. You and I both know, Mrs. Harkness, that it was in Agatha’s best interest to free herself from…the trace.”

“You know absolutely nothing ,” Evanora hissed. “Agatha belongs to me until her eighteenth birthday, which is over a month away! She had no right to–”

“I belong to no one!”

Evanora’s head turned slowly, her eyes finding Agatha, who was standing at the very cliff’s edge of the stage, staring up at her, defiantly.

“What did you say to me, young lady?” she demanded, and Agatha could imagine her crossing her arms over her chest wherever she physically was right at that moment. But she didn’t cower under her mothers glare.

“I said ,” Agatha said, “that I belong to no one. No one but myself . You never owned me. I was your daughter. You were not meant to control me. You were meant to protect me. And you failed .”

“You watch the way you speak to–”

“Or what ?” Agatha huffed, tears stinging her eyes as her fists clenched at her sides. “You’ve already caused me so much pain! Why do you even care if the trace is broken? Now at least you don’t have to concern yourself with me. It’s not like you ever really did! You can just tell all your friends that you have an ungrateful, evil child who would rather be homeless than be good! You can get their sympathy! Isn’t that better than any part of a child you hate?”

“I–you–I–” Evanora stuttered, her eyes wide as the spell flickered.

“You don’t want me,” Agatha said. “You don’t love me. That much has always been obvious. Just leave me alone. Let me be happy and you can be happy without me. Go have another child or adopt Harper or something. Don’t pretend like you care about me.”

“No!” Evanora roared. “You are mine ! You belong to me ! You cannot do this!”

Agatha felt her resolve starting to crumble. “What difference does it make?” she asked, genuinely exhausted. “Why do you care so much? Like I said, you never loved me. I don’t even know why you had me in the first place. Did you even want a child?”

“Of course I did!” Evanora huffed. “I’ve always wanted children!”

“Then why did you treat me like shit ?!” Agatha demanded, which seemed to take her mother by surprise. “You acted like I somehow ruined your life! Like my birth did something so horrible to you! Why ?!” Her hands started to glow purple at her sides, her anger and anguish filling her with fire. “I’ve seen the way your friends treat their children! They love them! They treat them with respect and kindness and affection! Why are you unable to give me even a fraction of that? You’ve never even hugged me! Not even when I was a little kid, when I still wanted your hugs! WHY? ”

Evanora pressed her lips together, stubbornly, just staring down at Agatha with a deep frown. Agatha gritted her teeth and shook her head.

“You are not my mother,” she said. “And you are never coming near me again. This is over.”

“Oh, little girl,” Evanora retorted, her voice low and even, “this is far from over.”

The head began to grow, but Agatha lifted her hands and sent a blast at it, forcing a large part of it to dissipate. Evanora let out a shocked gasp.

“How dare–”

A green blast hit her head next as Rio stepped up right next to Agatha and more of the head dissipated.

“Who the hell–”

A pink blast hit next as Jen stepped up, grinning. “I’ve been wanting to do that for years !” she exclaimed, snickering.

“You little dy–”

An orange blast, then a yellow one hit Evanora’s floating head. It was almost completely gone.

“This isn’t ov–”

One last purple blast had the floating head vanishing into thin air. Agatha felt the magic tingling in her fingers, and it felt so good. But she also couldn’t stop shaking. Her entire body was practically vibrating as she tried desperately to calm herself down.

“Hey,” Rio said, wrapping one arm around her waist and pulling Agatha against her side. “Hey, it’s okay. Just breathe.” Agatha pressed her face into Rio’s shoulders. 

She could feel the eyes of everybody in the auditorium around her, watching her, watching as she embraced Rio, as Rio pressed kisses to her temples and her hair, as Rio held her and whispered into her ear. But she didn’t care, for once, who saw this. 

Because it really didn’t matter anymore.

“She’s never going to stop,” Agatha murmured. “The trace is gone, but she’s not going to stop coming after me.”

“We’ll make her stop,” Jen said, placing a hand on Agatha’s shoulder, squeezing it. “Lorna and Alice aren’t going to let anything happen to you while you’re at their house. That place is a literal fortress. Evanora won’t be able to get anywhere near you. Especially with that little amulet you’ve got there.”

“Yeah,” Alice said. “My mom’s magic is pretty strong. And it can get really lethal when it needs to be. You’re in good hands, I swear.”

Agatha nodded, offering her a shaky smile as Alice stepped into her line of vision, placing her hands on Agatha’s shoulders.

“We’ve got you, Agatha,” she said. “Not just me and my mom. Not just me and Jen and Rio. Everybody in this room has you.” She motioned toward the audience, where several of her classmates had stood up, offering their support in the form of nods and serious looks and hearts they made with their hands over their chests. Agatha felt more tears begin to fall from her eyes at the sight of them all. She left Rio’s embrace, surging forward to wrap her arms around Alice, holding the shorter girl as tightly as she dared.

Alice hugged her back just as tightly.

“She’s not going to come anywhere near you,” Alice swore. “Not if I can help it.”

Agatha snorted. “Alice, you’re, like, two feet tall.”

“But I know how to cast a gnarly hex,” Alice retorted. “Protection magic isn’t all sunshine and rainbows, you know. We have fire magic.”

Agatha snorted again, rolling her eyes, holding her more tightly.

“Thank you,” she said.

“Anytime,” Alice replied, sincerely.

When she pulled back, she plucked her phone out of her pocket, her eyes widening. “Hmm,” she said, “my mom is here. She and Naomi just kicked your mom’s ass.”

“Seriously?” Agatha asked, eyes wide.

“That’s so hot,” Rio added

Jen elbowed her. “Shut up!”

“Not really,” Alice snorted. “But they did threaten her within an inch of her life. My mom even mentioned that my dad is a cop. They may not be together anymore, but he would do anything for her.”

“Because your mom’s a MIL–mfph!” Rio grunted, glaring at Jen, who had slapped a hand over her mouth.

“Keep talking about my future mother-in-law like that and see what happens,” Jen growled at her. Rio rolled her eyes, shoving the taller girl away. 

“Whatever,” she said. “You all know I’m right. Can we go now?” She looked toward Principal Davis. “Is the lockdown lifted?”

“I have to make another check, but if Mrs. Harkness is really gone, I don’t see why not. Hold on.” She pulled out her cellphone and made a call.

“Mom said your mother ‘ran away like a little bitch’,” Alice told Agatha. “Her exact words.”

“Did she film it?” Agatha asked, a little too excitedly.

Alice snorted. “I don’t think so,” she said. “But maybe she will film the day she finally kicks the crap out of that lady.”

“Fingers crossed,” Jen said.

“Okay,” Principal Davis said. “The threat is gone. You are all free to leave – if Miss Calderu says you can, that is.” She looked to Lilia.

“Yes,” Lilia said. “Everybody get home safely. Sharon, you and I need to have a drink. George, you too!”

George was sitting in the audience with the rest of the student body. “If you insist,” he said with a sigh.

“Agatha, you stay close to Alice and Lorna for the foreseeable future,” Lilia said. “If I ever see that excuse of a woman out in public, though, I’m going to make her wish she were dead.”

“Please film it,” Rio piped in before Agatha could encourage her.

“I might be too busy breaking my hands against her face,” Lilia retorted, “but I’ll do my best.”

“Do not encourage violence, Miss Calderu!” Principal Davis pleaded.

“I’m not encouraging them to kick Evanora Harkness’s ass,” Lilia shot back. “I’m simply stating that I am going to do it.”

“I didn’t hear that,” Principal Davis said, walking toward the door. “Come along, Sonny. I’ll give you a ride home.”

“Coming, Grammy,” Sonny said. “Stay safe, Agatha.” They gave her a tiny salute as they grabbed their bag and followed their grandmother out of the auditorium.

Agatha waved at them, weakly, suddenly feeling completely drained.

“Ready to go?” Alice asked, placing her hand on Agatha’s shoulder. Agatha nodded. “Cool. Jen and Rio are coming, too, if that’s cool. Unless you need to rest?”

“Rio’s cool,” Agatha said, already reaching for said girl’s arm.

“Just Rio?” Alice asked, raising an eyebrow.

“It’s not my house, so I can’t exactly bar you from having Kale over,” Agatha huffed, stepping down from the stage with Rio.

“And after I just helped you get rid of your mother,” Jen said, scowling after her. “Rude.”

“Jen’s okay, I guess,” Agatha said coolly, sinking against Rio’s shoulder as they walked toward the back door. Other people were staring at her and a few whispered, but there were also some whistles and cheers and too many people exchanging money. 

She glared at those people.

But she didn’t step away from Rio for even a second. She was too tired to pretend that she wasn’t completely head-over-heels in love with the girl at her side. Besides, no matter what she did, her mother was going to try to make her life a living hell.

Might as well be gay.

Chapter End Notes

Yeah, this STILL isn't the last we're gonna see of Evanora. Bitch is relentless, but at least Agatha's got backup.

Chapter 19: A Feast

Chapter Summary

Agatha finally sees Alice's home, which is MASSIVE. Alice is a rich girl, of course, but she and Lorna do everything they can to make Agatha feel welcome.

Chapter Notes

The story is going a little bit slowly, I know, but it's about to start speeding up with some time jumps. I feel as though I've said that before but this time is serious.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Nineteen

Agatha would never admit it out loud, but Jennifer Kale had been right: the Wu household was a fortress.

The front gates emanated a soft orange glow, which only lifted as Lorna’s SUV approached, making just enough space for the car itself to fit through. The gates themselves looked nearly indestructible, made of iron and embedded with several gemstones and runes all along their bars. The driveway was long and winding, lined with gravel and tall trees that gave the appearance of driving through a thick forest.

At the end of the driveway was what had to be one of the largest houses in Westview. Rio let out a low whistle as Lorna parked her car next to a three-car garage just a few steps away from the massive front door.

“Are you sure we’re not in Oz?” Agatha asked Alice, “About to meet the Wizard?”

“You’ve been to my house before,” Alice snorted, rolling her eyes as her mother laughed. 

“I don’t think I really understood that this was where you actually lived ,” Agatha admitted. “I just assumed that your mother rented the place for parties. But you actually live here?”

“It’s not as big on the inside,” Alice said, opening her door to hop out onto the gravel driveway. “A large part of it is also a recording studio for my mom.”

“ Still ,” Agatha said, climbing out before Rio, then offering her hand to the other girl, who gave her a kiss on the cheek in thanks. Agatha flushed, squeezing her hand. She immediately lost her train of thought.

She regained it as Lorna unlocked the massive door, using magic to push it open. The foyer was bigger than Agatha’s entire house.

“Not that big, huh?” Rio huffed, stepping in beside her. “I could fit three of my houses in this one room alone.”

“This is what happens when three of your albums go double platinum, ladies,” Lorna said, unapologetically. “Agatha, dear, let me show you to your room and we can start unpacking.” She motioned for Agatha to follow her. 

All four girls followed. Jen, who had been there so many times it might as well have been her second home, was silent as they walked, her arm slung around Alice’s shoulder. Agatha and Rio gaped as they walked up the marble staircase to the second floor.

“I know it looks rather large,” Lorna said, “and it is,” she admitted, “but your room will be cozy. Trust me. And you’re more than welcome to have your,” she eyed Rio, “ friend stay over whenever you’d like so long as you get her mother’s approval.” Agatha and Rio blushed bright red. Jen snickered, receiving an elbow to the ribs from Rio. “And you are also allowed to stay over at her house,” Lorna added, “provided I’m allowed to add a protection spell there to keep you safe from her .”

“My mom probably wouldn’t have a problem with that,” Rio informed her. “Though she’d probably mourn the chance to kick Agatha’s mom’s ass with her own bare hands.”

“Honey, we all would,” Lorna said. “That woman is foul. But I grew up in the 60’s; I’m a lover, not a fighter…just so long as you don’t mess with my kids.”

That caused Agatha to pause, falling behind everybody except for Rio, who was still holding onto her. She gave Agatha a look of concern, but she didn’t speak. Eventually, the others realized that Agatha and Rio were not with them, several feet down the hall. 

Alice was the first to turn around.

“Agatha?” she asked. “You okay?”

“Y-yeah,” Agatha said, looking down at her feet as her face began to flame. Lorna and Jen also looked back at her, and she suddenly felt microscopic. “I’m fine.” She cleared her throat and kept walking, feeling Rio’s arm wrap around her waist.

Lorna sent her a knowing look, her lips quirking up in a barely-there grin before she turned forward again. “Ah,” she said, “here it is: third door on the left.” She stopped at a door the color of amethyst (most of the doors were of different colors, like a rainbow up and down the hall) and smiled down at Agatha. “Allie tells me that you’re a fan of this color,” she said. 

“Allie?” Rio snorted, looking at Alice, who blushed. Kale pinched Rio’s side. Hard . “Ouch!” Rio slapped her hand away. Jen acted oblivious. 

Agatha rolled her eyes at all of them. “Yes,” she said. “Purple is my favorite color; even my magic is purple.”

“You have a strong connection to that color,” Lorna said. “Perfect.” She opened the door to the bedroom, stepping aside to let Agatha enter first. “You’re really going to love this room then.”

Agatha offered her a thankful smile as she stepped past her, into the room. Her eyes widened at the sheer size of it. 

“Holy…” she breathed. 

It was the size of a studio apartment, if not slightly bigger. The bed, as Alice had promised, was queen-sized with a canopy of sheer curtains around it and a purple comforter and pillows that looked fluffy as hell. There were large windows on one wall that looked out into the backyard, where Agatha could see a covered pool. She knew this place had a pool, but it had always been too cold during their cast parties to use it. 

She wondered if she’d be living with the Wus through the summer as well.

To the right were two more doors. One was a sliding door that opened from both ends – obviously a closet – and the other had a purple bathroom hanging from a hook on it. It was probably the ensuite Alice had told her about.

There was a sitting area to the left, complete with a loveseat, an easy chair, and a coffee table all arranged around a decently-sized television. There was even a wide bookshelf against the wall adjacent to the door, completely empty as if it had been waiting for Agatha to fill it.

There was a desk with vanity lights to the right of the door, too, with enough space for Agatha’s laptop and drawers to hold anything else she needed to store there. The desk chair was purple – most everything in this room was purple.

Lorna was right: Agatha had a strong connection to that color. She loved everything about this.

The floor was a dark hardwood with a purple rug that stretched across most of it, leaving just a foot or two of floor exposed around the perimeter. Agatha toed off her shoes before stepping onto it. She sighed as her feet sank in, feeling the softness even through her thick winter socks.

“This place…” She shook her head, tears starting to fall from her eyes for the dozenth time that day. “This is so amazing.” She turned to Lorna. “This is too much,” she said, shaking her head. “I don’t know how I’ll ever repay you.”

“Don’t you worry about it,” Lorna said, stepping forward to wrap her arms around Agatha’s shoulders, pulling her in for a tight hug. “I have plenty of money as it is. I mean, have you seen my house?” 

Agatha snorted against her shoulder. Lorna’s hold tightened on her. 

“You deserve so many good things, Agatha,” Lorna said, pulling back. One hand cupped Agatha’s cheek, swiping away a tear. “I remember when you were just a little thing, acting in plays with Jennifer, laughing with Alice as you all waited to get picked up after school. Your mother took that away from you, and it enrages me so much. You should never have had to deal with that. Not when you were just a child. Not ever . I hate that you’ve ever felt like you had nobody to turn to, nowhere to go. We’re making up for that now, okay? You stay here as long as you’d like, rent-free. You come back during your breaks from college and spend time with Alice and me. This house is way too big for the two of us, anyway.”

“True,” Alice piped in, appearing next to her mother. “It’s nice having more people around.”

“Hey!” Jen huffed. “I’m here, like, every day.”

“Ha!” Agatha said. “Your girlfriend likes me better!” She stuck out her tongue.

Jen flipped her off behind Lorna’s back.

“Okay, children ,” Lorna said, rolling her eyes affectionately, “let’s start getting Agatha unpacked. The food should be here soon.”

“Did you really hire caterers for Agatha’s first night?” Rio asked.

“Of course!” Lorna said, nonchalantly. “We have so much reason to celebrate! Besides, I gave Chef the night off.”

“Chef?” Agatha asked. “You have a chef ?”

“He only works two nights a week,” Alice said. “Mondays and Thursdays. He pretty much just meal preps for the week, leaving us with portioned-out meals to warm up. He posts the menu on the fridge.”

“You and I are in two entirely different tax brackets,” Rio murmured.

“You’re welcome over anytime, dear,” Lorna said, airily. “We always have plenty of excess.”

“Mom always gives any meals we have leftover on Sunday to the homeless guys that hang out down at the train station.”

“You are literally a saint,” Agatha said, looking up at Lorna, who scoffed, waving her off.

“I just grew up very poor,” she said. “And I remember watching my father starve just to make sure that I had enough food in my belly to keep going. I’m not about to let that happen to anybody else as long as I can do something to stop it. I’ve been getting on the mayor about turning that old abandoned office building into a second homeless shelter. I’m about to just buy the damn place myself and do it.”

“You totally should,” Jen said. “That would be amazing.” 

Lorna gave her an affectionate smile. “I’ll call a real estate agent tomorrow,” she said. “For tonight, go ahead and help Agatha unpack and I’ll let you know when the food gets here. I didn’t know exactly what you like, so I ordered a bit of everything. Tonight, we feast . Rio, is it?” Rio nodded. “Go ahead and invite your mother over. Jen, you too. Hopefully, Naomi has finished her case notes by now.”

“Doubt it,” Jen snorted, pulling out her phone, “but she’ll probably still want to come over.” She tapped out a message.

Rio pulled out her phone, too, placing a kiss on Agatha's check before she stepped out of the room to make the call. 

Lorna gave Agatha one last smile and a shoulder squeeze before stepping out of the room. 

Agatha turned to look at Alice, who was smiling at her expectantly.

“So,” Alice said, motioning to Agatha’s bookbag, “shall we?”

Agatha sighed and nodded, slipping her backpack from her shoulders and unzipping it to tug out Lilia’s cavernous bag of holding.

“Let’s get started,” Agatha sighed, unzipping the pouch.

 

It took nearly two hours for all four girls to empty the entire bag into Agatha’s bedroom. Agatha decided to forgo changing her comforter, instead designating her old favorite sheets and blankets as spares and tucking them away into the giant closet (where she also found a full dresser and a shoe rack) for later usage. Her books were organized onto the wide bookshelf, which had plenty of space for more. Her playbill and monologue connections were tucked safely away into the drawers on her desk, and her wastebasket fit perfectly in the corner next to it. The few stuffed animals she had sat on her bed or on the shelves on her walls, alongside a few knick knacks that she had brought from home. Her posters were taped to the walls in the order in which she had seen each play or show. Her bulletin board was hung right on the wall over her desk and littered with pictures of her and Rio (Alice had a photo printer in her room which could connect to Rio’s phone via bluetooth). Soon, the room had enough personal touches that it looked as though it had belonged to Agatha for far longer than just the last few hours.

The four girls stretched across Agatha’s bed – which was incredibly soft and sinfully comfortable – exhausted. Rio lay with her head on Agatha’s belly, her feet just barely reaching the other end of the bed.

Agatha still couldn’t believe that this was her life. It felt like a dream, like any second she would wake up and be back in her own bed at her mother’s house and be right back where she started, the trace still gripping her like a vice around her throat.

The thought must have caused her heart rate to speed up for her breathing to grow shallow because suddenly Rio was looking up at her with concern in her eyes. She didn’t verbalize anything, but her eyes asked Agatha if everything was alright. Agatha nodded, silently, running her hands through Rio’s hair.

“‘m fine,” she whispered. 

“Hmm?” Jen asked, lifting her head. “I think I may have passed out for a few seconds.”

“We know,” Agatha said. “You snore like a grizzly bear.”

“I do not !” Jen huffed, kicking Agatha’s foot.

“Don’t kick me!” Agatha huffed, kicking back. “Just get your damn sinuses checked!”

“Cut it out, you two,” Alice said, rolling her eyes. “Mom just texted me that the food is here. Everything is set up on the kitchen table and…oh, your moms are here.”

“At the same time?” Rio asked.

“They carpooled.”

“Oh goddess,” Rio groaned. “I just know my mom is trying to set up a ‘play date’ right now. Let’s go.” She groaned as she slid off the bed, stretching out her back. “I’m gonna need a few more of those drops later. Why do you have so many books, babe?”

“Excuse me for wanting to learn, Miss Valedictorian,” Agatha snorted, sliding off on the other side of the bed. “You probably have too much of something that I’m going to tease you about when I finally get to see your bedroom.”

“Finally, huh?” Rio asked, waggling her brows. Agatha flushed bright pink.

“Ew,” Jen said, wrinkling her nose. “Keep it in your pants, Vidal.”

“By ‘it’, you’re obviously talking about my giant di–”

“Quit it!” Alice groaned. “There’s food downstairs and I’m about to lose my appetite before I even taste any of it.” She shuddered. “Gross.”

She and Jen made their way to the door while Rio stepped in Agatha’s path, lowering her voice. “Seriously,” she said, “are you okay?”

“I’m…” Agatha looked over Rio’s shoulder, catching the look Alice threw her as she and Jen started toward the hall. “I’m fine,” Agatha insisted. “I just…I keep… thinking .”

“Nothing new there,” Rio said, tilting her head with a patient smile. “With your big brain.” She pushed a strand of hair behind Agatha’s ear. “About what?”

“What if this,” Agatha said, motioning around them, “isn’t real?”

“What?” Rio asked, furrowing her brow. “Why wouldn’t this be real?”

Agatha shrugged. “It’s just a thought,” Agatha said. “I dunno…” She looked down.

Rio reached forward and pinched her side.

“Ouch!” Agatha exclaimed. “What the hell?”

“So you could feel that then?” Rio asked. “It hurt?”

“Yes, of course it hurt!” Agatha huffed.

“And you’re still here?” Rio asked. “You’re still in this room? In this house?”

“Yes…”

“Then it’s real,” Rio said, placing her hands on Agatha’s shoulders. “It’s all real. Okay?”

Agatha took a deep breath and nodded. “Okay,” she said, her lips turning up in a small smile. “Did you really have to pinch me?”

“I was going to kiss you, but I didn’t think that would make the point I needed to make, you know? I mean, you could still think you’re dreaming and fantasizing about your amazingly hot girlfriend.” She winked.

Agatha rolled her eyes, shoving one of Rio’s shoulders with a laugh. “Come on,” she said. “I’m starving. I wanna see what Lorna ordered for dinner.”

 

Lorna ordered a little bit of everything, as she’d said, but Agatha was severely underestimating exactly what that meant.

There was a long, long table in the dining room, with enough chairs for a party of about thirty people (Agatha wondered why anybody would need that many chairs in a home of only two people) and it was piled high with all kinds of different cuisines from several different restaurants. There were different soups and meat dishes and vegetable dishes in various sauces. There were dumplings and perogies and gnocchi and empanadas and so much more. Agatha’s mouth began to water as she realized that she hadn’t really eaten much at lunch. She’d barely finished her wrap, staring at half of it and thinking of Rio, who usually would have traded it for half a bag of chips.

Rio, who was currently next to her, eyes wide and jaw on the floor as she stared at the spread before them. She heard something that sounded suspiciously like a growling stomach and almost snorted when Rio’s hands came to rest on her belly, her cheeks turning pink in embarrassment.

“This is so much food,” Rio said, looking up at Lorna. “More than anybody could eat in a month , let alone a single night.”

“More leftovers for the homeless,” Lorna said, with a grin. “Please, go ahead and make yourself a plate. Eat as much as you can handle. Ladies, feel free to bring home leftovers of whatever you like. We have so much .” She swept her hand toward the table with an inviting smile.

“Your mom rocks,” Rio said to Alice, immediately grabbing a plate and grabbing one of pretty much everything around the table.

“Well, she is a rockstar,” Alice replied, cheekily.

“Boo,” Agatha huffed, unable to suppress a grin as she knocked her shoulder into Alice’s.

“If this didn’t smell so good,” Rio said, holding up an empanada, “I’d throw it at you.”

“You would do no such thing!” Marisol huffed, making Rio jump and turn bright red as her shoulders hunched.

“Of course not, Mami,” she said. “I was just kidding.”

Marisol clicked her teeth at her while the others snickered. Then the older Vidal offered Agatha a bright smile.

“ Hola , dulcita ,” she cooed, cupping her cheeks in her hands. “How are you doing? Did you get everything unpacked well?”

“Yes, Ma’am,” Agatha said.

“I’m not ‘Ma’am’,” Marisol scoffed. “Please, call me Marisol . We are practically family, no?”

Agatha flushed, nodding slightly as she eyed Rio over Marisol’s shoulder. She had a mouthful of something, chewing slowly. She gave Agatha a thumbs up when their eyes met. Agatha took a deep breath, offering Marisol a smile.

“Okay,” she said. “Marisol, then. Thank you for your help today.”

“Anytime, dulcita ,” Marisol said, pinching her cheek gently. “Now let’s eat, huh? This all looks wonderful !” She offered Lorna a bright smile as she turned, her arm around Agatha’s shoulders as she led her to the table to grab their plates.

Before long, each of the women and girls in the room had their own plate piled high with different cuisines, but you wouldn’t know it by how little a dent it made in the feast that Lorna had ordered.

Agatha had opted for a cup of tomato soup and grilled cheese made with gooey, perfectly stringy mozzarella that stretched when she pulled apart the two halves of bread. She also had some veggie dumplings, half an empanada (the other half was on Rio’s plate), some mango habanero chicken wings, some yellow rice, and a cupcake that she kind of felt was too pretty to eat, but she really liked it.

She never got to eat like this with her mother, who believed so vehemently in the Seven Deadly Sins that anything with more than a singular gram of sugar was considered evil . That somehow also included seasoning.

Even just the simplicity of grilled cheese and tomato soup was a treat for her. And this bread was perfectly toasted and the cheese was heavenly and she once again thought she might have been dreaming if the tomato soup wasn’t so hot that it burned her tongue a little. Agatha fanned her mouth, but she didn’t stop eating. She practically inhaled the rest of the sandwich and the cup of soup before reaching for one of the wings.

“Try the empanada,” Rio said. “It’s so good and not that spicy.”

Agatha nodded, polishing off a wing and reaching for the empanada, taking a big bite. It was good, but it had a little kick to it from whatever pepper and spices had been added. Agatha reached for the glass of lemonade that Lorna had poured her, inhaling in relief as the icy drink cooled her mouth. She cleared her throat.

“It’s good,” she croaked, coughing a little.

“Too spicy?” Rio asked, fighting a grin.

Agatha shrugged. “I’m just not used to flavor, I guess,” she said. “My mom was a boiled chicken kind of person. If we ever went out to eat with her church friends, I was heavily encouraged to get a grilled chicken salad with light dressing.” She rolled her eyes. “ This ,” she motioned to the food on her plate, “is more flavorful than anything she’s ever made for me.”

“Pace yourself,” Alice said, “because Chef makes a lot of flavorful dishes.”

“I’m sure he’ll tone it down a little bit to accommodate, though,” Lorna assured Agatha. “We’ll work you up to our usual fare.”

Agatha nodded, taking another bite of the empanada. A wave of heat radiated from her mouth, making sweat appear on her forehead, but it was so good . 

“Are you torturing yourself?” Rio whispered in her ear. “You don’t have to eat the whole thing, you know.”

“It’s only half ,” Agatha huffed, taking another bite. “And it’s so good .” She took another bite. She was almost finished with it now.

“You have other food on your plate, though,” Rio said. “Try the rice; it helps soak up the heat a little bit.” 

Agatha nodded, spooning some rice into her mouth and letting out a soft moan. “That is also really good,” she said. “Man, who knew food could be good .”

“Everybody,” Jen said from across the table. “Except your mom, I guess.”

“I’m not surprised that woman preferred boiled chicken,” Naomi said, taking a bite out of her Jamaican patty. “That’s some serial killer food right there…unless she had some dietary restrictions?” She lifted her brow at Agatha, who shook her head.

“She always ordered seasoned chicken when we were out to eat with her friends. She forced me to have salad, but she ate what her friends ate. It never made her sick as far as I know.”

“Then, yeah, the lady’s a serial killer, mark my words.” 

The rest of the group laughed at that, including Agatha. She’d never really been free to talk about her mother like this. Nobody else in her church youth group spoke badly about their mothers at all, so Agatha had never felt safe telling any of them what her mother was really like. She didn’t really like them much at all, anyway. They were pious and snooty and very “better than thou” about every little thing. 

Here, she at least felt safe and surrounded by people who could see the same things she did.

Agatha finished the majority of her plate before she felt as though she couldn’t eat a single bite more. She sat back in her chair, rubbing her belly, smiling as Rio leaned her head on her shoulder, also looking rather stuffed from all that she had eaten. Alice and Jen mirrored them across the table. Naomi, Lorna, and Marisol ate slowly, conversing with one another at one end of the table, giving their daughters some space amongst themselves. It was Naomi who first noticed that all four girls had gone quiet, looking over at them with a soft smile.

“Looks like the girls ate themselves into some comas,” she said. “Maybe it’s time we start packing up and head home. They have school in the morning and I know my Jenny hasn’t even begun to do her homework for the night.”

“Ugh,” Jen grunted into Alice’s hair. “Too full,” she said. “No homework. Just write me a note, will you?”

“I’m not writing you a note to get you out of your responsibilities just because you ate too much, missy,” Naomi huffed. “Come on and get up. Now .” Naomi herself stood from the table, gathering her own plate and empty glass. Marisol followed.

“I’ll help you with the dishes,” she said. “Rio, help us clear the table.”

“Okay,” Rio groaned, pressing a kiss to Agatha’s shoulder before standing up. She grabbed hers and Agatha’s plates and cups, bringing them to the trash to scrape the remnants of their food out, then carried them over to the sink, where Marisol was already running some hot water.

“Oh, don’t worry about doing the dishes, Marisol,” Lorna said, standing up as well. “Just go ahead and put everything into the dishwasher. Our maid will be by in the morning to unload it and tidy everything up. We just need to get the food into the cold room.”

“The cold room?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

“It’s basically a big standing freezer,” Alice said. “Temperature controlled. That’s where Chef puts all our meals and the ingredients he uses to make our food to make them last longer.”

“Different. Tax Brackets,” Rio said, repeating the sentiment from earlier.

Alice just rolled her eyes and started popping lids back on the containers of food. “Help me out with this stuff, please,” she said. Agatha stood up and started to help, popping lids back in place on styrofoam bowls of soup and aluminum containers until everything was boxed up. 

“Do we bring this all to the cold room?” she asked, looking at Alice.

“First, let Marisol and Naomi pick what they’d like to bring home with them,” Lorna said. “Then pick out what you’d like to bring for lunch tomorrow. Then we’ll put everything away to bring to the train station later this week.”

“You really are a saint, you know that?” Naomi said, plucking up the dishes of Jamaican patties and vegetable lo mein. 

“That’s what I said,” Agatha said. Lorna waved her off again.

“If I have enough to give, why wouldn’t I?” Lorna huffed.

“Not enough people have that attitude,” Marisol said, taking the boxes of leftover empanadas and yellow rice. “Thank you, Lorna. This was a lovely meal.”

“You’re welcome anytime, Marisol,” Lorna said. “You and your daughter. Rio is a lovely girl.”

“Bet nobody’s ever said that before,” Jen muttered under her breath. 

Agatha glared and sent a purple shock at her. Jen let out a gasp and jumped, turning to glare at Agatha, who didn’t flinch away for even a second, lifting one brow in challenge. Jen said nothing; she just continued to glare.

“Go ahead and pick what you’d like to take home, girls,” Naomi said. “Then we gotta go.”

Rio snatched the leftover wings, of which there were plenty, licking her lips as she looked down at them. She handed them over to her mother, who piled them atop the other containers of food. Jen reached for the two leftover cupcakes and handed one to Alice with a soft smile. Alice smiled back, leaning in to kiss her lips.

“Gag,” Agatha said, wrinkling her nose.

“Homophobe,” Jen retorted.

“I have a girlfriend!” Agatha huffed, holding up Rio’s hand as if to demonstrate. Rio used that hand to flip Jen off, immediately getting scolded by Marisol.

“Good goddess,” Naomi huffed, shaking her head. “What are we gonna do with these girls?”

“ No sé ,” Marisol snorted. “But I may just cut off my daughter’s fingers if she doesn’t cut it out .” She hit Rio with a warning look. Rio’s shoulders hunched.

“ Lo siento, mami,” she said.

“Jennifer, if you open your mouth to make some smartass comment, you won’t be leaving the house for a month ,” Naomi warned. 

Jen pressed her lips together.

“That’s what I thought,” Naomi said. “Now pick your food and let’s go. You better not give Rio any issues as we’re driving home, either.”

“Yes, ma’am,” Jen said, picking up the dumplings and vegetable fried rice. She placed a kiss on Alice’s cheek before walking over to stand with Naomi, who flicked her ear, but not harshly. Jen pouted at her and Naomi squeezed her nose, making her giggle.

“See you tomorrow,” Rio said in Agatha’s ear. “I’ll meet you at the front of the school?” She gave Agatha a hopeful look.

“Instead of the stinky dressing room?” Agatha said. “Yes, please.”

Rio beamed and pressed her lips to Agatha’s, cursing the food in her hands for not allowing her to wrap her arms around Agatha’s waist. Agatha, thankfully, wrapped her own around Rio’s shoulders, keeping them tethered for a few moments before letting Rio go.

Rio felt the urge to say three little words then, but she bit them back in favor of three different words.

“See you tomorrow.”

Chapter End Notes

Hope y'all like where this is going. Lemme know in the comments!

Chapter 20: First Day Free

Chapter Summary

Agatha starts her first day of freedom, getting to hold Rio's hand freely and just being cute and all that stuff. Fluff chapter, basically. Still trying to figure out all the dynamics.

Chapter Notes

I don't have an outline for this story btw, I am just as surprised as you are with what comes next. This one will be mainly agathario fluff and a little Jen/Agatha bickering.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty

Agatha hadn’t expected to sleep as well as she did. She had never been really great at falling asleep, especially when there was a lot on her mind.
