Even with how soft the bed the Wus had given her was, she’d expected that she would end up tossing and turning for most of the night, only to end up with about three or four hours of fitful sleep.

Instead, she slept like the dead – the snoring dead. 

She woke up to Alice shaking her shoulder, Agatha’s eyes snapping open to see the other girl staring down at her, bleary-eyed, with a toothbrush sticking out of her mouth and her hair wild around her head.

“Wake up,” Alice slurred around the toothbrush. “Mom’s gonna drive us in a half hour.”

“What time is it?” Agatha mumbled, rubbing at her eyes. She glanced at her phone on the bedside table, where it had been charging. There were three notifications for the alarms she’d missed. “Shit!” she said, throwing off her covers and immediately tumbling out of bed, all while Alice watched, brushing her teeth. “Mother fuck –”

“Chill out,” Alice said, padding toward the door. “You have time.” She got to the door before turning back. “You drool in your sleep, you know that?”

“Fuck off,” Agatha huffed, pushing herself back to her feet and swiping at her face, which was, in fact, very damp with drool.

“Just saying,” Alice said. “Bathroom is fully stocked, by the way. Mom put a new toothbrush and toothpaste on the sink. There’s also a bunch of skincare products in the medicine cabinet. And other toiletries. And brushes.” She eyed Agatha’s hair with a raised brow. “You might need one of those.”

“You’re one to talk,” Agatha retorted, smoothing down her mane of hair. Alice just shrugged and exited the room, closing the door softly behind herself.

Agatha rushed through getting dressed, brushing her teeth, and brushing her hair, braiding it half-up as her toothbrush hung out of her mouth. She also rinsed her face with some foamy face wash that Lorna had left for her, her skin feeling a bit tighter as she washed it off with warm water and a purple washcloth (wow, they really made purple her entire personality in this house, huh?) and ran back into the bedroom to pull a sweater and a pair of jeans on. She also stopped in front of her closet to consider which shoes to wear.

Evanora had always hated her Doc Martens. They were purple with black stars all over them, and Agatha had spent her own money on them. She’d hardly ever worn them, though, because Evanora had always told her to go change them whenever she saw Agatha trying to leave the house with them on. Agatha had taken precautions at her mother’s house with a concealment spell so that Evanora could never dispose of them when Agatha was out of the house. 

They couldn’t be concealed when she wore them unfortunately, otherwise they’d be much more broken in.

Agatha grabbed the Docs and slipped into them, admiring herself in the full-length mirror on the inside of the closet door. She was wearing a forest green sweater with a light purple polo underneath, the collar sticking out over the neckline of her sweater. Forest green was Rio’s favorite color and it went well with the purple boots.

Her jeans were torn slightly at the knees, a style that she never wore though she always wanted to. Her mother hated distressed clothing like that. She told Agatha that it would make them (re: Evanora ) look bad to see her child wearing clothes with rips and tears on them, as if she didn’t have the money to get Agatha proper clothes or to have them mended. 

Agatha had bought these jeans at a thrift store in her sophomore year, but she’d never worn them. Until now. She honestly half-expected them to be too tight on her now. Her mother had commented on her weight a few times, telling her that she was looking a little full in the waist, but these jeans actually felt a little more loose now than they’d been when Agatha tried them on at the thrift shop.

She’d need to start filling them out.

Agatha gave herself a smile in the mirror, reaching for her usual pea coat and backpack, and made her way downstairs.

Lorna Wu was sitting at the kitchen counter when Agatha walked in, sipping on a travel mug with a tea tag sticking out of it. She gave Agatha a warm smile.

“How did you sleep, dear?” she asked.

“Better than I have in…ever, I think,” Agatha said, scratching the back of her neck as she flushed and gave an embarrassed laugh. “That bed is so comfortable; it’s like a cloud.”

“I’m glad you like it,” Lorna laughed. “Would you like some coffee or tea? We have some extra travel tumblers in that cabinet, next to the fridge. The coffee is already in the pot and the tea bags are next to the coffee maker.”

Agatha nodded. “Thanks,” she said.

“And, if you’re hungry,” Lorna continued, “there’s yogurt, granola, cereal, an assortment of different milks – Alice and I are both lactose intolerant, so we use oat and almond, but I picked up a quart of two percent if you want it – some pop-tarts (Alice’s are taking up the toaster right now), and an array of cereal bars.”

“Wow,” Agatha said, blinking up at her. “All my mom had was toast and butter.”

“We have that, too,” Lorna said. “White, wheat, rye, and cinnamon raisin bread are all in the bread drawer next to the dishwasher. If you open any of them, please put it in the fridge so it lasts longer.” 

Agatha nodded, opening the fridge to see it was completely stocked full of food. Her eyes widened as she glanced back over at Lorna, who gave her a soft smile.

“We may have over prepared for your stay,” she said. “Obviously, anything you see that you like, you can eat. Just make it quick because we need to go in,” she looked at her watch, “five minutes.” She placed her cup down and walked to the base of the steps. “Alice! Come on, honey! Time to go to school!”

“Coming!” Alice called down, her voice echoing slightly against the marble of the staircase.

She appeared ten seconds later in a black sweater and red leggings dotted with black skulls. Her feet were encased in her usual red Converse and her hair was brushed but fell loosely around her shoulders. She had a red leather jacket over her arm and her backpack slung over her other shoulder.

The Pop-Tarts popped just as she made it to the toaster, and Alice wrapped them up in a paper towel before she began to make herself a cup of coffee to bring with them to school.

“Don’t forget your lunches,” Lorna said. “I already heated them up for you.” She motioned to two lunch boxes sitting on the kitchen island that Agatha hadn’t noticed before. One was purple and the other was red.

She could guess which one was hers.

Agatha chose a strawberry yogurt and an apple, then filled a blue tumbler from the cabinet with coffee and a little bit of sugar and oat milk (which she’d never tried but found surprisingly sweet) and reached for the purple lunchbox. 

It was very warm.

“What’s this thing made out of?” Agatha asked, looking at Alice.

“Dunno,” Alice said, munching on a bit of her blueberry poptart, “some kind of space material or something. It keeps the food super warm until lunch, though. It’s pretty awesome.”

“Yeah,” Agatha agreed. “Wow, you really live a privileged life, huh?”

Alice shrugged. “I still have chores and shit,” she said. “I still have to work hard to get good grades. I still get grounded when I break rules at home or at school. I still have a curfew. I still have to earn things I want, like the drum set my mom got me in exchange for three honor roll periods.”

“It took you a year and a half to earn a drum set ?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow. 

Alice shrugged. “It was worth it,” she said. “Besides, she wanted to make sure I wasn’t going to let my studies fall behind the second I got the new drums, so I also have to keep up my grades in order to keep them.” She shrugged. “I have the luxury of a nice house and plenty of food, heat, electricity, cable, and wifi, but I work at the soup kitchen on holidays with my mom, we go to charity events and meet with the people who would be benefitting from those charities. I go to my dad’s house every other weekend and meet with him for dinner sometimes during the week.” She smiled softly. “He brings me to ballgames and buys me cheap, greasy food to ‘keep me humble’ and brings me on ride-alongs so I see just what can happen if I get on the wrong path. I’d say I’m pretty well-rounded, as a person.”

“Yeah, I guess,” Agatha relented.

“Alright girls,” Lorna said. “The car is warming up. Time to hustle.” She clapped her hands, and Agatha and Alice slipped into their coats, grabbed their bags and their chosen breakfast, and made their way to the SUV.

 

Agatha had never seen the drop-off line at the high school. Most of the students lived within walking or bussing distance to the school, or they carpooled with friends, so three or four students were dropped off at any given time. The line was short and close to the front security entrance of the school, which was down a long pathway filled with planters and benches. 

At the end of the pathway was Rio, sitting on a bench and absolutely housing a breakfast burrito in between sips of iced tea. Agatha paused at the end of the path as Lorna let her and Alice out of the car, blowing them a kiss and wishing them a good day at school.

“Is she even breathing?” Alice murmured, wrinkling her nose at Rio.

“Probably not,” Agatha said. “If she were, she’d probably choke.”

“You sure that’s who you want to be with?” Alice said, giving Agatha a side-eye.

“Yup,” Agatha said. “That’s my lady.” She smiled happily as she made her way to Rio, glancing around certain that somebody must have been watching her. She swallowed thickly as she perched next to Rio, who was animalistic in her hunger. “You’re going to bite your fingers off,” Agatha teased, startling Rio so that she swung her head around to look at her, eyes wide and mouth full, bits of egg and hot sauce dotting her lips and chin.

“Hrrgh,” Rio said through her mouthful of food.

“Come again?” Agatha snorted, lifting one brow. 

Rio flushed, wiping her mouth with the back of her hand. She chewed and swallowed what was in her mouth. “Hey,” she said, clearing her throat. “What’s up?”

“What’s up ?” Agatha snorted. “As if I didn’t just witness you shove a whole burrito in your mouth? What’s the rush?”

“Lilia hates when we eat during class,” Rio huffed. “And I was hungry.” She rubbed her stomach and popped the last bit of burrito into her mouth.

“Didn’t you eat your weight in food last night?” Agatha laughed. 

Rio let out a Simpsons -worthy belch, patting her stomach again. “That was over eight hours ago,” she said. “I’m a growing girl.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t tamp down her affectionate smile as she leaned her head on Rio’s shoulder. Rio’s eyes widened, and she looked all around them for a moment before relaxing against the other girl as well. Agatha could feel Rio’s smile against her forehead.

“So,” she said, “you’re really comfortable with this? Us? Being out in public?”

Agatha shrugged, pulling back a little. “If you are,” she said. Rio nodded. “Then I am…I guess.”

“That doesn’t sound so sure.”

Agatha sighed. “It’s going to take some time to stop looking over my shoulder for my mom and Harper ,” she wrinkled her nose in disgust, “but I’ll be holding your hand for comfort the whole time.” To demonstrate, she slipped her fingers between Rio’s between them on the bench. 

Rio smiled at her, so soft and affectionate, and leaned her forehead against Agatha’s. “Is there kissing involved in this, too?” she asked.

“Of course,” Agatha snorted, pressing a soft kiss to the corner of Rio’s mouth. It was shy and brief, but it was the most she’d ever done in public.

It was enough for now.

Rio’s beaming smile told her that, her hand tightening around Agatha’s.

“Why,” Agatha said, “are my lips burning?”

“Because I’m so hot?” Rio tried. Agatha furrowed her brow, unamused. “Because I used a lot of hot sauce in my burrito,” Rio admitted. There was still some smudged just under her bottom lip. 

Agatha pulled a napkin from her backpack and licked it before wiping Rio’s mouth with it. Rio wrinkled her nose, pulling back. Agatha placed a firm hand on Rio’s cheek, which sent a flush blooming under her fingers as Rio’s eyes widened and she stilled. Agatha successfully removed all the dried hot sauce on her girlfriend’s lips, tossing the dirty napkin into a nearby trash can. Then she leaned in, pressing a soft peck there.

“Much better,” she said, snorting at Rio’s goofy smile. “Come on, loverboy,” she said, rolling her eyes as she stood and held out her hand. “Let’s get to class.”

Rio gripped her hand, tightly, settling her backpack back on her shoulder as she followed Agatha toward the front door. 

They made it all the way down the hall before Agatha caught sight of Harper Caulfield, who was standing at her locker with two other girls dressed like clones of one another, with the same sweater in three different pastel colors and checkered skirts and moccasins. They all glared at Agatha and Rio as they walked back.

Agatha fought the urge to let go of Rio’s hand and instead tightened her grip, smiling sideways at Rio as the other girl beamed at her, knocking her head against Rio’s as they kept walking. 

Her step only stuttered when she caught a slur muttered under Harper’s breath, her breath catching in her chest. She forced herself to keep going, but Rio fully turned around, keeping a firm grip on Agatha’s hand.

“What was that, ginger?” she hissed at Harper.

“You heard what I said,” Harper said, an almost bored expression on her face.

“I did,” Rio said, “but I was giving you a chance to apologize before I tell your little friends what we did in the locker room in eighth grade on three separate occasions.”

Harper’s eyes went wide as saucers as her cheeks began to flame. “Wh-what are you talking about?!” she huffed, looking between her friends and Rio. “I didn’t – we didn’t!”

“Oh, did you forget ?” Rio asked, batting her eyelashes. “You said I was the best kisser you’d ever met .”

“I never –” Harper looked at her friends. “She’s lying !” she insisted. “I would never ! That’s dis-disgusting!”

“You’re only lying to yourself, baby girl,” Rio said, with a wink, before dragging a wide-eyed Agatha in the direction of Lilia’s classroom. Harper was left stuttering and panicking as she tried to assure her friends that she would never .

“What was that about?” Agatha asked as they entered the stairwell. “You kissed Harper Caulfield? Three times ?”

Rio snorted. “No,” she said, “but I do know somebody who did. A female somebody.” Agatha’s eyes widened. “Usually, I would feel bad about possibly outing somebody in an unsafe position, but I know at least a dozen kids that Harper has personally outed to their families. Most of them were accepting, but she didn’t know that and was definitely attempting to get them disowned. Besides, neither of those girls believed me. They think I’m insane.” She widened her eyes manically. 

“You are insane,” Agatha snorted. “But it’s kinda hot.”

Rio blushed, biting her bottom lip as they stopped at the landing. She leaned in, pressing a kiss to Agatha’s lips. They were fairly secluded there. It was still at least ten minutes before the bell rang, so Agatha allowed the kiss to go further than the two previous pecks, leaning back against the wall, crushing her backpack and lunchbox a little bit, and stroking Rio’s jaw as they kissed.

“Get a room!” a voice said as it passed by.

Agatha and Rio broke apart, but it was only Jen, who tugged Alice along after her up the rest of the stairs. She gave them a thumbs up as she followed her girlfriend. Agatha could also see the slight smirk on Jen’s cheeks, though she tried to hide it. 

Agatha rolled her eyes, pushing Rio a little bit until she could stand up straight, then she started tugging her the rest of the way to Lilia’s classroom.

When they stepped inside holding hands, Lilia clapped her hands. “Mazel Tov!” she exclaimed.

Agatha flushed and sat down at a seat adjacent to the one Rio selected and reached for her tumblr of coffee sticking out of the pocket of her backpack. She took a long sip and sighed. It felt like it was going to be a good morning.

“So,” a voice said from behind, “are you two like…a couple?”

Agatha and Rio both turned to Theo, who was sitting behind Agatha, blinking curiously between them with a soft smile on his lips. 

“Weren’t you there yesterday?” Agatha asked. “When all that… stuff went down with my mother?” She flushed, remembering the shame and embarrassment of having her mother’s huge floating head appearing in front of everybody that she might have considered her friend. “Also, we just walked in holding hands.”

“Yeah,” Theo said, “but I don’t like to just assume things like that. You could just be really good friends.”

“Like you and Sonny?” Jen said from another row back. Theo flushed, hunching his shoulders. “I knew it!” Jen exclaimed. “Olivia owes me twenty bucks.”

“Stop betting on people!” Agatha huffed.

“People gotta start coming out about their relationships and stop being such pussies,” Jen retorted. “You and Sonny are cute, Theo.”

“Thanks,” Theo grumbled. He looked up at Agatha. “You and Rio are a nice couple, too,” he said. “I always knew you had a crush on her.”

“I didn’t even come out until yesterday!” Agatha huffed.

“Girl, you’re a great actress,” Theo said, “but a horrible liar.”

Rio’s laugh died a quick death in her throat at Agatha’s glare. She gave her a pout and puppy eyes. Agatha rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t bite back her amusement.

The bell rang and Lilia clapped. “Okay!” she said. “Everybody quiet down and let’s get this class started. We’re gonna do a dramatic reading of Oedipus Rex .”

“Motherfucker,” Rio said.

“Language!” Lilia huffed.

“It’s an adjective!” Rio defended. “And totally appropriate for the situation.”

“Goddess help me,” Lilia muttered, opening her play as she perched on the edge of her desk.

 

The day went rather quickly. Agatha had been terrified that it would drag on and she’d have to deal with Harper and her cronies cornering her all day long or even her mother storming into the school at some point during the day, but everything was pretty quiet.

She and Rio smiled at each other in the halls, their hands brushing as they passed by on their way to class. They sat together during lunch again, their feet tangled under the table as they smiled adoringly at each other across the table. Jen made faces at them out of the corner of their vision. They ignored her as they split the leftovers from the night before between them.

When they finished eating, they went to Agatha’s locker so she could finally put the backpack she’d been dragging with her (her locker was so out of the way of her morning classes, it was ridiculous) and grab books for the afternoon. They walked, hand-in-hand, to the auditorium, where they sat against the back wall, sharing earbuds as they worked through the playlist of showtunes that Agatha had made for Rio. Rio really got into Hadestown and Mean Girls , especially. She made Agatha replay “I’d Rather Be Me” more than once. 

Agatha didn’t mind. She watched the enjoyment play out on Rio’s face as she mouthed along to the words on the third replay, her head laying in Agatha’s lap, her eyes closed. Agatha ran her hand through Rio’s loose hair, smiling softly when the other girl’s eyes slowly peeked open. Agatha leaned down, pressing a soft kiss to Rio’s lips, which was received quite happily.

When ninth period came along at the end of the day, they linked fingers as they headed toward the front exit, on the side of the school that faced the direction of the cafe.

“What are you dimwits doing?” 

The voice came out of nowhere, a full five seconds before Jennifer Kale revealed herself, the dramatic bitch that she was, stepping around the couple before they could exit the building.

“Going to get some matcha,” Agatha said.

“And hot chocolate,” Rio added. Agatha nodded, squeezing her fingers.

“Out in the open?” Jen huffed. “Where your mother could find you?”

“I’m wearing the stupid amulet,” Agatha huffed, pulling the necklace out from beneath her sweater. She hadn’t stopped wearing it since she put it on the day prior. “And there’s no trace on me for her to find me,” she added.

“She could still be watching you,” another voice said, making them jump and spin around to find Alice standing a few feet back, her head tilted in concern.

“ Jesus –DON’T YOU BITCHES HAVE CLASS?” Agatha huffed.

“We have plenty of class,” Jen retorted, smartly. “But our teacher played hooky today and left an imbecile watching us. The sub just sent a sheet around for us to write our names on it. I had Theo write ours down.”

“Still,” Agatha huffed. “I think we’ll be fine to take a five minute walk to get drinks. My mom can’t even touch me with this thing on.” She motioned to the necklace.

“Sure,” Alice said, coming around them to stand next to Jen, “she can’t touch you , but she can touch the people around you.” She looked pointedly at Rio.

“I can handle myself,” Rio said, crossing her arms over her chest, defensively.

“Can you?” Alice asked. “Because you’re a mostly untrained witch. Can you make a forcefield?”

“I can make plants come alive,” Rio said. “Including poisonous ones.”

“Yes, because there are so many poisonous plants planted in Westview,” Jen huffed. “Besides, what are plants gonna do anyway? Attack her ankles with their leaves? Use your brain, please.”

Rio frowned at her, lifting her hand, which began to grow green with her magic, and waved it at one of the planters that lined the front hallway. From the soil popped a thick, dark green, thorny vine that grew exponentially until it was looming over the four of them. Rio was obviously in perfect control of it as she waved her arm and the vine followed, going straight for Jen, who yelped and jumped behind her girlfriend, who raised her arms and made an orange shield appear, covering them both. The vine didn’t reach the shield, stopping just before impact.

Rio lifted a brow and smirked at Jen as she glared at her from behind Alice, who was nearly half a foot shorter than her.

“I can handle myself,” Rio said. “Besides, I doubt Evanora would do anything, physically, to Agatha in public. She’s kept her abuse and neglect under wraps for most of Agatha’s life, right?” She glanced at Agatha, who nodded. Rio frowned, squeezing her hand. Hers was still warm from the use of her magic. Agatha squeezed back. “I’ll take anything that bitch can throw at me,” Rio said firmly.

“Bitch, don’t be a hero,” Jen huffed, finally stepping out from behind her tiny girlfriend and her shield, which immediately disappeared. “Besides, we’re not stopping you from going.”

“Then why are you still blocking our path?” Agatha asked, brows furrowed. 

“Because we’re going with you,” Jen said. “You’re not the only one who likes matcha, Harkness.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but she really couldn’t bite back her grin. “Fine,” she said. “Let’s go then. Before school lets out and the line becomes impossible.”

Jen and Alice led the way, with Agatha and Rio still holding hands behind them.

 

Evanora didn’t show up at the cafe, thankfully. Nor did she show up on the path to and from the cafe at any point. Agatha was relieved that she was able to spend the time with her girlfriend and…friends? Kinda-foster-sister-and-foster-sister’s-gf? She had no idea what Alice was to her, or Jen for that matter, but they were alright, she guessed. She didn’t actively antagonize them.

Much.

“I’m just saying,” Agatha said, as they walked into the auditorium just as the school day ended, “Galinda is a soprano role; Lilia should have casted a soprano for it.”

“Just because it’s traditionally performed by a soprano,” Jen retorted, “doesn’t mean it has to be, especially when the best person for the role is an alto .” She motioned to herself.

Agatha scoffed. “I could have done Galinda just as well as you,” she said, taking a sip of her matcha.

“And I could have done Elphaba justice, too,” Jen said. “That was literally my dream role. I’m the taller one, just like all the Elphabas have been in actual productions!”

“Does this happen every year?” Rio murmured to Alice.

“Since we were eight,” Alice murmured back. “It’s best just to let them hash it out. Wanna practice your notes?”

“I do not want to do that, no,” Rio said, “but I feel as though I don’t actually have a choice.”

“You don’t,” Alice said cheerily, hooking her arm around Rio’s as she dragged her towards the piano at the front of the auditorium. Rio groaned, sipping her hot chocolate, leaving Jen and Agatha to continue bickering at the back.

Chapter 21: One of Us

Chapter Summary

Agatha and Jen have their Juilliard auditions.

I want to preface this with the fact that I don't know these auditions work IRL but it's probably not how I wrote them.

Just suspend your disbelief for my sake. Thank you.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Twenty-One

Agatha was a nervous wreck on Friday night.

She had gone over her monologue with Jen and Alice a hundred times, but she still felt as though something were missing. She didn’t miss a single word , of course, but there was still… something not right.

“You lack conviction,” Jen said from her perch on Alice’s bed. They were in her bedroom. Jen was perched on the end of the bed, legs and arms crossed as she listened to Agatha for the millionth time. Alice was sitting at her drumset, phantom-drumming a beat that nobody could hear. “You gotta believe what you’re saying, like you do in literally every other monologue.”

“I never actually believe what I’m saying,” Agatha huffed. “It’s just acting.”

“Girl, then act !” Jen said, throwing her hands up. “ Act like you believe wholeheartedly in the bullshit you’re spewing out. Come on! Let’s see some energy!” She clapped her hands. 

“I might just kill you,” Agatha said. 

“You ain’t gonna get convicted with that attitude,” Jen retorted.

This time, Alice did drum out a little ba dum tiss , shrugging at Agatha’s pointed glare. “That was funny, you gotta admit,” Alice defended.

“Thanks, babe,” Jen cooed. “Just act , Agatha,” she said, turning back to the other girl. “I see you do it at every audition. You’re freaking Elphaba , for goddess’s sake! I know that you can blow the socks off of those judges, okay?”

“Aww, Jenny, you have such faith in me. It’s touching,” Agatha said, placing her hand over her heart. She felt the amulet underneath her fingers, under the t-shirt she wore. It pulsed at her touch, or maybe she was just imagining it. 

“Don’t call me Jenny, Aggie ,” Jen huffed. “And do the monologue again, but try to feel the words, okay? You are Antigone. Act like it.”

Agatha nodded, closing her eyes and looking down, shaking the nerves out of her arms as she took a deep breath, trying to get into the new headspace.

“Why?” she began, clearing her throat a little. “Why do I feel this rage? I’ve wondered that myself , Lottie.” She started to pace. “I’ve tried to understand it. It can’t just be Creah, right? Because this rage has been building for so long I feel like I am going to explode. ” She stopped pacing, trying to feel the rage the character was feeling. 

Antigone was a tragic character. She had defied the law to bury her late brother. She was about to go to prison to spend the rest of her short life in solitary confinement for the simple act. That was infuriating . Agatha would be infuriated by such unfair punishment. She thought of the times her mother had locked her away in her room for lesser reasons, like the time she had corrected one of her mother’s friends on the pronunciation of a word. Agatha couldn’t even remember what word it was, and said friend hadn’t even cared that much (not that Agatha could tell, anyway), but Evanora was incensed at Agatha’s very nerve . 

Agatha had spent the next three weekends locked in her room, only let out to use the bathroom or go to church. Had it not been during the school year, she was certain that she would have been locked away for every single second during the week then as well.

Agatha felt that rage climb up her spine like a snake up a tree.

“ How long ,” she continued, her voice tight, “have I woken up with this pit in my stomach, shaking, thinking that I am doomed? We are doomed. I’ve wondered how the people of Thebes could watch this happen and do nothing. ”

She thought of her mother’s friends. They all put on the same façade as Evanora. The faithful, churchgoing wives and mothers. Pious and proper and a little bit witchy, but it was okay because that was how God had made them. They had all openly loved their children the way that Evanora pretended to love Agatha. But they had also seen the way Evanora treated Agatha even if they hadn’t seen everything Evanora did to her. The way Agatha visibly shrank every time Evanora glanced her way, how skinny she was despite her mother telling her that she needed to eat less , that she was starting to put on weight (in a joking way, of course, in an attempt to help Agatha), that she needed to try to do better, to be good like the daughters of her friends.

Flattery helped them all turn a blind eye, Agatha supposed, but she wondered how many of them were unsurprised that Agatha had run away from Evanora.

“Oh,” Agatha said, turning on her heel with her hands up, “now suddenly I hear some people are standing up for me. Now some are saying Creah’s law goes against everything we as a people believe in. But isn’t it too late now?” She rolled her eyes. “I’ll be sitting in Super Max. My prison.” She clenched her fists and her jaw. “My death bed. No high learning pod graduation. No final celebrations to end the year. I’m just one person, but sometimes I feel like this has been done to everyone . Like we’ve all been locked away. Why ?” She felt a lump form in her throat at the singular word. “What did I do wrong , Lottie?” She looked at Jen, whose eyes widened at the level of emotion in Agatha’s voice. Agatha couldn’t stop the tears from flooding her eyes. What law of Heaven did I transgress? My brother is dead . Both my parents are dead. So where am I to get another brother?”

Agatha had no siblings (probably for the better) but she still felt the loss of Antigone’s brother, her only remaining family, the last person in the world she had to love and love her. Gone . And she was being punished for saying a proper goodbye to him, against the rules of a tyrant. It was wholly unfair, as were many things in life. 

It was unfair that Agatha had no father. It was unfair that she had no grandparents or siblings or anybody who could share in her pain living under her mother. It was unfair that all she’d really had for the first seventeen years of her life was Evanora Harkness, the woman from whom’s body she’d entered this world and who hated Agatha with every fiber of her being and never let Agatha forget it. It was unfair that she didn’t have a single biologically related person who loved her.

Agatha took a deep breath, fighting past the tears and clenching her fists as she tried to calm her rapid heartbeat, her thoughts turning from Evanora to Rio. And Alice and Lorna. And even Jen.

Her shoulders slumped slightly. “Was I wrong?” she asked, looking at Jen as if she were Lottie, the reporter in this scene. “Is my anger wrong?” She pressed her hand to her chest again, glancing down as if in contemplation. She shrugged, looking back up. “If it is,” she continued, “I guess I’ll find out when I die. My only solace is knowing those who have done this to me, or stood by and let it happen, will suffer the same fate.” She kept her spine straight on the last line, taking a deep breath and she gave one last decisive nod. 

“Whoa,” Alice said from her spot at the drum set. 

“Damn,” Jen said in agreement. “Yeah, okay,” she said, “now that is conviction. Why couldn’t you do it the first million or so times you recited that monologue?”

Agatha shrugged, blushing and rubbing the back of her neck. “I have no idea,” she said. “I guess I was just focusing on…I dunno, reading. I barely registered what the words meant.”

“Well, at least you fixed it before you bombed the audition,” Jen said, chipperly.

“Fuck off,” Agatha huffed, tossing herself down on Alice’s bed. “Your turn.”

Jen was about to open her mouth when there was a knock at Alice’s bedroom door. Without waiting for a response, Lorna burst in with a great big smile, practically dancing on her tiptoes in place.

“Come in,” Alice deadpanned, lifting one brow at Lorna. “What can I do for you, Mother?”

“You’ll never guess what I just got for you girls!” Lorna said. Agatha noticed then that she was hiding something behind her back.

“Instant Juilliard acceptances?” Jen guessed. 

“Nope,” Lorna snorted, rolling her eyes. “You still have to work for that, Miss Jennifer.”

“A puppy?” Alice asked, her eyes wide with excitement.

“Unfortunately, no,” Lorna sighed. “Don’t give up hope, though, sweetheart. One day.”

Alice pouted. 

All three turned to Agatha for her guess. She shrugged. 

“My mother’s obituary?” Agatha asked.

Jen let out a honk of laughter.

“Dark,” Alice murmured, but she was grinning.

Lorna snorted again. “No,” she said, “but good guess.” She pulled her hand out from behind her back to show them an envelope with her own name on it, but she said nothing. The three girls just stared at it, blinking up at her. Lorna sighed. “Now you’re supposed to guess what’s in the envelope,” she said.

“Can we just be finished with these guessing games, please?” Alice begged. “Jen still needs to work on her audition for Juilliard.”

“You’re no fun,” Lorna sighed. “Fine. They’re tickets to see Wicked !” She opened the envelope and showed them seven green and black slivers of thick paper.

“What?!” Jen exclaimed, jumping off the bed. She and Agatha ran straight to Lorna, Alice struggling to get out from behind the drumset before she joined them, and stared at the tickets in her hands. “How did you get these?”

The date was clear on the tickets; they were for tomorrow, after their audition. The matinee. And they were Orchestra . Front row .

“Lilia pulled some strings,” Lorna said, beaming. “And, you know, I know a few people.” She shrugged, still grinning. “We’re lucky they had enough seats to accommodate us all.”

“Us all?” Jen asked. “Who’s coming?”

“Your mother,” Lorna said. “And I invited Marisol and Rio, as well.” She smirked at Agatha’s flush. “I figured it would be good for you to all see your professional counterparts on an actual stage! Lilia was going to come with us, but George is whisking her off to Spain for the weekend to see his husband.”

“She’ll live,” Agatha snorted. “Wow, this is…this is so nice, Miss–ahem, Lorna .”

“Don’t mention it, sweetie,” Lorna said, squeezing her shoulder. “You deserve nice things. Especially after living with that ogre of a mother.” She rolled her eyes.

Agatha felt the sudden urge to hug the older woman – so she did.

Lorna let out a puff of air as Agatha wrapped her arms around her waist, pressing her face against Lorna’s shoulder, squeezing her tightly as she closed her eyes tight against the onslaught of tears. She felt Lorna’s free hand land on her back as she reciprocated the hug.

“Thank you,” Agatha said against her shoulder. “For everything.”

“Sweetheart,” Lorna said, pulling back to look Agatha in the eyes. “You have thanked me so much already. The words are going to start losing their meaning soon.” She pressed a kiss to Agatha’s forehead. “I told you already,” she said: “anything you need or want, all you need to do is ask. I’m happy to help you get pretty much anything.”

“She really is,” Alice confirmed. “Except a puppy.” She pouted at her mother.

“Little girl,” Lorna huffed, “you’re about to go off to college and neither of us is here enough to take care of a puppy, anyway .” She softly swatted Alice’s head, making the shorter girl laugh and roll her eyes. “Anyway,” Lorna said, looking back at Agatha, “ you are a part of this household now, Agatha. You’re one of us.”

“One of us, one of us, one of us,” Alice whispered. Agatha nudged her, half-heartedly and Alice cackled.

“Anything you need, you just let me know, okay?” Agatha nodded and Lorna pressed another kiss to her forehead. “Good,” she said. “Now, Jennifer, your mother said that you are going to be staying here with us tonight. Do you have everything you need for your audition? If you don’t, your mom said she’ll bring it when she meets us at the train station tomorrow.”

“I’ll call her,” Jen said. “Thanks, Lorna.”

“Of course, baby,” Lorna said. “Now, when you’re ready to eat, come on down for dinner. Chef made some good meals last night and I don’t want them to go to waste.” She gave the girls another squeeze before letting go and practically floating out the door.

“You won the lottery,” Agatha said to Alice, “in regards to moms, at least.”

“So did you,” Alice retorted, shrugging one shoulder. “It was a little late, but still.”

Agatha’s eyes widened at that. “She’s not my…I mean, I just…it’s not the…” she stuttered, her face turning pink as she tried to find the words.

“Dude,” Alice chuckled. “Relax. You heard what she said: you’re one of us now. That basically means she’s your mom, too. I’m just the favorite.” She gave Agatha a cheesy grin and the taller girl rolled her eyes and shoved her. Alice chortled as she knocked into Jen, who rolled her eyes at both of them.

“Okay,” Jen huffed. “That was such a beautiful Hallmark family moment. Can we go eat now? What did Chef make, anyway?”

“I saw some ribs in the fridge,” Alice said. “And some bowtie pasta with butter and broccoli. It smelled super good when he was cooking it yesterday.”

Agatha’s stomach let out a low growl as if remembering that she hadn’t eaten much that day at lunch. She’d split her lunch with Rio again, but she’d been too nervous about the audition tomorrow that she’d barely eaten her half. Rio had tried to get her to eat more, but Agatha’s nerves affected her appetite, so it just wasn’t going to happen.

Now , though, her stomach was overriding those nerves. It growled the whole way down to the kitchen, where Lorna had already heated up four meals in the microwave and set up four places at the kitchen table. The food smelled amazing , and Agatha’s stomach growled even more insistently as she sat down to Lorna’s right while Alice and Jen sat across from her, already digging into their ribs and pasta.

Agatha didn’t take long to join them, forgoing silverware in favor of picking up the ribs with her bare fingers, immediately chomping down on one.

The night before, she had gone to a local diner with Alice, Jen, Rio, Theo, and Sonny. Alice had told her that on nights that Chef cooked, he preferred that nobody disturb him so she and Lorna usually either went out or ordered takeout. Tonight, however, Lorna was at her recording studio, so she gave Alice her card to treat herself and her friends. 

They’d had burgers nearly the size of their heads, fries, and milkshakes that Agatha was certain would help her put on ten pounds from the sheer size alone. A tiny part of her felt guilty at the thought of it, her mother’s words echoing in her head about her needing to keep a good figure, but Rio had stolen three of her fries and Agatha had immediately retaliated by taking a big bite of her burger, which had avocado and a serrano pepper that practically burned a hole in her esophagus.

Rio had given her half of her own milkshake to apologize.

The ribs had a little kick to them, as well. But the burn on her tongue and lips wasn’t as bad as the serrano had been. It was actually quite tasty. Agatha couldn’t believe that she’d spent the last seventeen years eating food with little to no seasoning in it because of her mother. She’d definitely have to fix that over the next few months before she went off to college.

That thought got her heart racing again. She had known that this audition was coming for a while, had known that the end of February would bring this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity to impress her dream school, the one that she had been hoping to attend since she was a little kid, when a reporter had raved about her performance in Annie in the local paper, saying that she was destined for Broadway and that Juilliard should just hurry up and send her an acceptance letter already. Her theater director had placed that review with countless others on the notice board outside her office at the local children’s theatre. 

Of course, Agatha had back-ups in case she didn’t get into Juilliard. She hadn’t been lying when she told Rio she was also interested in spellcasting. She loved learning about magic and how it worked and all the different elements that could be combined to create new spells. There were still so many spells that needed to be discovered or invented. She wanted to be one of the ones to do that.

Maybe.

If she didn’t get into Juilliard. She doubted Juilliard had a spellcasting minor, let alone a major.

“Agatha?” 

Agatha blinked and found three sets of eyes staring at her, her rib halfway to her mouth still, only a couple of bites taken out of it. Alice’s head was tilted in curiosity. “You okay?” she asked.

“Fine,” Agatha said, clearing her throat. “Sorry. I was lost in thought. What did you say?”

“Mom was just going over the plans for tomorrow,” Alice said. “The auditions are pretty early, right? So we’re going to have some time to kill before heading to the theater.”

“We might even stay overnight,” Lorna added, casually taking another bite of her pasta.

“Really?” Agatha asked. “Won’t that be expensive?”

“Mom has a loft in the city,” Alice said. “Four bedrooms, plenty of space for all of us. Great views of Central Park, too. I’ll probably be living there if I get into Juilliard.”

“First-years need to live on campus,” Jen reminded her. 

“So, we’ll live there for the last three years then,” Alice conceded.

“ We ?” Agatha asked. Obviously she just meant her and Jen.

“You and Rio will be welcome to live there as well, of course,” Lorna said. “So long as you keep it tidy and keep up your studies.” She looked at Alice.

“You get a C one time…” Alice huffed, pushing her pasta around on her plate.

“In Mandarin ,” Lorna retorted. “You know Mandarin.”

“It was an oral test !” Alice exclaimed. “She said I was ‘mumbling and stuttering too much to comprehend’.”

“Then speak more clearly.”

“I’m in AP Chinese Lang and Culture now, aren’t I?” Alice pointed out. 

Lorna conceded.

“Me and Rio are allowed to live there?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow in confusion.

“Of course,” Lorna said with a gentle smile. “She seems like a nice girl, and her mother told me that she’s planning on attending Columbia, which is close enough to the loft for a good commute. Plus, if it saves Marisol money?” She gave a thumbs up before plucking another rib from her plate.

Agatha’s head swam with thoughts. She had known Lorna – or about her, at least – since she was a kid. She was Alice’s mother. She was a rockstar. She used to give Agatha rides home sometimes after rehearsals at the children’s theater, when Alice was still part of the cast. She had always been friendly. She had always waited for Agatha to get inside her house before driving off. She had attempted to speak to Evanora the few times they’d seen each other at school pickup (on the rare occasion that Evanora bothered to show up to gather Agatha, usually when they had an event to go to for her friends), but Evanora had been rather cold, which embarrassed Agatha to no end. 

She had known that Lorna enjoyed hosting the cast parties, that she chaperoned as many school dances as she could, and that she had welcomed Agatha into her home without even a second thought.

She was more of a mother to Agatha in less than a week than Evanora had been in nearly two decades, and it was making Agatha’s heart clench at the thought.

“Thank you,” Agatha said, softly. “I know I’ve said it way too much already, but really. Thank you so much for everything you’ve done for me, not just this last week but also for all the times you drove me home when we were kids, when my own mother wouldn’t even show up, when she treated you horribly whenever she did show up. Thank you for all of it.” She took a deep breath. “That’s the last one, I swear.”

“It better be,” Lorna said, pointing a finger at her. She smiled softly. “You’re welcome, Agatha,” she said. “ Now , finish your food. I bought some tiramisu for dessert.”

“Ooh,” Jen said, eyes twinkling with delight as she shoveled more pasta into her mouth. 

“That’s not spicy, is it?” Agatha asked, looking between the three of them.

All three women stared at her.

“Oh, my dear sweet child,” Lorna said. “We really need to expand that palate.”

 

The next morning, they rose at a quarter to seven. Jen’s audition was at ten and Agatha’s was at 10:30. The train would take a little over an hour to get from Westview to Grand Central, then they were taking one of those big SUVs from the station (Lorna didn’t trust the subway to get them there on time and not smelling of pee), and they’d hopefully have enough time to stretch and do vocal warmups. Agatha and Jen had each been instructed to prepare sixteen bars of a song to sing a capella, but they were also assured that their acceptance into the acting program wasn’t contingent on said songs. 

Still, it couldn’t hurt to sing them well.

Jen had chosen “Unbreak my Heart” by Toni Braxton, claiming that she knew that song by heart because her mother had sung it nonstop in the car when she was a kid – and still did.

Agatha chose “I Have Nothing” by Whitney Houston. It was ambitious, she knew, but Rio had been speechless the first time she sang it in front of her. That may have been because Agatha hadn’t taken her eyes off of her the entire time the song slipped from her lips. Rio had swooned , which sent a chill down Agatha’s spine.

For the audition, Agatha chose a deep purple, collared dress. It fell around her knees and was comfortable to move around in, loose enough around the skirt that it swished when she moved.

And it had pockets.

Since it was still February, she put on a pair of black leggings underneath it, along with her usual winter boots which should provide her with enough comfort for the walking they’d have to do later on.

She put her hair up in a simple ponytail, a few tendrils falling around her face. Checking herself out in the mirror, she was satisfied with how she looked. It was a simple outfit. It wasn’t going to wow anybody, but it would get the job done. And it wouldn’t distract the panel from her monologue. She’d read that that was important.

By the time everybody was ready to go, it was nearly eight AM and Jen was practically dancing in place impatiently by the door.

“Need to use the potty before we go, Jen?” Agatha teased as she walked up with Lorna behind her.

“Shut up, Agatha,” Jen huffed. “You know being late makes me nervous.”

“We’re not even late,” Agatha snorted. “We’ll be there in no time. Just relax.”

“Easy for the person with the later audition to say,” Jen huffed. “Lorna, are we ready?”

“We’re ready,” Lorna said. “Come on, girls! Everybody in the car.”

She herded them out to the SUV with a wave of her arms, practically shoving all three girls across the driveway and into the car. It had already been warming up, so by the time they piled in and shut the doors, Lorna took off.

Rio and Marisol met them on the platform. Agatha watched Rio’s gaze take in her dress (partially hidden by her coat) and hair, the taller girl’s cheeks turning pink.

“Wow,” she said. “You look great.”

“Thanks,” Agatha said. “So do you. I’m glad you’re finally wearing a jacket.”

Rio frowned. “Mami made me,” she huffed.

“¡ Por supuesto! ” Marisol said, swatting the back of Rio’s head. “¡ Hace frio! Tonta. ”

“Rude,” Rio said with a pout.

“What does ‘tonta’ mean?” Agatha whispered as they shuffled onto the train. 

“Dummy,” Rio said, her pout deepening.

“Well,” Agatha snorted, slipping into a seat and pulling Rio down to sit with her. “She’s not wrong.”

Rio let out a dramatic gasp, clutching imaginary pearls on her chest. “Traitor!”

Agatha laughed and reached for Rio’s hand, bringing it up to her lips to kiss her knuckles.

“ Lo siento, cariño ,” she murmured against Rio’s skin. Rio became pinker than before, if that was even possible.

“Forgiven,” she said, clearing her throat. Agatha laughed, leaning her head on Rio’s shoulder as she took out her phone and ear buds, handing one over to her girlfriend as they settled in for the train ride.

 

By some miracle, even with all the traffic from the train station to the college, they arrived at Juilliard at 9:35. Jen had just enough time to change into her own audition outfit, a pink blouse and wool slacks, and do vocal warmups with Alice and her mom (Naomi could be a stage mom when the situation warranted) before she was rushing out of the car with Agatha right behind her. Agatha pressed a kiss to Rio’s lips for good luck before they disappeared into the building. 

“Break a leg,” Agatha said as they got to the room where the acting auditions were happening. “I hope you do only slightly worse than me.”

“I think that may be the nicest thing you’ve said to me in the last decade,” Jen said, bumping Agatha’s shoulder with her own as they signed in and took their seats in a long hall with other Juilliard hopefuls. 

Jen’s name was called not long after they arrived, leaving Agatha alone in a room full of people. People, she reminded herself, with whom might soon attend school if everything went her way.

Things rarely went her way in life.

But maybe this time.

Jen’s audition lasted fifteen minutes exactly. Agatha counted all the way to nine hundred, with Mississippis, before she reemerged. Jen had a soft smile on her lips and sweat dotting her forehead as she gave Agatha a thumbs up, making her way to the exit. Agatha offered her a nervous smile in return as she watched Jen leave the building.

She waited another fifteen minutes as somebody else took their turn before her name was called into the hallway.

“Agatha Harkness?”

Agatha stood up and made her way to the door where a pretty blonde woman was standing with a clipboard. “You nervous?” she whispered, guiding Agatha into the room, which was large with a small stage and an audience of chairs. Five people sat at a table in front of the chairs, each with a stack of papers in front of them, notes scattered about.

“No,” Agatha lied. “Not nervous at all.”

“Good,” the blonde said, “because they can smell fear.”

“Helpful,” Agatha snorted, taking a deep breath as she stepped up on the stage.

“Name?” The man in the first seat on the left asked.

“Agatha Harkness,” she said. 

All five sets of eyes looked up from their papers at the sound of her name. Agatha suddenly felt like a bug under a microscope.

“You’re Lilia’s girl,” the first man said, a soft smile on his lips. “I’ve heard about you.”

“You have?” Agatha asked, her heart hammering in her chest.

“We all have, dear,” the woman next to him said. “Lilia has sent us more students than we can count over the years. There was one not even a half hour ago, I believe.”

Agatha nodded. “Yeah,” she said, clearing her throat. 

“Well, if Lilia spoke highly of you,” a second man said, all the way to the right of the table, “then you must be good. I can’t wait to hear it.”

The rest of them murmured and nodded in agreement.

“Whenever you’re ready, Miss Harkness,” a second woman said, nodding.

Agatha nodded in return and shook out her hands, clearing her throat as she took a deep breath. She swallowed thickly and began:

“Why? Why do I feel this rage?”

 

Agatha couldn’t remember a single second of her interview. Except that it was quiet. 

It was quiet as she recited her monologue the first time.

It was quiet as she recited it a second time when they requested that she recite it with more “irony”.

It was quiet as she sang her song until they told her to stop singing.

It was quiet as they thanked her and asked her to step out of the room, that they’d be in touch in a few weeks, via email. 

She was quiet as she thanked them and walked out of the room, her legs moving almost independently from the rest of her body, carrying her back out into the hall and toward the exit.

Jen and Alice and Rio were all pacing on the sidewalk, waiting for her. Their moms were hanging out of the windows in the three-row SUV. Their driver was scrolling on his phone as he waited for his next instructions. 

Alice was the first one to notice her, eyes widening as Agatha approached them, dazed.

“So?” she asked, garnering the attention of the others. “How did it go?”

“I…have no idea,” Agatha replied honestly. “Good, I think. I kinda blacked out.”

“So did I,” Jen said, “a little bit. They had me do my monologue four different ways.”

“I had to do it three times,” Agatha said, nodding. She cleared her throat. “They said I’ll find out in a few weeks, via email.”

“Okay,” Lorna said, clapping her hands, “well then, there’s nothing we can do but wait for that email. Who’s hungry?”

“Ooh, me,” Alice said, hopping back into the car. Jen followed her into the third row, where she sat between Alice and Naomi. Agatha settled in next to Rio, Marisol on Rio’s other side. She laid her head down on Rio’s shoulder and smiled when she felt Rio’s lips on her hairline.

“I’m sure you did great,” Rio whispered in her ear. “You’ve definitely got a spot.”

“I hope so,” Agatha sighed, pressing her nose against Rio’s neck. “Otherwise, I gotta go to one of my backups.”

“Which are…?” 

“Columbia or NYU.”

“Columbia could be fun,” Rio said. Agatha felt the smile against her forehead. “I heard some really great, talented, successful people go to Columbia.”

Agatha snorted, closing her eyes as she settled in for the ride.

Chapter End Notes

The Antigone monologue was a find. It's a modern version of a Greek play, I believe. I'm pretty sure the original is by Sophocles if you wanna check it out.

The next chapter will have a time jump. I had actually started writing it to be THIS chapter before realizing that I forgot about the audition, oops! It should be out soonish.

Chapter 22: New Routines

Chapter Summary

Agatha starts to get used to her new routine

Chapter Notes

:)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty-Two

Agatha had already seen Wicked three times – now four – in person, but it never stopped taking her breath away. She, Rio, Alice, and Jen were all seated in the front row, center, with snacks in their hands (courtesy of Lorna’s deep pockets), and the three moms in the row immediately behind them. They were practically vibrating with excitement as they waited for the show to begin. Rio was at one end of the group, her fingers laced with Agatha’s on the armrest between them, and Alice was on the other end, her arms wrapped around Jen’s as Jen rested her cheek on her head, pressing kisses there every now and then.

As the lights flickered out, their excitement only increased and the first notes began to play. Rio was surprised by just how excited she was to see the play in person. She’d never been a musical person. She’d never had the urge to see a play on Broadway. She’d only ever seen Wicked and only because Lilia had strong-armed her into the role of Fiyero (which, in hindsight, was probably the best thing that could have happened to her, given the girl currently squeezing her hand as the overture boomed overhead) and she’d found a “slime tutorial” online. 

But her heart fluttered as the now-familiar music filled the room around them. She felt and heard her mother’s gasp behind them as the ‘flying monkeys’ ran around the stage, doing acrobatics and screeching. She sat up a little bit straighter when the Munchkinlanders entered and started singing about the demise of ‘the wicked witch of the west’ and how excited they all were for it. She heard Jen’s little whoop as Galinda started floating down in her bubble onstage. She grinned when Agatha squeezed her hand at the sight of Elphaba rushing forward with her suitcase, looking bright and happy as she stared out into the distance over the audience’s head.

She felt it all with them, the fluttering in her chest and her stomach.

Since her father’s passing, Rio had not known she could feel this kind of giddiness again. She had been a true ‘Daddy’s girl’ as a kid, always wanting to help him in the yard or his workshop. She’d learned how to change the oil when she was eight, had learned all the different parts of a car and what each one was responsible for. She had even helped him in the kitchen, on the odd nights that he cooked (usually during the winter, when he didn’t work as often due to the cold), and learned how to ‘properly season’ her food. Marisol would just watch them from the dinner table, amused as he gently guided her through stirring pots or shredding chicken or pork, or making good rice. He taught her how to make plenty of dishes so that Marisol wouldn’t need to handle dinner every single night after his passing.

When he passed, Rio’s entire world seemed to implode. They’d known it was coming for a while. He had gotten sick when she was twelve years old, but he’d kept it hidden from them both until he collapsed at work, while mowing a typically easy lawn. His workers had jumped into action immediately, calling an ambulance and reviving him, helping him up and lifting him into the ambulance. Rio had been thirteen at the time, her entire body cold with fear as she and her mother rushed to the hospital to meet him.

Her father had offered them a serene smile when they entered his room. He was hooked up to what had felt like a hundred machines, all beeping and flashing, but he didn’t seem to mind them. He only had eyes for his family. He welcomed Rio to climb into the hospital bed with him, to press her face into his shoulder as tears ran down her cheeks. He held Marisol’s hand as the doctor came in and revealed a heartbreaking diagnosis.

He was gone within a year after that. 

Rio had thought he took all the light in her life with him.

But now, holding Agatha’s hand in this darkened theater, as they watched their stage counterparts slowly fall in love (though Rio had to admit that Agatha was correct: Galinda and Elphaba totally had way more chemistry and they should have ended up together) she started to feel that light again.

Rio leaned closer to Agatha, detangling her fingers in favor of placing her arm around the other girl’s shoulders, pulling her closer. She leaned in, the words still threatening to slip from her lips and into Agatha’s ear, but she instead pressed her lips to Agatha’s temple, mouthing the words there instead.

They had plenty of time for that.

She woke up an hour before Lorna was meant to drive them to school. Some mornings, she lounged for about fifteen minutes in bed before getting up to wash her face and change. Other mornings, she rose immediately and took a shower. It usually depended on how late she’d stayed up texting Rio the night prior.

Nobody could even walk onto the property without express permission from either Marisol or Rio. Evanora, specifically, would practically burst into flames if she or anybody with ill intent went near the house. 

So far, she was smart enough to stay away.

Agatha just hoped that meant her mother had given up on trying to take control over her life again. She very much doubted it, though. Despite Evanora’s obvious loathing for her own daughter, she had a desperate need to control Agatha, to make her compliant, to make her good in only the way that Evanora thought was acceptable.

Agatha wondered if she’d have actually been free of her mother when she turned eighteen. She could imagine Evanora trying to pull some kind of bullshit to keep her under her thumb, or to somehow keep the trace on her indefinitely had she not had the help of Lorna, Naomi, Lilia, and Marisol, as well as her…friends?

Yes, they were her friends.

She and Jen might bicker and insult each other, but she knew that Jen still had her back when she needed her. And Alice had never been mean to her, even when she’d have every right to be. Now, they did their homework together at the kitchen island after theater rehearsals, asked each other for advice on shared assignments for their classes, and watched TV together in a den that was practically a full-sized movie theater.

Alice claimed that it had been a second formal dining room that Lorna had thought was a little too much, even for the extravagance of her mansion. Adding a full, wall-sized screen, projector, and half a dozen pieces of furniture to sit on with blankets and pillows and special trays for snacks and such wasn’t much less extravagant, in Agatha’s opinion.

Agatha could probably live there a hundred years and never make it through everything, especially since Lorna was part of the Motion Picture Academy (enough of her music had been used in movies and she was nominated enough times to be part of that scene) and always received the films for consideration. Sometimes, she and Alice would just stand in Lorna’s movie room – yes, it was an entire room of movies on shelves along the walls and in the center of the room – and pick three at random to watch.

Jojo Rabbit had made them sob. Bridesmaids had been a good palate cleanser after that. Eternal Sunshine of the Spotless Mind had left Agatha reeling as she went to bed that night. She added all three to the list of movies she’d have to show Rio at some point.

“A skip could jeopardize my Valedictorian eligibility.”

Agatha groaned. “And we wouldn’t want that, would we, nerd?”

Rio pulled back with a laugh. “You also have a four-point-oh average, nerd ,” she teased, cupping Agatha’s cheek, her thumb swiping over the ridge of her cheekbone as she leaned in, pressing their foreheads together, nudging her nose. “I love you,” she whispered in the space between their lips.

She leaned forward that last inch, kissing Rio slow and soft, pouring every ounce of affection and love into their embrace before she pulled back and reached down to interlock their fingers, tugging Rio up the next flight of stairs to Lilia’s classroom.

“What’s going on?” Agatha asked Jen as she and Rio slipped into their seats in front of her and Theo.

“Lilia just emailed everybody telling us that she was going to be late,” Jen said, looking at her phone. “You two lucked out. “Because I was sleeping ,” Jen huffed. “I live across the street. I’m not dragging myself out of bed a second too soon to come to this hellhole.”

“Dramatic bitch,” Agatha huffed, causing Rio to snort. Jen flipped her off.

Her hair was flying around just as wildly as those papers, sticking up at odd places all over her head, falling out of her usually semi-structured messy bun. Her clothes were even more mismatched than usual. There was a coffee stain on her yellow cardigan, but she held no coffee cup. 

She had on two different sneakers that may have even been different sizes.

“Are you okay, Lilia?” Theo asked, furrowing his brow in concern. “You look like you’ve had a rough morning.”

“Boy,” Lilia huffed, setting everything down on the table, “you don’t know the half of it.” She dropped into her chair, red-faced and exhausted. “My alarm didn’t go off this morning. I think I may have lost power at my house sometime during the night, actually. But that’s fine because I woke up only about twenty minutes later than usual. I got dressed and started my coffee machine…which exploded.”

“Exploded?” Jen gasped while others laughed. 

“ Exploded! ” Lilia emphasized, throwing her hands up. “I didn’t have time to change, but one of my shoes was absolutely drenched . Chapter 23: Hexenbesen

Chapter Summary

This is a short chapter, but there's a little bit of fluff and comedy.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Twenty-Three

Rio fell asleep halfway through Legally Blonde .

“She’s missing the best part!” Jen huffed, motioning to the screen, where Elle Woods was questioning the deceased’s daughter, Chutney. What kind of name even was Chutney?!?

Agatha paused the movie, careful not to jostle the girl sleeping (and drooling) against her shoulder as she did so.

It was nearing three in the morning and they’d already watched three movies before getting to the one currently playing on the wall-sized screen before them. Rio had been able to keep her eyes open through Who Framed Roger Rabbit?, Matilda ( the 90’s version, but she had plans to watch the musical later ), and Forrest Gump (which Agatha could swear had brought her to tears, but Rio would never admit to it). 

She had been fading halfway through Forrest Gump, but Rio had forced herself to sit upright on the couch next to Agatha, holding firm to the refilled popcorn bowl as she attempted to follow the convoluted story of the movie, making comments every now and then.

“Jenny’s kind of a piece of shit, isn’t she?” Rio had murmured. “I mean, I know Forrest loves her and all, but she slept with him, left him the morning after, got knocked up, and waited, like, five years to tell him he had a kid? What the hell?!” She looked at Agatha. “You’d tell me right away if I knocked you up, right?”

“I don’t think we have to worry about that anytime soon,” Agatha had laughed, feeling a flush crawl up her neck at the thought, “but yes, of course.” She kissed Rio’s lips, earning a happy smile from the other girl as she automatically cuddled back into her side.

She’d heard Rio’s sniffles as the movie ended, but her eyes had been dry as she got up to put the next film on. By the time she returned to her seat next to Rio, the other girl had a vacant stare, obviously exhausted.

“You wanna call it a night?” Agatha had asked, running her hands through Rio’s hair.

“No!” Jen and Alice whined from the other side of the couch.

“This is the best one!” Jen huffed. “She can suck it up for two more hours, can’t you, Vidal?”

“I’ve never seen this one before,” Alice admitted.

“You’re dating what is essentially black Elle Woods and you’ve never seen Legally Blonde before?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

“It’s not really my kind of movie,” Alice admitted. “But now I’m kind of excited to see it.” She pouted and made her eyes all big as she looked around at the three of them.

“I can hold on,” Rio said. “Just start it quickly.”

Agatha nodded and made quick work of switching the films, settling in next to her girlfriend as the opening credits started. Rio handed her the bowl of popcorn as she cuddled into Agatha’s side. Agatha wrapped her arm around her shoulders, popping some popcorn into her mouth. 

Rio was able to hold on for the first hour, but somewhere around the time Callahan hit on Elle (“What a bastard,” Rio said, sleepily) she started dozing off. By the time they got to the part where Elle’s professor was encouraging her to return, Rio let out a little snore, which woke her up a little bit.

By the time they got to the infamous courtroom scene, she was full-on drooling against Agatha’s pajama top, completely curled up against her side.

“Sorry,” she whispered, tossing the remote toward them. “I’m gonna take her to bed. When she swung around to see Jen and Alice, she found their eyes wide and jaws practically on the floor. “What?” Agatha huffed. “You’ve never seen anybody use a levitation spell before?”

She grunted slightly as she carried Rio out of the room and down the hall. Rio wasn’t heavy at all, but Agatha wasn’t exactly a lifter and untrained witchling magic could only do so much. She was just thankful that Lorna’s theater was on the same floor as her bedroom.

There were flowers and wedding dresses involved the last time she imagined it, and it had been a while since the thought had crossed her mind, actually. 

Also, Rio had been the one carrying Agatha in her daydreams. And Rio had been wearing a dapper, dark green suit and a black dress shirt beneath with gold accents… not an oversized green, off-the-shoulder shirt, dark gray sweatpants, and mismatched socks.

Not that Agatha had thought very much about it. Not at all.

She looked gorgeous, regardless, Agatha thought as she finally lay her down on the bed, smiling as Rio cuddled into Agatha’s pillow, letting out a contented sigh. Agatha pulled a blanket from the end of the bed to cover her before walking around to the other side to slip in under the comforter, automatically reaching for her girlfriend.

Agatha had never had a sleepover with anybody before. Her mother had never allowed it, not even with the daughters of her friends. She didn’t want Agatha to “embarrass” her in some odd way. And she wasn’t really allowed over to anybody outside their group’s house, so she had missed out on a lot of teen girl milestones.

Camp was the only exception, it seemed

Now, as she settled in for the night, watching the even rise and fall of her girlfriend’s chest on the other side of the bed, she started to wonder what it would have been like to have had a normal upbringing. What would her life have been like if she’d had a mother who loved her, who allowed her all the same freedoms as the other girls at school, who let her invite friends over or go to other girls’ houses for slumber parties…

Would she still have felt that connection to Rio? Rio, who was dark and strange and somewhat introverted and shy. Rio, who gave Agatha flowers and helped her with whatever she’d asked for. Would Agatha have asked for her help if she’d had anybody else? If Rio hadn’t been her only choice?

Rio turned over in her sleep, her arms reaching across the bed, fingertips just brushing against Agatha’s waist before she immediately scooched closer across the bed. Agatha met her halfway, smiling as Rio wrapped herself around her body like a koala – as much as she could with Agatha under the covers and Rio over them, anyway. Agatha wrapped her arms around Rio, pressing a kiss to the crown of her head as Rio’s nose found its rightful place in the crook of her neck.

Yes , Agatha decided. She liked to think that, in any universe, she and Rio would find each other and fall in love. Even in a universe where there was no magic, Rio would find a way to give Agatha flowers, to woo her with her awkward kind of charm. And Agatha would fall for it every single time, happily.

She wrapped her arms more tightly around Rio, pressing her lips to Rio’s forehead, and whispered, “I love you,” into the darkness that surrounded them. The sky outside was still navy blue, the white stars still twinkling against the dark backdrop. Everything was quiet…

“I love you, too,” Rio whispered back, still half asleep, and Agatha’s heart swelled as she closed her eyes, burying her face into Rio’s hair as they finally drifted off together.

 

The next morning, it took three blaring alarms to bring them back to life, as well as Jen and Alice practically shaking them awake.

“Yo, get up !” Alice huffed, kneeling on the bed next to Agatha, who had migrated to the very middle with Rio, the two of them tangling under the covers at some point in the last few hours, their bodies completely intertwined now. Alice is bouncing the bed, however, jostling them as best as her tiny body can. “It’s almost nine ! You’re gonna be late for rehearsal and then Lilia is gonna blame me for not getting you up in time!”

Agatha and Rio let out twin groans, holding each other a little more tightly as they attempted to ignore the interruption to their sleep.

“Five more minutes,” Agatha moaned.

“Five minutes, my ass!” Jen’s voice hissed. She appeared on the other side of the bed. “We don’t have five minutes! We gotta go!” She wrapped an arm around Rio’s waist, tugging her to the edge of the bed. Rio let out a strangled squeak, her arms reaching out for Agatha as she was pulled away. Agatha reached back, dramatically, but Alice used all of her strength to turn her over to face her.

“Get up !” she growled. “You are our Elphaba; we need you to show up to rehearsal on time!”

“But I’m so tired, ” Agatha groaned, pouting at Alice.

“Jen and I stayed up to watch the rest of the movie you abandoned ,” Alice reminded her, “while you two went to sleep. It was amazing, by the way.”

“Right?” Agatha laughed sleepily. “So good…” She started to close her eyes again, but Alice stopped her, literally prying them both open. 

“Wake up !” she said. “Go get some coffee and let’s get out of here before Lilia comes looking for us.”

“Ugh, fine,” Agatha groaned, shoving the shorter girl away and slipping out from under the covers. She stretched and turned to see Jen barking at Rio like a drill sergeant, urging her to hurry up and get dressed while she chased her around the bedroom. Agatha couldn’t help but snort, shaking her head as she grabbed a bra from the dresser and disappeared into the ensuite to put it on under her pajamas and relieve herself before washing her face for the day.

She forewent any kind of makeup and just tossed her hair into a ponytail before walking out to grab her girlfriend and the other two losers.

Rio was completely dressed (sneakers included) and waiting for her by the door when she padded out of the bathroom. She was slumped slightly against the doorframe, hands in her pockets as she attempted not to completely collapse back into slumber. Agatha smiled, approaching her, and placed a soft kiss on her sleepy lips, which was reciprocated immediately. 

“Ready?” Agatha asked, voice soft and filled with affection.

“As I’ll ever be,” Rio sighed. “It’s only a few hours, right? How bad could it be?”

“Just wait,” Agatha laughed.

Rio groaned. “That sounds way too foreboding for a Saturday morning.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, taking her hand and dragging her down to the kitchen, where Jen was screwing the caps on four tumblers at the kitchen island. She handed the orange one off to Alice with a loving smile.

“Come get your morning energy shots,” she said, holding out the green and purple tumblers. “Coffee and hot chocolate with a little bit of my own personal brew to give you the energy you need to withstand Lilia’s neuroticism.” 

“I’m telling her you said that,” Agatha snorted, taking a sip of her coffee.

“Go ahead,” Jen huffed. “She knows it’s true.”

“Where’s Lorna?” Rio asked, taking a sip of her hot chocolate with a sigh. “Isn’t she driving?”

“Nope,” Alice said. “Mom is sleeping in this morning; she had a super late night. She said we can take some of the old branches from the trees outside and do a hexenbesen.”

Agatha’s eyes widened at that. “Seriously?” she gasped. “A hexenbesen ? I’ve never done one of those before.”

“Jen and I have,” Alice said. “It’s not that difficult. We’ll show up.”

“Hurry up, though,” Jen said, already heading toward the backyard, where a bunch of old trees stood, branches gathered in a pile between them, “or else we’re leaving you in our dust.”

Rio and Agatha shared a grin as they hurried out after the others, tucking their hot drinks into the pockets on their backpacks. 

Jen was already plucking one of the branches from the pile, testing it out to make sure that it was big enough – it definitely was – before turning to her girlfriend. Alice did the same, smiling up at Jen as they started to spin in a circle, chanting in unison:

“ Pro te, dilecta, aperio viam. ” They exchanged brooms with a kiss.

“The kiss isn’t necessary,” Alice said, with a blush, “but it’s an added perk.”

“Damn right it is,” Jen said, pressing another kiss to Alice’s lips.

“Gross,” Agatha huffed, plucking another branch from the pile. It still had leaves clinging to one end. Perfect. 

Rio picked up another branch, which had a few dead flowers clinging to it. With a wiggle of her fingers, they were brought back to life, more vibrant than ever. She made a few more sprout as well before turning to Agatha, who rolled her eyes at her sentimentality, but she was smiling.

“Ready?” Rio asked. Agatha nodded and they placed the ends of their brooms together. 

“ Pro te, dilecta, aperio viam ,” they chanted as they spun in a circle. Then Rio leaned in, pressing a kiss to Agatha’s lips as they exchanged brooms, their fingers brushing.

“It is a nice perk,” she said, earning a snort from Agatha.

“Okay, lovebirds,” Jen said. “Let’s get going. All you gotta do is run forward a little, but the broom between your legs, and push off. The broom should do the rest. Steer with your body.”

Agatha and Rio nodded as they lined up with Jen and Alice on the lawn.

“Ready…set…go!” Alice said, running ahead of the rest of them. She placed her broom under her and jumped, letting out a whoop as she rose up in the air. Jen was close behind her.

Rio and Agatha shared another smile before taking off in tandem, jumping onto their own brooms and letting out excited shouts as they flew up into the air. Agatha reached out, grabbing Rio’s hand as she wobbled slightly on her broom. Rio’s grip was tight on hers, reassuring.

The forcefield that surrounded the Wus’ household glowed orange above their heads as they got closer, but it was easy to spot Alice using her own Protection magic to create an opening large enough for all of them to fly through before it closed up behind them.

“Stay vigilant,” Alice said. “We’re not as protected up here by outside threats.”

“Meaning my mother?” Agatha asked. “I honestly don’t even think she’s up this early on a Saturday.” Saturdays were the only day of the week that Evanora Harkness didn’t have work or church to get to, so she slept in…until ten. No later. Checking her phone, Agatha saw that it was a quarter-to.

“Still,” Alice said. “That woman seems unhinged. No telling what she’d try if she just happened to see you, or any of us, flying up here on brooms. You’re protected by the amulet, but the rest of us are pretty screwed when we’re not at home or in the school, so it would be great if we could find cover sooner rather than later.”

“Why can’t you just make amulets for the rest of you?” Agatha asked, flying up next to her, still holding Rio’s hand with one hand and keeping herself steady on her broom with the other.

“Because it requires a possession from the specific person you’re trying to protect yourself from, like that necklace.” Agatha didn’t touch it, but she could feel the necklace under her shirt as they flew. “I don’t think any of us wants to get close enough to your mom to get another personal item of hers.” She shuddered.

“Good point,” Rio said, shrugging, “but you can’t just make a general protection amulet?”

“Protection magic is more complicated than that,” Alice sighed, running her hand through her hair before letting it blow freely in the wind. “If I gave you a protection amulet, it would keep everybody away from you, including your family members and your girlfriend – not just the people who might cause you harm because anybody might cause you harm, you know?”

“That blows,” Rio huffed. Agatha squeezed her hand.

“Yeah,” Alice admitted, “but, hopefully, we don’t have to worry too much about it. So long as we’re at the school, my house, or your house, we are protected from the likes of Evanora Harkness. Speaking of…”

The school came into view…

There was smoke billowing out of a second floor window – Lilia’s window.

Chapter End Notes

Gonna blame the Rio-shaped Devil on my shoulder for the cliffhanger on this one. #noragrets

Chapter 24: Something Odd

Chapter Summary

Lilia is in danger and weird things are happening in her classroom.

Also, the first dress rehearsal is underway!!

(sorry this took so long but AAA Week took up a Lot of my time)

Chapter Notes

I'm baaaaaaaack! Didja miss me???

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty-Four
