The girls wasted no time in flying directly into Lilia’s window, Alice creating a forcefield around them and their brooms to avoid smoke inhalation. She was the first to touch down on the tile in Lilia’s classroom, followed closely by Agatha, then Jen, then Rio.

“Lilia!” Alice called out. “Lilia are you in here?”

The smoke was thick and white, filling the room with a soupy fog. They couldn’t see more than a few inches in front of them, their brooms clattering to the ground as they started to look around for the source of the smoke.

They heard coughing and Agatha nearly broke the forcefield in an attempt to reach the source of it, but Alice pulled her back.

“Stop!” she said. “We still don’t know what’s causing it!”

“It’s a fire, isn’t it?” Jen asked, looking around, her brows furrowed.

“No,” Rio said, shaking her head. “The smoke is too white. And it smells too…cold.” She looked at Alice. “Does it smell like a fog machine to you?”

“Yeah…” Alice said, dissipating the forcefield. The white smoke immediately moved in on her and she waved it away with her hand before taking a deep breath and sending a wave of air at the smoke, clearing as much of it from their path as possible.

A figure emerged from the smoke in the middle of the room: Lilia, with a scarf wrapped around her face, coughing and wheezing. Rio rushed to her side, rubbing her back as the smoke from a malfunctioning fog machine started to fill up the space again.

“Unplug it!” Alice called, sending another wave of air their way. Rio nodded and reached for the plug nearby, tugging it out of the wall. 

The machine’s light hum, which none of them had even noticed before due to Lilia’s incessant coughing, went quiet. The fog started to dissipate. Alice helped it along with one more wave aimed at the window, sending as much white smoke as possible out into the world, airing out the room.

Once the majority of the smoke was gone, it revealed Rio and Lilia once more, both coughing as Rio used the end of Lilia’s scarf to cover her own mouth, tears leaking from her eyes as she attempted to breathe through it. Agatha rushed to her side, waving away the smoke with one hand as she patted Rio’s back with the other. Jen did the same for Lilia while Alice continued to funnel the fog out of the room, opening the other windows to make it go faster.

“What happened?” Alice asked as soon as the room was fully clear. “Why is the fog machine in here?”

“I was testing it,” Lilia said, still coughing slightly as she hobbled to her desk and pulled an inhaler out of her purse. She took a puff, inhaling the soothing medicine. 

“Why in here?” Jen asked. “Why not on the stage?”

“They’re still setting up downstairs,” Lilia explained, collapsing into her seat behind the desk. She took another puff from her inhaler and shoved it back into her purse. “Besides, the fog machine was in the supply closet by the sound booth. It was easier to just drag it in here for testing. I didn’t think it would go berzerk !” She glared at the machine in question. “I shoulda known better; that thing’s as old as the hills! And that’s saying a lot considering my prom dress was medieval.”

“They had prom in the…oh, that was a joke.” Rio blushed and cleared her throat as Jen snickered. Rio flipped her off. “Anyway, let me check it out. Maybe it’s just a bad switch or something.”

She kneeled by the fog machine. Lilia was right: this thing was old . There was duct tape covering at least forty percent of it, with visible scuff marks and ages of wear and tear all over the other sixty. She found the switch on the machine, finding it flipped to the On position. She flicked it to the Off position. 

It flicked immediately back to the On position. 

Rio frowned, flicking it back to Off .

It flicked back to On .

“Hmm,” she hummed.

“What?” Alice asked, crouching down at her side.

“This is hexed,” Rio said, definitively. 

“How can you tell?” Jen asked from her space next to Lilia, still rubbing her back.

“The way it’s flicking back to On when I try to turn it off,” Rio explained. “It’s too smooth to be a machine malfunction, especially with no electricity running through it. This is definitely magical.”

“Who the hell would hex a fog machine ,” Lilia huffed. 

Jen and Agatha shared a look.

“Harper,” they said in unison.

“Or Agatha’s mom,” Rio pointed out.

“There’s no way she could have gotten to the fog machine,” Alice said, shaking her head. “She’s banned from the school. She can’t step foot anywhere on the grounds.”

“Then it’s almost definitely Harper,” Jen said. “Or one of her lackeys. You’d think a girl would learn after getting her nose stretched to nearly a footlong not to fuck with us.”

“Harper isn’t exactly a super genius,” Agatha huffed. “I’m surprised she could even do this hex on her own.”

“As am I,” Lilia muttered. All four pairs of eyes looked at her. “She was never my student, but teachers talk in the teacher’s lounge. She’s not doing well in school.”

“Not surprising,” Rio snorted, getting to her feet. “I think you should talk to Principal Davis about getting this replaced, unless anybody knows how to break this hex.”

“I probably do,” Lilia hummed, “but, honestly, I’ve been trying to get her to pony up for some new equipment for years . This may just be the excuse I need to replace at least one thing.”

“You can borrow one of my mom’s fog machines,” Alice said, “in case she still says no.”

“How many fog machines does your mom own?” Agatha snorted.

“A rockstar can never have too many,” Alice retorted, rolling her eyes goodnaturedly. “She has at least a dozen just in our house alone. She’d probably thrill at the chance to be helpful by lending the drama department one.”

“Well, we’ll take it,” Lilia said, “so long as she fool-proofs it first. I don’t trust that dolt not to pull the same trick twice.”

“Neither do I,” Agatha huffed, crossing her arms over her chest. “Anyway, should we make our way down to the stage? They’re probably wondering where their Elphaba is.”

“You’re so full of yourself,” Jen snorted, shaking her head as she bumped Agatha on her way out the door. Alice followed her, shrugging at Agatha’s scandalized look, then snorting when Agatha pouted at her.

“You two,” Lilia just chuckled as she followed them. 

Rio was last, taking Agatha’s hand as she passed, tugging her out of the room. “Come on, drama queen,” she said, affectionately, bringing Agatha’s fingers up to her lips as she tugged her out of the classroom and toward the auditorium. 

Agatha grumbled something under her breath, but she couldn’t hold back the grin that sprouted on her lips at the display of affection.

 

The stage looked… amazing . The tech crew really went all out. Even Rio was impressed, letting out a low whistle as she walked down the aisle with the rest of their group.

“Sweet Goddess ,” Rio exclaimed, her fingers slipping out of Agatha’s as she rushed toward the stage, her eyes wide as a smile stretched across her face. “Look at all this! You all did this without me ?”

“What?” one of the techies – a lanky kid with his black hair in a ponytail. “Like it’s hard?”

“I understand that reference now,” Rio said, pointing to him as she wrapped her arm around his shoulders to pull him down to her height, still looking around. “Man, I remember when you were just a widdle freshie!” She noogied him. “Now, look at you!”

“I’m only a year younger than you!” he grumbled. 

“And yet ,” Rio said, “it took you a whole year not to flinch at a power drill.”

“Fuck off, Vidal,” he huffed, shoving her away.

“Hey, just because I’m in the cast for this show doesn’t mean I’m not still your stage manager, ergo your boss ,” Rio reminded him. Then she softened. “But seriously, Wyatt – good going. This set looks incredible .”

The high school set was very much fashioned after the Broadway production, with gear motifs and platforms on the side of the stage. Rio could see the large head that was meant to be the Wizard just off stage-right. There were stairs and ladders painted in a very steampunk fashion. The workmanship was incredible, too, as she tested out all the parts of the set that were meant to hold the weight of one or more of the actors (herself included) and not one of them budged. 

Very good.

There were tears in her eyes, she was so proud of her little techies.

“Look at me,” she sniffled, “getting all choked up. Man, I wish I could be backstage with you all during this production, bossing you around like old times.” A chuckle went through the scattered tech crew members. “But it looks like you might be able to handle yourselves without me for this one.”

“Have you decided who’s going to be acting in your absence?” Wyatt asked. “I know it’s not me – not yet – but I doubt you’ll be able to do much while you’re waiting for your cues.”

“Oh, right,” Rio said with a sigh, “yeah I should probably do that.”

She felt somebody grasp her hand and turned to see Agatha standing beside her, smiling supportively at her. Rio smiled back, suddenly in awe of where she was. She never would have imagined she’d be in this position just a few months ago – leading the school musical with Agatha not only as her leading lady but also as her girlfriend , the girl she loved who loved her right back.

It was surreal.

Rio cleared her throat and looked around at the techies who had started gathering in front of the stage, looking up at her as though she were a king about to make a proclamation.

She kinda was.

“Um,” she said, smartly, her cheeks warming. “Wow,” she said, scratching the back of her neck with her free hand (because she was not willing to let go of her girlfriend’s comforting touch right now) “I don’t even know what to say right now. I’ve been stage manager since sophomore year when Lilia realized how much better I was than all of you bitches.”

“Fuck off, Vidal!” somebody laughed.

“Bruh,” another kid huffed.

Rio laughed. “For real, though,” she said. “I always loved being part of the tech crew because I liked building things and painting and fixing and…it reminded me of my dad.” She shrugged one shoulder and blinked away the tears that were already threatening to fall. She swallowed thickly and cleared her throat. “A lot of you know what this means for me.” She felt Agatha squeeze her hand. “Anyway, I learned most of what I know from him. The rest, I learned from Natasha, our previous stage manager who went away to that big sound booth in the sky…” She lowered her head and put her hand over her heart, somberly.

“Girl, she’s at Oneonta,” another voice said from the crowd, eliciting laughter from around her.

“And has she visited or called even once ?” Rio shot back with a huff. “No! So she’d dead to me!” 

It was just a joke, though. Nat had sent her a few texts threatening her if she fucked up the careful system she’d created in tech crew before she handed off the mantle at the end of Rio’s freshman year. She hadn’t been able to make it back for this year’s rehearsal schedules due to her own being hectic as hell in upstate New York, but she’d sent flowers all three nights for Rio during the last few shows they’d done.

“Anyway,” Rio said, “since Nat gave me a shot as an incoming sophomore to take over her mantle, I figure it’s my turn to give a shot to a sophomore that has shown a lot of promise.”

“What the fuck, man?” Wyatt whined.

“Dude, trust me when I say you do not want this job: it’s stressful as fuck and you are our resident fixer now. Let somebody else boss everybody around, okay? Somebody as bossy as her sister.” There was a gasp from the crowd in front of the stage, all the kids parting to reveal one tiny blonde girl with big green eyes, blinking up at her. Rio let go of Agatha’s hand to walk forward, crouching in front of her. “You ready for this, Yeller?” she asked.

Yelena Belova was the adopted sister of Natasha Romanoff. Both girls were adopted, actually, and both had retained their birth names, but they were inseparable as sisters. And they had pretty much never been apart from one another, even though only one of them (Yelena) had retained her thick Russian accent from the country where they’d both been born. Natasha had been incredibly protective of Yelena from the second Rio met them both. Yelena had been in middle school when Nat graduated, but Nat gave Rio clear instructions to look out for the younger girl.

When Rio first met her, though, it was quickly clear that Yelena didn’t need her protection. She was tiny (like Nat – seriously, how were they not biologically sisters?) but she was loud and aggressive and so incredibly tough, just like her sister.

That’s how she got the name ‘Yeller’. She was the only person who could get a whole room to quiet down with just her voice.

Rio held out her fist to the younger girl, who had proven herself as Rio’s right-hand woman for the last two years, learning everything she could from Rio, like how to use all the power tools and use her magic (green, like Rio’s) to mend things and help build set pieces. She got the second headset some nights when Rio needed help in the wings, using a poisonous look she had mastered to get techies and actors alike to shut the hell up.

Cautiously, Yelena balled her hand into a fist and reached it toward Rio’s, bumping her knuckles softly against the older girl’s. 

Rio frowned at her. “Come on, Yeller,” she huffed. “I know you can do better than that.”

Yelena twisted up her lips in annoyance, pulling her fist back a few inches before shoving it forward again, pounding her knuckles against Rio’s so hard that it actually hurt, but Rio didn’t pull away. Instead, she grinned and nodded.

“ That’s my girl!” she said. “Let’s go! You’re taking over the headset for this show. And it starts now. You’re running crew during dress rehearsal today. Think you can handle it?”

“With ease ,” Yelena scoffed, crossing her arms over her chest.

“Alright, love the confidence,” Rio said, reaching for her arms to help her climb onto the stage, slinging her arm around Yelena’s shoulders. “First, pick a second in command, just like you were mine.”

Yelena surveyed the crowd of techies, her eyes searching for a few moments before landing on a girl in the center of the crowd. Rio watched as her pale cheeks turned pink and she cleared her throat. “Kate Bishop,” she said.

The girl in question – Kate Bishop – was a sophomore, like Yelena, but she was a year younger than the rest. She was a smart one; she had skipped a grade back in elementary school and could probably skip another if she wanted. But, for some reason, she was happy just being a sophomore and continuing high school at a steady pace.

Rio didn’t miss the looks she and Yelena sent to each other during rehearsals and theater club meetings. They sat together at lunch, too, talking animatedly about whatever, in their own little world away from everybody else.

Kate Bishop was an heiress, but she didn’t act like it. Not really.

She was the rough and tumble type, a little Katniss with her bow and arrow. She was a master archer and brought their school team to national championships two years in a row now. She did stage crew because she was also pretty good with her hands – not as good as Yelena or Rio, but she could probably build a passable set on her own. She always had a bandaid somewhere on her body – usually her face.

She and Yelena were…inseparable. Rio didn’t know the exact nature of their relationship, but Yelena wasn’t shy about her sexuality or how disgusting she thought guys were. Whenever one tried to flirt with her, she would growl at them in thick Russian. Whatever she was saying probably wasn’t as bad as it sounded, but you wouldn’t be able to tell that from the venomous tone she used, making Kate laugh in the background.

They were cute, Rio decided, no matter what they were to each other, really.

“Kate Bishop?” Rio whispered to her. “You sure?”

She knew Yelena was certain. She knew that Kate would be the obvious choice. And she was a good one. Like Yelena, Kate could be a commanding presence. Even as a sophomore, she had the respect of others in the crew. Even without magic as she was.

Yelena nodded. “Yes,” she said. “I’m sure.”

Rio nodded. “Good choice,” she said. “But you know you two will have to be on separate sides of the stage all night, right?”

“It’s for the best,” Yelena said, blushing and swallowing thickly. 

Rio snorted and patted her back. “Okay,” she said. “Bishop!” she called. “You’re second in command! Go get your headsets, you two. Make me proud.”

Kate jumped up on the stage, with Yelena’s help, and the two ran off to the green room to start getting ready, their hands staying connected as they scampered off stage. Rio grinned at them, shaking her head fondly.

“Okay,” she said, “while your new stage manager gets ready, everybody else better start getting into position. We’re running this play with or without you – but with you would be a whole lot easier, wouldn’t it, Lilia?”

“You bet, kiddo,” Lilia said, helping Alice organize the band members. They weren’t doing a full orchestra, but there were enough instruments there so that they didn’t need to rely on a CD player. Alice sat at the piano, her guitar at her side. There was a mix of students and teachers behind her. The band teacher, Norm, was on the drums, tapping out a soft rhythm. 

“Come get your costumes on,” the student costumer, Peggy, called from the dressing room. “Before Lilia has my head!”

Most of the lingering cast and crew started to take their spots and go off to where they were needed while Rio continued to look around the auditorium from her spot downstage. 

For her entire high school theater career, she’d worked behind the scenes. She’d been a fixer, a painter, a stage manager, running the scene behind the scenes , acting as the Wizard himself. And now she was…not that. Now, she was a performer.

In just over a month, the majority of these seats – if not all of them – would be filled with parents, friends, family, and other loved ones and fans of the theater, there to see them put on their show. Rio’s first show.

Rio’s only show, really. 

Because, as fun as it was to perform in a play with Agatha, Rio was already certain that this wasn’t something she’d likely repeat once she left high school.

Maybe a karaoke night or two in college and beyond.

“You coming?”

Rio turned to see Agatha standing next to the curtains for stage right, smiling softly at her with her head tilted, patiently waiting for Rio to follow her toward the dressing room, where Peggy would squeeze them into their respective costumes as Elphaba and Fiyero, respectively (even though Rio’s entrance wasn’t for a while).

“Yeah,” Rio said, taking a deep breath as she considered the empty audience one last time and started to follow her girlfriend offstage. 

Agatha took her first opportunity to connect their hands, pressing a kiss to Rio’s jaw as they made their way to the dressing room, which, for the first time really since they’d started dating and sneaking off there, was completely full.

There were tons of new costumes on racks along the walls. Peggy was standing near one that seemed to hold only Shiz’s striped uniforms. There were big tags attached to each, designating to whom they went. Peggy started calling out names, handing out uniforms and directing them toward the chorus room down the hall to change. It was their impromptu extra room when there were way too many people to change all at once, even in the bigger girls’ dressing room.

Agatha, Rio, and Jen waited as the chorus got their costumes and left for the chorus room to change. Then Peggy pulled out the big guns.

“Jen,” she said, in her posh British accent, “since you are to be on stage first, I have your dress right here. We still need to do one more fitting, but this should do well enough.” She pulled out a poofy, light blue ball gown that was reminiscent of the original Disney Cinderella and Jen’s eyes grew to the size of saucers as her mouth gaped open, her jaw practically hitting the floor.

“So sparkly,” she breathed, reaching for the gown and holding it against her body. “Look at how sparkly this is!” She turned to Agatha and Rio, who both pretended to shield their eyes.

“You’ll only be wearing it for a few moments today,” Peggy told her. “Then you’ll have to change into your galindafied school uniform.” She pulled a white dress and blazer set off of the rack next, and Jen was practically vibrating with excitement as she snatched it.

“I am in Heaven ,” she practically squealed, hugging her clothes to her chest and smiling so wide Rio was certain that her face would split in two any second.

“You can set up in that corner,” Peggy said, pointing to one of the vanities on the far side of the room. “Most of your costumes will be set up there for quick changes. Make sure you don’t lose anything, right?” She leveled Jen with a hard look and Jen offered her a salute in response, before making her way to her vanity.

“Now, Miss Elphaba,” Peggy said, reaching for a costume in blue. “Here is your first costume.” She handed it to Agatha, who held the uniform to her own body, turning to look at herself in a nearby mirror. 

She was smiling dazedly, like she couldn’t believe what she was doing. It was just a high school musical, but Agatha was treating it as though she were about to make a Broadway debut. Rio just watched her, smiling softly. 

Peggy, of course, did not miss this. She rolled her eyes fondly as she reached for another costume, handing it to her.

“You’ll be wearing this for the majority of Act One,” she said. “I’m sure you’ll look quite dapper in it.” 

Rio took the offered suit and held it up in front of her body, standing next to Agatha to look at herself in the mirror. She met Agatha’s eyes in their reflection and they shared a shy grin, each looking down at their respective costumes. 

“For goddess’s sake,” Peggy huffed quietly behind them. “Go. Get changed. You’ll need to be in the audience in ten minutes or less. Lilia has her usual announcement before we begin our first dress rehearsal. Now go!”

She practically shoved Agatha toward another vanity, right next to where Jen was already happily slipping into her Galinda poofy gown. Then she dragged Rio to a different corner, blocking her off from the other two girls with a curtain.

“I don’t need help,” Rio huffed when she saw that Peggy had enclosed herself in the makeshift dressing room as well.

“Since when are you and Harkness a thing?” Peggy hissed, ignoring her snark. “Since when is Harkness…” She twitched her wrist.

“I don’t know what that means,” Rio lied. This was too ridiculous.

“You bloody well know what I mean!” Peggy huffed, shoving Rio’s shoulder. “Since when is she gay ?”

“Since…none of your business, actually,” Rio huffed. “Just drop it, Carter. Let me get changed and go get the other actors their costumes.”

“This isn’t over,” Peggy said, pointing at her as she disappeared behind the thin curtain.

“Yes it is,” Rio huffed back. But she was smiling as she looked at herself in the mirror of her little corner vanity, her cheeks tinged pink.

Chapter End Notes

Comments fuel me

Chapter 25: Sparkle

Chapter Summary

The kids do their first dress rehearsal for Wicked and we see the first Sparkle Prizes given out. Can you guess who will get one on Day One?

Chapter Notes

I was ill for a bit and then I got smacked with some writer's block, specifically for this story, but then I got through it. And work just ended for the year, so I have plenty of time to write.

You can also check out my other ongoing story, The Best Medicine. Please go read and comment over there because that is very important to me, considering I based Agatha's struggle with MS one mine a little bit.

I will try to update this one way more often, too. Thanks for reading!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty-Five

 

Before every rehearsal, Lilia did announcements. She basically just went over any last-minute cue changes or informed the cast about what she expected of them up on that stage. And she told them whatever news she deemed pertinent to improve their performance.

Sometimes, this included threatening them with a water bottle if they messed up. A water bottle that she held now, sitting on the stage as the rest of them sat in the audience, in full costume (or as full as they could be for their first dress rehearsal: some costumes were still being worked on or hadn’t yet arrived, like Agatha’s black lace Elphaba dress and the hat that matched it.)

Peggy stood next to her, giving the cast the stink-eye. You better not get sprayed today , she had warned, because these costumes cost a large part of our budget and I will not incur penalties if they are returned to the rental company waterlogged. Lilia had nodded sagely in agreement.

“First,” Lilia said, after she had threatened each of them with basically being waterboarded if they damaged their costumes or the set pieces or missed their cues, “let’s go over what I know is the favorite part of the year for some of you: the sparkle prizes.”

A cheer went through the audience around Rio as she blinked at Lilia. Even Jen and Agatha were grabbing each other in excitement, bouncing in their seats. Jen’s dress practically engulfed her seat and Agatha, tickling Rio’s legs from the other side of her girlfriend. She looked at them as if they each had three heads.

“What?” Agatha laughed. “Don’t you know what the sparkle prizes are? You’ve been here as long as either of us.”

“Techies don’t get sparkle prizes,” Rio reminded her. “I mean, of course I know what they are, but they don’t seem that exciting. It’s usually just some kind of cheap prop, isn’t it? Like the fake bag of beans from Into the Woods or the plungers you got for Urinetown .”

“It’s more than just that for us, Ri,” Agatha chuckled. “We only get sparkle prizes for sparkling on stage, which means we did so well that Lilia wanted to recognize it in front of everybody. It’s basically like our Tony awards.”

“Right,” Rio said, “I know that. The crew gets something similar – carabiners.”

“Carabiners?” Agatha asked, tilting her head.

“I’ll show you my collection later,” Rio said, with a wink and a grin.

Agatha rolled her eyes and nudged Rio’s shoulder, but there was a flush to her cheeks that did not go unnoticed by Rio.

“This year’s sparkle prize is…a surprise,” Lilia said. The crowd around Rio groaned. “We go over this every single year,” Lilia huffed. “None of you get to find out what the surprise is until at least one of you sparkles on stage. Do a good job today and the prize might just reveal itself.” Her eyes twinkled at that. “Now,” she continued, “onto the next bit of business…I have a few friends coming to see this year’s show. I want you to impress them.”

Sonny raised their hand in the back. They were wearing a fitted pin-lined pantsuit with a high collar and a pair of wire-rimmed spectacles as Madame Morrible . Theo was next to them, in his Munchkin Governor suit and stubbly chin, which he refused to shave as he was finally growing a “beard” (if it could even be called that). 

“Yes, Sonny,” Lilia said. “Question?”

“Yes,” Sonny said. “Who did you invite? Do we know them? Are they past students?”

“Most of them are, yes,” Lilia said. “As you all should know, previous members are always invited back to watch our plays for alumni night. Some are recent graduates, but others graduated decades ago. I’m happy to see all of them back and I even reserve a section in the audience for them.” She smiled proudly. “I hope some of you will return one day.”

There was a round of applause for that, accompanied by shouted promises to return for every play Lilia does in the future. Lilia blew kisses to them before returning to a clipboard that she’d placed down on the stage next to her.

Only Rio seemed to realize that she hadn’t answered Sonny’s question.

“This is our first dress rehearsal,” Lilia said, “so there are bound to be a few mishaps and missed cues. Despite my warnings, I will be frugal with the water bottle…but don’t push your luck. We’ve been working for weeks on all of your songs and movements, so make sure you’re doing your very best out there. We’re going to do a full run-through of the show, no stopping. We have our line readers sitting in the front row at either side of the stage, so if you forget a line, don’t hesitate to ask for a line or to improv, if the spirit moves you. Just keep it going, okay? And maybe you’ll stand out and receive our first sparkle prize.”

Rio raised her hand.

“Yes, Rio, my sweet baby bird?” Lilia teased, as if she were talking to a toddler.

Rio frowned at that.

“Does the person who earns the first sparkle prize get anything extra for being the first?” she asked.

“What do you want?” Lilia snorted. “Another carabiner?”

A ripple of laughter went through the audience and Rio’s frown deepened. She felt Agatha’s fingers lace with hers and her head lay down on Rio’s shoulder. Her body relaxed on instinct back into the other girl’s. 

“Okay, okay,” Lilia said, “all jokes aside…no, if you’re the first to win a sparkle prize, you don’t get anything extra except for the recognition of your peers for being the first to truly sparkle onstage. I think that should be enough of a prize, though, don’t you?”

“Eh,” Rio said, shrugging one shoulder.

Lilia rolled her eyes but moved on anyway.

“After this rehearsal, we will all reconvene right here after you change back into your street clothes to go over whatever notes I and our other principal crew members have. This includes our musical director, Alice Wu-Gulliver; our costumer, Peggy Carter; and our interim stage manager, Yelena Belova, and her second-in-command, Kate Bishop. They will be giving you notes based on their own expertise in the musical numbers, costumes, and stage cues. The last part will be mainly for the crew.” She turned her head. “You all hear that?!”

Several hands popped out from backstage, thumbs waving in the air in confirmation as the cast chuckled. Lilia nodded.

“But there will be notes all around that you should all hear,” she continued, “so please stick around for that as well as the possible sparkle prize handouts. We’ve never gone through a first dress rehearsal without somebody sparkling – don’t let today be the first time.”

There were murmurs of agreement throughout the audience. Rio felt Agatha squeeze her hand. She squeezed back, suddenly nervous.

“Okay,” Lilia said, clapping her hands. “Make me proud. And go break a leg – not really. Theo, I’m looking at you.”

Theo raised his hands in surrender. “That was one time !” 

A ripple of laughter went through the audience as everybody stood and made their way toward the stage to take their positions. Rio’s hands twitched at her side as she made her way backstage to wait for her cue.

Before she could disappear behind the curtain, she felt a hand grab hers and turned just in time to feel Agatha’s hands on her cheeks and their lips connecting. Rio exhaled into the kiss, feeling her body relax a little bit – but that was just the effect Agatha seemed to have on her whenever they kissed. She always felt a little bit relieved, like Agatha was a balm on whatever happened to be ailing Rio at the moment. Even if it was nothing.

“What was that for?” Rio asked, smiling when Agatha pulled away.

Agatha shrugged. “I just thought you could use it,” she said.

“You were right,” Rio said, sighing. “Thanks.”

“Anytime,” Agatha replied, winking at her.

And if Agatha hadn’t been Rio’s girlfriend for over a month at that point, hadn’t already professed her love for the other girl, hadn’t been kissing and holding her hand for so long that it felt as normal as breathing, Rio may have been embarrassed for blushing at that singular word. 

She could kiss Agatha Harkness anytime she wanted.

And that made her feel something close to invincible.

She let go of Agatha’s hand with a pep in her step as she practically skipped to her place backstage and waited for her cue. Yelena nudged her with a knowing grin, but Rio didn’t really care – she was far too happy to be teased about this.

 

The first dress rehearsal was…okay.

It could have gone better.

A few people forgot their lines, but they weren’t huge lines. A couple of improvisations didn’t hurt their runtime or flow that much, at least not for the first dress rehearsal. 

Nobody got sprayed, at least.

Rio didn’t miss her entrance, which was a plus. But Agatha had looked cute enough in her costume that she had stumbled over her line, fumbling a little bit as Agatha’s eyes twinkled with mischief and amusement. She would definitely be teased for that later.

But, otherwise, she’d like to think she did well.

She remembered all the steps that George had taught her and in which order they were supposed to go. Some of the background dancers stumbled, but they didn’t stop the performance, nor did Rio allow herself to get distracted from her song.

She did miss a few key notes, though, so she was probably going to get a note about that from Alice, she figured.

Her scenes with Agatha flowed the most naturally, despite her initial distraction. Agatha had been her acting coach in the beginning, so that was really nothing new, anyway. She tried to focus on acting like she was falling in love with the other girl all over again – which wasn’t a difficult feat. 

During “As Long as You’re Mine,” Rio’s hands stroked over Agatha’s cheeks and over her shoulders and through her hair and their chemistry crackled between them without any kind of effort as they kissed and sang, their arms holding each other as their voices harmonized perfectly. 

She didn’t spend as much time on the stage after that, but she sang with the chorus at all the appropriate parts. And she got into her last costume – which was mostly incomplete – as the Scarecrow and did her last few cameos before the end when Wyatt helped her through the trapdoor that Agatha later pulled her through so they could run away together, hands holding tightly to one another. 

She was in agreement with Agatha still: Galinda and Elphaba were the real star-crossed lovers. But she loved the chance to play her romantic interest, nonetheless. She loved being the one who held her hand and kissed her at the end of the play, running away with her to start their life anew. It felt like a perfect dream fantasy.

When the curtains finally fell, everybody rushed to do a practice curtain call, following Yelena’s instructions.

She went out as part of a trio with Jen on one arm and Agatha on the other, took her bow first but then stepped back to allow the girls to hold hands and bow together, like they were the best of friends as Alice played part of the overture for them.

Then, once they were done, Peggy and Lilia clapped and instructed them to go change and hurry back. Peggy followed the leads into the main dressing room to help them out of their very complicated costumes so that nobody ripped anything.

The Scarecrow costume was pretty simple – a flannel under overalls – and she was thankful that the straw inserts were still missing so she could get in and out of it with ease. The boots had also not yet arrived, which meant that she was still in her converse, which was fine. And it meant that she was back in her street clothes a lot more quickly than the others.

Except Agatha, who still didn’t have her black lacy dress or the hat that Galinda was meant to gift to Elphaba in the first act. For the second act of the show, Peggy had given her a pastel purple dress from a production of Little Women that they’d done well before Agatha had gotten to high school. It fit her pretty well, but it was purple, not black, so she looked like a lavender witch without a hat. Rio teased her a bit about it when they were changing during their short intermission. Agatha had just flipped her off and Rio pretended to swoon.

She had grabbed a perturbed Agatha around the waist when she tried to walk past her, pressing kisses to her face until she began giggling and slapping her away, even as she pressed a kiss to Rio’s lips before breaking away.

Rio had been smiling like a fool as she went to her spot to wait for her entrance into Act 2.

Now, they walked hand-in-hand out into the audience, still dressed in their casual Saturday comfy clothes. Jen and Alice were already seated, practically dead to the world as the lack of sleep and the adrenaline from earlier that morning caught up to them. Jen was sitting straight up, arms crossed, with her eyes closed, but Alice was sprawled in her seat, full on snoring and drooling on Jen’s shoulder.

“Isn’t she supposed to be giving us notes?” Rio murmured to Agatha as they sat down next to the two other girls.

“She will,” Agatha assured her. “Alice is like a sleeper agent when it comes to this kind of thing. Just watch.”

“Okay,” Lilia said, clapping her hands after the last stragglers filed into the auditorium. “Looks like we have everybody here. We’re going to start with costume notes because there are fewer of those. Go on, Peggy.”

Lilia sat on the stage with her oversized tumbler of tea in her hands, still steaming as she took a large sip while Peggy cleared her throat and read from the notebook in her hands.

“Alright, then,” she said. “I know that we still have several costume pieces missing, and I am working to get them to you all, but that doesn’t mean you should treat any of the pieces we already have like they’re lesser. I just had to pick up several shirts and ties and hats backstage that were left on the ground in the chorus room. Don’t forget that I know exactly who left each piece and now those who did leave them will not receive a sparkle prize even if you were meant to today.”

A groan went through the audience.

“Don’t fuck with my costumes,” Peggy retorted with a shrug. “I only get this job for one more year, and I will not be leaving here with any missing or damaged costume items on my record.”

“Anything else?” Lilia asked.

“Yes,” Peggy said. “Jen,” Jen’s eyes popped open, “your wigs are meant to be here on Monday by the time school ends. If you could be here right at the bell, we will do a little try-on to make sure that they fit comfortably. Please do not be late as we have quite a few to get through.”

“Hell yeah!” Jen said, fist-pumping and slightly jostling Alice on her shoulder. Alice let out a snort, but she did not wake up. Several people snickered behind her.

“Agatha, your dress will also be here around that time, but your hat…” She gave a sideways glance to Lilia, who smirked around the rim of her cup.

“What?” Agatha asked. “What is that look for?”

“I’ll let Lilia take that,” Peggy said, cryptically, “in due time. The rest of the costumes should all arrive by Wednesday, at the latest, so if you performed today with incomplete costumes, please arrive as soon as possible on Wednesday to do a final fitting so that we can make sure everything is as it’s meant to be. We have one singular month left until this show and I will not be blamed for them being anything less than stellar.”

Several kids in the audience cheered. One said: “You tell them, Carter!”

“That’s all for my notes,” Peggy said to Lilia, who nodded.

“Stage crew,” Lilia said, looking toward Yelena and Kate, who were sitting with their legs tangled upstage, going over their own scribbles in a messy notebook, “you’re up.”

They both tried to jump up at the same time, which just ended up with them falling over in a jumble of limbs. Kate’s chin hit the stage and she let out a soft ‘oof!’ as Yelena hastened to right herself before reaching for the other girl. Kate rubbed her jaw as she and Yelena limped toward the edge of the stage with their crumpled notebook and took a seat between Peggy and Lilia, who were just staring at them, wide-eyed like they were some kind of sideshow act.

Yelena cleared her throat, her cheeks pink.

“Several of you missed your cues,” she started, looking straight down at her notebook. “Ginette, you came out a little too late during the opening number and it kind of messed up the lighting cue for the Wizard.”

Most of their notes were technical and centered around the lighting and sound cues. They called out specific people in both the cast and the crew, Yelena speaking with a level of authority that made Rio genuinely swipe a tear from her eye – for which Agatha teased her mercilessly later.

When they were done, Lilia thanked them and warned them to be careful as they joined the rest of the crew in putting away the props and resetting the set.

“Alice,” Lilia said, her voice barely loud enough to be heard over the din of the auditorium. But Alice popped out of her seat, anyway, already reaching for her phone to pull up her own notes app, a line of drool still wet on her cheek.

“See what I mean?” Agatha whispered in Rio’s ear.

“That’s incredible,” Rio murmured back. “She’s like a robot.”

“Alice doesn’t play when it comes to her music,” Agatha said.

Most of Alice’s notes were about…well… notes . Mostly the missed ones or the ones that were not quite at the right pitch for the music. There were some dropped lines, she said, and some chorus numbers where certain melodies fell a little bit flat. 

Rio got the notes she was expecting, but Alice was incredibly nice about it, telling her she did an amazing job, regardless, and that they could work on it after school one day, but that she should consider working on it at home, as well. She even gave Rio a goofy thumbs up.

People applauded. Rio blushed. Agatha kissed her temple.

When Alice was done, she went right back to snoring on her girlfriend’s shoulder.

“Every single time,” Agatha snorted, shaking her head.

“Okay,” Lilia said, placing her tumbler down and reaching for her clipboard instead. “First thing to go over – my flying monkeys. Raise your hands so I can see you, please.”

Six hands went up in the air. 

“You all did really well, but I want to hear more screeching during the opening number. Don’t be shy! Project !” The six teens looked at each other, blushing. “Go on!” Lilia encouraged. 

Again, the teens looked at each other, their cheeks pink. Then one of the girls inhaled deeply and let out an animalistic screech, very monkey-like. 

The others followed suit. They screeched at each other and their classmates for a few moments while Lilia and others encouraged them with cheering and applause.

“Phenomenal!” Lilia said. “Okay, that’s enough for now. Save that energy for rehearsals. Fantastic job, all of you!”

The six teens sat down as people applauded around them.

“Next,” Lilia said, “Agatha.”

Rio felt Agatha stiffen in the seat next to her.

“Don’t look so terrified, doll,” Lilia snorted. “Relax. I just need you to get better at pretending you like Jen.”

“But I don’t,” Agatha said.

“Hey!”

“You don’t like me, either!” Agatha huffed. “It’s our thing!”

Jen rolled her eyes.

“But you’re actresses,” Lilia said. “So act . Work on that chemistry. Have a slumber party or something. Get mani-pedis together. Play a team sport. I don’t care. Just bond . I want that chemistry to improve by the next Saturday rehearsal, capisce?”

“Yeah,” Jen sighed.

“Whatever,” Agatha huffed, crossing her arms.

“Also, I know you can be more sarcastic than what you were doing today. Don’t hold back. Let your prickly side out more on stage.”

Agatha gave her a thumbs up.

“And Rio,” Lilia said, getting the other girl’s attention. “Be more of a himbo in Act One, please.”

“I will if you promise to never use that word again.”

“Deal.”

Lilia went on with more notes. First, she went over individual characters, then she focused on the larger chorus. She had plenty of notes to go around for their first major dress rehearsal. But none of the notes were super bad. 

Which meant, Lilia said, that there were actually a few people who sparkled on stage that day. Which meant that they would also find out what the sparkle prizes were that day. Jen and Agatha were practically vibrating with excitement (and Alice was still snoring).

“Yelena,” Lilia called. Yelena popped her head out from backstage. “Go get,” she looked at her notebook and counted, “ four sparkle prizes please. And the other thing.”

Yelena gave her a salute before flouncing off to grab the sparkle prizes from their hiding spot (which only the stage crew apparently knew about as Agatha and Jen had never been able to sniff it out.)

The room was suddenly all abuzz. Four was the most amount of sparkle prizes to be given out during the first dress rehearsal in a while – at least since Agatha had joined the club. It must have gone better than anybody thought.

She wondered what it would be this time. The time they’d done Urinetown , they’d received cheap plungers that they carried around school like badges of honor and then signed at the cast party. 

Would they receive miniature broomsticks this time? Or something else?

Agatha tried to imagine what they could get that would be attached to the show. It was usually something they could wear or carry around at school. Something they could show off.

Yelena popped back out onto the stage with a large cardboard box. She practically skipped to Lilia’s side before plopping down on the stage next to her, placing the box in her own lap as she waited for further instruction.

Rio didn’t miss the way Kate Bishop, standing just outside the cover of the backstage area, pressed her hands to her face to hide her smile and blushing cheeks, obviously overwhelmed by the cuteness that was Yelena Belova.

Even Rio had to admit she was adorable.

Lilia patted the blonde curls cheeks and cooed a thank you at her before opening the box and reaching one hand in.

“Now,” she said, “I know you’re all very interested to know what this show’s sparkle prize is going to be. You’re always interested in the sparkle prizes, even before I announce what show we’re doing. Don’t even try to deny it,” she said, pointing a finger at all of them. “I wasn’t born yesterday.”

“We know!” somebody brave yelled from the back of the auditorium. 

Lilia narrowed her gaze.

“Maybe there shouldn’t be any sparkle prizes today…” she said, lifting her empty hand from the box in warning.

“No!” several of the cast members whined.

“Sorry!” that same voice said, almost frantically.

“Hmph!” Lilia said. “That’s what I thought.” She cleared her throat. “Anyhoo, I know many of you have been waiting for this moment since you got back to school from winter break, so without further ado…”

She pulled the item from the box and everybody about lost their damn minds.

It was a hat. A stereotypical witch’s hat. The pointy kind. The kind that Galinda gave Elphaba in Act One.

And it was bright green. 

Lilia held up a finger, reaching in again. 

She pulled out a second hat, hot pink in color.

Jen let out a tiny squeak of delight, clapping her hands. “I need that hat,” she murmured under her breath.

“Yeah, babe,” Alice muttered in her sleep, “you get that hat, baby.”

Jen snorted and pressed her lips to her sleepy girlfriend’s forehead.

“You can all thank Peggy Carter for this show’s sparkle prize,” Lilia said. “I would have given you those party store decorative brooms – all the same size, shape, and color – and called it a day. But Peggy convinced me that this would be way more fun and better marketing for the show. Say thank you, Peggy .”

“Thank you, Peggy,” the cast sang in unison.

“You rock, Carter!” a voice said from the back.

“I know,” Peggy said with a grin and a slight blush on her cheeks. She flipped her hair.

“And, as a little special treat…” Lilia reached into the box one last time and pulled out a black witch hat, which had Agatha sitting up straighter. Lilia grinned as she stared directly into her eyes. “That’s right, Agatha,” she said. “This time, your sparkle prize will be your Elphaba hat.”

“What if she doesn’t get it?” somebody in the crowd asked aloud.

“Ye of little faith!” Agatha yelled back, but she looked nervous.

“Well, the show will be a little different, I guess,” Lilia replied airily with a shrug. “You better work hard, Miss Harkness.”

“I’m guessing that means I didn’t earn it today,” Agatha sighed, slumping in her chair.

“Nope,” Lilia said. “Not yet, darling. But there’s still time. Like Peggy said, we have a whole month for you all to earn your sparkle prizes.”

No show had finished without every single person in the cast earning a sparkle prize.

“Anyway,” Lilia said, “on to who did earn a sparkle prize.” She motioned to the two hats. “I got an equal amount of both colors,” she said, “so if I call your name, you will come up here, point to the one you want, and I shall bestow it on you. Wear your hats with pride , chickies!” She cleared her throat and picked up her clipboard. “Our first sparkle prize winner is a senior. He’s close to my heart and has been doing a phenomenal job this entire semester, but he especially shined today as our Governor Thropp and Dr. Dillamond. Theo Parker, come get your hat, baby!”

She beamed as Theo hopped up and practically tripped over himself and several others in his way as he raced to the stage, throwing his arms around Lilia, who hugged him back incredibly tight, pressing kisses to both cheeks in a very Italian way. 

“Pick a color,” she said, motioning to the two hats she’d placed on stage.

Theo stared at them for a long moment, before motioning to the pink one and immediately kneeling as though he were about to be knighted.

“Good Goddess,” Lilia muttered, rolling her eyes as she grabbed the pink hat and placed it on his head. She then tugged him to his feet and turned him around to face the audience. “Our first sparkle prize of the year!” she exclaimed to thunderous applause.

Theo raised his fists in the air as he ran back to his seat, receiving pats on the back and congratulations. Lilia reached into the box again and pulled out a replacement pink hat.

“Next,” she said, “is a newcomer. This person has done incredibly well this year and especially in this rehearsal. They’ve proven that they can act cold and yet affectionate, they can be manipulative and charming. They are the whole package. Sonny Davis, come on down!”

Sonny’s entire face was bright red as they stood and shuffled down to meet Lilia, who just pinched their cheeks as they laughed nervously and pointed to the green hat. She placed it on their head gently, smiling affectionately at them as she patted their shoulders and they turned back to the crowd to more cheering.

They waved nervously and padded back to their spot next to Theo, who embraced them with an arm around their shoulders and something whispered in their ear that made them giggle, the rims of their hats knocking together.

“Third,” Lilia said, once the applause had died down, “is a member of our crew. Somebody who works tirelessly and never complains and does everything she’s meant to do. She never misses her cues and stays late with me to help plan and cast this show. And she works with each member of the cast individually to make sure they’re comfortable using their voice. I’m sure you’ve all guessed whom I’m talking about by now. Let’s see if we can wake her up. Alice Wu-Gulliver!”

Once again, like a sleeper agent, Alice stood up straight from sleep and walked to the stage like a woman possessed, blinking first at Lilia, then the rest of the crowd.

“Huh?” she said. “What’s happening?”

“You won a sparkle award, babe!” Jen informed her as she continued to applaud.

“I did ?” Alice asked, blinking owlishly at the crowd. “Already?”

“You did an amazing job today, doll,” Lilia said. “You deserve this more than perhaps anybody.”

“Aww, thanks, Lilia,” Alice said, blushing as she looked down at the two hats. “Hmm…I’ll take a pink one,” she said. “Gotta support my girl.” She turned her head to wink at Jen, who giggled and said, “oh, you!” as Lilia reached for the pink witch hat and placed it on Alice’s head.

Alice returned to Jen’s side, but stayed very much awake, smiling happily as she played with the rim of her hat.

“Perfect,” Lilia said, “one last green hat left. This will be perfect for the person who has won the last sparkle prize of the day.” She cleared her throat. “This person was not meant to be in the play. I kind of tricked them into it.” 

Rio felt her heart stutter.

“And, hey, at first I wasn’t even going to cast them, actually. I didn’t honestly think they’d do as great a job as they ended up doing in their audition. And then I figured that yeah, they could act, but could they sing or dance or do any of the other things that I needed them to be able to do in order to be in this show. And, at every turn, they surpassed my expectations. I think they even surprised themself. Never have I been so pleased to be so wrong about somebody in my entire life – and I’ve lived a long, long time, as you all know.” Several groans from the audience. “Okay, okay,” Lilia laughed, “Rio Vidal, just get up here and take your hat.”

Thunderous applause rose up around Rio as several people patted her on the back. Next to her, Agatha was squeezing her arm and telling her to get up, but Rio was rooted to her seat.

Finally, Agatha stoof and pulled Rio up with her, encouraging her to walk the last few feet to the stage, where Lilia had already plucked up the green hat and was beaming at her.

“Really?” Rio asked as she got close enough for Lilia to place the hat on her head.

“Really, kid,” Lilia said, proudly, giving her a tight hug. “Congrats. You did great today.”

Rio smiled proudly as she turned back to the crowd, who gave her a standing ovation. She mirrored Theo’s stance with her fists in the air, but almost fell over when Agatha wrapped her arms around her shoulders and pressed a kiss to her lips in front of everybody. 

Rio’s entire body buzzed like she’d been struck by lightning as the entire rest of the world dimmed around them. All she could feel was Agatha. All she could see was Agatha. 

And all she could hear was Agatha saying, “Congratulations, my love.”

Chapter End Notes

Sparkle Prizes or Awards are something my director gave out when I was in high school. My first show was Urinetown (yes that is a play about paying to pee, thanks for asking) and we got plungers that everybody carried around for months. My next show was Footloose and we got the gym shirts that we were meant to wear for a specific scene (if you didn't get one, it was obvious during dress rehearsals and the show nights). We did Once on this Island and got floral baseball caps that we all wore around school. For Beauty and the Beast, we got "magic" roses. We treasured all of our Sparkle Awards, especially since the director made a speech while he was handing out each one at the end of each rehearsal. It was very special to us so I really wanted to incorporate them into this fic.

I miss high school drama sometimes. This kind, at least.

And of course Rio needed to be one of the first to get hers. Agatha will (probably) get hers eventually too. Don't worry.

Comments motivate me.

Chapter 26: Trust

Chapter Summary

Rio's up to something, but Agatha can't figure out what it is. She spirals a little bit.

Chapter Notes

I'm sorry! I know it's been over a month, but I promise I haven't forgotten about this story. I'm just busy with stuff and now work is about to start up again for the school year, so I'm focused on that. I will not abandon this fic, though. I swear.

Enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty-Six

In the weeks that followed, Agatha gave it her all at every single rehearsal, trying desperately to earn her hat. She studied her lines incessantly, forced Rio, Alice, and Jen into impromptu rehearsals, and practiced her songs in the shower (she also took more showers, if only to keep rehearsing). 

At the same time, Rio spent more time at Alice’s house with them. Marisol had extended her stay with cousin Marta to two weeks, promising that she’d be back before Agatha’s birthday, but Marta was going through it and needed more help than just a single weekend could afford. She’d asked Lorna to keep watch over Rio, which meant that Rio actually ended up practically moving into the Wu mansion, as well. 

She never spent time in the guest room Lorna designated for her, however. 

When the girls weren’t passing out during their third or fourth movie in the theater room, Rio and Agatha cuddled up in her own bed (fully-clothed, they always hastened to assure both Lorna and Marisol whenever pressed) and fell asleep wrapped up in one another. Sometimes, Agatha even kept Rio up practicing their lines together. 

If Rio was ever annoyed by this, she said nothing. Agatha worried, though, and made sure to let Rio know that she wouldn’t hold it against her if Rio decided not to opt out of helping her. Rio had just rolled her eyes and taken her script out of her bag, raising one expectant eyebrow at Agatha. 

There were times, however, when Agatha couldn’t quite get a hold of Rio. Her texts would sometimes go unread for hours during school (which was unusual, even for the projected-Valedictorian), and Rio would often skip the rehearsals where she didn’t have a role call (rare, but they happened on occasion). 

Once, she showed up to Lilia’s with bandaids on her fingers after Agatha had woken up alone that morning (even though Rio had been practically plastered to her back when they fell asleep the night before), and Agatha furrowed her brow at the other girl. Lilia had already begun to talk, so she didn’t get the chance to ask any questions, but she found herself staring at Rio throughout the entirety of the class.

By the time the bell rang, Rio had healed whatever was under those bandaids and tossed them in the trash, offering Agatha a noticeably-awkward grin as she rushed off to her next class with no more than a simple brush of her lips to Agatha’s cheek.

At lunch one day, Rio was nowhere to be found – not even in the dressing room. Agatha showed up to the cafeteria and took a seat right across from Alice and Jen, frowning deeply. Jen was the first one to notice when Agatha did nothing about her stealing a Dorito from her tray.

“What crawled up your ass?” Jen asked.

“Do you think Rio is cheating on me?” Agatha asked.

Jen choked on her Dorito, and Alice’s eyes just widened, her sandwich halfway to her mouth, her jaw dropping at the question. 

Okay, Agatha had to admit, it was kind of a ridiculous question. There was actually no way that Rio was cheating on her. Even if Rio did have the inclination to cheat, there was no way that she had the time. Despite her repeated disappearing act over the last week and a half, Rio always ended up at the Wu household by dinner, sitting right next to Agatha and whispering jokes in her ear that nearly made water or soda squirt out of her nose more than once. 

And the way she looked at Agatha…

No, Rio wasn’t cheating. Obviously. 

Agatha’s shoulders slumped. Before Jen or Alice could answer her, she held up at hand. “No,” she said. “I know. She’s…that was a really dumb question. I just…I can’t find her anywhere lately. When we’re not at rehearsal or in class, she just… disappears .”

“She’s at my house, like, every night,” Alice said. 

“Yeah, but where does she go when she’s not there?” Agatha asked. “I mean, she packed enough clothes to last her the whole time her mom’s gone, so she’s definitely not going home, right? She used to come watch us at rehearsals when she wasn’t called, but now she’s not there. I’m just…worried.”

“Don’t be,” Jen said, stealing another chip. This time, Agatha moved her tray further from her, frowning deeply. “Maybe she just needs a little space.”

“Space?” Agatha asked, her heart clenching. “Like…from me?”

Even when they were just friends, Rio had never really seemed to want space from Agatha. She gravitated toward Agatha whenever they were near. In any classes they had together over the last three years, Rio always chose the spot directly next to or behind Agatha, whispering jokes that made Agatha snort under her breath. She was always in the library at the same time as Agatha so that Agatha could run through her lines together. Agatha could have looked around at pretty much any point during any rehearsal and seen Rio either in the wings or in the audience, watching her.

Rio had never wanted space before. Why now?

Was Agatha suffocating her? Was she becoming fatigued by Agatha’s presence?

A hand landed on Agatha’s arm, startling her. She looked up to find Jen staring into her eyes, one eyebrow raised. “Stop spiraling,” she said.

“I’m not–”

“Girl, I’ve known you since we were kids,” Jen reminded her (for the millionth time): “I know when you’re overthinking shit. Rio’s probably just…doing homework or something, I dunno.”

“You think she’s sneaking around to do homework ?” Agatha scoffed, disbelievingly.

“Not like she could focus on it with you around,” Jen snorted, trying to snatch a third Dorito. Agatha slapped her hand away with a glare. “Ouch! Stingy,” Jen huffed. “Girl is over the moon for you. She’s not about to jeopardize that. But she’s also not going to jeopardize her Valedictorian status. I mean, that’s the whole reason she’s in this play, isn’t it?”

“More or less,” Agatha admitted, nibbling at her Doritos. She usually waited until Rio was there to start eating her wrap now. She always gave half of it to Rio. She reached for her half now. “So you think she’s just…doing homework? But why did she have bandaids on her fingers this morning?”

“Papercuts?” Jen suggested, shrugging. “Or maybe some apothecary project thing? I dunno. She’s in all the advanced classes, isn’t she? Probably something to do with her green magic. I get burns sometimes from my potions classes.”

“You do?” Alice asked. “Aww, baby.” Alice reached for one of Jen’s hands, bringing it to her lips. Jen smiled fondly at her.

“I’m okay,” she giggled. “We have balms for that kind of thing.” She looked at Agatha. “Rio isn’t avoiding you,” she said. “She’s just doing her own thing every once in a while. Don’t overthink it.”

“Do you two ever ‘do your own thing’?” Agatha asked, looking between them. “You’re practically attached at the hip.”

“You only really see us at rehearsal, class, Alice’s, and here,” Jen pointed out. “Of course we do our own thing sometimes. I don’t sleep over at Alice’s every single night, you know. I have my own interests, and Alice has hers. It’s healthy to spend some time apart.”

Agatha nodded. “I just wish it didn’t feel like she was keeping secrets from me,” she admitted. “I mean, why can’t she just tell me what she’s doing?”

“Why can’t you ask ?” Alice pointed out, not unkindly. 

Agatha blinked at her for a long moment.

It honestly hadn’t even occurred to her to ask Rio what she’d been doing. She’d just suffered in silence, wondering why her girlfriend wasn’t around as much. She had thought that asking where she was going would be somehow…invasive. Like she didn’t really have the right to ask where she was when she wasn’t with Agatha. Asking questions like that wasn’t something that Agatha did. Not really.

Evanora had asked those questions of Agatha when she was even just five minutes late getting home sometimes. She didn’t accept that sometimes Agatha needed to talk to a teacher or a classmate or stay late for something at school. When her mother wasn’t home when Agatha got there, she could usually get away with getting home later than usual, but she never knew when that would be. 

Besides, when she had the trace on her, Evanora would grill her about her whereabouts whether she’d been home to greet Agatha or not (even when she’d been able to see/sense where Agatha was due to that very trace). 

If Agatha ever asked her mother where she had been after she got home late, it typically resulted in rants or icy words of condescension. She didn’t make that mistake more than a handful of times, at most.

She was still unlearning these habits, it seemed.

Agatha pulled out her phone and opened her message thread with Rio.

A: Where are you?

It was straightforward and a little blunt, but Agatha didn’t really know how to put a cute twist on the question. She added a couple of purple heart emojis. 

Rio responded in less than a minute.

R: had a free period. went home to do homework and have lunch and chill. on my way back now.

R: did u miss me, baby? 

She sent a smirking emoji next, and Agatha rolled her eyes.

“She had a free period before lunch,” she told Jen and Alice. “She’s fine.”

“Told you so,” Jen said. “Stop panicking. Rio isn’t your mom.”

“Ew,” Agatha huffed, wrinkling her nose. “I should hope not. Gross, Jen.”

“Girl, I’m gonna put a hex on you.” Jen pointed a finger at her. It sparked pink and Agatha held up her hands in surrender.

Rio met them outside the cafeteria, immediately wrapping her arms around Agatha, pulling her against her body and pressing her face into her shoulder. Agatha hugged her back, inhaling her familiar scent…which was mixed with something else.

Agatha wrinkled her nose as she pulled back. “What’s that smell?” she asked. “It smells like…wet dog?”

Rio furrowed her brow and smelled the collar of her own hoodie. “Manure maybe?” she said. “I was working in my dad’s garden. Spring is coming, you know?” She chuckled and rubbed the back of her neck.

“I thought you were doing homework,” Agatha said, stepping back, her arms folded over her chest.

“I was,” Rio replied, too casually, one hand still placed on Agatha’s hip. “I didn’t have that much to do. And I wanted the manure to get laid before my mom comes home. Hopefully it doesn’t snow before Saturday.”

“You don’t smell like poop,” Agatha said, raising an eyebrow. “You smell like an animal.” She narrowed her eyes. “Did you ‘rescue’ a squirrel again?”

“Hey, Bushy needed help!” Rio defended. “I would do it all over again.”

“Including the rabies shots?” Alice asked. 

“Including that part,” Rio confirmed. “She fell out of a tree! She had a limp!”

“Did you rescue another Bushy?” Agatha asked. “I really don’t feel like kissing a rabid girlfriend.”

“I don’t have rabies,” Rio huffed. “Nor am I in need of any more rabies shots. I promise.”

“Then what have you been up to?” Agatha asked. “Seriously, Rio. Where have you been lately?”

Rio opened her mouth, then she closed it. Then she opened it again. Closed it. Then she pressed her lips together, firmly.

Finally, she sighed.

“Okay,” she said. “I…I can’t tell you exactly what I’ve been up to. Not without ruining the surprise.”

“Surprise?” Agatha scoffed. “What surprise?”

“Well, Rio said, “in exactly,” she counted on her fingers, “ five days, somebody here is going to have a birthday.”

Agatha blinked at her. “You got me a squirrel for my birthday?”

Rio’s let out a groan. “Will you let go of the squirrel, please?” she said, pressing her fingers to her temples. “This has nothing to do with a squirrel.”

“Then why do you smell like a squirrel?”

“Agatha, it’s manure,” Rio insisted. She sniffed her collar again. “Maybe weed killer? Regardless, it’s not a squirrel.”

“Then what is it?” Agatha demanded.

“Have you never had a birthday before?” Rio huffed, then frowned. “Oh shit,” she said. “Have you never had–”

“My mom did birthdays,” Agatha assured her. “She had to keep up appearances, after all, and all her friends’ daughters had birthdays. She was never this secretive about gifts, though.”

“Because she – unlike me – never gave a fuck,” Rio pointed out. “I, on the other hand, give several fucks. Your birthday gift is gonna be amazing , just wait and see.” Agatha opened her mouth, but Rio held up a hand, stopping any further questions. “It’s also going to be a surprise,” she said. “So don’t even try.”

Agatha deflated. “I’m not a huge fan of surprises,” she said. 

“I know,” Rio said, once again wrapping her arms around Agatha’s waist and placing a kiss on her forehead, “but this will be a good one, I promise.”

“If you say so,” Agatha murmured. 

“Do you trust me?” Rio asked, pulling back to look into her eyes.

Agatha searched them for a long moment, just thinking. She didn’t trust many people in this world. She had trusted her mother as a child, but that ended quickly, when she realized that her mother lied as easily as breathing after too many broken promises to manipulate Agatha into doing what she wanted. It was really hard to trust anybody after that. After all, if she couldn’t trust her mother, who could she trust?

But she did trust Rio. Rio had never lied to her – at least as far as Agatha knew – and had never caused her intentional harm. She knew that Rio wouldn’t do anything to harm her, and she really had no reason to lie about something as ridiculous as a birthday surprise . Even though Agatha didn’t like surprises, she knew that whatever Rio had in store for her would likely be…enjoyable. Harmless, at the very least.

“Yes,” Agatha said, finally, “I trust you.” 

“Good,” Rio said, flashing that gap-toothed grin at her as she squeezed her. “You’re gonna love it.” She suddenly frowned. “I hope. I can’t really return it.”

Agatha furrowed her brow at that. “What the hell is it?” she asked.

Rio’s grin returned and she just winked before pressing a kiss to Agatha’s cheek and releasing her from her grasp. “See you after school, babe,” she said. 

“You’re so annoying,” Agatha groused, watching her go as she crossed her arms over her chest.

“Love you, too!” Rio called out over her shoulder as she picked up her speed into a jog toward her next class.

“You two are gross.” Agatha jumped at the sound of Jen’s voice. Jen glared at her. “Don’t be so dramatic,” she said. “We’ve been here the whole time.”

“Just watching us?” Agatha asked. “Like creeps? Get a life, Jen.”

“Or you could, I dunno, not be a rude bitch and remember that your friends are right here , too,” Jen retorted.

“As if you and Alice don’t forget that you’re not the only people in the world whenever you’re getting all lovey-dovey with each other,” Agatha snapped back. “Hypocrite.”

“I hate it when you two fight,” Alice said, looking like the child of divorced parents. 

Which she was. But still.

“We still love you, Alice,” Agatha teased, reaching out to pinch her cheek. Alice slapped her hand away with a roll of her eyes, and Agatha snickered.

As they walked to their next class together, Agatha felt something strange in her chest. Something like…affection for the two girls next to her. Genuine affection that she hadn’t really felt in years.

It felt…good. Comfortable. Strange, but not in a negative way at all.

Agatha couldn’t keep herself from smiling about it as she waved goodbye to them outside her next class. Alice gave her a happy wave back. Jen gave her an odd look, but didn’t question it as she, too, waved back at Agatha in return.

 

Chapter End Notes

Comments are always welcome!

What do you think Rio is gonna give Agatha for her birthday?

Chapter 27: Bunny Stew

Chapter Summary

Rio goes home and finds more than one surprise -- and at least one enemy.

Chapter Notes

Hey! It's been a while. Thanks everybody who is still here and reading! I've had a crazy couple of months, so hopefully I'll be able to get right back into the swing of updating on a regular basis.

Enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty-Seven

Despite waking up in Agatha’s bed that morning, Rio had insisted that she needed to go home before school to clean up a few things before her mom got home that afternoon.

“Why didn’t you just sleep at home last night then?” Agatha had asked, a bit grumpily, as Rio shuffled around her bedroom, slipping into her sneakers and hoodie and combing her fingers through her hair.

“Because,” Rio said, “you fell asleep in my lap, and you looked too cute to just abandon like that.”

They’d stayed up late again, watching more movies from Agatha’s neverending list. This time, she’d insisted that Rio needed to finally watch Who Framed Roger Rabbit? which Rio had to admit was pretty decent. Her face had gone as red as Jessica Rabbit’s dress when the character herself showed up on screen, and Agatha had teased her mercilessly about it.

“Don’t worry,” Agatha had snorted, “I reacted the same way when I first saw her. I think that was my first real inkling that I wasn’t all that straight. Or straight at all.”

“I feel like this is a potential couple’s Halloween costume,” Rio had murmured, shoving a handful of popcorn into her mouth. “I would of course be Roger Rabbit.”

“You just want to see me in a sparkly red dress, don’t you?” Agatha teased, leaning in. “We don’t have to wait until Halloween, you know,” she whispered in her ear.

Rio choked and Agatha let out a peal of laughter. “You are too easy!” she snorted, shaking her head as she tuned back into the movie. “Ooh, this is a good part! Watch, watch!”

It was still a school night, so they hadn’t queued up a second one. As lax as Lorna typically was, she still wanted them to be relatively well-rested for school the next morning.

Not that it mattered since Agatha fell asleep during the last ten minutes of the film anyway, curled up against Rio’s shoulder while she snored, her arms loosely wrapped around Rio’s body. Rio could barely pay attention to the ending when Agatha’s breath puffed out against her neck. She looked adorable. Rio pressed her face into Agatha’s hair, pressing a kiss to the crown of her head as the credits began to roll and she reached for the remote, turning off the projector.

Then, using every bit of strength she had (and a levitation spell), she carried Agatha to her bedroom, laying her down and tucking her in.

She had fully intended on going home to spend the night in her own bed. Her mom was coming back the next day, after all, and there were a few things she had to handle before she came back. There was at least one thing she’d need to explain before Marisol saw it. 

But then Agatha’s hand had reached out for her, tugging at her t-shirt and pulling her back toward the bed in her half-asleep state.

“Don’t go,” she’d whined. “Please don’t leave me.”

Rio was defenseless. “I’m not going anywhere,” she promised. “Just to my side of the bed.”

Because now she had a her side of the bed. Not that she stayed on it for too long. She and Agatha typically met in the middle at some point, spooning or cuddling, or at the very least holding hands, waking with their fingers tangled up between them.

That’s how they’d woken that morning. Agatha had been on her stomach, facing away from Rio, though her hand had reached back to find Rio’s, clutching it like a lifeline. Rio’s alarm had woken her two hours before they were meant to be at school, giving her more than enough time to get home, eat breakfast, and tidy up a little bit before heading off to school.

If only Agatha hadn’t resisted when she first attempted to leave the bed.

“Don’t go,” Agatha had whined. “Stay with me.”

“I have to go home,” Rio whispered in her ear, pressing a kiss to her cheek, then to her hand before gently slipping out of Agatha’s grasp. “I’ll see you at school.”

Agatha had pouted sleepily at her, and she looked adorable enough that Rio really reconsidered if she absolutely had to go home before school. Her mom probably wouldn’t mind the mess all that much, right?

Wrong.

Rio knew that was very much wrong. Her mom would definitely mind the mess. The second she got home, she would almost certainly be blowing up Rio’s phone at what she found. Rio had to find a way to mitigate that the best she could.

No matter how adorable her girlfriend’s pout was. She had to be strong.

Her spine felt like Jello looking at Agatha, though, so she did her best to look away as she gathered her things and pressed one final kiss to Agatha’s forehead before practically sprinting from the bedroom and down the stairs. 

The faster she ran, the easier it should be to resist the siren call of Agatha’s arms, right? Right.

She ran practically the whole way home. The sun was just starting to come up as she unlocked her front door and stepped inside, frowning at the little piles of presents a certain rodent had left her.

Said rodent was sitting on her couch like he owned the place, giving her a bored expression as he twitched his nose.

“How the hell did you get out of your cage?” Rio huffed. 

She had originally named him Señor Scratchy because of his sharp as hell little claws that tore her up the first day she brought him home from the shelter, but she was starting to think that she should have named him Houdini instead.

He was a floppy-eared bunny that had been surrendered after his previous owners realized that their adorable little Easter Bunny wasn’t just some prop for the holiday but an actual living, breathing being that they needed to care for. He had been at the shelter for nearly a year, the only bunny amongst about a thousand cats. Rio was certain that that was where he’d gotten his ill temper from.

He very much did not like her.

But Agatha had said that she wanted a bunny, so Rio had gotten a bunny – after getting Lorna’s permission, of course. Lorna had thought it was a great idea, actually. Eighteen was the traditional age for a witch to start bonding with a Familiar. And if anybody deserved a lifelong companion, she said, it was Agatha. 

Alice probably wouldn’t be too happy about it, considering she’d been asking for a dog for years, but Alice wasn’t really Rio’s concern. Lorna and Jen could deal with that fallout when it came time. For now, Rio just needed to keep this creature alive and not let him destroy her entire house before she gifted him to her girlfriend.

“Dude,” Rio huffed, “why is the wee-wee pad the only place you haven’t shit or pissed? It’s supposed to attract you to it!”

The devil bunny just blinked at her.

“I should turn you into a stew and serve you to Agatha for her birthday dinner,” Rio grumbled, stomping into the kitchen for a plastic bag to start cleaning up the little shitty pebbles that the rodent had left everywhere.

She almost jumped out of her skin when she entered the kitchen and saw Marisol sitting at the kitchen table, sipping from a steaming mug of coffee.

“Holy shit!” she exclaimed before she could stop herself. “Mami?”

“Buenas dias, mijita,” Marisol greeted. “¿Por qué hay un conejo en mi sala de estar?”

“Uh…” Rio replied intelligently. “I can explain.”

“I certainly hope so,” Marisol said, raising one eyebrow. “But first, go clean up after your new pet before I cook you into a stew.”

“Yes, Mami,” Rio sighed, grabbing a pair of gloves, a plastic bag, some paper towels, and the bottle of cleaning solution from under the sink.

She made quick work of Scratchy’s little messes, tossing everything into the outside trash before scrubbing her hands clean with hot water and soap. She then wrangled the bunny back into his cage (getting bit and scratched to within an inch of her life) and re-entering the kitchen, where Marisol had plated them each some eggs, bacon, and potatoes with tortillas. She also handed Rio her own mug of coffee with a kiss to her temple.

Rio immediately placed her mug down and embraced her mother in a hug, holding her tightly.

“I missed you,” she murmured against Marisol’s shoulder.

“My sweet girl,” Marisol replied, stroking her hair. “I missed you, too.” She pulled back. “But I’m sure you did just fine with Miss Lorna and your little novia, huh?” She waggled her eyebrows teasingly.

“Ay, Mami!,” Rio huffed, flushing bright pink as Marisol laughed and pinched her cheek.

“Sit down,” she said, “and eat your breakfast while you tell me all about what you’ve been up to while I’ve been away. Starting with that sweet little creature that made a mess of my living room.”
