Rio took a deep breath and collapsed into a chair, exhausted and suddenly starving. She picked up her fork and shoved as much into her mouth as possible before downing it all with a big gulp of coffee and letting out a long belch.

“Who raised you?” Marisol huffed. 

“You did,” Rio retorted through another mouthful of food.

“I thought so, but now I have my doubts,” Marisol said. “Chew with your mouth closed at least.”

“Sorry,” Rio said, hunching her shoulders. She swallowed her food and took another sip of coffee, then burped into a napkin. “Excuse me,” she murmured, clearing her throat.

“So what’s with the bunny?” Marisol asked.

“He’s a birthday gift for Agatha,” Rio informed her. “Lorna and I got him from the animal shelter.”

“Then why isn’t he at Lorna’s?” Marisol asked. “And why were you so mean to him when you first walked in?”

“Because he’s meant to be a surprise, and Agatha’s birthday isn’t until Saturday,” Rio replied, scooping up more food onto her fork. “And he just happens to be a little demon. No wonder his previous owners gave him up.” She shoveled more food into her mouth, tearing off a piece of tortilla and wrapping some of her eggs in it.

“He seems pretty sweet to me,” Marisol said, scraping the last bits of her food into a half-tortilla. “He came right up to me and flopped on his back. He let me pet his belly. He’s so soft. I think Agatha’s really going to love him.”

Rio’s fork dropped to the table, as did her jaw. “You’ve got to be kidding me,” she huffed, standing up and storming over to where the little jackass’s cage stood, in the corner of the kitchen. He was munching on a couple pieces of lettuce that Rio had made him. His nose twitched at her as she crouched down in front of him, pointing a finger in his face. “You little shit,” she hissed. “I get nothing from hisses and bites from you for three whole days, but you wanna act all cute and innocent the second my mom shows up? What the hell, dude?”

“Oh, quit it, Rio,” Marisol snorted. “He can’t be that bad.”

“He is a monster!” Rio insisted, standing up and pointing down at the bunny, who once again just blinked up at her.

“Si,” Marisol said, “qué monstruo tan aterrador.”  

Rio’s eye twitched. “He peed and pooped all over the living room, Mami,” she reminded her.

“So he needs to be house-broken,” Marisol said with a shrug. “You took three years to start using the toilet.”

“They told me he was pad-trained!” Rio exclaimed. “He just hates me!”

“Oh, I don’t think he’s capable of hate. Look at him!” She stood and walked over to the cage, moving Rio to the side as she opened the door and reached in for him.

Whereas Scratchy might have attempted to bite Rio’s fingers clean off, with Marisol he just went prone as she lifted him out of the cage and cuddled him under her chin, pressing kisses to his little head. Scratchy shut his eyes and practically purred, pressing up into her in bliss. 

“Tan suave,” Marisol cooed, scratching under his chin. His little butt wagged as he melted into her embrace. “You see? He’s such a sweetheart.”

“I hate him,” Rio grumbled. She could swear Scratchy glared at her just then. Of course, Marisol didn’t catch that as he continued to cuddle against her chest.

“Don’t be so dramatic,” Marisol chuckled, pressing another kiss to Scratchy’s forehead. “You two just gotta get to know each other a little better.”

“He tries to bite me every time I go near him!” Rio argued. “How, exactly, am I supposed to ‘get to know him’??!!”

“Try harder,” Marisol said with a shrug. “Be nicer to him.”

“I am so nice to him!” Rio whined. “I give him all the flowers he can eat. His favorite are dandelions.”

She grew a dandelion in her hand and offered it to him. Scratchy’s nose twitched at the flower for half a second before he reached out and chomped on it, narrowly missing Rio’s fingers. Rio pulled her hand away as if burned.

“He did that on purpose,” she huffed. 

Marisol just rolled her eyes, pressed another kiss to his little twitchy nose, and placed him back into the cage.

“Go get ready for school,” she said. “And make sure to invite Agatha over for dinner tonight.”

“What? Why? Her birthday isn’t until Saturday.”

“So? Does she not eat dinner on days that aren’t her birthday?”

“No,” Rio huffed, blushing, “I just meant…well, what’s the occasion?”

“I’m back in town and I want to see her. I’ll make pernil.”

Rio’s stomach instantly started growling at that. “Okay,” she said. “I’ll ask, but she might be busy.”

“Busy?” Marisol snorted. “With what?”

“I dunno,” Rio said. “She has homework and stuff, you know.”

“Well, tell her that I would really like it if she came to dinner,” Marisol said. “It would mean a lot to me.”

“That’s emotional blackmail,” Rio said, “but alright.”

Marisol rolled her eyes again.

“Wait,” Rio said, before she left to go change for school, “where are we gonna hide the demon?”

“Stop calling him that!” Marisol said, swatting her shoulder. “We can put the bunny in my room since I assume Agatha will like to spend some time in yours.” She wiggled her eyebrows at Rio, who flushed bright pink.

“Don’t say it like that, Mami!” she huffed.

“What? I’m not naive, mijita. I know how teenagers think and act. You’ve had this whole house to yourself for two weeks, but Lorna tells me you’ve been spending every night with Agatha. What else am I supposed to think?”

“Ay, Mami, no! We haven’t…done that.” Her entire face was as red as a tomato. She did not want to be talking about this with her mother.

“It’s not like you could get pregnant, anyway,” Marisol said. “Not without some very strong magic.”

“Okay, this conversation is over,” Rio said. “I’m gonna go take a shower.”

Marisol cackled as Rio sprinted from the room.

 

Agatha was sitting at her desk in drama when a couple of hands covered her eyes.

“Guess who?” a gruff – and obviously fake – voice said behind her.

“Whomever it is,” Agatha replied with a dry voice, “your hands smell like cheese.”

“What?” Rio asked, pulling her hands back to sniff at her own fingers.

“You’re too easy,” Agatha snorted, turning in her chair to face her. 

“And you’re mean,” Rio retorted, pouting.

“Aw, poor baby,” Agatha cooed, scratching under Rio’s chin.

Rio purred.

“I don’t even wanna know how you learned to make that sound,” Agatha murmured.

“It only happens when I’m really happy,” Rio informed her. “Like when I’m around you.” She batted her eyelashes at Agatha, whose cheeks went pink.

“Shut up,” she mumbled, turning to look at her notebook open on her desk.

Rio snickered and leaned in, pressing a kiss to Agatha’s cheek as she sat down in her own seat. Agatha shrugged her off, but Rio could see the adorable little smile she tried to hide.

Soon enough, the bell rang and class began. Lilia had started a unit on stage adaptations, talking about films and books that had been adapted into plays, then going into classic fairy tales that have taken on many different forms over the years.

She was right in the middle of a lecture on the pros and cons of adapting a musical from screen to stage when the bell rang and she blinked in confusion, looking at her watch.

“Has it really been forty minutes already?” she gasped. “My, how time flies. I didn’t even get to the subject of our next project. Well, I’ll just email everybody the details tonight, then. Keep an eye out! Now, shoo!” She waved her hands at them. 

Rio waited for Agatha to gather her things before she took her hand and tugged her out into the hall. 

“So,” she said, “as they began walking toward Agatha’s next class, “my mom came home.”

“Already?” Agatha gasped. “I thought she wasn’t getting home until tonight!”

“Me too,” Rio said. “I guess she got an early start or something, I dunno. Anyway, the point is she wants you to come for dinner.”

“At your place?” Agatha asked, eyes wide.

“Where else?” Rio replied with a snort. “She’s gonna make pernil. It’s so good.”

“I wouldn’t expect anything less,” Agatha laughed. “This will be the first time I come over your house.”

“Yeah,” Rio said, softly. “Are you…do you not want to?”

“No, I do!” Agatha said. “I just…it feels like a significant step. Should I bring something?”

Rio shrugged. “You can if you want to, but I don’t think my mom’s going to be expecting anything, you know? So you’ll come?”

“Of course I will,” Agatha said, stroking her cheek. “Sounds great, honestly. I missed Marisol, too.”

“I think she may have missed you more than she missed me,” Rio admitted.

“I’m sure that’s not true,” Agatha cooed, patting her cheeks somewhat condescendingly. 

Rio rolled her eyes but still pulled her in closer as they approached her next class. She leaned down and pressed a kiss to Agatha’s cheek. “I’ll see you at lunch?” she asked.

“So long as you don’t go home to visit your pet squirrel.”

“There is no squirrel!” Rio insisted as Agatha snickered and made her way into the classroom.

“Whatever you say, babe,” she said, blowing a kiss over her shoulder.

“You save a critter one time,” Rio grumbled as she started toward her next class.

Chapter End Notes

I will forever love the Rio/Scratchy Beef unashamedly.

Chapter 28: Jarritos

Chapter Summary

Marisol cooks a delicious dinner with a nice surprise for Rio and Agatha.

Chapter Notes

I desperately wanted to get this finished before 2026 and...well, I did. For my peeps in North and South America, anyway.

For anybody who's reading this in other continents, what's the future like?

Anyway, enjoy this chapter and Happy New Year!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty-Eight

The furry little bastard was the closest he’d ever come to being made into a stew.

Rio was chasing him around the house with a pair of gardening gloves (in an effort not to lose a finger to his huge-ass teeth) but she couldn’t seem to catch up with him. Her mother was in the kitchen, stirring up some yellow rice with vegetables and keeping an eye on the pernil that was roasting in the oven.

Usually, she would have gotten the pork at the butcher’s a couple of days beforehand and let it marinate in the fridge for two days before popping it in the oven for about six hours, sans magic, but this time was different. She’d gotten a smaller cut of pork (it would only be the three of them after all) and had bought it pre-marinated from one of their neighbors, who worked as a butcher but also sold seasoned meat out of his own refrigerator on the side.

Rio knew how much her mami hated doing that.

“Carlo has no idea what he’s doing,” she’d complained once, preheating the oven for the marinated meat she’d bought just that morning because Rio’s cousins were dropping by, last-minute, on a trip to upstate New York. “He doesn’t put the right balance of spices and it comes out tasting all wrong!” She had tried to remedy this by adding her own blend, but it didn’t quite taste the same as her own, homemade pernil. 

“Then why do you buy it from him?” Rio asked. “Why don’t you just season some pork yourself in the morning and start cooking it right away?”

“Because the meat needs to marinate,” Marisol said. “It’s an integral step of the whole process, mija. Without it, this would not be pernil.”

“But if he’s doing it wrong…” Rio started.

Marisol just waved her off, unwilling to explain herself. Rio learned to stop questioning her, anyway.

She certainly didn’t question her mother as she muttered about Carlo’s incompetence while she opened the oven door to check on the food. She just placed a kiss on her cheek in greeting before going to feed the little demon who had taken up residence in a corner of the living room. 

She had had hoped that providing Scratchy with a handful of baby carrots and a full head of cabbage would buy enough goodwill for him to allow her the honor of carrying him toward her mother’s room, where he’d be staying for the rest of the night while Agatha was there, but the little shit had seen her coming – even with her arms full of tasty vegetables just for him – and sprinted away from her, practically leaving a dust cloud in the shape of himself in his wake.

Rio had just blinked at him, bouncing around the room, showing more energy than she’d seen from the bunny in the weeks since she’d gotten him from the shelter.

“I should have just gotten her a cat,” she huffed, dumping the veggies into his food dish and chasing after him. “Get back here, you little monster!”

Scratchy hissed at her every few steps, standing on his hind legs and waving his front paws at her like he was a little Mike Tyson, about to take her out with a one-two combo or something.

“Are you kidding?” Rio groaned, reaching out for him. “Stop being so–JESUS!”

He full on chomped at her hand, nearly taking a couple of fingers, then he growled at her.

“What the hell is wrong with you?” Rio huffed, counting her digits. “What circle of hell did you come from?”

Scratchy twitched his nose at her.

“Dude, just let me take you into the other room,” Rio said, reaching for him again.

Scratchy hissed and took off before her fingers could even brush his fur. She let out a loud groan and watched him hop around the room at warp speed for a minute before retrieving her gardening gloves from the coat closet and slipping them on.

“Okay,” she said, clapping them together. “Let’s do this.”

Marisol occasionally looked over her shoulder as her daughter chased the little bunny past the doorway to the kitchen, cursing up a storm at the little ball of fur as he evaded capture. She rolled her eyes and stirred the rice and checked on the meat, inhaling the savory scents as it cooked. It would not be as good as the pernil she made from scratch, she knew, but at least it would get the job done.

At the one hour mark of watching Rio chase Scratchy around the living room, Marisol turned the heat down on the pernil and let the rice sit for a moment on low, making her way into the living room, where her daughter was lying, face-down, on the carpet, her arms and legs splayed out like she’d just fallen from a great height.

Scratchy was on her back, laying down in a loaf shape, his little nose twitching.

Rio didn’t move a muscle to grab him. She knew he’d bounce the second she even attempted to lift her head. It was useless.

Marisol reached down and took him into her arms, cradling him like a baby as she pressed her face into his fur. “Who’s a naughty boy, huh?” she cooed, kissing his head. “Are you a naughty boy?”

Rio turned her head to glare sideways up at her mother and the bunny. “He’s a demon,” she growled. 

“No es un demonio,” Marisol tutted. “He just doesn’t like you very much.”

“I hope he feels the same about Agatha,” Rio sighed. “This way I have a reason to return him to the shelter.”

Scratchy hissed at that.

“I hope it’s a kill shelter!” she growled back at him, pushing herself back to her feet. He bared his teeth at her, and she mirrored him.

“Behave,” Marisol demanded, flicking her daughter’s forehead.

“Ow! Mami!” Rio whined, rubbing her forehead and pouting. “Why don’t you tell him that? He started it! I was just trying to put him in your bedroom before Agatha–”

The doorbell rang.

“Shit!” Rio huffed. “That’s gotta be her. Mami, can you please put Scratch n’ Sniff in your bedroom for me? He likes you.”

“Fine,” Marisol said, tucking the bunny against her chest. “Go answer the door and then stir the rice for me. Wash your hands first.”

“Okay,” Rio said, ridding herself of the gardening gloves on her way to the front door. She tossed them into the hall closet, then she checked her appearance in the hallway mirror, running her fingers through her hair and straightening the wrinkles in her shirt. Then she sniffed her pits and wrinkled her nose.

She was sweaty from chasing the demon bunny for the last hour.

She grew some lavender and rubbed it against her underarms before turning to the door and taking a deep breath. Then she painted on a big smile and opened the door, greeting her girlfriend…

…who looked very pretty tonight.

Agatha was dressed in a knee-length violet dress with a white daisy pattern and a white knitted cardigan over it. She had on a pair of purple Converse high-tops on her feet. She was also wearing light makeup and carrying a bottle of wine?

“Where’d you get that from?” Rio asked, after greeting her with a kiss on her cheek, pulling her into the house.

“Lorna sent it,” Agatha informed her. “She said never to show up at somebody else’s home empty-handed. I was just going to buy some cider or something, but she said this would be better. It’s ‘vintage’, apparently.”

“Cool,” Rio said, taking the wine bottle in one hand and lacing her fingers with Agatha’s with the other. “I’m sure Mami’ll love it.”

Marisol rarely drank, even on holidays, but she would definitely appreciate a vintage wine even if she never opened it. Rio could imagine the bottle still sitting in the pantry a few decades from now, her mother raving about the vintage but not allowing anybody a single sip of it.

It was the thought that counted, anyway, right?

“Something smells so good,” Agatha hummed, walking further into the house with Rio trailing after her, still carrying the wine as they made their way to the kitchen.

“That would be the pernil,” Rio informed her with a grin. “Mami only makes it on special occasions.” She placed the bottle of wine on the kitchen counter and opened the oven, inhaling the aroma with a deep sniff. Her stomach let out a soft rumble and her mouth watered.

“Wow,” Agatha said, placing her hands on her own stomach. “That smells so good. All this for me?” She motioned to the rice on the stovetop. Rio closed the oven and gave it a stir, inhaling that scent, as well. 

“Of course,” she said. “This is the very definition of a special occasion; it’s your first time at Casa Vidal!” She waved the spoon around with a flourish, scattering grains of rice on the floor and in her hair.

Rio winkled her nose and put the spoon back down and started to pick the grains out of her hair and off the floor as Agatha snorted at her.

“Who’s here?” Marisol called out, the click of her bedroom door closing reverberating around the house. “Is my Agatha here?”

Agatha’s face turned pink as Marisol turned the corner and immediately enveloped her in a hug, squeezing tightly. Agatha’s eyes widened slightly before closing as she sank into the embrace, hugging Marisol tightly back.

“Hola, Señora,” she murmured against Marisol’s shoulder.

“Agatha, por favor,” Marisol said, pulling back and cupping her cheeks. “It’s Marisol or Mami.”

Agatha’s face pinkened again. She cleared her throat. “Marisol,” she decided. “Hello.”

“How are you, my dear?” Marisol asked, wrapping her arm around Agatha’s waist and guiding her to the kitchen table while Rio continued to stir the rice and watch them over her shoulder. “Has Rio been treating you well while I’ve been away?”

Agatha chuckled at that. “Yes, Ma-a–ahem, Marisol,” she said, nodding. “She has.”

“I hear she’s been spending a lot of time at your place while I’ve been away, ah?” It wasn’t exactly suggestive, but Rio could practically hear the twinkle in her mother’s eye. She rolled hers as she gave the rice one more stir before turning off the heat completely.

“I think the rice is done, Mami,” she said. “Want me to put it into a bowl?”

“Un momento,” Marisol said. “Let me check.” She stood and made her way over to the pot, shooing Rio away. “Go set the table.”

“Okay, okay,” Rio huffed. “Jeez!”

She made a face at Agatha, who shook her head at her, but smiled. Rio took three plates out of the cabinet, grabbed some silverware, and got to setting the table.

“You want some help?” Agatha asked.

“Can you grab some cups?” Rio asked. “They’re in the cabinet next to the–”

“No cups tonight,” Marisol said, reaching for a serving bowl in the lower cabinet next to the oven. “Check the fridge.”

Rio placed the last fork down on the table next to her own dish and padded to the fridge, her eyes widening to the size of saucers when she opened it and saw what was inside.

“Jarritos?” she gasped. “Really?”

“Carlo says they sell them at the bodega two doors down from his butcher shop. I asked him to pick up a case for me, as a treat. One bottle per night; no te chifles.”

“Hell yeah!” Rio exclaimed, reaching in and taking one yellow glass bottle out. “Agatha, what’s your favorite flavor?”

“Of what?” Agatha asked, walking over to peer inside the fridge.

“Jarritos!” Rio answered, excitedly, cradling her own pineapple soda against her chest. “It’s a Mexican soda. So good.” She looked back at the bottles sitting on the shelf. “We have Mango, Fruit Punch, Grapefruit, Watermelon, Lime, and Guava: one of each.”

“Hmm,” Agatha said. “I like Mango as a flavor, but I’ve never had this before.”

“Sad childhood,” Rio tutted.

“Yes, but we already knew that,” Agatha snorted. Rio’s eyes widened when she realized what she’d just said. She opened her mouth to apologize, but Agatha held up her hand and shook her head. “Don’t worry about it,” she said. “I’m not.” She reached for the soda in the fridge, tugging it out to look at the label. “This looks like orange soda,” she said. 

“It’s way better,” Rio huffed. “Trust me.”

Agatha pressed a kiss to her cheek. “Always,” she said, softly.

Rio stopped functioning, sputtering for a few moments while Agatha snickered. “You are so easy,” she said, walking away from the fridge. 

Rio frowned at her and reached in to grab her mother’s Jarritos of choice, Watermelon, to bring it to the table. 

Marisol had already placed a platter with the pernil and the bowl of rice down on the table. Agatha was sitting to her left while Marisol served her the meat and rice. Rio placed the drink out of the way for her mother and went to retrieve the bottle opener from one of the drawers. She opened all three bottles for them.

“What a gentleman,” Agatha teased, which made Rio’s cheeks go warm as she took her own seat across the little table from her mother, to Agatha’s left. She softly kicked her ankle. Agatha stuck out her tongue. Rio mirrored her.

“Children,” Marisol tutted. “Behave.” She placed Agatha’s plate in front of her, then started on Rio’s.

“I can make my own, Mami,” Rio assured her, standing up to take her plate back. 

“Don’t be ridiculous,” Marisol said, waving her away as she spooned a generous helping of rice and gave Rio a large portion of pernil. She handed the food over and Rio leaned down to press a kiss to her temple.

“Gracias, Mami,” she said.

“De nada, querida,” Marisol replied. “¡Sientate!”

Rio sat down with her food and drink, lifting it over the center of the table as soon as her mother had served herself food.

“Salud!” she said.

“Salud!” Marisol echoed.

“Salud!” Agatha added, clinking her bottle shyly with theirs.

They each took a sip of their soda, and Rio watched as Agatha’s eyes widened at her first taste of the mango Jarritos. She pulled it away from her lips and smiled at Rio.

“That’s really good,” she said. 

“Told you,” Rio said. “Now try the pernil. Your mind is about to be blown.” Rio took a bite of her own and let out a moan. “So good,” she whispered with a contented sigh.

Agatha wasted no time digging into her own food, practically demolishing her first helping in less than ten minutes. She’d never tasted anything so good in her life. The drink was delicious, too. The mango was sweet and the soda itself was pleasantly bubbly. She let out a soft belch at one point and covered her mouth with her hand, clearing her throat. Before she could say ‘excuse me’ however, Rio let out an ear-shattering belch.

“Rio Cristiana Vidal!” Marisol chastised.

“No regrets,” Rio sighed, patting her stomach.

Marisol sent a green zap at her, making Rio jump. “¡Disculpe!” Rio squeaked, flushing as Agatha giggled at her. 

“So,” Marisol asked as they ate, “how are preparations for the play going? Have you received your twinkle prize yet, Agatha?”

“Sparkle prize, Mami,” Rio corrected gently.

“Lo que sea,” Marisol said, dismissively, waving a hand at her. “Did you get it, querida?”

“Unfortunately, no,” Agatha said with a sigh. “Lilia thinks I’m holding back my best.”

“Well, are you?” Marisol asked, taking a sip of her drink. 

Agatha shrugged. “I didn’t think I was,” she said, “but now I’m not so sure.”

“You’ll get it soon,” Rio said, reaching for her hand. “I’m sure of it.”

Agatha turned to her with a soft smile. “Tha–is that a bunny?”

Rio’s eyes went wide and she spun around to see Scratchy in the doorway that led from the hallway into the kitchen. He was glaring at her, his evil little nose twitching.

“Shit,” she murmured, her shoulders slumping. “How the hell did you get out of your cage?”

“I didn’t put him in his cage,” Marisol said, wiping her mouth with a napkin as she stood and made her way to the bunny. He let her pick him up with zero issues, cuddling against her chest as she stroked his back and kissed his little head. “I put him on a pillow on my bed. He was napping. Eras un conejito con mucho sueño.” She scratched him under his chin and his little cotton tail wiggled.

“When did you get a bunny?” Agatha asked, standing up and moving closer to Marisol and the fluffy little demon. She reached out her fingers so that he could sniff them. Rio watched with caution, praying that he wouldn’t bite her.

He didn’t. He licked her fingers, purring as Marisol handed him over, looking over Agatha’s shoulder at Rio, cautiously.

“We didn’t,” Rio said. “I mean…not really? He’s not ours.”

“Did you ‘rescue’ him?” Agatha snorted, stroking his soft fur. Scratchy immediately took to Agatha, settling himself in the crook of her arm like a baby, his eyes closing in bliss as she scratched his belly.

“Only in the sense that he came from a shelter,” Rio admitted. 

“You went to a shelter to get him?” Agatha asked, furrowing his brow. “But he’s not your pet? I don’t…” 

Her eyes widened then, realization dawning on her face.

“Is…is he for me?” she asked, looking down at the little creature in her arms that was giving her heart eyes as he basked in her attention. “You got me a bunny for my birthday?”

“Technically,” Rio said, “Lorna paid his adoption fees. And his vaccination fees. And for pretty much everything else for him. I just agreed to house him for a few days until your birthday.”

Tears filled Agatha’s eyes as she handed Scratchy back to Marisol and ran to hug her girlfriend, burying her face in her shoulder. “I love you so much,” she murmured into Rio’s shirt. She pulled back, cupping Rio’s cheeks, squishing her face a little bit while Rio gave her that goofy, love-filled grin.

“I love you, too,” she said. “And I’m glad you like him because he does not like me.”

As if to prove it, Scratchy let out a little hiss from behind Agatha, upset at having been taken from his new owner’s arms. Rio hissed back at him and Agatha rolled her eyes.

“You two are going to have to get used to each other,” she said, wrapping her arms around Rio’s waist. “You’re his mommy, too, now.”

“I am not that thing’s mother,” Rio huffed. “I’m his stepmom, at most. And I am not stepping up to raise that little shit.”

“Be nice,” Agatha laughed, leaning up to press a kiss to Rio’s lips. Rio hummed into the kiss, melting into Agatha’s embrace. “For me?” Agatha asked, pulling back to hit her with the big blue eyes.

Rio folded instantly. “Fine,” she sighed. “I’ll be nice. For now.”

Agatha rolled her eyes and snorted, turning around to see Marisol with her phone in one hand, poised like she was snapping a photo, tears in her eyes.

“My babies,” she sniffled. 

Agatha snorted and hugged her before taking the bunny from the crook of her arm, pressing her nose to his and kissing his forehead. He let out a purr. 

“What a little cutie,” she said. “Did you name him yet?”

“Scratchy,” Rio told her. “On the account of him scratching me every time I try to go near his ungrateful ass.” Scratchy hissed at her again. “I saved you from euthanization!” She huffed, pointing directly at the bunny.

He just bared his teeth at her.

“Be good,” Agatha said, the hint of a laugh in her voice. She pressed another kiss to his head. “Scratchy is a nice name, I think,” she said, scratching under his chin. He purred again. “You seem to like it, too. Scratchy it is, then. Named by your other mommy.”

“Stepmom,” Rio corrected again.

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Stepmom, then,” she said. “What a perfect little gift you are.”

“You can’t have him yet,” Rio said.

“What?” Agatha moaned. “But whyyyy?” She held Scratchy close to her chest, pressing her face into his fur.

“Because Lorna would kill me if she knew I gave him to you early. She wants to be there when you meet him for the first time. On Saturday.”

“But,” Agatha said, pouting and looking down at her bunny. 

“Sorry,” Rio said. “I know it sucks, but you can’t let Lorna know that you know about Scratchy. And you can’t take him home.”

“But you can come back every day to see him, if you’d like,” Marisol said. “You two have spent more than enough time at Lorna’s anyway. It’s time for me to spend some time with my nuera, anyway.” She wrapped an arm around Agatha’s waist, pulling her in for a side-hug as she continued to cuddle Scratchy.

“Fine,” Agatha sighed. “I’ll leave him here.”

Scratchy let out a noise of protest, as if he understood.

“I know, baby,” Agatha cooed, “but I’ll come back to see you. And then you can come home with me this weekend.”

Rio had never seen a bunny pout, but Scratchy was doing it.

Agatha kissed his forehead again before placing him down on the ground. He hopped around her legs and rubbed up against her while she giggled. Rio smiled at them as she made her way out of the kitchen, toward the bathroom.

But then she stopped dead in her tracks once she saw the state of her mother’s bedroom door.

“Uh…Mami?” she called back down the short flight of steps. 

“Yes?” Marisol asked, poking her head out of the kitchen doorway.

“You might want to see this,” Rio said, grimacing as she glanced back at her mother’s bedroom door, which had a little, bunny-sized hole chewed in the bottom left-hand corner of it.

Little demon.

Chapter End Notes

Little demon or little angel? Depends who you ask, I guess.

Again, Happy New Year! I hope 2026 is...survivable? We'll see.

Chapter 29: Complete

Chapter Summary

This is part one of Agatha's birthday chapters. Part two will be up ASAP.

Chapter Notes

Sorry this took so long, but I just switched to a new job and I'm struggling to adjust. Plus the other job that I had started giving me more hours just as this one started, which is annoying but it is what it is.

I am so tired.

Please enjoy this chapter, however short it is. The next part will be up as soon as possible.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Twenty-Nine

Rio’s bedroom was…very Rio.

There were posters all over the walls, just like Agatha’s bedroom. Instead of posters of Broadway shows, however, there were bands and musicians and a few old movie posters with Audrey Hepburn and Marilyn Monroe in them. There were also bookshelves and a desk littered with books and papers. There was a dresser that had pictures of Rio with her mother and a man who was tall and stocky with that same goofy, gap-toothed grin that Rio had. 

Rio’s late father, Agatha’s mind supplied as she held her girlfriend’s hand a little more tightly. Scratchy was held in the crook of her left arm, snoozing with his head pressed into her armpit. She placed him on the bed.

“No, don’t,” Rio said. “He’ll probably pee or shit or something.”

“Don’t do that,” Agatha said, wagging her finger at him. He continued to snooze, his little nose twitching.

“You sure told him,” Rio teased, sitting up against her headboard, far away from where Scratchy lay at the foot of the bed. 

Agatha slipped in next to her, tucking herself into Rio’s side as she continued to look all around. The walls were sage green, comforting. The floor was hardwood, but mostly covered by an area rug with a funky leaf pattern. Most of the stuff in the room was organized, but there were a few spots where Rio had haphazardly thrown a sweater or kicked off a pair of sneakers. There was a giant stuffed spider in the corner by the open closet door. It was scary realistic.

“That’s Queen Victoria,” Rio said when she realized where Agatha’s eyes had gone. “I’ve had her since I was six.”

“Why?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

Rio shrugged. “My aunt brought me to the zoo with my cousins,” she said. “We went to the reptile house, which also had a bunch of insects and arachnids. My cousins were terrified of the tarantulas, but I thought they were fascinating.”

Agatha snorted. “Of course you did,” she said.

“I became obsessed with them. I checked out a bunch of books from the library about them and started begging my parents to let me get one.” She smiled fondly at the memory. “Obviously, Mami was deadset against it, but Papi…” She took a deep breath. Agatha reached down to squeeze her hand. Rio pressed her cheek to Agatha’s head and took a deep breath. “He gave me Queen Victoria that same Christmas,” she said. “He said he hoped her size made up for the fact that she wasn’t alive.” She snorted. “I used to torture my cousins whenever they came over by chasing them around the house, holding her over my head.”

Agatha let out a laugh just imagining a tiny Rio running around with the giant tarantula held out, chasing after other kids and laughing maniacally. It wasn’t hard to imagine.

“You must have been a menace,” she teased, squeezing Rio’s hand. 

“Oh, I was,” Rio laughed. 

They lapsed into a comfortable silence after that, their fingers tangled between them, Agatha’s head on Rio’s shoulder and Rio’s on Agatha’s head. Scratchy continued to snooze by their feet.

“Thank you for my birthday gift, by the way,” Agatha said. “I love him.”

“It’s not really my gift,” Rio said. “I’m just housing him until Saturday. Lorna’s the one who paid for everything.”

“So you have another gift for me then?” Agatha asked, teasingly.

“Keeping this demon alive isn’t enough?” Rio retorted, motioning at Scratchy, who was now laying on his back with his little paws in the air. Agatha found him adorable, but Rio was still glaring at him in disgust.

They’d grow to love each other, she was sure of it.

“It is,” Agatha said. “Everything you’ve done for me over the last few months is more than enough, actually.”

“What have I done, exactly?” Rio asked, looking down at her with genuine confusion in her eyes.

“You loved me,” Agatha said, the words falling off her tongue easily. “That’s more than enough. That’s more than I’ve had for most of my life.”

“You’re easy to love.”

Her own words repeated back to her made Agatha’s heart swell as tears filled her eyes. She leaned up, pressing a kiss to Rio’s lips, which was welcomed with enthusiasm.

Then Rio suddenly pulled back with a grimace.

“What’s wrong?” Agatha asked, blinking up at her.

Rio’s gaze turned to a glare down the bed, where Scratchy was sitting at her feet, glaring back. There was a tiny tear in the big toe of her sock. The bunny’s nose twitched.

“Mister!” Agatha gasped. “No! Bad boy!” She let go of Rio’s hand to crawl toward the bunny, gently tapping him on the head. “No biting. You need to be nicer to Rio.”

Scratchy let out a displeased noise, but Agatha didn’t budge. She showed him no affection when he attempted to rub himself against her knee, instead moving away from him. He let out another displeased noise. 

“Be nice to Rio,” Agatha reiterated. “She’s the one taking care of you right now.”

“Yeah, ya little sh–” At Agatha’s glare, Rio pressed her lips together.

“You be nice, too,” she murmured. “You two need to learn to get along, for my sake.”

Rio took a deep breath. “Fine,” she said. “He won’t be living here much longer, anyway.”

“But he’s going to become my Familiar,” Agatha reminded her. “So he’ll be around for a long while.”

“Fantastic,” Rio groused. 

Scratchy echoed the sentiment with another noise, but at least he didn’t bite her again, instead flopping against her feet as a show of peace. Rio nudged him with her foot, but she didn’t kick him away completely.

That was about as much as Agatha could hope for.

 

For the rest of the week, Agatha went home with Rio for lunch. Mostly that just consisted of her cooing at Scratchy while Rio cleaned up after the little demon, who still apparently hadn’t mastered the wee-wee pads. 

Agatha offered to do the cleanups, but Rio waved her off, letting her have her bonding time with her new pet. 

When it was time to go, they left him with a few hand-grown vegetables (“You see how nice Rio is to you?”) and Agatha pressed about a million kisses to his face before she left as though it would be a year before she’d see him again, rather than just a few hours.

They’d return to spend their free period with the bunny as well while running their lines. 

At rehearsal, Agatha would do her very best on stage. She had the majority of her wardrobe now, but she still didn’t have that damn hat. She had no idea why Lilia was keeping it from her. She had always gotten her Sparkle Award long before this point in rehearsals. They were already doing full run-throughs and Jen was still having to mime gifting her the hat because Agatha hadn’t earned it yet.

Agatha was about to throw a full-on tantrum when she still didn’t receive it on Thursday even though she had received no notes.

“What’s the deal?!” she’d huffed at Lilia after most of the cast had dispersed to get back into their street clothes. “Why are you keeping my hat away from me?”

“Nobody’s keeping anything away from you,” Lilia snorted. “You just haven’t earned it yet. You will. Eventually. I hope.”

“Ugh!” Agatha huffed, tossing her arms in the air as she walked away.

“You’re mean,” Alice murmured, watching her walk away.

Lilia shrugged. “She’ll get over it,” she said, taking a sip of tea from her mug.

Agatha consoled herself by spending all of Friday afternoon at Rio’s, playing with Scratchy while Rio worked in the garden. The weather was really starting to warm up with April’s arrival, and her vegetable garden was already seeing results. 

Nice.

She plucked one of the daffodils from her flower garden and presented it to Agatha with a bow. Agatha blushed and thanked her with a kiss to her cheek, which made Rio’s entire face go red to the tips of her ears.

Scratchy had kicked her, but only because he’d been trapped between their bodies for a second too long. At least he didn’t bite her this time, though.

At the end of the night, Agatha showered kisses on the bunny before she left Rio’s, promising that tomorrow he’d be coming home with her for good. Then she’d kissed Rio, stroking the ridge of her cheekbone with her thumb, softly. The kiss was filled with affection and longing. Rio melted into it, her arms wrapping themselves around Agatha’s waist like she would never let go.

But, of course, she did have to let go. Eventually.

She mourned the loss by laying, face-down, on her bed. She didn’t even kick Scratchy out when he flounced into her bedroom, obviously following the scent Agatha had left behind from being there the last few days.

“You are so dramatic,” her mother had said, passing by the room on the way to her own. “You’ll see her tomorrow.”

“Tomorrow is so far away,” Rio moaned, pathetically.

“Teatrera,” Marisol snorted, flicking off the lights in Rio’s bedroom. “¡Duérmete!”

Rio did as she was told. In the morning, she woke up to find Scratchy sleeping on the pillow next to hers, his little nose twitching as he inhaled Agatha’s scent.

 

At rehearsal, Rio ran straight for Agatha, embracing her with a tight hug and a kiss that she could swear made the other girl weak in the knees. When Rio pulled away, Agatha’s entire face was bright pink. Rio just grinned at her, feeling cocky.

Agatha glared and flicked her between the eyebrows. “Don’t gloat,” she chastised.

“Ow!” Rio moaned, rubbing the spot. “Who was gloating?”

Agatha rolled her eyes.

“Alright, everybody!” Lilia said, coming in with a comically large thermos. “Go get dressed! Curtains up in ten! I expect all of you to be fully off-book! If anybody says ‘line’ today, you’re running ten laps on the track after rehearsal.”

“Can she do that?” Rio asked. 

“I don’t think it matters,” Agatha retorted. “We’re all gonna do it, anyway.”

“That’s wild.”

“That’s power,” Agatha corrected. “Come on.” She took Rio’s hand and tugged her toward the dressing room.

When they were fully dressed (sans Agatha’s hat), Agatha and Rio joined the rest of the cast in the audience. There were two spots right in the front row and they felt everybody’s eyes on them as they claimed their seats.

“Before we begin our dress rehearsal today,” Lilia said. “A certain somebody has a very important birthday today. Eighteen years old, in the magic world, as many of you know, is the age of maturity. It is the age at which a witch traditionally sets off on her own and blah, blah, blah,” she waved her hand around while other cackled. “Anyway, let’s sing!” She clapped her hands together and Alice started playing ‘Happy Birthday’ on the piano.

Every year was the same on Agatha’s birthday. She’d had the luck to have had all four of her high school birthdays now on days that she was in rehearsal, so she was always sung to by the rest of the club, led enthusiastically by Lilia, who waved her arms and sang most beautifully of all before planting a big, lipsticked kiss on Agatha’s forehead while the girl flushed bright red and covered her face with her hands. 

Rio, as always, was right next to her. This time – unlike the three previous years – she was able to wrap her arm around Agatha’s shoulders, pulling her in to lay a kiss on her cheek and whisper a soft “happy birthday, babe,” in her ear. 

Agatha half-heartedly shoved her away before burying her face into Rio’s shoulder while all of their friends cooed and ‘aww’ed teasingly at her.

“Okay!” Lilia said, clapping her hands. “That’s enough of that! Time for the show! Places, people! Full run-through!”

Agatha was the first to get to her feet and run toward the stage, leaving Rio with her lips still pursed, kissing the air. 

 

Agatha made sure to put on her very best show at that rehearsal. They had two weeks left until opening night, after all, and she needed to earn her hat finally. Thankfully, nobody else forgot their lines, so it was easy to do her part without the need for any kind of improv.

By the end of the show, she was certain that she’d get a call any day now that she was nominated for a Tony.

Even was Lilia was on her feet clapping, cheering, “Brava! Brava!” with a big, bright smile on her face. The tech crew joined her, whistling from backstage, whooping and throwing pretend flowers (and a few real ones from the green witches on the crew) onto the stage as they practiced their bows. Agatha plucked one up and tucked it behind Rio’s ear, smirking at the flush that spread across her girlfriend’s cheeks. 

When they finally took their seats back in the audience, Lilia was already beaming at them all, her clipboard held tight to her chest, her lips spread almost painfully wide as she looked out at them.

“In all my many, many years,” she said, “I have never seen quite a fantastic rehearsal! That was incredible! Magical, even! Give yourselves all a round of applause!” As if to demonstrate, she began to clap. The cast and crew followed, cheering for themselves and high-fiving each other. Agatha was smiling so hard that her cheeks hurt. “Magnificent!” Lilia said. “If only George were here to witness it! Rio, your dancing has come so far, he wouldn’t even threaten to bang that cane of his!” Another cheer went up as Rio flushed and sunk down in her seat, giving her an embarrassed grin.

“Thanks,” she murmured. Agatha pressed a kiss to her temple and wrapped her arms around her from the side. Rio buried her face in Agatha’s hair, still flushing as their friends and classmates continued to cheer for her.

“Okay, okay,” Lilia said, after a solid minute of people cheering. “Let us now continue. I have Sparkle Prizes to give out today, but…no notes.”

“No notes?” somebody in the crowd gasped.

“That’s what I said,” Lilia snorted. “No notes today. You were all phenomenal! My only note is to keep that energy up for opening night!”

More cheers, this time for themselves and maybe a little for Lilia.

“I have a record number of Sparkle Prizes to give out today,” Lilia said. “For this show, at least. Eight.”

A gasp rippled through the crowd, and Lilia nodded. “Mhmm,” she said. “So many of you really stood out today and sparkled despite the fact that all of you were so fantastic today. The fact that so many of you caught my eye during this run-through is nothing short of a miracle. So, in no particular order, let us begin doling out prizes…”

Agatha sat ramrod straight in her seat, reaching out to squeeze Rio’s hand in hers. Rio squeezed back as they waited for the first name to be called.

“Today’s first recipient of a Sparkle Prize has been busting her butt on stage all week and it really showed how far she’s come since her first year here. She nailed all her dance moves and her lines, moving effortlessly across the stage as she charmed our witches. I’m of course talking about our Wizard, Ginette!”

A wave of applause went across the crowd as Ginette stood up and was patted on the back by her friends and classmates, her cheeks turning red as she shuffled up to the front of the auditorium to pick her hat from the box on the stage. 

She chose a green one. Lilia gave her a tight hug. “Congrats, doll,” she said. “You earned it.”

“Thanks, Lilia!” Ginette said, hugging her back before plopping her hat on her head and practically skipping back to her seat.

Lilia went through the next five recipients much the same way. She tried to play up the mystery of who was next by describing them and how hard they worked for their Sparkle Prize, then announced their name, gave them a tight hug, and sent them back into the cheering crowd.

Agatha watched with poorly contained envy every single time. She sunk lower and lower into her seat with every name that was called, starting to lose hope that she would finally be receiving her hat today. By the time the sixth name was called, she had given up on ever receiving her hat.

But then, Lilia locked eyes with her. 

“And now,” Lilia said, “I think this is the one we’ve all been waiting for – some more than others.” She smirked as a ripple of sound went over the audience and students shared looks between themselves. Some even glanced in Agatha’s direction as she pushed herself back up.

“This has been a long time coming,” Lilia said. 

Agatha reached for Rio’s hand, squeezing so tightly that Rio let out a soft grunt. Agatha loosened her hold, but Rio tightened hers. She took Agatha’s hand into her lap and held it with both of hers, offering Agatha a soft, supportive grin. Agatha’s heart and stomach both fluttered as she returned the smile and then turned forward.

Lilia’s sharp gaze caught hers immediately. Agatha nearly choked on her own saliva when she saw what Lilia was holding in her hands.

“This person has been a pain in my ass from the second she first stepped into this auditorium.” A few chuckles went through the crowd. “But in the time since, I’ve also grown quite…fond of her.” She took a breath. “Despite my better judgement,” she continued, wryly. The look in her eyes belied her words. They were twinkling as she looked straight at Agatha, a slight smirk on her lips as she played with the brim of the black hat. Agatha felt her own eyes beginning to burn. “She’s been one of my biggest stars on stage,” Lilia said. “And I’m not just talking about in her own class, or in the current student body.” More murmurs and a few gasps as eyes flicked toward Agatha, whose face had gone pink.

“I’ve been doing this job a long time,” Lilia went on, “and I’ve never seen somebody embody the characters they play quite like…Agatha Harkness.” A tear fell from Agatha’s eye as Rio squeezed her hand and Lilia’s smile widened and dazzled. She felt pats on her shoulders and back from the surrounding classmates. “Come up and collect your well-deserved prize, Miss Harkness. Before I change my mind.”

Agatha jumped to her feet and started to run forward, but there was something pulling her back. She turned to see Rio staring up at her, eyebrows raised as her gaze flicked between Agatha’s face and their still joined hands. Her grip had loosened, but Agatha’s had certainly not. 

Her face turned red and she untangled their fingers, grasping Rio’s hand one last hand to press them briefly to her lips with a small smile, practically transferring her own blush to Rio’s face (while their classmates let out a real mature “ooooooh!”) before she turned and sprinted straight at Lilia.

Lilia grinned wide as she held out the hat for Agatha to take. Instead of taking it, however, Agatha knocked Lilia’s hand aside and wrapped her arms around the older woman in a tight hug that knocked the wind out of her. Lilia’s eyes widened as the hat slipped from her grasp and fell to the ground with a soft thump. Her arms were held out at her sides for a long moment before slowly wrapping around Agatha’s waist.

“Thank you,” Agatha said. 

“For what?” Lilia asked. “The hat? You were always going to get it, doll.”

Agatha pulled back to look into Lilia’s eyes. Her own were filled with tears. “Not for the hat,” she said. Then she gave a watery chuckle. “Not just for the hat.” She swiped at the tears and took a deep breath, closing her eyes for a moment to collect herself. When they opened again, they were a clear crystal blue that made Lilia nearly gasp. “You’ve always been there for me,” Agatha said, her voice cracking. She cleared her throat. “Even when I was being a pain in the ass, you were there for me. You did more for me in these last four years than my mother has done for me in my entire life, and you didn’t even have to do any of it.” She swallowed thickly again, trying to pause the quiver of her lower lip. “I could have been just another student that passes through here.” She looked around the room. “You had–have no obligations to me. I’m just some annoying theater kid.”

“Hey,” Lilia said, placing her hands on Agatha’s shoulders as she looked her in the eyes. “No,” she said. “You could never be just anything, Agatha Harkness. You have always been extraordinary.” 

Tears began to fall down Agatha’s cheeks and she fought hard against them, her chin quivering even harder now.

“You are one of the most talented actresses and witches of your generation. You are going to do so many great things when you get out of this place, no matter what path you choose. And if somebody cannot see that about you, well, that’s their problem. You are one of a kind.”

The dam broke and Agatha threw herself back into Lilia’s arms, sobbing into her shoulder as the teacher’s hands rubbed soothing circles on her back. Lilia rocked her a little bit, whispering words of encouragement into her ear, holding her safe and warm in her arms. 

“It’s okay, love,” she said. “It’s okay. Let it all out.”

There were no words said by the rest of the students sitting in the audience, watching their classmate fall apart in their teacher’s arms. There were no murmurs or gasps of surprise or strange looks shared among them. There may have been a few sniffles and hands swiping away tears, but that was about it.

They just watched in respectful silence as Agatha and Lilia embraced, the former feeling safer than she ever had in an adult’s arms. The latter feeling more affection for the child in her arms than she thought was ever possible.

For the first time ever, they each felt complete.

Chapter End Notes
