Chapter 30: Surprise

Chapter Summary

Agatha gets a nice surprise when she goes home to the Wu household. Then a not so nice surprise. Then another nice surprise.

This one is kind of a rollercoaster to be honest. Buckle in.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Chapter Thirty

Agatha wanted to go home with Rio after rehearsal, but both Alice and Jen were tugging her in the opposite direction. 

“Don’t even try to get out of my mother’s birthday celebrations,” Alice was saying as she practically dragged Agatha toward the SUV parked outside the school. “It will not end well for you. Rio will be there, too. Eventually. But mom wants us to have a nice, quiet family lunch together.”

“Family lunch?” Agatha asked, finally giving up the struggle as Alice tugged her along. She felt her heart swell and her belly fill with butterflies. She tried to ignore them and act casual – especially after that frankly embarrassing display with Lilia in rehearsal. “Then why’s Jen coming?”

“Screw you,” Jen huffed, pinching Agatha’s arm with her bony fingers. “I’m family!”

“Family doesn’t kiss the way you two do,” Agatha murmured, receiving another pinch. “Agh! Quit that!”

“Family is more than parents and siblings,” Jen said, shoving Agatha into the backseat of the SUV before helping Alice in and getting in beside her. “Lorna is basically my mother-in-law.”

“You two aren’t married,” Agatha pointed out.

“Yet,” Alice said, cuddling against her girlfriend while Agatha made gagging noises. “You are a child. Your eighteenth birthday should be rescinded.”

“I’m pretty sure that’s not how that works,” Agatha said. 

“Whatever,” Jen huffed. “The point is, we’re all gonna have a nice lunch together, as a family.” She reached over Alice to attempt to pinch Agatha again, but the other girl crowded herself against the door, out of her reach. “And we’re gonna have a good time.”

“If you’re family,” Agatha pouted at her, “then how come my girlfriend isn’t family?”

“You two have been dating for two months,” Jen shot back.

“Two and a half,” Agatha corrected.

“Alice and I have been together for four years.”

“Almost five,” Alice chirped, happily. Jen placed a kiss against her temple.

“You can wait a couple of hours to see your girlfriend,” Jen said. “Just be patient.”

“But I don’t want to,” Agatha whined and pouted, stomping her foot on the car floor for good measure. “It’s my birthday. I should get what I want on my birthday, shouldn’t I?”

“Within reason,” Alice said. “And I think asking you to wait a max of, like, two hours before seeing your girlfriend is reason enough.”

“I disagree,” Agatha said.

“Too bad,” Jen and Alice chorused.

Agatha continued to pout.

She pouted all the way to the Wu residence. She pouted as she was pulled out of the car and walked to the front door with Jen and Alice tugging on her arms. She pouted as Alice opened the door into a darkened foyer.

She continued to pout until the lights turned on and several people appeared out of nowhere, screaming at her.

Agatha screamed back.

Well, it was more like a shriek as she jumped behind Jen, shoving her forward. 

“Agatha, what the hell?!” Jen exclaimed, turning around to look at the shorter, cowering girl. 

“Panic response?” Agatha suggested with a shrug. She peeked around Jen’s body to see the majority of their classmates and friends from drama standing around in the foyer, watching her with barely restrained amusement in their faces. “What are you all doing here?” she huffed. “And how did you get here before us?”

“Hexenbesen, mostly,” Billy said.

“Gesundheit,” Agatha retorted. 

“You’re hilarious,” Billy said in a deadpan voice, rolling his eyes. 

“I’m aware,” Agatha said, straightening out her spine and flipping her hair as she glanced around at all the people gathered in Lorna Wu’s foyer. 

Including Lorna Wu, who gave her a big smile and stepped forward, slipping something over her head as she placed a peck against her forehead.

“Happy birthday, sweet girl,” she said, hugging Agatha tightly. “I hope you don’t mind the company for lunch.”

Agatha shrugged, blushing. “It’s your house,” she said.

“Our house,” Lorna corrected, cupping Agatha’s cheeks in her hands. They were soft and gentle, but slightly callused around the fingers from years of playing instruments. Her thumbs stroked Agatha’s cheeks as she looked down into her eyes. “You are part of this family now, Agatha. You are as much my daughter as Alice or Jennifer.”

Agatha furrowed her brow. “Jen isn’t–”

“Spiritually,” Lorna interrupted, patiently. “And, hopefully soon, legally my daughter-in-law.” She glanced over at Jen and Alice.

“Mo-om,” Alice groaned, flushing as Jen wrapped her arms around her shoulders. “We’re eighteen!”

“I had my first marriage at eighteen,” Lorna pointed out. 

“1. That wasn’t even my dad, and 2. You’ve been divorced four times,” Alice pointed out.

Lorna shrugged. “Weddings are fun,” she said. “Besides, you two are gonna last. I can feel it.”

“We’ve lasted longer than two of her marriages,” Alice muttered to Jen. “Combined.”

Agatha heard that, but if Lorna heard it, she chose to ignore it as she hugged Agatha tightly, rocking her a little bit.

“Now, come and enjoy your party for a bit,” she said. “In your home.”

Agatha would never admit it, but she was fighting back tears for the second time in as many hours as Lorna embraced her. She schooled her features as the woman let her go and gave her a gentle nudge toward her party guests.

Agatha had never had a birthday party before. Except for the small parties her mom threw with her church friends and their daughters, which were just for show as all the gifts she’d gotten from those parties were never things she wanted. The money that she received from them was mostly taken by her mother, who chastised Agatha’s greed whenever she asked for it. She got to keep a couple of twenties and tens here and there, but most of the money went into ‘household expenses’ which Evanora never actually needed Agatha’s help to pay for when it wasn’t her birthday.

Agatha didn’t really care that much about birthdays as a result. They didn’t even matter to her until high school, where Lilia always made a big deal out of them by singing ‘Happy Birthday’ with the whole cast and crew. And Rio gave her flowers.

Those were the only celebrations that Agatha really cared about.

But this was nice, too.

All it was missing was…

“Hey, babe!” 

Agatha practically jumped out of her skin and spun around to see Rio standing just inside the open door, arms outstretched with a lot of bandaids littering her fingers. Behind her, Marisol was hefting a box on her hip with a few subtle holes in the sides. 

The box was moving. 

Agatha could just barely bite back her smile as she ran toward her girlfriend, then past her to get to Marisol, offering the woman an awkward side hug and receiving a kiss on the cheek in return.

“Look at you, birthday girl!” Marisol cooed. “That sash looks good on you, querida!” 

“Gracias,” Agatha said, laughing. “Is that for me?” Agatha pointed to the box.

“It is,” Marisol confirmed, subtly pulling it away when Agatha reached for it, “but for a little later.” She leaned in. “He’ll be fine. Rio put in a whole head of cabbage before we left the house,” she whispered in Agatha’s ear.

“Which is more than he deserves,” Rio grunted, appearing right next to them. “Where’s my hug and kiss?” She pouted at Agatha and gave her sad eyes.

“I hugged and kissed you like an hour ago,” Agatha laughed, even as she fell into Rio’s arms, squeezing her tightly and pressing kisses all over her face while her girlfriend giggled and held her back just as tightly.

“Get a room!” Jen called out to them.

“Don’t be rude,” Naomi said, swatting the back of her daughter’s head as she walked by with a drink. “Happy birthday, Agatha baby!” she called out.

“Thanks, Mrs. Kale!” Agatha called back, giving Jen a smirk. Jen subtly flipped her off. Agatha blew her a kiss before turning back to her girlfriend to kiss her for real. Rio accepted her affection with open arms – and lips. 

“Girls, behave!” Lorna said, bumping Agatha’s hip with her own. “We have company. Also, your mother is watching you, Rio.”

Rio’s face bloomed red as she turned her head to glance at her mother, who was standing by the refreshments table, sipping a drink as she spoke to Naomi Kale. Rio could see that she was only pretending to pay attention to whatever Naomi was saying as her eyes glanced back over at her the next second. She caught Rio’s eye and gave her a thumbs up and a big smile.

Rio hunched her shoulders. “Dios mio,” she groaned. “That’s embarrassing.”

“Presents in five minutes,” Lorna told them. “Go mingle with your friends in the meantime.”

“Presents?” Agatha asked, furrowing her brow.

Lorna motioned toward a table piled high with gifts. The huge box that Marisol had carried in was still moving, making a slow and steady trail…somewhere. Agatha pretended not to notice, trying to focus on the other gifts, which had not occurred to her as something she should expect at an honest-to-Goddess birthday party.

“Presents already?” Rio asked. “Don’t those happen last?”

“Well, there’s at least one really special present I’d like for Agatha to open before the party really gets underway,” Lorna said, practically vibrating with excitement. “But go, mingle. I’ll call everybody over when it’s time.” She shooed them away with a sweeping motion of her hands.

Agatha and Rio made their way over to a group of their theater friends. 

Theo and Sonny were amongst the group, their shoulders brushing as they traded shy glances at one another, both sets of cheeks pink as they sipped from their cups and listened to another student – Greg, Agatha thought his name was – talk about…something? It might have been some kind of nerdy game that Agatha really didn’t care to listen to. She just nudged Rio and motioned to the way Theo tentatively stretched his pinky toward Sonny’s, hooking it around theirs. Sonny bit back their smile and gave him a sideways glance.

“And they said we should get a room,” Agatha whispered in Rio’s ear.

Rio let out a puff of air that could have been a laugh, but she covered it with a cough.

“They’re cute,” she murmured back. “Let them be cute.”

“We were cute like them once,” Agatha said, laying her head on Rio’s shoulder.

“Still are,” Rio said, pressing a kiss to her temple. Agatha turned her head so that she could peck her lips instead.

“You two are so gross,” Theo said, but he was smiling as he raised his cup at them. “Mazel tov.”

“I didn’t know you were jewish,” Agatha said.

“My grandma is,” Theo informed her. “She wanted to throw me a bar mitzvah after I came out as trans, but my mom is all about me waiting until I’m officially an adult to choose a religion.” He shrugged. “I think it’s sweet, though.”

“It is,” Sonny said, smiling sideways at him. His cheeks turned pink.

Agatha wanted to be annoyed at how stupid and lovey-dovey they were, but it was hard to be judgemental with how goosebumps rose wherever Rio touched her body. So she just leaned closer to her girlfriend and let them be cute, or whatever.

Agatha and Rio made their way around the foyer and dining room, where Lorna’s hired caterers had set out all kinds of food, much like the spread she’d set out on Agatha’s first night there. They picked at a few finger foods and filled their cups with some kind of homemade purple punch that tasted like fresh berries. 

Agatha went back for a second cup before Lorna called everybody to the sitting room, where she had set up a large, royal purple sitting chair with balloons and a banner that said ‘It’s My Birthday!’ on it. The moving birthday gift was right next to it, still inching across the floor, though Marisol was attempting to keep it still with her foot on the box, muttering chastisements to the creature inside.

Lorna took Agatha’s hand and practically dragged her to the chair, pushing her down with a big smile before turning and clapping her hands.

Immediately, like a record scratch, the music that had been playing in the background of the party shut off and everybody in the room looked in Lorna’s direction. Even a few people from the hallway poked their heads inside to see what was happening. Lorna waved at them with a big, friendly smile.

“It’s time for our birthday girl’s special surprise!” Lorna exclaimed, motioning at Agatha, who was beginning to feel hot as a blush covered all perceivable skin. She hunched her shoulders and gave a shy wave to everybody who looked her way.

“I thought the party was my surprise,” she whispered to Lorna, even as she felt Scratchy move in the box at her feet.

“It was only the precursor to your actual surprise!” Lorna retorted, excitedly, taking a step back so that Agatha had full access to the big, slightly mobile box. 

Marisol had given up trying to keep it still and was now just staring at it with the rest of the party guests.

“Ta-da!” Lorna exclaimed, smiling proudly. “Rio’s been keeping it safe for you at her house for the last couple of weeks, but now it’s here! Go ahead and open it, sweetie!”

Agatha smiled brightly, trying not to give away the fact that she most certainly knew what the box held as she fell to her knees next to it and carefully undid the purple ribbon keeping the top from flying off – which it promptly did the second it was no longer secured. 

Scratchy tried to hop out, but he was too small and chubby, and the box was too deep. He let out a pitiful sound as he attempted to pull himself out and into Agatha’s arms. Agatha let out a happy squeal, careful not to say the bunny’s name as she pulled him out of the box and cradled him against her chest.

“A bunny!” she exclaimed.

“A bunny?!” Alice echoed. “What the hell, Mom?!”

“Alice Wu-Gulliver!” Lorna chastised. “Watch your mouth!”

“Watch my mouth?!” Alice huffed. “I’ve been asking for a dog for pretty much my entire life, but we’ve always been ‘too busy’ to care for one, but you’re perfectly fine giving Agatha a bunny?! That’s so messed up!”

She stormed out of the room with Jen not far behind. Agatha heard their footsteps ascend the steps and felt guilt settle in her chest even as she embraced the bunny, tucking his little head under her chin. She looked up at Lorna, who was frowning, tears in her eyes. 

When she caught Agatha’s eye, she quickly swiped them away and sniffled, forcing a smile at the young woman. “Don’t you worry about her,” she said. “She’ll be fine. I’m just going to go talk to her real quick. Go ahead and acquaint yourself with your new little friend, sweet girl.” She stroked Agatha’s hair once before making her way out of the room, clapping her hands as she went to restart the music.

Slowly, people began to resume their conversations, however awkwardly, while Agatha continued to stroke Scratchy as he cuddled into her, practically gluing himself to her chest.

“Alice probably hates me now,” Agatha said as Rio sat down on the floor next to her. Others gathered around to coo at Scratchy. She placed him on the floor to let him explore a little bit. He hopped around the circle her friends were making with their bodies. 

“I don’t think she does,” Rio said, soothingly, “or will.”

“But I got a pet after only being here a couple months,” Agatha pointed out, “even though she never did.”

“Her mom is getting her a dog,” Rio whispered, leaning in real close so nobody else could hear her.

Agatha’s eyes widened. “She is?” she asked. 

Rio nodded, grinning. “She told me while we were at the animal shelter, looking for your little demon there.” She motioned to Scratchy, who was eating celery off of Billy’s plate while he giggled. “I mentioned that Alice might be a little ticked off that she was giving you a pet while denying Alice one for so many years, and she showed me a really cute picture of a German shepherd in a police vest.”

“Can people have police dogs as pets?” Agatha asked. “Do they get their paychecks or something?”

Rio snorted and shook her head. “Apparently, he failed his training because he was too friendly. He wouldn’t attack on command, especially not the guys he trained with all the time that he knew weren’t a real threat. But he knows how to sense where drugs are hidden. And bodies.”

“Jeez,” Agatha said. “Perfect pet for Alice, huh?”

“He’s a good boy,” Rio snorted. “He’s staying with Alice’s dad right now. They were going to wait until her birthday to tell her about him, but, well…” She looked pointedly at Scratchy. 

“You think I spoiled the surprise?” Agatha asked, frowning.

“Not you, mi amor,” Rio said, pressing a kiss to her knuckles. “Lorna definitely should have told Alice before she gave you a bunny, though, so she didn’t get all her big feelings out in the middle of a birthday party.”

Agatha nodded in agreement. “I’m gonna go find them,” she said. “I know it’s not my fault, but I still kind of feel like I owe Alice an apology.”

“You don’t,” Rio insisted, tugging on her hand. 

Agatha squeezed hers back. “I know,” she said, “intellectually. But I have an uncomfortable feeling in my belly that’s still telling me I should check on her.” She wrinkled her nose. “What’s that called?”

“Guilt?” Rio asked.

“I don’t like it.”

“Pretty sure you’re not supposed to,” Rio snorted. “I’ll come with you,” she offered. “I have something to give you, anyway.”

“Ooh, a birthday gift?” Agatha asked, fluttering her lashes. “Can it wait a couple minutes? I need to talk to Alice and Lorna in private for a minute.”

“Sure,” Rio said, offering her an understanding smile. “I’ll meet you in your room in five?”

“Deal,” Agatha said, leaning down to press her lips against Rio’s head in a short and sweet peck before rushing off to ascend the steps. 

She heard the ‘oohs’ and ‘awws’ from behind her and rolled her eyes, but she couldn’t bite back her happy grin.

 

“Honey, if you just let me explain,” Lorna was saying as she followed Alice around her bedroom. Alice was throwing clothes and other items into the suitcase open on her bed.

“What is there to explain?” Alice huffed, her voice tight like she had been crying. She sniffled and swiped at her face. “You obviously have a new favorite child. I’m not needed here so I’m leaving.”

“Alice, don’t be like that, baby girl,” Lorna was practically begging. “Nobody could ever replace you, you know that!”

“Do I?” Alice demanded, even as she threw a pair of jeans toward her suitcase. Jen was watching her silently, neither helping nor deterring her from packing. She was simply observing. “Because I’ve been asking – begging – for a dog for over a decade and all I’ve ever gotten were reasons why I couldn’t have one. We’re not home enough or I’m not responsible enough or whatever else you wanted as justification to not get me one!” She sobbed a little. “But then you take in one of my classmates – a girl that bullied me, by the way, for a bit there – and she mentions wanting a bunny one time and poof! Suddenly, she gets a bunny on her birthday, and I still have nothing!” 

Agatha’s heart fell. She had teased Alice almost as harshly as she had teased Jen for a while, just for knowing Jen, for being her girlfriend. She’d stopped when Alice didn’t give her anything back except for those sad puppy dog eyes and made teasing her absolutely no fun (Jen gave as good as she got, though, so Agatha didn’t feel half as bad about teasing her) and pretty much treated Alice as just another acquaintance – until she moved in with her and Lorna.

Then she felt like Alice was becoming more like…like a sister.

She had no idea that Alice was holding any resentment about the teasing. She should have apologized sooner, nonetheless. 

“You don’t have nothing!” Lorna exclaimed. “You have a mother who loves you and would do anything for you!”

“Anything except get me a dog!” Alice shot back. “But that’s fine. I’ll go stay with Dad. Maybe he’ll get me a dog!”

“Alice Wu-Gulliver, you stop this temper tantrum right this second!” Lorna said, her voice taking on a hard edge that Agatha had honestly never heard before. “You are too old to throw a fit over not getting your way.”

“I think she’s pretty valid, actually,” Agatha said, stepping into the room. All eyes turned to her, wide with shock and – in Alice’s case, anyway – anger. 

“Agatha, sweetie,” Lorna started, “this has nothing to do with–”

“Actually,” Agatha said, “I’m pretty sure this has a lot to do with me.” She cleared her throat and turned toward Alice, who was evading her gaze as she continued to pile her things into her suitcase. The pile was so high that there was no way it would close even with magic at this point. “I’m sorry, Alice,” she said, fighting past a lump that had suddenly started forming in her throat.

“There’s no need for you to apolo–” Lorna started.

“Yes, there is,” Agatha interrupted. “Sorry, but there is. I never apologized for all the mean things I’ve said in the past. All the homophobic shit I said in middle school after you and Jen got together. All the, uh, racist stuff I said when I definitely knew better.” She felt tears well up in her eyes. “I was emboldened by my mother’s approval of all that stuff. It was the only time she ever approved of anything I said, and I really let it get to my head.” She attempted a deep breath, but it came out shuddery. “That’s not an excuse though. I shouldn’t have said it. I knew what kind of person my mom was. I knew none of what I was saying was right or fair. Hell, I didn’t even believe a single word of it, so saying it…it was wrong. I am so sorry that I hurt you, Alice. I’m so sorry that I let such vile bullshit come out of my mouth in the first place. You…you’re a really nice person, though, and you were so nice to me the entire time, anyway. You never said anything mean back, not once.” Agatha sniffled and swiped at her face. “But, still, you deserved this apology a long time ago. So…I’m sorry, Alice Wu-Gulliver, for everything I’ve ever done to hurt you.”

More tears dripped down Alice’s face and she rushed forward, wrapping her arms around Agatha’s shoulders, taking Agatha by surprise. She had figured that Alice would still be too angry about the bunny and lack of her own pet to even forgive Agatha, no matter how nice she was or how heartfelt the apology was.

Once again, though, she seemed to have underestimated Alice.

“I forgive you,” Alice murmured against her shoulder. “Of course I forgive you. You’re my sister.”

She hugged Alice back just as tightly, feeling the tears slip down her own cheeks as she squeezed the shorter girl back. Her sister. 

It didn’t matter that they weren’t biologically related.

It didn’t matter that they didn’t grow up together (other than through school).

It didn’t matter that Lorna hadn’t officially adopted her (and now it was probably too late since Agatha was legally an adult.)

It didn’t even matter that they’d barely been more than acquaintances up until recently.

Alice was her sister. 

Agatha knew that she would do anything to protect her. And she knew, despite Alice never explicitly saying it aloud, that the other girl would do the same for her.

Alice Wu-Gulliver was her sister.

Agatha pressed a kiss to her temple as she continued to squeeze her.

The hug only ended when Lorna approached and placed a hand on Alice’s shoulder. “Honey, I–”

Alice shrugged her off and went back to packing her things, but not before giving Agatha’s hand one last squeeze and offering her a tearful smile.

She didn’t even spare her mother a glance.

Lorna looked at Agatha with desperate, tear-filled eyes.

“Just tell her,” Agatha murmured. Lorna furrowed her brows in confusion, and Agatha nodded toward Alice, who was still stomping around the room. “Tell her,” she insisted.

Lorna’s eyes widened at that, realizing that Agatha knew her little secret. She let out a sigh as she pulled out her phone.

“You can’t go to your father’s,” she said.

“Then I’ll go to Jen’s,” Alice said. “And you’ll have to worry about one of us getting magically pregnant because of you.”

Jen’s eyes widened at that. “Alice!” she exclaimed, flushing. “Miss Wu – Lorna, we are not having sex. Nobody is getting pregnant, I swear!” She smacked Alice on the shoulder next time she approached the bed. “Why would you even say that!?”

“You’re not going to Jen’s either,” Lorna huffed. “Will you just stand still for a second?” She grabbed Alice’s hand and tugged her closer. 

Alice tried to fight against her grip, but she paused when she saw what was on the screen that her mother was holding up to her. “What’s that?” she asked, her eyebrows knitted together.

“That’s Ringo,” Lorna said. “Your puppy.”

Alice’s eyes widened. “My puppy?” she asked, her voice full of wonder. 

“Yes, you absolute drama queen,” Lorna said. “I swear, this is what I get for birthing a Gemini.”

“Feeling so very loved right now,” Alice deadpanned, taking the phone from her mother’s hand and zooming in on the pic. Looking over Agatha’s shoulder, she saw a lanky German shepherd puppy with a still-too-large police vest on him, giving the camera a big, toothy grin with his tongue lolling out the side. His eyes looked blank, like there were no brain cells to be found. His tail was blurry like it was wagging furiously. “This is my puppy?” Alice asked, her voice a little choked. “Really?”

“Really,” Lorna confirmed with a sigh. “Your father has a few friends in the K-9 unit and he asked if there were any failures up for adoption.”

“Failure?” Alice asked, her eyes filled with tears. “He’s not a failure. Look at how sweet he is.” She sat down on the bed next to Jen to show her.

“Oh my goddess,” Jen squealed, “what a cutie! His name’s Bingo?”

“Ringo,” Lorna said. “Or whatever you wanna name him, I guess. He’s at your dad’s right now, which is why you’re not allowed to stay with him this month.”

“So Dad’s not renovating the kitchen?” Alice asked.

“He repainted the walls and got a new fridge,” Lorna said. “He figured you’d buy the renovation story with just that. Act surprised when you meet Ringo for the first time; your dad would kill me if he knew I spilled the beans already.”

Agatha snorted at the irony then covered it up with a sniffle as she wiped her eyes.

“Why didn’t you just tell me that I was getting a dog in the first place?” Alice huffed.

“That was supposed to be your birthday surprise,” Lorna insisted. “It’s not my fault you were born in late May!”

“Well, technically…” Jen started. At the look Lorna sent her way, she shut up and started cooing at the picture of Ringo again. “Look at that puppy,” she said. 

“Okay,” Agatha said, swiping at her eyes again. “Now that that’s settled…I’m gonna go to my room real quick to grab something.”

“Okay, honey,” Lorna said. “We’re gonna have cake in about an hour though, so don’t take too long!”

“Roger that!” Agatha said, making her way out of Alice’s bedroom and down the hall to her own. 

Rio was laying on her bed with her head hanging off the edge when Agatha walked in. 

“Hey, you!” Rio said, immediately giving her a lopsided (upside down) grin. She pushed herself up to sit on the edge of the bed, running her hands through her mussed hair. “I was wondering where you’d gone.”

“There were a lot of emotions,” Agatha informed her. “And Lorna had to tell Alice about Ringo.”

“Ringo?”

“The dog,” Agatha clarified. “Because she was understandably very upset and was actually packing to go to her dad’s when I walked in.”

“Oh shit,” Rio said. “Is she okay now that she knows about Roscoe?”

“Ringo,” Agatha corrected. 

“That’s what I said.”

Agatha snorted, shaking her head. “Yeah, she’s okay now. She called me her sister.”

Just the very word brought more tears to Agatha’s eyes. She furiously blinked them away and sniffled. Rio wrapped her arm around Agatha’s shoulders and gave her a sideways hug, pressing a kiss to her cheek.

“Okay, okay,” Agatha said, pulling away. “Where’s my birthday gift?”

“You are so impatient,” Rio snorted, “you know that?”

“Excuse you,” Agatha huffed. “I waited a whole two minutes before even bringing it up even though that’s the only reason I agreed to meet you in here during my birthday party. How’s that for impatient?”

“My mistake,” Rio laughed. “Lo siento.” She reached into her pocket and pulled out a small box, offering it to Agatha, whose eyes widened as her cheeks reddened.

“Uh…” Agatha said, looking at the box in her hand like it was radioactive. “Rio, we’ve only been together for a few months. I know lesbians do the U-Haul thing, but–”

“Just open it,” Rio huffed. “It’s not what you think.”

Agatha eyed the box for another moment before flicking it open, gasping at the jewelry inside.

It was a silver heart with an emerald embedded in it. It glowed subtly when Agatha’s thumb brushed over it. 

“This is beautiful,” Agatha murmured, looking down at it. “But why an emerald? My birthstone is a diamond.”

“You hate diamonds,” Rio said. “You think they’re overrated.”

“They are,” Agatha said. “But I still don’t understand why an emerald. I prefer–”

“Amethyst?” Rio said, pulling a similar charm out from beneath her shirt collar. It was the same silver but with an amethyst embedded into the heart.

“Why do you get the amethyst?” Agatha asked with a little pout.

“Because it reminds me of you,” Rio said, leaning forward to press her forehead against Agatha’s. “And I figured the emerald would remind you of me since, you know, green witch and all that. And it’s my favorite color.”

“You’re such a sap,” Agatha said, pressing a soft kiss to Rio’s lips. “I love it. Thank you.”

“And they glow,” Rio said, grinning. “When you press your thumb over yours, they both glow. And when I press my thumb over mine, they both glow. But feel what happens when we press both of our thumbs over them at the same time.”

She pressed her thumb over the gemstone on her necklace and Agatha mirrored her, her eyes widening when she felt it.

“They’re pulsing,” she said, furrowing her brow. “Is that…is that a heartbeat?”

“That’s my heartbeat,” Rio informed her. “And I can feel yours. No matter where we are. No matter how far away. We’re linked.”

Tears flooded Agatha’s eyes again. 

She needed to stop crying. It was her goddamned birthday!

She surged forward and pressed a firm kiss against Rio’s lips. Rio laughed against her mouth, cupping her cheeks and pushing a strand of hair out of her face.

“I love you so much,” Agatha murmured against her lips.

“I love you too,” Rio replied before pulling away. “Come on, let me help you put the necklace on so we can get back to your party.”

Agatha placed one last kiss to Rio’s lips before handing her the box and turning so that Rio could clasp the necklace around her neck. The heart settled at Agatha’s collarbone and she pressed her fingers to it, feeling it pulse. She turned around to see Rio doing the same with a smile.

Agatha leaned in again, still touching her necklace, and pressed one last kiss to Rio’s lips before grasping her hand and pulling her off the bed, running with her back down to the party, laughing and still pressing their fingers against the gemstones to feel each other’s heartbeats. 

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 31: Antici.........pation

Chapter Summary

Rio and Agatha start to think about what the future has in store for them. Agatha gets a Very Important Letter in the mail....stress.

Chapter Notes

....so much has happened over the last couple of months.

I lost my job at the end of March. Then somebody was stabbed in my apartment building on April Fool's Day (twas not a joke). I still don't have a full-time joke and rent is due soon and my unemployment is running out and I wrote 83k for Big Bang and...so much.

Anyway, I decided to give Agatha some of my stress. Enjoy that.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Chapter Thirty-One

Over the next week, the students fought to keep up their energy as the show got closer and closer to opening night. Lilia was coming down a bit harder on every mistake they made. Every dropped line or flub was met with an entire reset of the scene from the top. If somebody missed a step in a dance number, she stopped the song entirely and sent them back to the beginning. George had come back from visiting his husband in Spain and used his cane almost like a gavel, banging it on the ground every time something went even remotely wrong in his eyes.

Agatha went home every night entirely exhausted. As did Alice and Jen and Rio.

Agatha and Rio barely spent any time with one another after rehearsals ended for the night, both too tired to do much else but sleep. Agatha was used to this, but Rio was definitely struggling. She had to make time during lunch and her free periods to get her homework done so that she didn’t fall completely behind and mess up her Valedictorian chances after she’d already worked so hard to get the role.

But she was so tired.

And she wasn’t sleeping well.

It wasn’t hard to fall asleep most nights after rehearsal. Marisol would have dinner waiting for her when she dragged herself through the front door, practically falling asleep at the kitchen table as she shoveled her dinner into her mouth. Most nights, she even forewent a shower in favor of crawling into bed, half-dressed, asleep practically before her head even hit the pillow.

But then she’d wake up in the middle of the night. And she’d instinctively reach across the bed…and find only cold space.

She’d gotten too used to sleeping over at Agatha’s.

Her mother and Lorna would probably have allowed them to continue having their sleepovers if they’d only asked, but Rio knew that it would have made waking up in the morning even harder. She would have wanted to continue cuddling Agatha until the last possible second.

At least now, without Agatha there, she was able to force herself to get up and jump into a shower to wake herself up after spending an hour or two just staring at the empty pillow next to hers.

It was starting to get ridiculous, though.

Rio wanted to shut her eyes and turn over, but she kept imagining Agatha appearing next to her, taking space on her pillow, her hand reaching out for Rio. Rio wanted to reach out and feel her warmth, wrap her arms around the other girl’s body and pull her in. Instead, her fingers just met cool sheets and empty space.

Rio sighed and pressed her face into her pillow. It just barely smelled like Agatha from the last time she was there. It had been a week, though, and the smell was starting to fade. Rio inhaled as deeply as she could, squeezing her eyes tight as she tried to imagine that it was—

Her phone vibrated on Rio’s end table, practically making Rio jump out of her skin. She turned over and reached for it, blinking blearily at the lit-up screen.

Open your front door.

She furrowed her brow at the screen. The text was from Agatha, but the words didn’t make any sense.

Why? she texted back.

Why do you think?

Hurry up! It’s cold!

Cold? Rio sat up, blinking at the time on the corner of her screen. It was four in the morning. She hurried out of bed and crept out of her bedroom toward the front door. She unlocked it and opened it as quietly as she could, peeking out to see Agatha standing there, dressed in her pea coat and a pair of bunny-patterned pajama pants. She had on fuzzy slippers instead of shoes. Her hair was in two braids under a crocheted beanie. Scratchy was sticking his sleeping head out from the collar of her coat, his floppy ears sticking up at odd angles. Agatha had her backpack and also an overnight bag.

Lorna’s car was behind her, but Lorna wasn’t in the driver’s seat. It was the guy that usually drove them around when Lorna was unavailable. He looked just as tired as Rio felt. He waved to her and gave a thumbs up as he pulled away from the curb. Rio waved back as she opened the screen door.

Agatha practically fell into her arms, wrapping Rio up in her embrace. Rio didn’t think for a second to resist, practically melting into Agatha’s arms.

“What are you doing here at four in the morning?” she asked.

“I missed you,” Agatha murmured, pressing in more tightly. Scratchy let out a disagreeable sound from between them, but she ignored him as she pressed her lips to Rio’s jaw. “I couldn’t sleep. Lorna told me that I could call John whenever I needed a ride, so…”

“You woke that poor man up just so he could drive you to your girlfriend’s in the middle of the night?” Rio snorted. “That’s so unhinged.” She pressed a kiss to Agatha’s forehead. “I love you.”

“I love you, too,” Agatha murmured. “Now, come on. Need sleep.”

“Okay,” Rio whispered, “but be quiet. We don’t want to wake my—”

She turned around, freezing when she saw her mother standing at the bottom of the steps, in her nightdress and bonnet, one eyebrow lifted.

“Heyyy, Mami,” Rio said, giving her mother an awkward smile.

“Hello,” Marisol retorted. “What are you doing at this hour?” She eyed Agatha, who was peeking just over Rio’s shoulder. “Agatha, querida, what are you doing here?”

“Uh…”

“Agatha couldn’t sleep,” Rio said. “Neither could I.”

Marisol nodded: that was all the explanation she really needed.

“Bien,” she sighed. “Come in. Lock the door and go to bed. It’s late and you need to be up for school in a couple of hours.”

Rio hurried to lock the door before ushering Agatha toward her bedroom.

Marisol cut them off at the hallway, pulling Agatha into a hug and pressing a kiss to her cheek. “Hola, querida,” she said. “Hola, Scratchy,” she pressed a peck to the bunny’s soft fur, and he let out a happy squeak in response. “Sleep well,” she said, yawning.

“Gracias, Señora,” Agatha said, smiling softly as Rio took her hand and practically dragged her toward her bedroom.

“Gracias, Mami!” Rio called over her shoulder. As soon as they were inside, Agatha took off her pea coat, revealing Scratchy practically strapped to her chest with some kind of scarf thing.

“Couldn’t you leave the bunny demon at home?” Rio huffed, eyeing him. Agatha reached into her overnight bag and pulled out a cushion, placing it at the foot of the bed before she carefully extracted the bun from the scarf and placed him atop it.

“I tried,” she admitted. “He started crying.” She pouted, stroking his back as he settled on his cushion. “I couldn’t leave him behind after that.”

“Demon,” Rio huffed, even as she got into bed, scooting over so that Agatha could get in next to her. Scratchy was only mildly disturbed on his cushion before everything settled. Rio wrapped her arm around Agatha’s waist. “I’m glad you’re here, at least,” she said, pressing her face against Agatha’s shoulder.

“Me too,” Agatha admitted. “I’ve barely slept at all this last week.”

“This might become a problem when we get to college,” Rio sighed. “If we can’t spend even a full week sleeping apart. Especially if we’re going to separate schools.”

“Maybe I’ll go to Columbia with you,” Agatha murmured, her eyes already closed. “Then we can request a dorm together.”

“Still haven’t heard back from Juilliard?” Rio asked.

Agatha shook her head. “I should have by now, shouldn’t I? I mean, they said by the first or second week in April. The first week is over already.”

“It’s snail mail,” Rio reminded her. “It’s just slow.”

“I know,” Agatha sighed. “I’m just…anxious, I guess. What if I didn’t make it?”

“Don’t think like that,” Rio said, pushing herself up to look down at Agatha’s face. She cupped her cheek, and Agatha’s eyes fluttered open. Rio could see, even in the dark, that they were shiny with unshed tears. “You’ll get in,” she said. “And, if you don’t, we’ll just hex them.”

Agatha let out a tiny snort at that. “You’re gonna hex a whole performing arts school?” she asked, dubiously.

“What are they gonna do about it?” Rio scoffed. “Sing a showtune? Do a little tap dance?”

Agatha let out a cackle and smacked Rio lightly on the wrist. “You’re ridiculous,” she said.

Rio fell back down to the bed and wrapped her arms around Agatha’s waist, pulling her into her embrace. “Ridiculously in love with you,” she replied, kissing her shoulder again.

Agatha let out a groan, but she pressed her body against Rio’s, hiding her face in the crook of Rio’s neck. “You are such a sap,” she murmured against her neck. “I love you.”

Rio grinned into her hair. “I love you,” she said again. “Now go to sleep before the sun rises.”

Agatha was already snoring. Rio soon joined her.

Marisol drove them to school the next morning, barely conscious. She made Agatha keep Scratchy at the house despite Agatha’s protests that ‘nobody would even notice him at school’ and promised that they could go see him at lunchtime if she really wanted. Rio wasn’t looking forward to that.

Scratchy was still a little shit in her eyes. He no longer bit her (because Agatha had punished that behavior by ignoring him) but he still obviously hated Rio for whatever reason. The feeling was mutual, so it was okay.

Now, at least, they tolerated each other’s presence. For Agatha.

At least when he was staying at Alice’s house, Agatha didn’t have time to go back and forth during lunch to see him. But Rio lived much closer, which meant that Agatha was going to drag her home for lunch to see the little demon, who probably already urinated on her bed the second the door shut behind them.

At least Marisol stopped by the coffee shop with them and bought them each a drink and a pastry to help wake them up. Agatha thanked her profusely and even tried to give her some money for her tea and croissant, but Marisol just scoffed and waved her away.

“It’s nothing, querida,” she tutted. “You must eat, no? Just say thank you and go to school.”

“Thank you,” Agatha sighed, rolling her eyes affectionately as she hugged Marisol tightly.

Marisol pressed a kiss to her forehead before letting her go. Rio stepped in next, pressing a smacking kiss to her cheek, which Marisol giggled and groaned at, lightly shoving her away.

The girls walked the rest of the way to the high school, waving goodbye to Marisol as she drove away, blowing them both kisses, which they returned.

It was a nice day in April. The leaves had started to grow back on the trees back in March and now they were almost back to their full glory. The temperature was decently in the mid-sixties and climbing, and the sun was peeking out from between the clouds as they approached the high school. Agatha inhaled deeply in between bites of her croissant and sips of her chai. She felt good even though her stomach was still a bit tense.

Jen and Alice met them at the front doors of the school. Jen was doing a dance like a three-year-old that needed to go to the potty. She was holding a couple of envelopes in her hands.

“What’s up with her?” Agatha asked Alice as they got closer. Alice was writing something in a notebook in her hands and practically jumped at the sound of Agatha’s voice.

“There you are!” she exclaimed, jumping to her feet from the bench she’d been lounging on. “Mom was worried sick about you!”

“No, she wasn’t,” Agatha snorted. “She knew where I was the whole time. She called John to give me a ride.” She lifted her brow at Alice and smirked. “Were you worried sick about me?” she asked, teasingly.

“What?” Alice scoffed. “No!”

She was blushing, her arms crossed over her chest.

“Aww, Allie!” Agatha cooed, wrapping her free arm around Alice’s shoulders and pulling her into a side-hug.

Alice struggled against her, shoving at Agatha’s face as she attempted to playfully press a kiss to Alice’s temple. “Get offa me!” Alice huffed. “And don’t call me Allie! You know I hate that!”

Agatha pouted at her, but Alice just rolled her eyes, continuing to frown.

“Mean,” Agatha huffed. “Anyway, what’s up with Jen?”

Jen was still doing her little dance, holding something in her hands. Upon closer inspection, Agatha realized that she was holding a couple of envelopes.

She immediately handed her cup and the remnants of her croissant to Rio, who was in the middle of inhaling her own breakfast. Rio took them without question, watching as Agatha ran up to Jen.

“Jen!” she exclaimed. “Is that—”

“There you are!” Jen huffed. “We’ve been looking for you all morning!”

“School doesn’t even start for another twenty minutes,” Agatha said, looking at her phone. “Where did you look?”

Jen ignored the question, instead holding up the envelopes in her hands. One had Agatha’s name on it. Both were from Juilliard.

“What?” Agatha gasped, reaching for the one with her name. “Wh—how did you get this?!”

“They both came to my house!” Jen exclaimed. “They were half hidden under the hallway rug when I was on my way out to get to school. The mailman probably shoved them a little too hard through the mail slot.”

“Why did they both go to your house though?” Agatha asked. “Mine should have gone to Lorna’s.”

“Beats me,” Jen said. “But they’re here! Our acceptance letters are here!”

“Or rejection,” Agatha murmured.

Jen flicked her on her forehead.

“Agh!” Agatha exclaimed, slapping her hand away. “What the hell?!”

“Think positive!” Jen huffed. “Dumbass.”

“You should be a motivational speaker,” Agatha grumbled, tearing the envelope with her name from Jen’s grip.

She stared at her name printed on the envelope for a while, then at the Juilliard crest on the upper left corner. Her heart was pounding in her ears as she stared at it, trying to imagine what lay inside the thick envelope. It was small, which usually meant bad news, right? Didn’t acceptance letters come in the big envelopes? The envelopes that had information packets about the campus and the student body and the drama program? Surely, if they intended to admit Agatha and Jen into these programs, they’d be receiving those big envelopes and not these tiny little normal-sized ones…right?

“You wanna open them together?” Jen asked, her voice low and almost completely silent.

“Not yet,” Agatha said, her voice just as quiet, breaking slightly. She cleared her throat. “Let’s wait for a bit,” she said. “If we get denied—”

“We won’t,” Jen said, certain.

“If we do,” Agatha continued, “then I don’t want to carry that through the school day.” She slipped her backpack off and shoved the envelope inside.

“Maybe we can ask Lilia to open them with us,” Jen suggested.

Something in Agatha’s chest tightened, and she immediately wanted to brush off the idea. Sharing her rejection with Jen was one thing, but sharing it with Lilia? She didn’t know if she’d be able to survive that.

“Maybe,” she murmured. “Let’s just…go to class.”

She didn’t wait for any of them to respond as she started making her way into the school. Rio, who was still holding her tea and pastry, hurried after her, catching up with Agatha as she started up the steps.

“Hey,” she said, lightly touching her arm as they climbed the steps. “Are you okay?”

Agatha didn’t really know what to say to that. Her breathing felt shallow, but that might have been due to the steps she was climbing. Her throat felt tight, but that might have been from thirst. She reached for the green tea in Rio’s hand. Rio let it slip from her fingers easily, then she handed over the croissant, as well. Agatha took a bite of the pastry, then washed it down with a sip of tea – all without losing her stride.

It was hard to swallow past the lump in her throat, but she managed it, reaching the second-floor landing and racing down the hallway to Lilia’s classroom. Lilia was already there, writing something on the board. She turned as Agatha entered but said nothing as Agatha rushed to her seat and sat down, heavily, with her breakfast in her hands. She did, however, share a curious look with Rio, who entered seconds later, cheeks pink with the exertion of running after her girlfriend.

Lilia gave Rio a look, asking a silent question, but all Rio could do was shrug in response. She shuffled over to her seat, next to Agatha’s, and sat down, sparing Agatha sidelong glances as they both finished their breakfast.

Neither said a word, and the bell rang soon after.

Agatha felt the presence of that envelope in her backpack for the rest of the day.

She tried to ignore it as best as she could, pulling out only the books that she needed for each class and barely even allowing her fingers to brush against it as she exchanged supplies at her locker. She even forced her book under her desk, trying to forget about it completely as she listened to her teachers drone on and on about…whatever they were talking about. Agatha had never really focused that much in class, anyway. She learned most of what she did by reading the textbooks and copying down the notes from the blackboards into her notebooks. The teachers’ voices usually just grated on her nerves, anyway.

Lilia’s was the only voice she really cared about when it came to class. After first period, however, Agatha tended to tune out.

How she had such consistently good grades was beyond her, honestly.

“Sounds like you’re an autodidact,” Rio said as they walked to her house for lunch.

Agatha had left her backpack in the dressing room at school. It felt somehow heavier with the envelope in it, like the paper was made out of lead. She could do without that for a little while.

“An autodidact?” Agatha echoed, only half-listening as she kicked a pebble down the road.

“Somebody who teaches themselves by simply reading,” Rio explained.

“I know what the word means,” Agatha said. “I read it in a book once.”

“Funny,” Rio deadpanned. “Anyway, it sounds like that’s what you are.”

“Maybe,” Agatha hummed. “I’ve always been a pretty good reader.”

“Who taught you how to read?” Rio asked.

“My mom, funny enough,” Agatha sighed. “She wanted to make sure I could keep up in church – and that she could brag that her four-year-old could recite hymns.”

“Was she cruel to you while teaching you?” Rio asked, cautiously.

Agatha thought on it for a moment, then shook her head. “I think she knew that I would be less likely to retain the skill if I was being screamed at or spanked for getting words wrong. She usually just gave me candy.”

“I thought you weren’t allowed to have candy,” Rio said. “It’s like satanic or something.”

“It was some kind of special candy that the church gave us,” Agatha snorted. “Like some kind of holy M&Ms. Every time I got a word right, I got one. Every time I made a mistake, I gave her two.”

“Wow…” Rio said. “That…was not equal at all.”

“Nope!” Agatha laughed. “But I learned, so I guess it worked. I didn’t even like the holy M&Ms, but it was candy, so…” She shrugged. “And it was one of the few times I can actually recall my mom being somewhat kind to me. She didn’t even yell.”

Agatha felt a small lump form in her throat at the memory of her usual harsh, biting mother talking in a soft tone to four-year-old Agatha, dangling a baggy of pastel-colored chocolate pieces in front of her as she held a book of hymns and tried to sound out the words.

She felt Rio’s hand close around hers and glanced sideways to see Rio offering her a sidelong glance and a sympathetic smile. Agatha smiled back without any teeth. She squeezed her hand.

They spent their lunch break on the floor in the living room, playing with Scratchy.

Well, Agatha played with Scratchy; Rio cleaned the messes he made and tried to appease him with more dandelions and cabbage. In return, he did not bite her…much.

The walk back was quiet. Agatha was sad to leave her bunny (even though Rio reminded her that they’d see him in a couple hours when they used their free period to bring him back to Lorna’s) and was still stressed out about the envelope in her backpack.

“You really think you were rejected?” Rio asked.

“I don’t know,” Agatha said. “The envelope is so…small. Did you get a small envelope from Columbia?”

Rio’s silence was louder than any words she could have said.

“Exactly,” Agatha sighed. “If I was rejected, I don’t even want to know.”

“But what if you were accepted?” Rio asked. “Wouldn’t you want to know then?”

“I wish there was a way for me to know for certain.”

“There is,” Rio said. “Open the—”

“A different way, jackass!” Agatha huffed, shoving Rio’s shoulder lightly just as the school came into view.

“Have Lilia give you a tarot reading,” Rio suggested. “She’s a divination witch, isn’t she?”

“Tarot is entirely subjective,” Agatha huffed. “She’s just going to tell me that I got in and then I’ll be even more disappointed when I’m rejected.”

“If,” Rio corrected. “If you’re rejected.”

“So you think it’s a possibility?” Agatha asked.

“Only one way to find out,” Rio said. “Otherwise it’s Schrödinger’s Letter – both a rejection and an acceptance until you break the seal on the envelope.”

“You’re such a nerd,” Agatha snorted, nudging her shoulder as they walked into the school together.

“Hey, you understood the reference,” Rio pointed out.

There was really no arguing with that.

After dropping Scratchy off back at Lorna’s (via a hexenbesen with the bunny strapped to Agatha’s chest, his floppy little ears slapping her in the face) Agatha and Rio returned to the school, both for rehearsal and the moment of truth.

Agatha had left her backpack in the dressing room again. When she went to retrieve it, she found Jen already there, pacing back and forth, her own envelope twisted and crumpled in her hand but still sealed. She looked up when Agatha entered, chewing on her bottom lip.

“Hey,” she said.

“Hey,” Agatha said. “You still didn’t open it?”

“Nope,” Jen said. “We said after school, didn’t we?”

Agatha nodded. “Right.” She took a deep breath. “Are we still going to do this with Lilia?”

“Yeah,” Jen said, nodding. “She should be in her classroom.”

Agatha nodded, grabbing her letter from her bookbag. It was in better condition than Jen’s, but only because Agatha had avoided touching it for so long. Now, she couldn’t help but bend it a little as she and Jen made their way toward Lilia’s office. Rio and Alice followed behind them, sharing a nervous glance.

Lilia was marking papers at her desk when they walked in.

“Thirty minutes,” she sighed, not even looking up. “All I want is thirty minutes to grade these sorry excuses for essays that your classmates—”

“We got our Juilliard letters,” Agatha said.

That got Lilia’s attention. Her gaze snapped to them as they held up their envelopes.

“Your Juilliard letters?” she echoed.

“Yep,” Jen said. “We…wanted you to be there when we open them.”

“You haven’t yet?” Lilia asked, putting down her pen and pulling away from her desk.

“Nope,” Agatha said. “Still sealed.” She waved her letter around, feeling as though she were waving around a bomb.

“Well, what are you waiting for?” Lilia huffed, walking toward them. “Open! Open! Hurry up!”

“Okay, okay,” Agatha snorted. “Don’t get your granny panties in a twist.”

She and Jen shared a look as the latter slipped one manicured finger under the flap of her envelope and started to pull at it, separating the glued edges.

Agatha followed her lead, and soon the both of them had torn open envelopes in their hands, staring at the folded pieces of paper within. Agatha swallowed thickly as she looked down at it. She watched from the corner of her eye as Jen slowly pulled the piece of paper out. It was still folded. Her eyes were closed.

She mirrored Jen’s movements.

“You ready for this?” Jen asked as soon as the paper was in Agatha’s hand.

“Not at all,” Agatha replied honestly. “You?”

“I feel like I’m going to throw up,” Jen said.

“Well, don’t.”

“That helps.”

“Would you two just open the damn letters!” Lilia huffed. “Quit stalling!”

Jen and Agatha both sent her glares, which she returned, full-force, before they turned to look at each other, communicating their intentions silently.

Then they opened their letters, glancing down at the papers at the same time.

“Dear Agatha Harkness,

            Thank you for participating in the auditions for The Juilliard School. We appreciated the opportunity to meet you and become acquainted with your talents.

            As a result of your audition and application evaluation by the Drama Division faculty and Committee on Admissions, it is with regret we must inform you…”

The letter fell from Agatha’s hands, fluttering to the ground with what felt like a deafening thud. She felt the very second her heart shattered in her chest as her vision blurred and her hearing failed entirely. She felt hands on her arms and tears on her cheeks as Rio’s voice said her name from what felt like a hundred miles below the sea.

“…it is with regret…”

Regret. Rejection. Failure.

Agatha pushed her way out of Rio’s arms and ran straight out the door, just barely registering the voices calling out her name.
